致谢

Acknowledgments

 

一本书在某种程度上是一种产品，一种软件产品。与任何可行的软件产品一样，一本书在向公众发布之前应该进行测试，以最大限度地降低其对读者无用的风险。我的图书测试团队——James Bach、Michael Bolton、Fiona Charles、Elisabeth Hendrickson、Pradeep Soundararajan 和 Dani Weinberg，他们一起发现了本书早期草稿中的数十个错误——我衷心感谢他们。我最初制造了错误，消除或修复它们是我的工作，所以如果仍然存在，那是我的责任，而不是他们的责任。

A book is a product, a software product, in a way. Like any viable software product, a book should be tested prior to release to the public to minimize the risk of its not being useful to its readers. To my team of book testers—James Bach, Michael Bolton, Fiona Charles, Elisabeth Hendrickson, Pradeep Soundararajan, and Dani Weinberg, who together detected dozens of bugs in early drafts of this manuscript—I give wholehearted thanks. I made the bugs originally and it was my job to eliminate or fix them, so if any remain, it's my responsibility, not theirs.

对于来自世界各地的客户和学生，我要感谢他们贡献的故事和例子，为本书的创作增添了血肉。所有的例子都是真实的，所有的故事都是真实的，尽管大多数都以某种方式进行了伪装以保护机密。

To my clients and students from all over the world, I give thanks for their having contributed the stories and examples that add flesh to the bones on which this book is built. All the examples are authentic and all the stories are true, though most have been disguised in some way to protect confidentiality.

如果你，我的读者，发现了一些我遗漏的错误或者一些合适的故事或例子，我希望你能引起我的注意。提前感谢您加入测试团队。

Should you, my readers, find some bug that I missed or some story or example that fits, I hope you will bring it to my attention. I thank you in advance for joining the test team.

前言

Preface

 

半个多世纪以前，当我开始从事计算机行业时，计算机极为稀有和珍贵。当我发现自己坐在一个装满硬件的巨大房间前的控制台前时，我还不到十几岁，这些硬件可能占世界计算能力的 10%。我可以用手指轻轻一按将其关闭——有时确实如此。

More than half a century ago, when I started in the computer business, computers were extremely rare and precious. I was barely more than a teenager when I found myself sitting at a console in front of a huge room full of hardware that comprised perhaps 10 percent of the computing power in the world. I could turn it off with a press of my finger—and sometimes did.

如果你愿意轮到你，你可以租用所有的电力一个小时，大约是我月薪的两倍。如今，电脑的价格如此实惠，以至于我实际上已经赠送了比那些早期型号快 50,000 倍、内存大 50,000 倍的机器。这些赠品机器非常小巧轻便，我可以轻松地将一台放在公文包中，但它们的计算能力甚至不及当今世界的十亿分之一。

If you were willing to wait your turn, you could rent all that power for an hour for approximately twice my monthly salary. Today, computers are so affordable that I have actually given away machines that are 50,000 times faster than those early models, with 50,000 times the memory. These giveaway machines, which are so compact and lightweight that I easily can carry one in my briefcase, don't account for even a billionth of the computing power in the world today.

是的，我看到技术取得了长足的进步，但它逐渐影响了我。直到几年前，当我听到新闻广播报道卡纳维拉尔角的火箭发射被擦洗时，我才真正注意到这些变化。当播音员结束他们的报告时，其中一位评论说：“NASA 说这是一个计算机软件错误。”

Yes, I've seen technology come a long way, but it crept up on me gradually. I didn't really take note of the changes until a few years ago when I heard a newscast reporting on the scrubbing of a rocket launch at Cape Canaveral. As the announcers wrapped up their report, one commented, "NASA says it was a computer software error."

第二个播音员回答说：“像计算机这样简单普通的东西会犯这样的错误，难道不奇怪吗？”

The second announcer replied, "Isn't it strange that something so simple and common as a computer could make such a mistake?"

“是的，”第一个回答。“你认为他们不会测试他们的软件吗？”

"Yes," responded the first. "Wouldn't you think they would test their software?"

 

 

* * *

* * *

 

 

是的，我认为他们会测试他们的软件。事实上，我确信他们做到了。不过，显然，播音员的思想测试必然会产生完美的产品。

Yes, I think they would test their software. In fact, I'm sure they did. Evidently, though, the announcer thought testing must inevitably lead to a perfect product.

我无法停止思考这段对话和广播员不切实际的期望。起初，我只是耸耸肩告诉自己，“这就是公众对软件测试的无知”，但为时已晚。我的意识现在提高了。我开始看到，即使是我的软件构建客户的经理也表现出同样的无知。尤其是管理人员。软件测试让他们发疯。

I couldn't stop thinking about this dialogue and the broadcaster's unrealistic expectations. At first, I simply shrugged and told myself, "Such is the ignorance of the general public about software testing," but it was too late to shrug it off. My consciousness was now raised. I began to see how even the managers at my software-building clients display the same ignorance. Especially the managers. Software testing was driving them crazy.

我是一个有同理心的人，当我周围的人受苦时，我会和他们一起受苦。我可以看到软件经理以及他们的员工和客户都在受苦。我现在还可以看到，几乎所有人都不是因为测试复杂、耗时或费力而受苦；他们因为不合理的期望和错误的软件测试模型而受苦。

I'm an empathic person, and when people around me suffer, I suffer with them. I could see that the software managers were suffering, along with their employees and customers. I could also now see that almost all of them were suffering not so much because testing was complicated or time-consuming or laborious; they were suffering because of their unreasonable expectations and fallacious models about software testing.

最后，当我发现无知导致痛苦时，我决定做我似乎总是做的事情：我写下问题和可能的解决方案。我写的东西最终成了这本书。

Finally, I decided to do what I always seem to do when I find ignorance causing pain: I wrote about the problem and probable solutions. What I wrote eventually became this book.

 

 

* * *

* * *

 

 

多年前，当我写《计算机编程心理学》时，我的目的是帮助那些想了解编程的人。[1] 很多人告诉我它有帮助，所以也许那本书的成功在一定程度上启发了我写这本书：帮助那些想了解测试的人。

When I wrote The Psychology of Computer Programming many years ago, I intended it to help people who want to understand programming. [1] Quite a few people have told me it helped, so perhaps, in part, the success of that book inspired me to write this book: to help people who want to understand testing.

我的目标读者是广泛的：我设想这本书掌握在专业测试人员、开发人员、消费者、分析师、设计师、程序员、他们所有的经理和他们所有的同事手中。

My intended audience is broad: I envision this book in the hands of professional testers, developers, consumers, analysts, designers, programmers, all of their managers, and all of their coworkers.

大多数专业测试人员都知道本书中的大部分内容，但我希望通过继续阅读，他们将看到新的方式来与他们的经理、开发人员、同事和客户交流他们所知道的内容。

Most professional testers will know most of what's in this book, but I hope that by reading on, they will see new ways to communicate what they know—to their managers, developers, coworkers, and customers.

我想帮助开发人员和测试人员了解他们的经理在遇到软件测试问题时所面临的问题。

I'd like to help both developers and testers understand what their managers face when they confront software testing issues.

我想帮助客户——购买软件的人——成为消息灵通的消费者。

I'd like to help customers—the people who buy the software—to be better-informed consumers.

而且，由于当今每个人都受到软件的影响——并受到测试不当的软件的伤害——我想帮助每个人更加关心测试。

And, since everyone is affected by software today—and hurt by poorly tested software—I'd like to help everyone to care more about testing.

因为我希望接触到广泛的受众，所以我选择尽可能使用通俗易懂的语言，避免使用高度专业的术语和过于详细的分析。（对于那些有兴趣了解有关软件测试的更多技术细节的人，我在本书末尾的附加阅读部分指出了一些特别扎实的书籍。）为了让我专注于帮助那些想了解测试的人，我围绕最让大多数人困惑的问题组织了本书：

Because I hope to reach a broad audience, I've chosen to use plain language wherever possible, avoiding highly technical terms and overly detailed analyses. (For those who are interested in learning more technical detail about software testing, I point to some particularly solid books in the Additional Reading section at the end of this book.) To keep my focus on helping people who want to understand testing, I've organized the book around the questions that puzzle the most people:

当它似乎会减慢我们的速度时，为什么我们还要费心测试呢？

Why do we have to bother testing when it just seems to slow us down?

为什么人们不能正确地构建软件，所以它不需要测试？

Why can't people just build software right, so it doesn't need testing?

我们必须测试一切吗？

Do we have to test everything?

为什么不测试一切？

Why not just test everything?

是什么让测试如此困难？

What is it that makes testing so hard?

为什么测试需要这么长时间？

Why does testing take so long?

完美的软件甚至可能吗？

Is perfect software even possible?

为什么我们不能只接受一些错误？

Why can't we just accept a few bugs?

2008 年 4 月

April 2008

GMW，新墨西哥州阿尔伯克基

G.M.W., Albuquerque, New Mexico

第 1 章_我们为什么要进行测试？

Chapter_1_Why Do We Bother Testing?

 

“......我完全意识到我余生的大部分时间都将花在寻找我自己程序中的错误上。” - William Aspray 和 Martin Campbell-Kelly，计算机：信息机器的历史。（纽约：Westview Press，2004 年），第 3 页。167.

". . . the realization came over me with full force that a good part of the remainder of my life was going to be spent in finding errors in my own programs." - William Aspray and Martin Campbell-Kelly, Computer: A History of the Information Machine. (New York: Westview Press, 2004), p. 167.

假设您有一个可以计算理想投资策略的软件程序的好主意。您计划使用该软件将您微薄的毕生积蓄变成数百万美元。您编写了软件，并且确信自己已经完美地完成了。现在你会怎么做？

Suppose you have a great idea for a software program that will compute the ideal investment strategy. You plan to use the software to turn your meager life savings into millions. You write the software, and you're sure you've done it perfectly. Now what would you do?

在根据其投资策略建议投资您节省的每一分钱之前，您是否会测试该程序？

Would you test the program before investing every penny you've saved based on its investment-strategy advice?

如果其他人编写了程序，您会测试它吗？

Would you test it if someone else had written the program?

如果您回答了第一个问题，“不，我不会费心测试它”，请不要继续阅读。本书不适合那些认为自己可以编写出完美程序并确信它是完美的人。如果你对第二个问题的回答也不是，那你一定相信人的思维是可以完美的。对这两个问题中的一个或两个都回答“否”意味着，对我来说，你属于不会喜欢这本书的一类人，因为你不明白为什么需要这本书。马上放下。让自己免于更多的痛苦。

If you answered the first question, "No, I wouldn't bother to test it," don't read any further. This book is not for people who think that they can write a perfect program and be perfectly sure that it is perfect. If you also answered no to the second question, you must believe that human thinking can be perfect. Answering no to either or both of these questions means, to me, that you are in a category of people who will not enjoy this book because you won't understand why it's necessary. Put it down right now. Spare yourself further pain.

人类不是完美的思想家。

Humans are not perfect thinkers.

如果你的想法是完美的，你就不需要测试。如果你相信你必须永远是完美的，那么你会发现测试或测试人员的存在相当令人沮丧，因为这意味着你的想法不可能是完美的。但是如果你说，“好吧，在我投入毕生积蓄之前，我可能想做一点测试，”那么你不会总是因为测试这个想法而感到沮丧。你应该继续读下去。

If your thinking were perfect, you would not need testing. If you believe that you must always be perfect, then you would find the existence of testing or testers rather upsetting, because it would imply that your thinking cannot be perfect. But if you say, "Well, before I invested my life savings, I might want to do a little testing," then you won't always be upset by the very idea of testing. You should read on.

如果你还在阅读，欢迎。你向我展示了你是一个真正的人，而且你知道你是。真正的人都知道，无论他们多么努力地把工作做得完美，他们有时还是会犯错误。真正的人类也知道他们并不孤单，其他人也相似。知道了这一点，您可能会喜欢阅读这本书，因为它讲述了真实的人类如何做出比未经测试更好的决定。事实上，比那些认为自己必须永远完美的人做出的决定要好。但只有更好，没有完美。

If you're still reading, welcome. You're showing me both that you are a real human being and that you know that you are. Real human beings know that no matter how hard they try to do a perfect job, they will sometimes make mistakes. Real human beings also know they are not alone in their fallibility, and that other human beings are similar. Knowing this, you just might enjoy reading this book, because it's about how real humans can make decisions that are better than they could make without testing. Better decisions, in fact, than those made by people who think they must always be perfect. But only better, not perfect.

我们需要做出关于软件的决定。

We need to make decisions about software.

在最简单的层面上，人们一直在做测试。我们经常在不知情的情况下运行和分析测试。在这里，用我自己在日记中的话来说，是我在写这本书时所做的一些测试，这些测试我真的没有意识到，有意识地，作为测试。

At the simplest level, people are doing testing all the time. We often run and analyze tests without even knowing it. Here, in my own words from my journal, are some tests I did while writing this book, tests I really didn't think of, consciously, as tests.

日记账分录 1：

Journal entry 1:

“我想要一个与 Mac OS X 兼容的网络编写应用程序。我读到的一篇评论描述了一个非常棒的应用程序，充满了我想要的功能。然后我读到它不能在 OS X 下运行。

"I want a Web-writing application compatible with Mac OS X. A review I read described a rather wonderful application, full of features that I'd like to have. Then I read that it doesn't run under OS X.

"测试结束：该应用不符合我的约束条件（系统兼容性），我不会购买。"

"End of test: The application doesn't meet my constraint (system compatibility). I will not buy it."

回顾：我们进行测试以确保我们的软件不会因为未能满足基本的客户约束而被拒绝。

Recap: We test to be sure our software isn't rejected because it fails to satisfy an essential customer constraint.

（注意：这是一个测试，尽管我从未接触过键盘。稍后会详细介绍。）

(Note: This is a test, even though I never touched a keyboard. More on that later.)

日记条目 2：

Journal entry 2:

“我仍在寻找一个网络写作应用程序，今天我看到了一个五星级的免费照片编目程序评论。我正要下载它时我意识到照片编目程序不会做Web 编写应用程序的工作。我想保留的照片不超过十张，所以无论多么美妙，谁需要照片编目程序来管理十张图片？

"I'm still looking for a Web-writing application, and today I ran across a five-star review of a freeware photo-cataloging program. I was about to download it when I realized that the photo-cataloging program won't do the work of a Web-writing application. I don't have more than ten photos that I want to keep, so no matter how wonderful it is, who needs a photo-cataloging program to manage ten pictures?

"测试结束：该应用程序不符合任何要求（我正在寻找 Web 编写应用程序），因此我不需要它。"

"End of test: The application doesn't meet any requirement (I'm looking for a Web-writing application), so I don't need it."

回顾：我们进行测试以确保我们的软件不会因为没有完成人们希望它做的事情而被拒绝。（再次注意，这是我在没有敲击任何键的情况下进行的测试。）

Recap: We test to be sure our software isn't rejected because it doesn't do the things people want it to do. (Note, once again, that this was a test I did without banging any keys.)

日记条目 3：

Journal entry 3:

“我找到了一个免费的网络编写应用程序，它可以在 OS X 下运行并且可以完成我想要它做的事情。宣传材料表明它可以免费下载和使用一个月，并且可以选择永久启用它带有一个我可以花 49 美元购买的密钥。我已经下载了试用版并尝试安装它，但安装失败，因为我没有正确型号的内部磁盘驱动器。

"I've found a free Web-writing application that runs under OS X and does the things I want it to do. The promotional material indicates that it can be downloaded and used for one month for free, with the option of enabling it permanently with a key that I can buy for $49. I've downloaded the trial copy and tried to install it, but the installation failed because I don't have the right model internal disk drive.

“测试结束：我无法在我的配置上安装该应用程序而不会使我的保修失效，所以我不会购买它。我的搜索继续。”

"End of test: I cannot install the application on my configuration without voiding my warranty, so I won't buy it. My search continues."

回顾：我们进行测试以确保我们的软件不会因为给我们的客户带来不可接受的成本和/或要求而被拒绝。（注意：我终于触动了一个键，但只有一个，来执行这个测试。）

Recap: We test to be sure our software isn't rejected because it imposes unacceptable costs and/or requirements on our customers. (Note: I finally touched a key, but only one, to perform this test.)

日记条目 4：

Journal entry 4:

“我找到了另一个在 OS X 下运行并提供 30 天免费试用的网络编写应用程序。我已经下载并成功安装了它。这很好，但是当我打开一个我正在构建的网页时，做了一个小修改，当我试图保存页面时应用程序崩溃了。

"I found another Web-writing application that runs under OS X and offers a free 30-day trial. I've downloaded it and installed it successfully. So that is good, but when I opened a Web page that I had under construction and made a small modification, the application crashed when I tried to save the page.

”测试结束：如果这个common的一个功能失败了，我对这个应用就没有太大的信心了，所以我也不会买这个。”

"End of test: If a function this common fails, I cannot have much confidence in the application, so I won't buy this one either."

回顾：我们进行测试以确保我们的软件不会因为其故障破坏客户信心而被拒绝。

Recap: We test to be sure our software isn't rejected because its failures destroy customer confidence.

日记条目 5：

Journal entry 5:

“我终于发现了一个在 Web 上运行的 Web 编写程序，满足我的所有限制，不会在我尝试做的前几件事上崩溃，并允许我保存我的工作。一切都很棒，但有一个主要缺点：每次保存都需要一分钟多的时间。

"I've finally discovered a Web-writing program that runs on the Web itself, meets all of my constraints, doesn't crash on the first few things I try to do, and permits me to save my work. All that is great, but there is a major drawback: Each save takes more than a minute.

"测试结束：每次保存我的工作时，我都不能等待超过一分钟。这样的性能在我的工作日至少要花费我半个小时。我无法使用该程序。"

"End of test: I cannot afford to wait more than a minute each time I save my work. Such performance would cost me at least a half-hour during my workday. I can't use the program."

回顾：我们进行测试以确保我们的软件不会因为它迫使我们的客户浪费他们的时间而被拒绝。

Recap: We test to be sure our software isn't rejected because it forces our customers to waste their time.

日记条目 6：

Journal entry 6:

“一位朋友推荐了她使用的 Web 编写应用程序。它在 OS X 上运行，据她说，它从不崩溃。它具有我想要的功能，而且售价 999 美元。

"A friend recommended a Web-writing application she uses. It runs on OS X and, according to her, never crashes. It has the features I want—and costs $999.

“测试结束：我不想要一个 Web 编写的应用程序，以至于花近 1000 美元是合理的，所以我不会购买它。”

"End of test: I don't want a Web-writing application badly enough to justify spending almost a thousand dollars, so I won't buy it."

回顾：我们进行测试以确保我们的软件不会因为对大多数客户而言成本太高而被拒绝。

Recap: We test to be sure our software isn't rejected because it's too costly for most of our customers.

* * *

* * *

那么，在所有这些测试之后，我最终做了什么？我继续在我的旧操作系统 OS 9 下使用我的旧的、可靠的、孤立的、不受支持的软件。我决定，至少在其他软件的进一步测试会引导我改变我的决定之前，旧的方法已经足够好了.

So, after all of these tests, what did I end up doing? I kept on using my old, reliable, orphan, unsupported software, under my old operating system, OS 9. I decided that, at least until further tests of other software would guide me to change my decision, the old way would work well enough.

我上面描述的可以称为“验收测试”，但是当你反过来看时，你会看到原因——从生产者的角度进行测试的原因。您测试您的软件产品是否会销售。“销售”包括您认为用户将“被迫”使用该软件的情况，例如当他们是强制使用该软件的组织的员工时。别开玩笑了。软件用户会找到不使用他们不想使用的软件的方法。因此，即使是内部用户也必须被“出售”——尽管并非所有测试人员都以这种方式考虑他们的工作。

What I've described above could be called "acceptance testing," but when you turn it around, you see the reasons—the reasons for testing from the producer's point of view. You test to see whether your software product will sell. And "selling" includes cases in which you think users will be "forced" to use the software, such as when they are employees of an organization that mandates its use. Don't kid yourself. Software users will find ways of not using software that they don't want to use. So, even internal users have to be "sold"—though not all testers think of their work this way.

决策可能有风险。

Decisions can be risky.

显然，我们完全可以在不进行测试的情况下做出决定。选择彩票号码是一个决定，即使我们有额外的信息（例如测试样本结果）也无济于事。如果可以，那就不是彩票了。但在许多决策中，获得一些额外信息可以提高我们获得满意结果的机会。换句话说，信息可以帮助降低风险。

Obviously, we can make decisions without testing at all. Choosing a lottery number is a decision that can't be helped much by our having additional information (such as test-sample results). If it could, it wouldn't be a lottery. But in many decisions, having some additional information can improve our chances of a satisfactory outcome. Expressed another way, information can help reduce risk.

如果决策涉及正在构建、借用或购买的软件，则测试可能是获取降低风险信息的方法之一。良好的测试涉及平衡降低风险的需求与试图收集过多信息的风险。在开始测试之前，问问自己：我对该产品的风险有什么疑问？测试会帮助回答这些问题吗？

If the decisions concern software that is being built, borrowed, or bought, testing may be one of the ways to obtain that risk-reducing information. Good testing involves balancing the need to mitigate risk against the risk of trying to gather too much information. Before you even begin to test, ask yourself: What questions do I have about this product's risks? Will testing help answer these questions?

如果您对产品的风险没有疑问，那么就没有理由进行测试。如果您至少有一个这样的问题，那么请问：这些测试的执行成本是否会高于其答案的价值？

If you don't have questions about a product's risks, then there's no reason to test. If you have at least one such question, then ask: Will these tests cost more to execute than their answers will be worth?

让我们看看它是如何工作的：大约在我执行最后一次 Web 编写应用程序测试时，我的一位客户询问我对嵌入式心脏监视器起搏器软件的一系列测试的建议。与嵌入式心脏起搏器性能变化相关的风险与 Web 编写应用程序性能变化相关的风险可能看起来很明显，所以你认为我推荐的测试过程与我用来寻找个人网络写作应用程序？你认为我会建议我的客户在现场患者身上安装随机的免费起搏器，直到他找到他喜欢的东西吗？为什么不？

Let's see how this works: About the time I was executing the last of my Web-writing-applications tests, one of my clients asked my advice about a series of tests for the software in an embedded heart-monitor pacemaker. It may seem obvious that the risks associated with variations in performance in an embedded heart monitor pacemaker are vastly different from the risks associated with variations in performance in Web-writing applications, so do you think I recommended the same testing process I used for finding a personal Web-writing application? Do you imagine I recommended that my client install random freeware pacemakers into live patients until he found something he liked? Why not?

您知道使用哪种起搏器软件的决定与使用哪种个人网站编辑器的决定有着截然不同的后果。但这是一个相当极端和明显的对比。一般来说，虽然测试提出的问题的答案应该具有降低风险的潜力，但风险评估是主观的。它必须是，因为它关乎未来，而且据报道，正如 Woody Allen、Niels Bohr 和 Yogi Berra 都曾打趣的那样，我们可以预测除未来之外的任何事物。

You know that the decision about which pacemaker software to use has rather different consequences than the decision about which personal Website editor to use. But that's a rather extreme and obvious contrast. In general, though the answers to questions posed by testing should have the potential of reducing risk, assessment of risk is subjective. It has to be, because it's about the future, and—as Woody Allen, Niels Bohr, and Yogi Berra all reportedly have quipped—we can predict anything except the future.

风险也是主观的，因为相同的风险对不同的人有不同的感觉。有些人会毫不犹豫地从飞机上跳下来，但又非常害怕皮下注射针，以至于他们不会注射流感疫苗。其他人在任何情况下都不会跳出飞机，但他们每年都会毫不犹豫地接种流感疫苗。

Risk is also subjective because the same risk feels different to different people. Some folks wouldn't hesitate to jump out of an airplane, yet fear a hypodermic needle so much that they won't get a flu shot. Others won't jump out of a plane under any circumstances, but they don't think twice about getting a flu shot every year.

以下交流说明了一个人对风险的看法如何影响该人对什么是适当测试的看法。开发经理 Denise 在将开发人员 Ralph 的工作移交给专业测试人员之前，一直难以让开发人员 Ralph 进行有效的单元测试。

The following exchange illustrates how a person's ideas about risk influence that person's ideas about what is proper testing. Denise, a development manager, has been having trouble getting Ralph, a developer, to do effective unit testing before turning his work over to the professional testers.

Denise：“你认为你在单元测试方面做得足够好吗？”

Denise: "Do you think you're doing an adequate job of unit testing?"

拉尔夫：“是的，我很彻底。”

Ralph: "Yes, I'm very thorough."

Denise：“所以你现在的项目准备好交给测试人员了吗？”

Denise: "So your present project is ready to pass to the testing people?"

拉尔夫：“当然。”

Ralph: "Absolutely."

丹妮丝：“好吧，既然你确信它已经过充分测试，我将向你提供以下慷慨的报价：如果在测试期间你的组件中出现的错误少于三个，我会给你加薪。但如果三个或者在测试期间出现更多错误，你今年不会加薪。”

Denise: "Okay, since you're so sure it's adequately tested, I'm going to make you the following generous offer: If fewer than three bugs turn up in your component during testing, I will give you a raise. But if three or more bugs turn up during testing, you won't earn a raise this year."

拉尔夫：“嗯……”

Ralph: "Um . . ."

丹妮丝：“嗯什么？”

Denise: "Um what?"

“我可以把组件拿回来做一些我想做的小测试吗？”

"Could I just have the component back for a few little tests I want to do?"

在这次交流中，Denise 提出了通过单元测试漏掉错误的后果，而 Ralph 关于什么构成适当的单元测试的想法突然改变了。

In this exchange, Denise raises the consequences of errors slipping through unit testing, and Ralph's idea of what constitutes an adequate unit test suddenly changes.

测试可以提供降低风险的信息。

Testing can provide information that reduces risk.

不同的人、不同的项目、不同的时间可能意味着对风险的不同看法，因此测试可能旨在帮助回答不同类型的问题。例如，我们可能会问的一个基本问题是，

Different people, different projects, different times, may mean different perceptions of risks and thus different sorts of questions that testing might be designed to help answer. For example, one basic question we might ask is,

软件能做我们想让它做的事吗？

Does the software do what we want it to do?

任何不值得做的事情都不值得做对，所以如果这个问题的答案是否定的，那么我们就不需要问其他问题了。然而假设，尽管该软件有相当大的缺点，我们想要更多的信息，询问，

Anything not worth doing is not worth doing right, so if the answer to this question is no, then we don't need to ask other questions. Suppose however, that despite the software's considerable shortcomings, we want more information, asking,

如果该软件没有按照我们的要求执行，修复它需要多少工作量？

If the software doesn't do what we want it to do, how much work will be involved in fixing it?

测试本身不能回答这个问题，但它可以提供信息，结合我们开发过程的信息，帮助我们确定要完成的工作并降低估计完成该工作所需的风险。

Testing cannot answer this question by itself, but it can supply information that, combined with information about our development process, helps us identify work to be done and reduce the risks in estimating what it will take to do that work.

软件不做我们不希望它做的事吗？

Does the software not do what we don't want it to do?

在某些方面，这是最容易与风险相关联的问题。软件可能会做的一些不需要的事情可能会对生命、肢体或财产造成损害。不止一个组织被执行了它不希望它做的事情的软件杀死。可悲的是，还有不止一人被杀。

In some ways, this is the question most easily associated with risk. Some of the unwanted things software might do could cause damage to life, limb, or property. More than one organization has been killed by software that did something it didn't want it to do. Sadly, more than one person has been killed, too.

该软件是否按照我们的预期进行？

Does the software do what we intended?

这个问题是关于做正确的那些值得做的事情。如果某件事值得做，那么它就值得做对。回答这个问题可以降低软件未按预期运行的风险。

This question is about doing right those things that are worth doing. If something is worth doing, it's worth doing right. Answering this question reduces the risk that the software is not doing what was intended.

该软件会做我们客户想要的吗？

Will the software do what our customers want?

任何销售产品的人都知道担心客户根本不会购买，或者会购买但不满意。测试无法预测有多少人会购买您的产品，但它可以帮助降低人们不会购买它的风险，因为它没有达到他们愿意支付的价格。

Anyone selling a product knows the fear that customers simply will not buy, or will buy and be unsatisfied. Testing cannot predict how many people will buy your product, but it can help reduce the risk that people won't buy it because it doesn't do what they're willing to pay for.

该软件是否会满足其他业务需求？

Will the software satisfy other business needs?

如果客户不购买您的产品，您的企业就不会成功。但是，即使他们确实购买了，如果技术支持成本超过产品价格，您也可能会在每次销售中赔钱。测试有助于降低意外维修成本和支持的风险。

If customers won't buy your products, your business won't succeed. But even if they do buy, you could lose money on each sale if, for instance, the technical support cost exceeds the price of the product. Testing can help reduce the risk of unanticipated repair costs and support.

失败的可能性和后果是什么？

What are the likelihood and consequences of failure?

由于测试提供了可以降低失败风险的信息，因此我们进行的测试量受失败的可能性和后果的影响，如下表所示：

Since testing provides information that can reduce risk of failure, the amount of testing we do is influenced by both the likelihood and consequences of failure, as suggested by the following table:

失败的可能性低，失败的后果低-->最少的测试

Low Likelihood of Failure, Low Consequences of Failure-->Least Testing

失败的可能性低，失败的后果高-->适度测试

Low Likelihood of Failure, High Consequences of Failure-->Moderate Testing

失败的可能性高，失败的后果低-->适度测试

High Likelihood of Failure, Low Consequences of Failure-->Moderate Testing

失败的可能性很高，失败的后果很严重-->大多数测试

High Likelihood of Failure, High Consequences of Failure-->Most Testing

概括

Summary

测试源于心理学，源于对人脑行为的研究。如果人类是完美的思考者，我们就不需要测试我们的工作。如果我们是没有感情的机器人，我们总是会以理性的方式使用测试，以降低我们决策的风险。如果我们是相同的克隆人，我们都会以相同的方式评估风险。但我们是不完美的、非理性的、价值驱动的、多样化的人。因此，我们测试，我们测试我们的测试。

Testing has its roots in psychology, in the study of the behavior of the human brain. If humans were perfect thinkers, we wouldn't need to test our work. If we were unemotional robots, we would always use testing in a rational way, to reduce risk in our decisions. If we were identical clones, we would all assess risks in the same way. But we are imperfect, irrational, value-driven, diverse human beings. Therefore, we test, and we test our testing.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.追求完美：我们将在第 3 章中看到完美是不可能实现的。尝试做不可能的事会要了你的命。

1. Striving for perfection: We'll see in Chapter 3 that perfection is impossible to achieve. Trying to do the impossible will kill you.

2.不做决定：管理者的工作是做管理决策。不要问测试人员诸如“软件准备好发布了吗？”之类的问题。这是经理的决定。测试人员的工作是提供信息（但不是所有信息）以告知该决定。

2. Not making decisions: A manager's job is to make management decisions. Don't ask testers questions like, "Is the software ready to ship?" That's the manager's decision. The testers' job is to provide information (but not all the information) that informs that decision.

3.没有认识到决策所需的所有信息：在做出决策时没有考虑所有相关信息，您将面临管理层、员工和客户满意度的风险。例如，如果您没有考虑客户的特殊需求而仅仅听取开发人员和测试人员的意见，您就不可能拥有满意的客户——无论您的技术人员认为什么是“正确的”。

3. Not recognizing all the information needed for decision-making: By not taking all relevant information into consideration when making a decision, you're risking management, staff, and customer satisfaction. For example, if you fail to consider your customers' special needs and merely listen to the opinions of developers and testers, you're not likely to have happy customers—regardless of what your technical staff thinks is "right."

4.将各种风险放在错误的优先级上：如果您担心如果不按时发货产品会失去晋升机会，那么您可能会发货一个有缺陷的产品，从而使您的组织损失数百万美元。当然，如果你只关心你的促销，那么只要你不再对产品负责，你就不会关心快速运输的费用何时到期。

4. Putting wrong priorities on various risks: If you're afraid of losing your promotion if you don't ship a product on schedule, you may ship a buggy product that costs your organization millions. Of course, if all you care about is your promotion, then as long as you no longer have responsibility for the product, you won't care when the cost of quick shipping comes due.

5.相信测试可以改进产品：测试收集有关产品的信息；它不会修复它发现的错误。测试不会改进产品；改进是由人们修复测试发现的错误来完成的。通常，当经理们说“测试时间太长”时，他们应该说的是“修复产品中的错误花费的时间太长”——这是一个不同的成本类别。确保您在正确的成本类别下计算工作量和时间。

5. Believing testing can improve a product: Testing gathers information about a product; it does not fix things it finds that are wrong. Testing does not improve a product; the improving is done by people fixing the bugs that testing has uncovered. Often when managers say, "Testing takes too long," what they should be saying is, "Fixing the bugs in the product takes too long"—a different cost category. Make sure you're accounting for effort and time under the correct cost category.

6.相信有一个“测试阶段”，在此期间完成所有测试——并且只进行测试：软件测试专家和作家 James Bach 喜欢问他的客户，他们的过程中是否有测试阶段。詹姆斯报告说，“几乎每个人都说是。然后我建议‘测试阶段’实际上是‘修复阶段’。我怎么知道？因为测试阶段似乎经常在测试完成之前就结束了，但在做出决定的人相信每个真正重要的问题都已得到解决之前，很少会看到产品发货。”

6. Believing there's a "testing phase" during which all testing— and only testing—is done: Software testing expert and author James Bach likes to ask his clients whether they have a testing phase in their process. James reports, "Almost everyone says yes. Then I suggest that the 'testing phase' is really the 'fixing phase.' How do I know? Because the testing phase seems so often to end before testing is completed, yet it is much rarer to see a product ship before the people who make that decision believe that every really important problem has been fixed."

James 然后让他的客户考虑开车：“什么时候是驾驶的'看挡风玻璃阶段'？几乎所有的驾驶都在看挡风玻璃！这不是一个阶段。说'测试时间太长'有点就像说‘安全驾驶需要太长时间’。”

James then asks his clients to consider driving a car: "When is the 'look out the windshield phase' of driving? Pretty much all driving is looking out the windshield! It's not a phase. Saying 'testing takes too long' is a bit like saying 'safe driving takes too long.'"

而且，当然，安全驾驶通常需要更长的时间——如果您不考虑发生事故时会发生什么，因为您没有往窗外看。

And, of course, safe driving often takes longer—if you don't consider what happens when you have an accident because you're not looking out the windows.

Chapter_2_测试不能做什么

Chapter_2_What Testing Cannot Do

 

“不要害怕完美——你永远达不到它。”

"Have no fear of perfection—you'll never reach it."

——萨尔瓦多·达利，西班牙超现实主义画家（1904-1989）

—Salvador Dali, Spanish Surrealistic Painter (1904–1989)

想象一下，您是负责价值数百万美元物流系统的高管。公司总裁贝尼托 (Benito) 是一个充满活力、强势的人，他以在员工会议上解雇那些没有给他想要的答案而闻名。他渴望推出该系统。他在给你压力。你去找向你汇报的项目经理，然后问，

Imagine you are an executive in charge of a multimillion-dollar logistics system. The company president, Benito, is a dynamic, forceful character known for firing people in staff meetings when they don't give him the answers he wants. He is eager to have the system rolled out. He's putting pressure on you. You go to the project manager, who reports to you, and ask,

“系统进展如何？”

"How's progress on the system?"

项目经理回答说：“我不知道。”

The project manager replies, "I don't know."

你现在会做什么？很可能，您想要的信息比“我不知道”要多。有多种获取方式：

What would you do now? Quite likely, you'd want more information than "I don't know." There are various ways to acquire it:

A。也许酷刑会起作用。

a. Maybe torture will work.

一次一个地拔掉项目经理的指甲，直到她尖叫起来，“哦，是的，我知道。这太棒了！” 如有必要，继续处理脚趾甲。

Pull out the project manager's fingernails one at a time until she squeals, "Oh, yes, I do know. It's great!" If necessary, proceed to toenails.

b. 也许宣传马屁精会奏效。

b. Maybe promoting a toady will work.

解雇项目经理并提拔一个说“我知道”的人。根据需要重复此步骤。

Fire the project manager and promote someone who says, "I do know." Repeat this step as needed.

C。也许收集信息会起作用。

c. Maybe gathering information will work.

当有人试图以现实的方式使用它时，寻找一些关于程序实际做什么的信息。

Look for some information on what the program actually does when someone tries to use it in a realistic way.

如果你想要可靠的信息，a和b可能无法胜任，但c至少有机会。收集有关程序在使用时实际做什么的信息是某些人所说的“测试”的一种形式。

If you want reliable information, a and b probably won't do the job, but c at least has a chance. Gathering information on what a program actually does when used is one form of what some people call "testing."

信息不一定有助于降低风险。

Information doesn't necessarily help reduce risk.

软件业务的经理们经常不得不做出冒险的决定，如果基于对以下问题的回答，这些决定的危险性可能会降低：

Managers in the software business frequently have to make risky decisions, which can be made less dangerous if based on answers to questions such as the following:

• 我们现在发货吗？之后？曾经？

• Do we ship now? Later? Ever?

• 我们是否取消该项目？

• Do we cancel the project?

• 我们是否继续该项目并增加更多资源？

• Do we continue the project and add more resources?

• 我们是否缩小项目范围？

• Do we reduce the scope of the project?

• 我们是否试图将产品推向更广阔的市场？

• Do we attempt to bring the product to a wider market?

• 我们是否以较低的价格出售该版本的产品？

• Do we sell this version of the product at a lower price?

当然，这样的决定可以在完全没有信息的情况下做出——而且经常是这样。更常见的是，它们是在决策者获得了一些信息之后做出的，同时坚决忽略可能获得的其他信息。由于测试是一个信息收集过程，因此始终存在是否值得为更多测试付费的问题。那是另一个决定。

Of course, such decisions could be made in the complete absence of information—and they frequently are. More often, they're made after the decision-maker has obtained some bit of information, while resolutely ignoring other information that might be obtained. Since testing is an information-gathering process, there's always a question of whether it's worthwhile to pay for more testing. And that is another decision.

组织中的某个人有权在有或没有信息的情况下做出决定。如果无论出现什么附加信息，该人都会做出相同的决定，那么进行测试以收集更多信息就没有意义了。如果贝尼托决定按原样继续使用新的物流系统，为什么还要麻烦他获取更多信息呢？为什么要费心测试？

Someone in the organization has the authority to make decisions, with or without information. If that person will make the same decision no matter what additional information arises, there is little point in testing to gather more information. If Benito has decided to go forward with the new logistics system as is, why bother getting him more information? Why bother testing?

事实上，有时进行更多测试会增加风险。如果贝尼托在等待对物流系统进行更多测试的同时推迟了产品的发布，他进入市场的时间可能就太晚了。或者，他可能会因为花钱进行测试而破产。所以，在决定是否测试时，我们总是要考虑金钱和时间：

In fact, sometimes doing more testing adds to the risk. If Benito delays the product while waiting for more tests on the logistics system, he might enter the market too late. Or, he might go broke spending money on testing. So, we always have to consider money and time in the decision about whether to test:

测试不能零时间完成，也不能免费完成。

Testing cannot be done in zero time and cannot be done for free.

有时，所产生的信息也会增加风险。如果开发人员知道某些东西运行不正常，他们可能想花时间修复它。从贝尼托的角度来看，这可能会增加破坏某些运行良好的东西的风险。

Sometimes, the information produced also adds to the risk. If the developers have information that something isn't working well, they may want to spend time fixing it. From the point of view of Benito, this could increase the risk of spoiling something that was working well enough to use.

您可能认为真正的风险在于拥有一个您无法控制的开发组织，但这是另一个危险。如果人们因为你开发和销售的软件存在错误而起诉你，他们可以传唤你的开发过程记录。如果记录表明你的测试人员发现了这个错误而你却没有修复它，那么你的麻烦就比他们一开始就没有发现它要大。有时，无知真的是（合法的）幸福。

You might think the real risk is in having a development organization you can't control, but here's another danger. If people sue you because of an error in software you developed and sold, they can subpoena the records of your development process. If the records indicate that your testers found this bug and you didn't fix it, you're in more trouble than if they'd never found it in the first place. Sometimes, ignorance really is (legal) bliss.

即使不涉及诉讼，同样的幸福无知原则也适用于个别经理。如果现场的产品有问题，而经理可以诚实地说，“我不知道”，其影响通常不如经理知道但没有采取任何措施那么严重。寓意：仔细思考哪些信息可能属于过多信息。但是更仔细地考虑一下你的哪个目标是最重要的。您是想生产出成功的产品，还是想避免诉讼，或者只是为了发展您的个人事业？

The same blissful-ignorance principle translates down to the individual manager, even if no lawsuit is involved. If there's a problem with the product in the field and the manager can honestly say, "I didn't know," the repercussions usually are less severe than if that manager knew but didn't do anything about it. The moral: Think carefully about what may qualify as too much information. But think even more carefully about which of your goals are foremost. Are you trying to produce a successful product, or avoid lawsuits, or simply advance your personal career?

我们可能不会使用我们付费购买的信息。

We may not be using the information we're paying for.

“我们应该做更多测试吗？”这个问题从来没有简单的答案。因为信息可以指导降低风险，但不一定如此。因此，当我对一个运行不佳的 Web 编写应用程序进行验收测试时（请参阅第 1 章），我很容易得出结论：“这一定没有经过良好的测试！” 也许，也许不是。也许它经过了很好的测试，但没有人根据这些信息采取行动。测试不是修复。

There's never an easy answer to the question "Should we do more testing?" because information can guide risk reduction, but doesn't necessarily do so. Consequently, when I acceptance-tested a Web-writing application that didn't work well (see Chapter 1), it would have been easy for me to conclude, "This must not have been tested well!" Maybe, or maybe not. Perhaps it was well tested, but no one acted on the information. Testing is not fixing.

这种观察会引出一个问题，即您是否收到了您付钱给测试人员以生成的信息。有时，当测试人员没有生成大量文件时，很容易决定您的钱花得不值。您成为将信息质量与数据量（错误数、测试报告页数、运行的测试用例数等）等同起来的牺牲品。

This observation leads to the question of whether you are receiving the information you're paying testers to produce. Sometimes, when testers don't generate reams of paper, it's easy to decide you're not getting your money's worth. You fall victim to equating information quality with data quantity (bug counts, pages of test reports, number of test cases run, and so on).

当心。这可能是缺少信息导致最重要信息的情况之一。为了从测试中获得您的金钱价值，您将不得不继续质疑和解释超出测试报告中明确说明的情况的过程。

Be careful. This may be one of those situations in which an absence of information leads to the most important information. To obtain your money's worth from testing, you will have to continue the process of questioning and interpreting what's going on beyond what's stated explicitly in test reports.

也许测试人员并没有发现大量的错误，因为尽管他们已经花费了六个星期的加班时间，但他们仍然无法安装该软件。如果是这样，测试人员确实发现了关键信息。如果他们无法安装您的应用程序，您凭什么认为用户可以安装？

Perhaps the testers are not uncovering vast quantities of bugs because they cannot install the software despite having spent six weeks of overtime in the attempt. If this is the case, the testers have uncovered critical information indeed. If they cannot install your application, what makes you think a user could do so?

或者，也许测试人员不了解该软件。如果他们对软件的预期功能只有一个模糊的概念，那么您最终可能得不到有关该软件的有用信息。但是，您对组织中的信息流有所了解。如果测试人员在理解软件方面有困难，也许一两个开发人员也有类似的问题，并且编写了无法运行的代码。

Or, perhaps the testers do not understand the software. If they have only a vague idea of what it is expected to do, you may end up with little useful information about the software. You do, however, know something about information flow in the organization. If the testers have trouble understanding the software, perhaps one or two of the developers had similar trouble and wrote code that doesn't work.

另一种可能性是测试人员不知道如何测试，或者不擅长测试，或者根本不在乎。

Another possibility is that the testers don't know how to test, or aren't very good at it, or don't really care.

如果您不追寻隐藏在表面之下的问题，您通常不会从测试投资中获得金钱的价值。我听到的关于测试的抱怨中有一半来自未能追查测试结果中所有信息的经理。如果您不打算使用生成的信息，请不要为测试付费。

If you don't pursue the questions beneath the surface, you generally won't obtain your money's worth out of your investment in testing. Half of the complaints I hear about testing come from managers who fail to pursue all of the information in their test results. If you're not going to use the information generated, don't pay for tests.

我们的决定是感性的，而不是理性的。

Our decisions are emotional, not rational.

因为测试提供的信息可以帮助您降低决策风险，所以您可能认为每个人都会喜欢并重视测试。但是人们有很多心理原因做出与合理使用信息无关的决定。我们都听过这样的表达：“我已经下定决心了；不要把我和事实混淆了。” 我们中的一些人甚至自己也说过。

Because testing provides information that can help you take the risk out of decisions, you might think that everyone would love and value testing. But people have many psychological reasons for making decisions that have nothing to do with rational use of information. We've all heard the expression, "My mind is made up; don't confuse me with the facts." Some of us have even said it ourselves.

人们在不发现自己犯了错误的过程中投入了情感。一些经理不想知道他们的项目正在滑向失败的斜坡。一些开发人员不希望人们知道他们的代码有错误。

People have an emotional investment in not finding out that they've made mistakes. Some managers don't want to know that their project is headed down the slippery slope to failure. Some developers don't want people to know that their code is buggy.

每当你试图影响这些情绪化的因素时，这些干预措施很容易适得其反。

Whenever you attempt to influence such emotion-laden factors, the interventions can easily backfire.

例如，假设您为错误数量较少的开发人员制定了奖励计划，希望激励他们编写更好的代码。这种奖励计划可能会适得其反，因为它比以前支付的费用更多地关注已发现的错误。这种关注满足了开发人员希望人们不知道他们的错误的愿望，这可能会导致不同的开发人员走向不同的方向。

For example, suppose you establish a bonus scheme for developers who have low bug counts, hoping to motivate them to produce better code. This reward scheme can backfire because it calls even more attention to found bugs than may have been previously paid. This attention feeds into the developers' desire to have people not know about their bugs, which could lead different developers in different directions.

一位开发人员可能会按照您的意愿做出回应，并将奖励视为更仔细地工作和仔细测试的激励。然而，另一方面，同样的奖励计划可以作为一种激励措施，使产品难以测试，理由是，“如果他们找不到它，我就不会花掉我的奖金。” 或者，假设你想激励你的经理按时发货，所以你会显着提拔每个产品按时发货的经理。一切都按计划进行，直到出现以下情况：您的一位经理有一个项目，其中测试人员报告了许多问题。因为按时发货的经理得到了提升，这位经理认为，我想要促销，所以我需要按时发货，但那些错误报告妨碍了我。我知道我会做什么！我会把测试人员放在另一个项目上，直到开发人员有机会赶上来。

One developer might respond as you intended, and will view reward as an incentive to work more carefully and to test meticulously. For another, however, the same reward scheme could serve as an incentive to make the product difficult to test, the rationale being, "If they can't find it, it won't cost me my bonus." Or, suppose you want to motivate your managers to ship products on time, so you conspicuously promote each manager whose product goes out the door on schedule. All goes as planned until the situation arises in which one of your managers has a project where the testers are reporting numerous problems. Because managers who have shipped products on time have been promoted, this manager thinks, I want that promotion so I need to ship this on time, but those bug reports are getting in the way. I know what I'll do! I'll put the testers on another project until the developers have a chance to catch up.

（经理注意：在这种情况下，开发人员永远不会赶上来。）

(Note to manager: In such situations, developers never catch up.)

糟糕的测试可能比根本没有测试更糟糕。

Poor testing may be worse than no testing at all.

构思不当的测试或执行不当的测试——为了本书的目的，我将这两个类别归为一类，称为“糟糕的测试”或“糟糕的测试”——可能会给你一种产品比实际更好的印象，导致你在准备好之前发货。或者，糟糕的测试可能会给您一种产品比实际情况更糟糕的印象，从而导致您推迟发货并失去潜在的利益。

Poorly conceived tests or poorly executed tests—for purposes of this book, I lump these two categories into one, called "poor tests" or "bad tests"—may give you the impression that a product is better than it is, causing you to ship before it's ready. Or, poor tests may give you the impression that a product is worse than it actually is, causing you to defer shipping and lose potential benefits.

您如何识别糟糕的测试？没有做好的原因有很多种，事实上，我在整本书中介绍了糟糕的测试以及如何识别它们。同时，如果您怀疑自己的测试效果不佳，请考虑根本不进行测试。

How can you recognize poor tests? There are numerous flavors of not doing it well, so many, in fact, that I cover poor tests and how to recognize them throughout this book. In the meantime, if you suspect that you're going to test poorly, consider not testing at all.

您的产品可能尚未准备好进行测试。

Your product may not be ready for testing.

您的产品何时准备好进行测试？这个问题并不总是容易回答，但您可以提出更容易回答的问题来提取信息，这些信息会在您还没有准备好接受测试时告诉您：

At what point is your product ready for test? That question is not always easy to answer, but you can ask more-easily-answered questions to draw out information that will tell you when you're not ready for test:

• 是否至少有一个关于您的产品的问题测试可以帮助您回答？如果没有问题，那么就没有理由进行测试。

• Is there at least one question about your product that testing can help you answer? If there's no question, then there's no reason to test.

•你想知道那个问题的答案吗？如果你不想知道答案，就不要问问题——也就是说，不要费心去测试。

• Do you want to know the answer to that question? If you don't want to know the answer, don't ask the question— that is, don't bother testing.

•您是否只是懒惰地对测试结果感到好奇？如果您不打算评估问题的答案或根据问题的答案采取行动，请忘记测试。它太贵了，不能仅仅用来满足无聊的好奇心。另一方面，积极的好奇心是有效测试的一个重要属性，因为你永远不会确切地知道你应该寻找什么。因此，如果您准备好花一些时间探索，保持好奇心将帮助您从测试中获得金钱的价值——前提是您坚持自己的发现。

• Are you merely idly curious about the results of testing? If you're not going to evaluate or act on the answers to your questions, forget testing. It's too expensive to be used just to satisfy idle curiosity. Active curiosity, on the other hand, is an important attribute of effective testing, because you'll never know exactly what you should be looking for. So, if you are ready to spend some time exploring, being curious will help you get your money's worth out of testing—if you follow through on what you discover.

• 你能否事先与测试人员就什么是通过测试达成一致？如果您不同意什么是通过测试，什么不是，那么您从测试中寻找什么？

• Can you agree with testers in advance as to what constitutes a passed test? If you don't agree about what is a passed test and what isn't, what are you looking for from your tests?

•您是否事先就成功测试的模样达成一致？考试不成功？您是否同意任何为您提供新信息的测试至少是部分成功的？

• Do you have agreement in advance on what a successful test would look like? An unsuccessful test? Do you agree that any test that gives you new information is at least partially successful?

•您认为测试结果会为您做出决定吗？不能从纯粹的技术角度做出业务决策。当然可以使用来自测试的信息来影响您的业务决策，但不要用测试代替业务决策。例如，发布未通过一项或多项测试的系统可能是一个很好的业务决策。相反，发布一个通过所有测试的系统可能是一个糟糕的商业决策。除了测试结果，管理层还必须考虑其他因素。

• Do you think the outcome of testing will make your decisions for you? Business decisions cannot be made from a purely technical perspective. Certainly use information from testing to color your business decisions, but don't substitute testing for business decisions. For example, it can be a good business decision to ship a system that fails one or more tests. Conversely, it can be a bad business decision to ship a system that passes all your tests. Management has to consider other factors in addition to test results.

•相反，是否有任何可能的测试结果会让您改变决定？如果不是，你为什么要知道结果，更不用说为此付出代价了？

• Conversely, is there any possible test outcome that would make you change your decisions? If not, why would you want to know the outcome, let alone pay for it?

概括

Summary

您不必测试是否出于任何原因不打算使用结果信息。而且，如果信息不相关或不可靠，您最好不要使用它，所以一开始就不要费心购买。

You don't have to test if, for any reason, you're not going to use the resulting information. And, if the information isn't going to be relevant or reliable, you'd better not use it, so don't bother to buy it in the first place.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.不尊重测试人员：如果你不相信测试人员发现的东西，要么你找错人了，要么你需要认真帮助他们建立信誉。测试绝不仅仅是雇佣和希望的问题。

1. Not honoring testers: If you aren't going to believe what the testers uncover, either you have the wrong people or you need to get serious about helping them build their credibility. Testing is never just a matter of hiring and hoping.

2.过度尊重测试人员：如果让他们替你做决定，那你就应该下台，让他们拿经理的薪水。

2. Over-honoring testers: If you let them make your decision for you, then you should step down and let them earn the manager's salary.

3.给测试人员找替罪羊：比过度尊重测试人员更糟糕的是假装尊重他们——操纵他们给你你想要的答案，表现出对“独立”评估采取行动，然后如果评估证明是有害的，则稍后指责他们错了（如果事实证明是正确的，则归功于此）。

3. Scapegoating testers: Even worse than over-honoring testers is pretending to honor them—manipulating them to give you the answers you want, appearing to act on that "independent" assessment, then blaming them later if that assessment turns out to be damagingly wrong (or taking credit if it turns out to be right).

4.不使用从测试或其他来源收集的信息：如果你打算忽略信息或不顾测试的结果继续执行预定的计划，请不要费心测试。（实际上，如果您不使用它，则不能真正将其视为信息。）

4. Not using the information gleaned from testing or other sources: If you're going to ignore information or go ahead with predetermined plans despite what the tests turn up, don't bother testing. (Actually, it can't really be considered information if you don't use it.)

5.情绪化而不是理性地做决定：并不是说你可以完全理性，但你至少可以在做决定时尽量保持冷静并控制自己的情绪。

5. Making decisions that are emotional, not rational: Not that you can be perfectly rational, but you can at least try to be calm and in control of your emotions when you make decisions.

6.不评估测试数据的质量：数字只是数字。学会问，“获得这个数字的过程是什么？” “这个数字是什么意思？” [2]

6. Not evaluating the quality of test data: Numbers are just numbers. Learn to ask, "What was the process used to obtain this number?" "What does this number mean?" [2]

7.没有充分准备的测试：所谓“充分准备”，我的意思是当问题出现时，你必须准备好识别问题，这可能包括对被测应用程序的目的和性质有基本的了解。我并不是说在开始运行该测试之前，您需要为每个测试确定一个完整且明确的预期结果。要做好充分准备，您还必须做好个人准备：准备学习、准备设计、准备有效执行。

7. Testing without adequate preparation: By "adequate preparation," I mean that you must be prepared to recognize problems when they turn up, which may encompass as little as developing a basic understanding of the purpose and nature of the application under test. I don't mean that you will need to have identified a complete and unambiguous expected result for every test before you begin running that test. To be adequately prepared, you must also be personally prepared: prepared to learn, prepared to design, prepared to perform effectively.

8.未能协调测试与项目的其余部分：如果你不打算给你的开发人员所需的时间或资源来解决测试中发现的问题，测试将是一种浪费，所以跳过它。测试是一种技术开发支持活动，必须与需求、设计、编程、文档编制、制造和支持过程相协调。为了协调测试与项目周期的其余部分，顾问兼测试专家 James Bach 问了自己三个问题：我现在可以做些什么来为这个项目提供最多的服务？我现在需要做什么才能为明天或下个月的项目服务做好准备？现在可能需要停止哪些测试活动，因为我们已经达到“足够好”

8. Failing to coordinate testing with the rest of a project: If you're not going to give your developers needed time or resources to fix problems found in testing, testing will be a wasted effort, so just skip it. Testing is a technology-development-support activity that must be coordinated with the requirements, design, programming, documenting, manufacturing, and support processes. To coordinate testing with the rest of the project's cycles, consultant and testing expert James Bach asks himself three questions: What can I do right now to be most of service on this project? What do I need to do now to get ready to be of service on the project tomorrow or next month? What test activity might need to be cut off now because we've reached 'good enough' and need those cycles for something new?

9.催促测试人员：测试通常是一项微妙的工作。推动测试人员更快地进行测试通常会产生危险的误导性结果——尤其是当测试人员感到害怕、疲倦或愤世嫉俗时。

9. Rushing the testers: Testing is often a subtle business. Pushing testers to test faster generally produces dangerously misleading results—especially when testers are frightened, tired, or cynical.

10.不坚持经理的尽职调查：如果你允许经理以不了解测试过程为借口让错误通过，你还不如不测试。谨防测试人员声称“不可能知道我们是否已经找到所有错误”来为真正被称为疏忽的事情找借口。管理人员需要对测试有足够的了解，以识别疏忽和无意犯错之间的区别。如果他们做不到，他们需要培养他们可以信任的测试经理和领导来为他们执行评估。

10. Not insisting on due diligence from managers: If you allow managers to plead ignorance of the test process as an excuse for allowing bugs to pass, you might as well not test. Beware of testers claiming "it's impossible to know if we've found all the bugs" to excuse what could truly be called negligence. Managers need to understand enough about testing to recognize the difference between negligence and an honest mistake. If they cannot, they need to develop test managers and leads whom they can trust to perform that evaluation for them.

11.假设别人的决定不合理只是因为他们不同意你的决定：根据不同的价值观，许多看似不合理的决定是合理的。记住这个原则可以避免经理、测试人员和开发人员之间的大量冲突。

11. Assuming that others' decisions are not rational just because they don't agree with yours: Many decisions that seem irrational are rational according to a different set of values. Remembering this principle can save an enormous amount of conflict among managers, testers, and developers.

12.没有意识到测试信息的用途不止一种：在许多情况下，项目成员可能希望在交付产品后继续测试，以收集对客户服务和支持人员有用的信息。

12. Not realizing there is more than one use for information from testing: In many cases, project members might want to continue testing after delivering a product in order to collect information that will be useful to customer service and support staffs.

Chapter_ 3_为什么不测试所有的东西？

Chapter_3_Why Not Just Test Everything?

 

“测试可以令人信服地证明错误的存在，但永远无法证明它们不存在。”- Edsger W. Dijkstra，计算先驱（1930-2002），“编程作为一门数学性质的学科”，Am。数学。月刊，81 (1974)，第 6 期，第 608-12 页。

"Testing may convincingly demonstrate the presence of bugs, but can never demonstrate their absence."- Edsger W. Dijkstra, Computing Pioneer (1930–2002), "Programming as a discipline of mathematical nature," Am. Math. Monthly, 81 (1974), No. 6, pp. 608–12.

我最近被一位测试经理叫来咨询，他的经理要求他“测试一切”。这不是我第一次听到这种不可能的要求。

I was called in to consult recently by a test manager whose manager had demanded that he "test everything." It was not the first time I'd heard this impossible demand.

为什么不可能？首先，人脑不仅会犯错误，其容量也是有限的。第二，没有人永远长生不老。因此，尽管我们很想执行所有可能的测试，但我们无法想到它们，而且即使我们可以，我们也没有足够长的时间来完成所有这些测试。此外，在大多数情况下，它的成本太高了——因为任何给定程序的可能测试次数都是无限的。让我们看看为什么。

Why is it impossible? First of all, the human brain not only makes mistakes, its capacity is finite. Second, nobody lives forever. So, as much as we would like to perform all possible tests, we can't think of them, and, even if we could, we wouldn't live long enough to do them all. Besides, for most situations, it would cost too much—since the number of possible tests for any given program is infinite. Let's see why.

有无数种可能的测试。

There are an infinite number of possible tests.

让我们想想我们能想到的最简单的测试程序：一个程序，它的功能是通过输入“Hello Dolly!”来响应空格键的敲击。屏幕上的消息。我们要测试什么？为了简单起见，我们想要测试每次按下空格键时，我们都会得到“Hello Dolly!”。消息，每次我们按下任何其他键或键组合时，屏幕上都没有显示任何内容。

Let's think of the simplest program we could conceive of to test: a program whose function will be to respond to tapping on the space bar by putting a "Hello Dolly!" message on the screen. What would we test for? To keep it simple, we'd want to test that every time we pressed the space bar, we got the "Hello Dolly!" message, and every time we pressed any other key or combination of keys, we never got anything on the screen.

如果您看不到程序内部，您需要执行多少个测试用例才能打赌您已经测试了所有可能性？确定测试用例的数量，记下该数量，然后阅读下一段以查看您是否做对了。

If you can't see inside the program, how many test cases would you need to execute in order to bet your life that you've tested all possibilities? Identify the number of test cases, write that number down, and then read the next paragraphs to see if you got it right.

由于您看不到程序内部，因此您不知道程序员可能设置了哪些奇怪的条件。例如，程序可能被设计成在外部看起来一切正常，除非用户键入了一个极不可能的击键序列。假设我设置程序，如果你按 W 键，然后按空格键 3 次，然后按 M 键，然后按空格键再按 3 次，然后按 J 键，然后再敲 168 次一次不使用字母 L，程序将在屏幕上显示一条消息，询问“Whaaa?” 您详尽的测试用例集是否会检测到这种奇怪的情况，在这种情况下，程序中隐藏了不需要的和意外的 Whaaa 响应？

Since you can't see inside the program, you have no idea what bizarre conditions the programmer might have set up. For example, the program might be designed so that everything looks normal on the outside unless the user types an extremely unlikely sequence of keystrokes. Suppose I set up the program so that if you hit, say, the W key, then the space bar three times, then the M key, then the space bar another three times, then the J key, then you type exactly 168 more keystrokes without once using the letter L, the program will put a message on the screen asking, "Whaaa?" Would your exhaustive set of test cases have detected this outlandish condition in which an unwanted and unexpected Whaaa response is hidden in the program?

你认为这些条件很奇怪吗？不切实际？在对一个据称高度安全的应用程序进行技术审查时，我们发现一个名叫 Wanda Marilyn Jones（不是她的真名，而是她的真实名字首字母）的程序员在软件中放置了这个后门，编写了密码保护，这样她就可以绕过普通的密码保护，不管真正的密码是什么，让她随时可以闯入。在严格控制下执行的高度复杂的测试计划没有发现这个隐藏了三年的后门，直到我们进行技术审查。用 Edsger Dijkstra 的话说，“测试可以揭示错误的存在，而不是它们的不存在。”

Do you think these conditions are outlandish? Unrealistic? During a technical review of a supposedly highly secure application, we discovered that a programmer named Wanda Marilyn Jones (not her real name, but her real initials) had placed exactly this backdoor into the software, writing the password protection so that she could bypass the ordinary password protection, regardless of what the real password was set to be, thereby enabling her to break in at any time. A highly sophisticated test plan, executed under strict controls, had not found this backdoor, which lay hidden for three years until we performed a technical review. To paraphrase Edsger Dijkstra, "Testing can reveal the presence of bugs, not their absence."

你现在明白了吗？如果您没有猜到彻底测试软件所需的测试次数是无限的，或者至少是“比我有生之年所能运行的次数还要多”，那么您就没有理解本章的重点。你现在做。

Do you get the point by now? If you didn't guess that the number of tests required to exhaustively test software is infinite, or at least "a number greater than I could run in my lifetime," you didn't understand the point of this chapter. Now you do.

请注意，我什至没有提到在不同配置下测试此程序的可能性，这是产品开发人员经常面临的问题。如果一个程序必须在十个不同的 CPU 上运行，每个 CPU 有十种可能的内存大小和十种不同的磁盘驱动器大小，这意味着需要测试 10 次 10 次 10 次不同的配置。

Notice that I didn't even mention the possibility of testing this program on different configurations, a problem commonly faced by product developers. If a program has to work on ten different CPUs, each with ten possible memory sizes and ten different disk-drive sizes, that would mean 10 times 10 times 10 different configurations that would have to be tested.

但这对于许多实际测试情况来说太简单了，在这种情况下，测试人员必须处理不同制造商、驱动程序、操作系统版本、同时运行的其他程序以及其他不同外围设备的组合所固有的复杂性，其中任何一个都可能包含错误。像这样“完全”处理所有可能的配置将需要千万亿个不同的测试用例。而且这还没有考虑对程序应该使用这些配置中的任何一个执行的所有不同功能的测试。

But that's way too simple for many real testing situations, where the tester has to deal with the added complexity inherent in having different manufacturers, drivers, operating system versions, other programs simultaneously operating, and combinations of other different peripheral devices, any of which could contain errors. Dealing "completely" with all possible configurations like this would necessitate quadrillions of different test cases. And that's not considering tests for all the different functions that program is supposed to perform with any of these configurations.

即使是这个巨大的数字也忽略了反映测试执行顺序的序列效应。如果用户可能调用十个函数，那么使用十个不同的测试是不够的，因为如果以不同的顺序执行它们可能会产生不同的结果。因此，我们需要十个阶乘（10！）测试（超过六百万）测试来覆盖所有序列，而不是十个测试。

Even this immense number ignores sequence effects reflective of the order in which the tests are performed. If there are ten functions a user might invoke, it isn't enough to use ten different tests because they might produce different results if performed in different orders. So, instead of ten tests, we'd need ten factorial (10!) tests (over six million) tests to cover all sequences.

但这也不够，因为如果程序有内存（所有真实程序都有），那么我们第二次执行测试序列时，它可能不会产生与第一次相同的结果。

But that wouldn't be enough, either, because if the program has memory (and all real programs do), then the second time we perform a test sequence, it may not produce the same results as it did the first time.

这些巨大的数字（全部相乘）也忽略了真正的随机性，例如外部设备导致中断的精确纳秒或您敲击 J 键时精确到微秒的时间。总而言之，测试可能会让人筋疲力尽，但它永远不会面面俱到。

And these immense numbers (all multiplied together) also ignore true randomness, like the exact nanosecond an external device causes an interrupt or the exact timing to the microsecond of when you strike, say, the J key. All in all, testing can be exhausting, but it can never be exhaustive.

测试充其量只是抽样。

Testing is, at best, sampling.

由于我们无法测试所有内容，因此任何一组真实测试都是某种样本——以某种方式代表一整套可能测试的部分、片段或片段。我们当然希望它是一个好的代表，但这会带来一个问题，“对谁有好处？” 从根本上说，采样是另一种心理过程——也是一种情感过程。使一个人满意的样品可能不会让另一个人满意。

Since we can't test everything, any set of real tests is some kind of sample—a portion, piece, or segment that is in some way representative of a whole set of possible tests. We, of course, hope it's a good representative, but that brings up the question, "Good for whom?" Fundamentally, sampling is yet another psychological process—and an emotional one. A sample that satisfies one person may not satisfy another in the slightest.

那么我们如何决定采样什么？我们怎么知道我们正在采取足够大的样本来充分代表一切？我们怎么知道我们采集了合适的样本？

So how do we decide what to sample? How do we know we're taking a large enough sample to adequately represent everything? How do we know we've taken an appropriate sample?

在新墨西哥州佩科斯峡谷的一场暴雨中，我和我的同事伊丽莎白·亨德里克森 (Elisabeth Hendrickson) 一起看着我的雨量计，正在思考这个问题。安装在我家门廊外部的量表有一个小开口，它应该通过这个开口采样雨水——当时，雨水由每隔几秒钟溅落在地面上的大而宽的水滴组成。对于西雅图来说，它本来是一个足够的雨量计，因为它会在持续数小时的细雨中表现良好，但是当佩科斯风暴在十分钟后停止时，我的雨量计底部完全干燥，掩盖了事实下雨了。

I was musing about this problem with my colleague Elisabeth Hendrickson as we watched my rain gauge during a rainstorm in Pecos Canyon, New Mexico. The gauge, which is attached to the exterior of my porch, had a small opening through which it was supposed to sample rain—which, at the time, consisted of large, widely spaced drops splattering on the ground every few seconds. It would have been an adequate rain gauge for Seattle, because it would have done well with a fine, misty rain that fell for hours, but when the Pecos storm stopped after ten minutes, the bottom of my gauge was completely dry, belying the fact that any rain had fallen.

但伊丽莎白和我看到雨下了，事实上，我们都湿透了。我们很快意识到，在处理暴风雨持续的几分钟内相距几英寸的巨大水滴时，仪表采集的样本不足。伊丽莎白看着我滴着水的胡须说：“你的雨量计比门廊上的好。”

But Elisabeth and I had seen the rain fall and, in fact, we were soaked. We quickly realized that the gauge was taking an inadequate sample when dealing with such huge drops falling several inches apart over the minutes the storm lasted. Elisabeth looked at my dripping beard and said, "You are a better rain gauge than the one on the porch."

请注意，它可以以其他方式工作。如果这些大雨滴中只有一两滴碰巧落入它的小开口，则该仪表可能会报告整整四分之一英寸的降雨量，这也不准确。我们经常在测试中看到同样的现象：我们取了一个小样本——在这里和那里尝试一些事情——最终低估或高估了整个产品中问题的密度。

Notice that it could have worked the other way. If just one or two of those huge drops had happened to fall into its small opening, the gauge might have reported a full quarter-inch of rain, which wasn't accurate either. We regularly see this same phenomenon in testing: We take a small sample—try a few things here and there—and end up under- or over-reporting the density of problems in the whole product.

信息的成本可能超过无知的成本。

The cost of information can exceed the cost of ignorance.

不可能进行详尽的测试将我们挤在两个困难但同时又令人向往的目标之间：

The impossibility of exhaustive testing squeezes us between two difficult and simultaneously desirable objectives:

1. 我们想要涵盖所有有趣的条件。

1. We want to cover all interesting conditions.

2. 我们希望将测试集减少到可管理、负担得起的水平。

2. We want to reduce the set of tests to a manageable, affordable level.

要理解我所说的第一个意思，请考虑测试人员在没有寻找特定类型的错误时偶然发现关键错误的次数。他们找到它是因为他们很幸运（或者不幸，如果他们不想知道的话），而不是因为他们正在执行一组旨在发现特定问题的精心设计的测试。错误刚刚出现，就像葡萄干麸皮中的一只蚂蚁。但这是纯粹的运气吗？是否有某种心理学可以弄清楚如何找到更多这些令人惊讶的错误？我相信部分答案在于扩展我们的测试理念。

To understand what I mean by the first, consider the number of times testers stumble across a critical bug when they aren't looking for that particular type of bug. They find it because they are lucky (or unlucky, if they don't want to know about it), not because they were executing a set of meticulously designed tests intended to find that specific problem. The bug just appears, like an ant in your raisin bran. But is it pure luck? Is there some psychology to figuring out how to find more of these surprise bugs? I believe that part of the answer lies in expanding our idea of testing.

我们可以通过更少的测试获得更多的信息——也许吧。

We can obtain more information with less testing— perhaps.

这些天来，与我交谈的许多人都关心上述第二个目标——将测试集减少到可管理、负担得起的水平。他们被要求或命令在更小的团队和更大的责任下生存，甚至茁壮成长。

These days, many of the people I talk with are concerned with the second objective stated above—reducing the set of tests to a manageable, affordable level. They're asked, or commanded, to subsist and even thrive with smaller teams and greater responsibilities.

在我所描述的一个更极端的案例中，一位测试人员就处理以下困境寻求顾问的建议：“我们刚刚从 30 名测试人员团队缩减为 3 人，但我们仍然应该‘确保’产品。我如何决定要测试什么？”

In one of the more extreme cases described to me, a tester sought a consultant's advice on handling the following dilemma: "We were just downsized from a team of thirty testers to three, but we're still supposed to 'ensure' the product. How do I decide what to test?"

一种说法是测试人员根本无法“确保”任何事情，因此他们甚至不应该尝试。但这种论点无法说服在经济不景气时期努力维持公司运转的高管人员。那么该怎么办？诚然，缩小规模的团队无法完成大型员工过去所做的所有事情，但它可以从可能执行的测试中进行挑选。它可以识别最充分利用有限资源的测试。

One argument would say that testers can't "ensure" anything at all so they shouldn't even try. But that argument won't persuade an executive staff struggling to keep a firm afloat during rough economic times. So what to do? Admittedly, a downsized team can't do everything the larger staff used to do, but it can pick and choose from among the tests it could possibly perform. It can identify the tests that make the best use of limited resources.

这位顾问的建议是有根据的：“首先，要认识到任何一组测试都是一种抽样策略，然后，无论你的资源有多少，都尽可能选择最具代表性的一组测试。”

The consultant's advice was grounding: "First of all, recognize that any set of tests is a sampling strategy and then, no matter how many or how few your resources, choose the best representative set of tests you can."

想象一下，您即将在 Testing Buffet 用餐。

Imagine you are about to dine at the Testing Buffet.

你站在一张满是用例、边界条件、兼容性测试、交互测试、权限矩阵等的长桌前，拿着一个盘子。测试自助餐只允许用餐者排队几次，所以您知道最好明智地选择。你该怎么办？

You stand at the head of a long table full of use cases, boundary conditions, compatibility tests, interaction tests, permissions matrices, and so on, holding a single plate. The Testing Buffet allows a diner only a couple of trips through the line, so you know that you'd better choose wisely. What should you do?

好吧，如果你曾在自助餐中看到人们面临这种情况，你就会知道不同的性格以不同的方式解决问题。有些人会向领班或服务员抱怨盘子的大小，并在整个用餐过程中继续抱怨，破坏其他人的用餐。其他人只会转身气呼呼地走开，因为他们认为不应该限制自己的进食量。

Well, if you have ever watched people faced with this situation in a food buffet, you know that different personalities attack problems in different ways. Some people will complain to the maitre d' or waiter about the size of the plates and continue whining throughout the meal, spoiling everybody else's meal. Others will simply turn around and walk away in a huff because they believe they shouldn't be limited in the amount they may eat.

有些人会排在队伍的最前面，用最吸引他们的前两道菜装满盘子。这是明智的吗？也许在餐厅，但在资源有限的情况下可能不会。

Some people will start at the head of the line and fill the plate with the first two dishes that appeal to them. Is this wise? Maybe at a restaurant, but probably not when testing with limited resources.

当面对一组无法克服的测试任务时（实际上，测试中总是如此），您可能很想从头开始，看看测试在分配的时间内进行了多远。或者，您可以在整个功能集中挑选简单、快速的测试。这两种方法对测试人员来说都很方便，但是它们是否提供了足够的测试餐？

When faced with an insurmountable set of testing tasks (which is, really, always the case in testing), you may be tempted to begin at the beginning and see how far the testing progresses in the allotted time. Alternatively, you might pick and choose easy, quick tests across the entire feature set. Both approaches are convenient for the tester, but do they provide an adequate meal of testing?

要进行良好的测试，测试人员必须了解有限测试、资源和时间的限制。测试人员还必须了解自己的个性——他们攻击自助餐的方式。

To test well, testers must be aware of the constraints of finite tests, resources, and time. Testers must also be aware of their own personalities—the way they tend to attack the buffet.

管理人员还必须了解这些限制和趋势。无论您多么喜欢奢侈，都不能指望测试人员执行“详尽”的测试。你必须让自己适应以其他方式满足你对控制的渴望。

Managers also must be aware of these constraints and tendencies. No matter how much you'd love the luxury, you can't expect testers to perform "exhaustive" tests. You'll have to reconcile yourself to satisfying your appetite for control in some other way.

概括

Summary

可以对特定的候选产品执行基本上无限数量的测试。管理人员和测试人员必须努力了解通过抽样添加到测试过程中的风险，而不是要求执行“所有”测试。

There are an essentially infinite number of tests that can be performed on a particular product candidate. Rather than asking for "all" tests to be performed, managers and testers must strive to understand the risks added to the testing process by sampling.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.要求“测试一切”：当你要求不可能的事情时，你不知道你会得到什么——除了它不会是不可能的。

1. Demanding "test everything": When you demand the impossible, you have no idea what you'll get—except that it won't be anything impossible.

2.不了解抽样：很少有管理者（实际上很少有人）非常了解抽样。要么自学，要么聘请专家来审核您的抽样。在任何一种情况下，都要随时准备好可能出现的抽样错误。

2. Not understanding sampling: Very few managers (very few people, in fact) understand sampling very well. Either educate yourself or hire an expert to audit your sampling. In either case, always be ready for the possibility of a sampling error.

3.为不值得的信息花费太多：你的地下室或车库里是否堆满了你从未真正想要的昂贵小玩意？您是否意识到您可以用所花的钱（或​​占用的空间）做些什么？如果是这样，您就理解了这个错误。小心你的要求。

3. Spending too much for information that's not worth it: Do you have a basement or garage full of expensive gadgets that you never really wanted? Do you realize what else you could have done with the money spent (or the space occupied)? If so, you understand this error. Be careful what you ask for.

4.为了外观而测试：一些客户和认证机构要求“测试”。如果你觉得有必要，你可以通过这些动作，但至少不要在你收到的信息的质量上欺骗自己。

4. Testing for the sake of appearance: Some customers and certifying agencies demand "testing." You can go through the motions if you feel you must, but at least don't deceive yourself about the quality of the information you receive.

5.不使用所有的信息来源：从测试结果中收集的信息，就其本质而言是有限的，但是如果你足够警觉可以看到其他类型的信息。

5. Not using all sources of information: Information gathered from test results is, by its very nature, limited, but there are other kinds of information sitting around if you're alert enough to see it.

6.认为机器可以进行详尽的测试，即使人做不到：不仅仅是人脑受限；测试工具也很有限。不要购买任何声称可以“执行所有测试”的产品。即使可以，您也不可能查看所有结果。

6. Thinking that machines can perform exhaustive testing, even if people can't: It's not just the human brain that's limited; testing tools are limited, too. Don't buy any product that claims it can "perform all tests." Even if it could, you couldn't possibly look at all the results.

7.通过限制资源增加风险：当测试资源被削减时，最简单的应对方法是限制样本量——运行更少的测试。但随着样本量的减少，抽样错误的可能性更大。一个多样化的样本可能比一个大样本发现更多的问题。同样，与扩大测试团队相比，使您的测试团队多样化可能会发现更多问题。

7. Increasing risk by constraining resources: When testing resources are cut, the easiest way to respond is by limiting sample size—running fewer tests. But with a reduced sample size, sampling errors become more likely. A diverse sample might find more problems than a large sample. Likewise, diversifying your test team might find more problems than enlarging your test team.

Chapter_ 4_测试和调试有什么区别？

Chapter_4_What's the Difference Between Testing and Debugging?

 

“只是定义可以防止或结束争端。” - Nathanael Emmons，神学家（1745-1840），引用自Nathanael Emmons 的作品：他的生平回忆录，编。Jacob Ide（波士顿：Crocker & Brewster，1842 年）。

"Just definitions either prevent or put an end to a dispute." - Nathanael Emmons, Theologian (1745–1840), as quoted in The Works of Nathanael Emmons: With a Memoir of His Life, ed. Jacob Ide (Boston: Crocker & Brewster, 1842).

由于混淆了测试的确切内容和应该做什么，因此测试实践常常声名狼藉。如果经理想要在理解和改进测试方面取得任何进展，他或她将不得不澄清流程。矛盾的是，如果经理有丰富的软件开发经验，那么澄清可能会更加困难。让我们看看这是如何工作的。

The practice of testing has often received a bad reputation because of confusion over exactly what it is and what it's supposed to do. If a manager wants to make any progress understanding and improving testing, he or she is going to have to clarify the process. Paradoxically, that clarification may be more difficult if the manager has a great deal of experience developing software. Let's see how this works.

在她职业生涯的早期，Jane 是一名项目经理，她是一家为小型企业编写定制应用程序的小型软件咨询公司的一名女性开发和支持团队成员。她的工作要求她身兼数职。有时简是一名程序员，负责编写构成产品的代码。在其他时候，她测试她的代码，确保它完成了她想要的一切，没有她没有做的事情。还有一些时候，她接听客户的电话。在一个典型的日子里，Jane 完成了所有这些任务，这也是她在测试方面学到最多的地方。让我们回首过去，和她一起走过这样一天的一部分。

Early in her career, Jane, a project manager, was a one-woman development and support team in a tiny software consulting company that wrote custom applications for small businesses. Her job required that she wear many hats. Sometimes Jane was a programmer, creating the code that made up a product. At other times, she tested her code, making sure it did everything she intended and nothing she didn't. At still other times, she took calls from customers. On a typical day, Jane did all of these tasks, and that's where she learned the most about testing. Let's look back and travel with her through part of such a day.

测试发现

Testing for discovery

上午 8 点 56 分，简上班。她小心翼翼地将 Venti Caffe Latte 放在办公桌上，小心不要洒到键盘上，然后将午餐带来的沙拉和包放在办公桌下。到 9 点 06 分，Jane 已检查夜间代码构建是否正常，并启动了生成的可执行版本。

At 8:56 A.M., Jane arrives for work. She gingerly places her Venti Caffe Latte on her desk, being careful not to spill it onto her keyboard, then stows the salad she's brought for lunch and her bag under her desk. By 9:06, Jane has checked that the nightly code build went okay and that it launched the resulting executable version.

在接下来的半小时内，Jane 经历了一个又一个场景，检查她前一天所做的更改是否达到了她的预期，而没有影响任何其他功能。

For the next half-hour, Jane runs through scenario after scenario, checking to see if her changes from the preceding day did what she expected without affecting any other functionality.

回顾— Jane 正在测试：对被测软件执行有可能发现新信息的操作。

Recap—Jane is testing: performing actions on the software under test that have the potential to discover new information.

精确定位

Pinpointing

上午 9 点 36 分，简遇到了意外行为。没有更新数据库。她重新运行相同的场景。果然，她抓到了虫子。

At 9:36 A.M., Jane encounters unexpected behavior. An update to the database didn't take. She reruns the same scenario. Sure enough, she's caught a bug.

回顾—Jane 仍在测试：对被测软件执行有可能发现新信息的操作。在这种情况下，新信息是错误是可重复的。在确定错误是可重复的时，Jane 还开始了另一个过程。

Recap—Jane is still testing: performing actions on the software under test that have the potential to discover new information. In this case, the new information is that the bug is repeatable. In determining that the bug is repeatable, Jane's also beginning another process.

是什么原因造成的？简想知道。她进一步调查。该错误是否可通过所有更新或仅包含可选字段的更新重复？更新字段中的数据类型重要吗？

What could be causing that? Jane wonders. She investigates further. Is the bug repeatable with all updates or just updates that include optional fields? Does it matter what kind of data are in the updated field?

回顾——Jane 现在在精确定位：隔离 bug 发生的条件。

Recap—Jane is now pinpointing: isolating the conditions under which the bug occurs.

定位

Locating

到 10:17，Jane 知道只有在她清除可选字段时才会出现错误。她打开源代码，设置断点，然后开始逐步执​​行控制数据库更新的代码。

By 10:17, Jane knows that the bug only occurs when she's clearing optional fields. She opens the source code, sets a breakpoint, and begins stepping through the code that controls updates to the database.

回顾——Jane 现在正在定位：找到代码中错误的位置，以便她可以修复它。

Recap—Jane is now locating: finding the location of the bug in the code so that she can fix it.

确定意义

Determining significance

十五分钟后，简找到了导致问题的代码段。她看到，如果要消除更新问题，大约需要更换 50 行代码。她想着在实际使用数据库的时候遇到这个bug是多么的少。由于修复 50 行具有一定的风险，她权衡了这些风险与在某些情况下无法更新数据库的风险。她认为这次修复意义重大，足以承担风险。

Fifteen minutes later, Jane has located the piece of code causing the problem. She sees that about fifty lines of code will have to be replaced if the update problem is to be removed. She thinks about how rarely this bug will be encountered in real use of the database. Since the repair of fifty lines carries certain risks, she weighs those risks against the risk of failing to update the database in certain circumstances. She decides this repair is significant enough to take the risk.

回顾— Jane 现在正在确定重要性：平衡修复和不修复代码中此错误的风险。

Recap—Jane is now determining significance: balancing the risks of repairing versus not repairing this bug in the code.

修复中

Repairing

Jane 花了一点时间思考是否有任何风险较小的方法可以在不更改代码的情况下解决问题，例如向用户发出警告。她认为警告不足以提供足够的保护，然后花了一些时间思考修复代码的各种方法：编写新代码、修补旧代码、从另一个程序复制类似代码等等。她决定修补代码，并在接下来的两个小时内这样做。完成后，她会重复第一次检测到错误并开始整个过程​​的测试——这可能称为调试，尽管这个术语通常用于表示部分过程。

Jane spends a little time thinking about whether there are any less risky ways to fix the problem without changing the code, such as issuing a warning to users. She decides that a warning would not be sufficient protection, then spends some time thinking about various ways to repair the code: writing new code, patching the old code, copying similar code from another program, and so forth. She decides to patch the code and spends the next two hours doing so. Once she is finished, she repeats the test that first detected the bug and started the whole process—which may be called debugging, although this term is often used to mean parts of the process.

回顾— Jane 现在正在修复：更改代码以解决问题。

Recap—Jane is now repairing: changing code to remove the problem.

故障排除

Troubleshooting

12 点 46 分，简的电话响了。“Jane Chow，”她一边回答，一边从桌下拿出沙拉，咬了一口。

At 12:46, Jane's phone rings. "Jane Chow," she answers as she pulls her salad out from under her desk and takes a small bite.

“哦，我很高兴你在那里！” 另一端的声音略带歇斯底里。简试图确定声音的位置。哦，是的，谢尔曼——在 Acme 那边。

"Oh, I'm glad you're there!" The voice on the other end has a slight tinge of hysteria. Jane tries to place the voice. Oh, yes, Sherman—over at Acme.

“谢尔曼，很高兴收到你的来信。我能为你做点什么吗？” 简尽量不翻白眼，而是专心叉起一叉金枪鱼和西红柿。当他之前唯一的计算机经验是玩视频游戏时，他被要求支持 Acme 的软件系统并不是 Sherman 的错。

"Sherman, good to hear from you. What can I do for you?" Jane tries not to roll her eyes and concentrates instead on spearing a forkful of tuna and tomato. It's not Sherman's fault he's been asked to support Acme's software systems when his only prior computer experience was playing video games.

“我需要从备份中恢复一些东西，但系统不允许我这样做。为什么它不起作用？”

"I need to restore something from backup and the system won't let me. Why isn't it working?"

简问谢尔曼一系列问题：“你确定你有正确的备份吗？” “你能通过操作系统看到这些文件吗？” “备份软件给你什么错误？” “您使用的是哪种恢复过程？” 在 Sherman 回答时，Jane 记得备份例程中的一个错误可能会影响 Sherman 的恢复尝试。她带领他完成了一个不同的恢复过程，看看这是否有效。

Jane asks Sherman a series of questions: "Are you sure you have the right backup?" "Can you see the files through the operating system?" "What error did the backup software give you?" "Which recovery process are you using?" As Sherman answers, Jane remembers a bug in the backup routines that might be affecting Sherman's attempts to restore. She walks him through a different recovery process to see if that will work.

回顾— Jane 正在排除故障：尝试移除和/或绕过障碍，使软件执行它应该执行的操作。

Recap—Jane is troubleshooting: trying to remove and/or work around obstacles to make the software do what it's supposed to do.

测试学习

Testing to learn

Jane 在下午 1:40 完成了 Sherman 问题的故障排除并挂断了电话。当她吃完最后一块金枪鱼、生菜和西红柿时，她检查了自己的任务清单，发现她已经完成了早上安排的工作——在下午的会议之前还有 20 分钟的空闲时间。她大声说：“如果我能得到这个新的图形包来生成自定义符号，二十分钟的时间可能就足以从我的测试中绘制出一些统计数据。” 她阅读了文档并且知道它没有提供任何直接的解释。她用二十分钟的时间尝试了几种关于自定义符号如何工作的理论。

Jane finishes troubleshooting Sherman's problem at 1:40 P.M. and hangs up the phone. As she eats the last chunks of tuna, lettuce, and tomato, she checks her task list and sees that she has finished the work she'd scheduled for the morning—with twenty minutes to spare before her afternoon meeting. She reasons aloud, "Twenty minutes might be enough time to graph some statistics from my tests if I can just get this new graphics package to produce custom symbols." She's read the documentation and knows that it doesn't offer any straightforward explanation. She uses her twenty minutes to try out several theories about how custom symbols might work.

回顾— Jane 再次进行测试，但她并没有尝试在图形包中查找错误（尽管如果她碰巧遇到错误，她会报告）。我们可以说她通过测试来学习：一项基本技能，否则可以称为黑客、逆向工程或游戏。

Recap—Jane is testing again, but she's not trying to find bugs in the graphics package (although if she happens upon one, she'll report it). We could say she's testing to learn: an essential skill that might otherwise be called hacking, reverse engineering, or playing.

任务切换

Task-switching

简很容易在活动之间转换——测试发现、精确定位、定位、确定重要性、修复、故障排除和测试学习。只要她继续为她的客户服务，她在任何给定时间执行的任务并不重要。

Jane easily shifts among activities—testing for discovery, pinpointing, locating, determining significance, repairing, troubleshooting, and testing to learn. As long as she continues to serve her customers, it doesn't really matter which task she performs at any given time.

然而，在拥有专职测试人员和/或客户支持人员的大型组织中，混淆测试发现、精确定位、确定重要性、修复、故障排除和测试学习之间的差异可能会导致冲突、怨恨和失败的项目。

However, in larger organizations with dedicated testers and/or customer support personnel, confusion about the differences among testing for discovery, pinpointing, locating, determining significance, repairing, troubleshooting, and testing to learn can lead to conflict, resentment, and failed projects.

随着组织的发展，测试会发生什么变化？

What happens to testing as an organization grows?

现在让我们切换到现在，再看看简。我们看到她离开了她职业生涯早期的小型软件咨询公司，并搬到了一家更大的公司，担任其商业软件产品之一的项目经理。这个特定的工作日从 Stan 的到来开始，Stan 是一名软件测试员，他的直属经理是 Ken，Jane 项目的中层经理之一。

Now let's switch to the present to look in again on Jane. We see that she has left the tiny software consulting company where she spent the early part of her career and has moved to a much larger firm as project manager for one of its commercial software products. This particular workday begins with the arrival of Stan, a software tester whose line-manager is Ken, one of the middle managers on Jane's project.

8 点前几分钟，Stan 在他的办公桌前检查错误数据库，看看是否有任何错误修复可供他测试。他的队列中有一个错误，错误号 25073。这就是我昨天提交的那个，他想。他们不可能那么快修好它。看起来很讨厌。他打开记录，发现错误已返回给他并标记为需要更多信息。在程序员评论区，开发者Suni曾留言：“请测试所有类型的用户、所有备份选项、所有显示选项，并告诉我在什么情况下会出现这种情况。”

At his desk a few minutes before 8, Stan checks the bug database to see if there are any bug fixes for him to test. There's one bug in his queue, bug number 25073. That's the one I filed yesterday, he thinks. They couldn't have fixed it that fast. It looked nasty. He opens the record and discovers that the bug has been returned to him marked Need More Information. In the Programmer Comments section, Suni, the developer, has left a note: "Please test with all types of users, all backup options, and all display options, and tell me in which situations this occurs."

Stan 在测试时发现了 bug 25073，现在 Suni 要求他查明触发该 bug 的确切条件。有时精确定位是测试组工作的一部分。有时不是。通常，没有人明确指定谁负责精确定位。测试人员假设他们的工作是测试（发现），而开发人员假设测试人员的工作是支持开发——对开发人员来说这意味着测试、精确定位，有时甚至定位或确定重要性。或者甚至去拿咖啡。

Stan found bug 25073 while testing and now Suni is asking him to pinpoint the exact conditions that trigger the bug. Sometimes pinpointing is part of the test group's job. Sometimes it isn't. More often than not, nobody specifies explicitly who is responsible for pinpointing.
