The testers assume that their job is to test (discover) while the developers assume that the testers' job is to support development—which to the developers means testing, pinpointing, and sometimes even locating or determining significance. Or even fetching coffee.

拿咖啡？是的，在一些组织中，开发人员对待测试人员就好像他们是某种低级的杂工。当这种角色混淆发生时，您可以想象创建一个合理的测试修复过程将是多么困难。然而，Stan 知道无论由谁负责查明，重要的是要记住查明和测试是两个不同的过程。

Fetching coffee? Yes, in some organizations, developers treat testers as if they're some kind of low-level gofers. When that kind of role-confusion happens, you can imagine how difficult it will be to create a sensible test-to-fix process. Stan, however, knows that no matter who is responsible for pinpointing, it's important to remember that pinpointing and testing are two different processes.

在上午的大部分时间里，Stan 都在运行 Suni 要求的不同场景。上午 11 点 33 分，就在 Stan 完成按错误表单上的“提交”以将其连同附加信息返回给 Suni 时，Stan 的直属经理 Ken 来到了 Stan 的隔间。“嘿，Stan，你能像你承诺的那样在中午之前把那些测试结果给我吗？”

For the better part of the morning, Stan runs the different scenarios Suni has requested. At 11:33 A.M., just as Stan finishes pressing Submit on the bug form to return it to Suni with additional information, Stan's direct-line manager, Ken, stops by Stan's cubicle. "Hey, Stan, will you be able to get me those test results by noon like you promised?"

斯坦看了看手表。“哦，垃圾。不。我整个上午都在研究我昨晚告诉你的那个错误。” “我以为你昨晚提交的？有什么要处理的？” 斯坦叹了口气。“苏尼把它还给我，让我运行一堆场景来获取更多信息。”

Stan looks at his watch. "Oh, crud. No. I just spent all morning working on that bug I told you about last night." "I thought you filed that last night? What's to work on?" Stan lets out a sigh. "Suni returned it to me to run a bunch of scenarios to get more information."

肯盯着斯坦，无法相信自己听到的。“那不是你的问题。你有一个可重复的案例。你提交了它。你已经完成了。” 看到斯坦痛苦的表情，肯松了口气。“好吧，下次如果开发人员让你做那种工作，就来找我。现在，请在今天结束之前把那些测试结果给我。”

Ken stares at Stan, unable to believe what he is hearing. "That's not your problem. You had a reproducible case. You filed it. You were done." Seeing Stan's stricken expression, Ken eases off. "Okay, next time, come to me if a developer asks you to do that kind of work. Now please get me those test results before the end of today."

当 Stan 从为 Ken 准备测试结果的午后休息时，他重新检查了他的错误队列，发现 25073 又回来了，再次标记为需要更多信息。Suni 再次要求他运行一系列场景以进一步查明错误。然而这一次，斯坦问肯他是否应该为苏尼做这件事，并得到了响亮的“不”回应。Stan 将 bug 返回给 Suni，并在评论部分留言：“抱歉，没办法。”

When Stan takes a mid-afternoon breather from preparing the test results for Ken, he re-checks his bug queue and finds 25073 is back, again marked Need More Information. Once again, Suni is asking him to run through a slew of scenarios to further pinpoint the bug. This time, however, Stan asks Ken whether he should do this for Suni, and receives a resounding "No" in response. Stan returns the bug to Suni with a note in the Comments section: "Sorry, no can do."

斯坦没有因为清楚地了解他的测试角色而感到宽慰，而是感到沮丧，在帮助苏尼和做他的直线经理要求他做的事情之间左右为难，但他并不是简的项目中唯一感到沮丧的人. 苏妮很不高兴，因为她认为斯坦是来帮助她的。Ken 很不高兴，因为 Stan 一直花在为 Suni 查明错误的时间是他本应该花在查看测试结果以寻找新错误的时间。Jane 很不高兴，因为 Ken 的测试子团队打乱了她的项目进度。

Instead of feeling relieved at having a clear understanding of his testing role, now Stan feels upset, torn between helping Suni and doing what his line-manager has asked him to do, but he isn't the only one on Jane's project who feels upset. Suni is upset because she thought Stan was there to help her. Ken is upset because all the time Stan spent pinpointing the bug for Suni was time he should have spent looking through the test results for new bugs. And Jane is upset because Ken's testing sub-team has disrupted her project's schedule.

问题是组织中没有人同意测试人员应该精确定位到什么程度，因此冲突是不可避免的。当我们面临加速测试的压力时，为发现而进行的测试、精确定位、定位、确定重要性、修复、故障排除和学习测试之间的区别变得更加重要。有时很难确切地知道我们正在执行哪一项任务。例如，当我们试图了解错误是否可重复时，我们是在测试还是在查明？

The problem is that no one in the organization agrees to what extent testers are expected to pinpoint, so conflict is inevitable. The distinctions among testing for discovery, pinpointing, locating, determining significance, repairing, troubleshooting, and testing to learn become even more important when we are under pressure to speed up testing. Sometimes it's difficult to know exactly which one task we're doing. When we try to learn whether a bug is repeatable, for example, are we testing or pinpointing?

作为一名项目经理，她对互动的子团队有高层次的了解，Jane 可以通过避免将这些类型的活动归为一个标记为“测试”的大块来结束关于谁负责什么任务的混淆。集总完成的唯一事情就是让测试过程似乎永远持续下去。但当然，实际测试——检测故障——只占一般标签测试下所占时间的一小部分，而且这种模糊性使得准确估计和调度变得不可能。

As a project manager with a high-level view of her interacting sub-teams, Jane can end the confusion as to who is responsible for what tasks by avoiding lumping these types of activities into one big blob labeled Testing. The only thing that lumping accomplishes is making the test process seem to take forever. But of course the actual testing—detecting failures—is only taking a fraction of the time accounted for under the general label Testing, and the fuzziness makes accurate estimating and scheduling impossible.

由于 Jane 的职责范围涵盖测试团队、开发团队和支持团队，因此她必须明确哪些人对哪些任务负有主要责任。多年前，当她自己完成所有这些任务时，她不必随时弄清楚自己在做什么。但现在，如果她不这样做，她就无法改进她的整体项目及其成功的可能性。

Since Jane's span of responsibility covers the test team, the development team, and the support team, she's the one who must clarify which people have primary responsibility for which tasks. Years ago, when she performed all these tasks herself, she didn't have to clarify which one she was doing at any time. But now, if she doesn't do this, there's no way she'll be able to improve her overall project and its likelihood for success.

将时限启发法作为管理口号——但根据需要进行调整。

Make the time-limit heuristic a management mantra—but adjust it as needed.

一种有助于理清谁做了多久的启发式简单陈述了这个概念：

A heuristic that helps untangle who does what for how long states the concept simply:

项目中的任何人都不应粗心地浪费项目中任何人的时间。

Nobody on a project should carelessly waste the time of anyone on the project.

身为项目经理的 Jane 运用了这一原则，教导她的测试人员将调查错误的时间限制在不超过 10 分钟，然后才提醒程序员。Jane 明白，对于 Stan 来说可能是一个晦涩难懂的问题，对于程序员来说可能是一个显而易见的问题，在这种情况下，Stan 会浪费自己的时间来消耗十多分钟，然后再寻求可能更有知识的帮助。

Jane, in her role as project manager, applies this principle by teaching her testers to limit their time when investigating a bug to no more than ten minutes before alerting the programmer. Jane understands that what may be an obscure problem to Stan may be an obvious problem to the programmer, in which case Stan would be wasting his own time to consume more than ten minutes before seeking possibly more knowledgeable assistance.

时间限制是一种启发式原则，而不是一成不变的规则。斯坦使用许多因素来调整简的启发式。例如，如果程序员相距五个时区，Stan 可能会调查更长时间并批量提交他的错误报告。可能存在他同意以特定方式处理的特定类型的错误——对某些人来说更快，对其他人来说更慢。

Time-limiting is a heuristic principle, not a hard and fast rule. Stan uses many factors to adjust Jane's heuristic. For instance, if the programmer is five time zones away, Stan may investigate longer and batch his bug reports. There may be specific kinds of bugs that he has agreed to handle in specific ways—faster for some, slower for others.

一些测试团队通过聘请专门的错误调查员来帮助解决需要几分钟以上才能锁定的任何错误，从而节省了开发人员的时间。

Some test teams save developer time by having a dedicated bug investigator who lends a hand on any bug that requires more than a few minutes to lock down.

该原则的另一个应用是不要浪费时间进行过于精细的区分。例如，发现和精确定位之间没有明确的界线可以适用于所有情况（或者即使有，我也不知道）。与其浪费时间争论特定活动是否精确定位，不如让测试人员和开发人员共同参与并完成工作。

Another application of the principle is not wasting time making too-fine distinctions. For instance, there's no clear line between discovery and pinpointing that can be readily applied in all cases (or if there is one, I don't know of it). Rather than waste time arguing whether or not a specific activity is pinpointing, have both tester and developer pitch in and get the job done.

概括

Summary

需要许多不同技能的许多不同任务通常都集中在测试的标题下。这种混为一谈会扭曲计划、估算和工作分配，从而损害整个项目。

Many different tasks requiring many different skills are often lumped under the rubric Testing. Such lumping distorts planning, estimating, and job assignments, to the detriment of the entire project.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.认为可以安排定位错误：我们知道定位错误需要多长时间的唯一方法是知道它们在哪里。如果我们知道这一点，我们就根本不需要找到它们。

1. Thinking that locating errors can be scheduled: The only way we could know how long it would take to locate bugs would be to know where they are. If we know that, we wouldn't have to locate them at all.

2.不考虑因任务切换而损失的时间：正如我们所见，任务切换可能是有益的，但与其他任何事情一样，它也是有代价的。每次任务切换都会浪费一点时间，所以如果你在大约五个任务之间切换，你可能什么也做不了。大多数人通过简单地完全放弃一些任务来应对这种情况，这可能很危险。

2. Not considering time lost to task-switching: Task-switching can be beneficial, as we've seen, but like anything else, it has a cost. Each task-switch loses a bit of time, so if you're switching among about five tasks, you may be accomplishing nothing. Most people react to that situation by simply dropping some of the tasks altogether, which can be dangerous.

3. 将测试视为低优先级的任务，几乎可以出于任何原因中断：如果要可靠地完成测试，就需要集中注意力。

3. Treating testing as a low-priority task that can be interrupted for just about any reason: Testing requires concentration if it's to be done reliably.

4.要求测试人员查明每一个失败：测试人员可以帮助开发人员完成这项工作，如果他们的时间已经安排好的话，但这最终是开发人员的责任。至少从长远来看，这是我所看到的最好的方法。

4. Demanding that testers pinpoint every failure: Testers can help developers with this job, if their time has been scheduled for it, but it is ultimately a developer responsibility. At least that's what I've seen work best in the long run.

5.要求测试人员定位每一个故障：这完全是开发人员的工作，因为开发人员具备所需的技能。测试人员通常不具备这些技能，尽管有时他们可能会有有用的提示。

5. Demanding that testers locate every fault: This is totally a developer's job, because developers have the needed skills. Testers generally don't have these skills, though at times, they may have useful hints.

6.修理而不重新测试：仓促修理很可能使事情变得更糟。如果您不着急，您可能会非常小心地修理不需要重新测试，但如果您不着急，为什么不重新测试呢？

6. Repairing without retesting: Repairs done in a hurry are highly likely to make things worse. If you're not in a hurry, you might be careful enough with the repairs not to need retesting, but if you're not in a hurry, why not retest?

7.忽略交叉连接：通常，程序员的行为驱动了测试的需要，从而使测试和编程绑定在一起。例如，如果程序员延迟或在低于标准的条件下向测试人员交付代码，那么您将不得不调整测试预期。

7. Ignoring cross-connections: Commonly, the actions of programmers drive the need for testing, so that testing and programming are bound together. For instance, if programmers deliver code to testers late or in sub-par condition, then you'll have to adjust test expectations.

8.对可测试性关注不够：设计和构建可测试的代码可以大大减少与测试各个方面相关的时间和精力。

8. Paying insufficient attention to testability: Code that is designed and built to be testable can greatly reduce the time and effort associated with all aspects of testing.

9.坚持所有的bug都是“可重现的”：间歇性的bug需要大力追查，不能作为拖延测试或修复的借口。使用您拥有的信息，不要将测试人员的时间浪费在不合理的要求上。

9. Insisting that all bugs be "reproducible": Intermittent bugs need to be pursued with great vigor, not used as an excuse to delay testing or repairing. Use what information you have, and don't waste testers' time with unreasonable demands.

10.将测试与“创建和执行测试用例”相混淆：测试人员的大部分工作没有被捕获或封装在可识别的测试用例范围内。考虑从测试活动的角度来思考。

10. Confusing testing with "creating and executing test cases": Much of the testers' work is not captured or encapsulated within the confines of an identifiable test case. Consider thinking instead in terms of test activities.

11.在你的公司要求流程改革：如果你在一个组织中工作，认为查明和定位错误，或者为开发人员端咖啡和甜甜圈是测试人员的单独工作，你现在可能会想用粗鲁的方式面对你的老板，革命的态度。即使您有兴趣在您的组织中增加对测试人员的尊重，您也不会用粗鲁的要求来改变环境。你可能会对你的老板说，“我读到测试人员是尝试不同方法以使事情正常工作的人。我开始怀疑如果这里有些不同，我们的测试人员可以做得更好。我很乐意有时间和你讨论这些事情。”

11. Demanding process overhaul in your company: If you work in an organization that thinks it's the testers' job alone to pinpoint and locate bugs, or fetch coffee and donuts for the developers, you may now be tempted to confront your boss with a crass, revolutionary attitude. Even if you're interested in increasing respect for testers in your organization, you're not going to change the environment with rude demands. You might say to your boss, "I read that a tester is someone who tries different methods in order to make things work. I've come to suspect our testers could do better work if some things were different here. I'd love to have some time to discuss these things with you."

Chapter_ 5_元测试

Chapter_5_Meta-Testing

 

“通过观察你可以观察到很多东西。”

"You can observe a lot by watching."

- 棒球运动员和经理 Yogi Berra（生于 1925 年）和 Dave H. Kaplan，你可以通过观察观察到很多（Hoboken：Wiley，2008 年）。

- Yogi Berra, Baseball Player and Manager (b. 1925),and Dave H. Kaplan, You Can Observe a Lot by Watching (Hoboken: Wiley, 2008).

我们知道，软件测试的工作是提供有关产品质量的信息。许多人认为获得此类信息的唯一方法是在计算机上执行软件，或者至少检查代码。但这样的信念是极其有限的。为什么？总是有其他关于产品质量的信息可供使用——但只有那些正在观察并认为这些信息相关的经理才可以使用。[3] 由于他们与客户问题的心理距离，外部顾问通常能够看到逃脱客户眼睛和耳朵的信息。想想我的妻子兼搭档 Dani Weinberg 讲述的以下故事，讲述她在训犬界的一次咨询经历：

The job of software testing, we know, is to provide information about the quality of a product. Many people believe that the only way to get such information is to execute the software on computers, or at least to review code. But such a belief is extremely limiting. Why? There's always other information about product quality just lying around for the taking—but only by managers who are watching, and who recognize it as relevant. [3] Because of their psychological distance from a client's problems, external consultants are often able to see information that escapes the eyes and ears of their clients. Consider the following tale from my wife and partner, Dani Weinberg, about one of her consulting experiences in the dog-training world:

“一位养着 Sheltie 小狗的女人不知所措，因为‘他总是在客厅的地毯上拉屎。’” 她很喜欢这个小家伙，所以在放弃带他去人道协会之前，她来找我咨询。我听了那个女人描述了问题，然后问，“还有其他行为问题吗？” “女人想了想，然后说，‘嗯，是的，有一个。他有这种烦人的习惯，会在前门上抓挠并抱怨。'”

"A woman with a Sheltie puppy was at her wits' end because 'he always poops on the living-room rug.' She loved the little guy, so before giving up and taking him to the Humane Society, she came to me for a consultation. I listened to the woman describe the problem, then asked, 'Are there any other behavior problems?' "The woman thought for a while, then said, 'Well, yes, there is one. He has this annoying habit of scratching on the front door and whining.'"

很容易嘲笑别人无法看到两个“问题”之间的联系，但那种盲目是典型的人太亲密，太情绪化的情况。学会识别免费信息是成功管理测试的秘诀之一。您可以快速了解组织产品的质量或从机器测试中获得的信息的质量。

It's easy to laugh at someone else's inability to see the connection between two "problems," but that sort of blindness is typical of people who are too close, too emotionally involved with a situation. Learning to recognize free information is one of the secrets of successful management of testing. You can learn quickly about the quality of an organization's products or the quality of the information it has obtained from machine testing.

让我们再看看我自己和其他人的咨询实践中的一些“Sheltie 故事”。测试你自己：看看你可以从他们那里获得哪些关于产品质量的信息，或者通过测试获得的关于产品的信息的质量。

Let's look at some more "Sheltie stories" from my own and others' consulting practices. Test yourself: See what information you can derive from them about the quality of a product or the quality of the information that's been obtained about the product through testing.

我们有规格，但我们找不到它们。

We have specs, but we can't find them.

我被要求帮助一个组织评估其开发过程，包括测试。我问测试经理，“你使用规格来测试吗？”

I was asked to help an organization assess its development processes, including testing. I asked the test manager, "Do you use specs to test against?"

他回答说：“是的，我们当然知道。” “我可以看看他们吗？”

He replied, "Yes, we certainly do." "May I see them?"

“你可以，”他说，“但我们不知道它们在哪里。” 无法找到关键文档几乎是对组织开发过程的第三次打击。除了这条元信息（关于信息质量的信息）之外，我不需要太多细节就知道这个组织一团糟，但我确实继续问，“你需要多长时间才能找到他们？”

"You could," he said, "but we don't know where they are." The inability to find key documents pretty much is Strike Three against an organization's development process. I didn't need a whole lot of details beyond this one piece of meta- information (information about the quality of information) to know that this organization was a mess, but I did continue by asking, "How long would it take you to find them?"

测试经理回答说：“我不知道。”

The test manager replied, "I don't know."

我接着问：“好吧，那你估计要花多长时间才能找到他们？”

I then asked, "Okay, then how long will it take you to estimate how long it will take you to find them?"

对此他回答说：“也许一个月。”

To this he answered, "Maybe a month."

事实证明他是一个乐观主义者，但这并不重要。我用几个简单的问题测试了他们的测试过程。

It turned out he was an optimist, but it didn't really matter. I had tested their testing process with a couple of simple questions.

我们有太多错误，我们的错误数据库无法有效工作。

We have so many bugs, our bug database doesn't work efficiently.

我被叫去帮助一个产品开发组织的测试小组。我了解到测试人员正在测试一个大约有 40,000 行代码的产品。

I was called in to help a product development organization's testing group. I learned that the testers were testing a product with about 40,000 lines of code.

“问题是，”测试经理说，“是我们的错误数据库。”

"The problem," said the test manager, "is with our bug database."

“它出什么问题了？” 我问。“是马车吗？”

"What's wrong with it?" I asked. "Is it buggy?"

“不，它非常可靠，但一旦它拥有超过 14,000 个错误报告，它的性能就会开始迅速下降。我们需要你向我们展示如何提高性能，以便我们能够处理更多的错误报告。”

"No, it's very reliable, but once it holds more than about 14,000 bug reports, its performance starts to degrade very rapidly. We need you to show us how to improve the performance so we can handle more bug reports."

最后两句话增加了信息宝库。首先，测试人员认为这是一个数据库性能问题，至少，这是一个产生 14,000 个错误的开发过程的问题。关于他们的测试过程，我们可能只需要了解这些，因为没有任何合理的测试过程能够在任何可接受的时间内清除这些错误——如果它彻底清除了这些错误的话。（事实证明，开发产生更多错误的速度比解决现有错误的速度更快，这是我接下来调查的事情。）

These last two sentences add a treasure-trove of information. First of all, the testers think this is a database-performance problem when, at the very least, it's a problem with a development process that produces 14,000 bugs. That's probably all we need to know about their testing process, because no reasonable testing process was ever going to clear these bugs in any acceptable time—if it ever cleared them at all. (It turned out, development was producing more bugs faster than the existing bugs were being resolved, which was the next thing I investigated.)

最后，最重要的信息可能是测试经理报告这两句话时缺乏情绪。搞砸流程已经够糟糕了，但对此一无所知更糟糕。

The most important piece of information, in the end, was probably the lack of emotion with which the test manager reported these two sentences. Having a messed-up process is bad enough, but being clueless about that is much, much worse.

我们没有发现很多错误，尽管我们并没有真正去寻找。

We didn't find many bugs, though we didn't really look.

Irene 被要求帮助改进包含 22 个组件的产品的测试。客户通过每行代码发现的大量错误确定了“最差的三个组件”。Irene 询问哪些是最好的组件，并得到了非常低的每行代码错误数。

Irene was asked to help improve the testing of a product with 22 components. The client identified "the worst three components" by the high number of bugs found per line of code. Irene asked which were the best components and was given the very low, bugs-per-line-of-code figures for each.

然后她检查了配置管理日志，发现对于这三个“最佳”组件中的每一个，超过 70% 的客户代码尚未成功签入构建。

She then examined the configuration management logs and discovered that for each of these three "best" components, more than 70 percent of the client's code had not yet successfully been checked in for a build.

在这里，我们很容易了解到客户对其测量系统是多么的无知，这使得组织完全不了解真正发生的事情。他们在盲目飞行——或者更糟——因为他们使用了错误的地图。他们不知道如何衡量质量，所以他们不太可能得出质量。

Here, we easily learn how clueless the client is about its measurement system, which is making the organization totally out of touch with what is really going on. They are flying blind—or worse—because they are using the wrong map. They have no idea how to measure quality, so they aren't likely to arrive at quality.

我们修改我们的记录以使错误看起来不那么严重。

We modify our records to make bugs look less severe.

琳达受邀到一家公司帮助首席开发经理评估其测试部门的工作。她首先查看有关每周发现的漏洞数量和严重程度的报告。她注意到严重性计数已被涂白并改写。她刮掉每一个涂白的部分，发现每个最严重的数字下面都有一个更高的印刷数字。在每个最低严重性计数下都有一个较低的印刷数字。琳达不解地向开发经理寻求解释。

Linda was invited into a company to help the chief development manager evaluate his testing department's work. She started by looking at reports on the number and severity of bugs found each week. She noticed that the severity counts had been covered with white-out and written over. She scratched off each white-out and discovered that a higher printed number was under each highest severity count. Under each lowest severity count was a lower printed number. Puzzled, Linda asked the development manager for an explanation.

“那些是产品开发经理的更正，”他解释道。“有时测试人员没有分配适当的严重性，因此产品开发经理会纠正它们。”

"Those are corrections by the product's development manager," he explained. "Sometimes the testers don't assign the proper severity, so the product development manager corrects them."

片刻的想法就会表明，该组织总是会高估其在优质产品方面的进步。它没有花一点时间思考的事实有力地证明了它的麻烦远不止是伪造记录。

A moment's thought would show that this organization is always going to overestimate its progress toward a quality product. The fact that it hasn't spent a moment's thought is strong evidence that its trouble goes much deeper than simply falsifying records.

它不在我的组件中，所以我不记录它。

It's not in my component, so I don't record it.

我正在观看测试人员在软件产品的一个组件上运行测试。当测试人员导航到目标组件时，我注意到其中一个菜单中存在错误，并向测试人员指出了该错误。测试人员使用直接分支诅咒并绕过错误。

I was watching a tester running tests on one component of a software product. As the tester was navigating to the target component, I noticed an error in one of the menus and pointed it out to the tester. The tester cursed and navigated around the error by using a direct branch.

我称赞测试人员的聪明才智和足智多谋，然后问他将如何记录错误。“哦，我不需要记录它，”测试员回答道。“这不在我的范围内。”

I complimented the tester on his ingenuity and resourcefulness, then asked how he would document the error. "Oh, I don't have to document it," the tester replied. "It's not in my component."

这是另一种造假，会导致高估产品质量的进步，但我认为它可能比前一种情况更严重。该案涉及一位伪造记录的经理。这种情况可能被证明是组织文化中的一种普遍态度——一种更难根除的缺陷。

This is another kind of falsification that will lead to overestimating progress toward a quality product, but I think it's likely to be even more serious than the previous case. That case involved one manager who was falsifying records. This case may prove to be a widespread attitude in the culture of the organization—a defect that will be much more difficult to uproot.

我正在测试错误的应用程序，但我不知道。

I'm testing the wrong application and don't know it.

Matt 被要求进行参与者观察审查，在审查中他必须在不以任何方式干预的情况下观察测试人员的工作。他看到一位测试人员花费了大部分时间来测试基于 Web 的企业系统上的滚动条。当然，滚动条是 Web 浏览器的一部分，而不是被测系统的一部分。

Matt was asked to perform a participant-observation review in which he was constrained to observe testers at work without interfering in any way. He watched one tester spend the better part of several hours testing the scroll bars on a Web-based enterprise system. The scroll bars were, of course, part of the Web browser, not part of the system being tested.

很容易将此案例视为有关单个测试人员无知或智力低下的不幸信息，但除此之外还有更多。为什么允许该测试人员在本应在几分钟内完成的任务上继续执行这么长时间？监督在哪里？或者，也许更严肃地说，培训在哪里？测试人员的选择过程在哪里？像这样的行为是一种症状，所以我们需要问一个最重要的问题：它背后的疾病是什么？

It would be easy to dismiss this case as unfortunate information about the ignorance or low intelligence of a single tester, but there's more to it. Why is this tester allowed to go on so long on a task that should have been accomplished in a few minutes? Where is the supervision? Or, perhaps more serious, Where is the training? Where is the selection process for testers? Behavior like this is a symptom, so we need to ask a most important question: What's the disease behind it?

我们不会测试最差的组件，因为它需要太长时间。

We don't test the worst components because it takes too long.

我被要求评估一个组织的流程，我问开发经理她项目的开发人员是否对他们的代码进行了单元测试。

Called in to evaluate an organization's process, I asked the development manager whether the developers on her project unit-tested their code.

“当然，”她说。“我们对几乎所有代码进行单元测试。” “几乎全部？” 我问。“您不对哪些代码进行单元测试？” “哦，有些代码迟到了，所以我们当然没有时间对其进行单元测试，否则我们将不得不推迟系统测试的开始。” 在这里，我们看到了一个健忘的经理的迹象，以及该经理的经理缺乏关注的迹象。为什么没有人问为什么某些代码迟到了？如果他们询问，他们会发现已经晚了，因为开发人员无法使其正常工作。如果要对任何代码进行最彻底的测试，它应该是最新的代码。在这里，管理层倒退了。还有什么，我想知道？

"Absolutely," she said. "We unit-test almost all the code." "Almost all?" I asked. "Which code don't you unit-test?" "Oh, some of the code is late, so of course we don't have time to unit-test that or we'd have to delay the start of systems test." Here we see a sign of an oblivious manager, as well as that manager's manager's lack of attention. Why is nobody asking why certain code is late? If they asked, they would find out that it's late because the developers had trouble making it work. If any code was to be tested most thoroughly, it ought to be the latest code. Here, management has things backwards. What else, I wonder?

我们发现了太多错误，再也找不到了。

We found so many bugs, there couldn't be any more.

Melinda 的一位客户举办了一整天的 BugFest，在此期间，开发人员因在最新发布的候选版本中发现错误而获得现金奖励。他们发现了 282 个错误，这让他们确信他们“接近发布”。

One of Melinda's clients conducted an all-day BugFest during which developers earned cash rewards for finding bugs in their latest release candidate. They found 282 bugs, which convinced them they were "close to shipping."

客户对结果非常满意，因此在下一个发布日期之前的周六重复了该活动。这一次，开发者发现了 343 个新的 bug，并兴奋地宣布，发现如此多的 bug 表明他们“即将”出货。

The client was so happy with the results that it repeated the event on the Saturday before the next release date. This time, the developers found 343 new bugs and excitedly announced that finding so many bugs indicated that they were "on the verge" of shipping.

发现的错误数量可能是系统状态的指示，我们可以使用此信息来查看（因为客户不会）该系统状况不佳。但这里最重要的线索是客户对发现的错误和剩余的错误之间的关系一无所知。还有什么是它不知道的？

The number of bugs found might be an indication of the state of the system, and we could use this information to see—as the client doesn't—that this system is in poor shape. But the most important clue here is that the client is clueless about the relationship between bugs found and bugs remaining. What else doesn't it know?

我们的测试证明程序是正确的。

Our tests proved the program was correct.

我咨询了一位在地毯上的总经理，因为最近发货的产品被证明在客户手中存在严重的错误，我问他为什么允许该产品发货。他没有任何讽刺意味地回答说：“因为我们的测试证明它是正确的。”

Consulting with a general manager who was on the carpet because a recently shipped product was proving terribly buggy in the hands of customers, I asked him why he had allowed the product to ship. Without any hint of irony, he replied, "Because our tests proved that it was correct."

总经理不需要了解有关测试的大量细节，但他们需要知道再多的测试也永远无法“证明”程序是“正确的”。他们还需要知道“正确”甚至不是一个可以定义的概念。怎么连这么简单的检测机构都没有对管理层进行教育呢？

General managers don't need to know a great deal of detail about testing, but they do need to know that no amount of testing will ever "prove" a program is "correct." They also need to know that "correct" isn't even a definable concept. How come the testing organization hasn't educated its management even to this simple extent?

我们运行了太多的测试用例，以至于我们无法查看所有的测试用例。

We ran so many test cases that we couldn't look at them all.

另一位经理向 Raj 声称，他知道他的产品已准备好发货，因为“我们已经运行了 60 万个测试用例，没有出现系统崩溃的情况。” （注意这里的第二个谬误：任何不会崩溃的东西一定是好的。）

Another manager claimed to Raj that he knew his product was ready to ship because "we've run six-hundred-thousand test cases and nothing crashed the system." (Notice the second fallacy here: Anything that doesn't crash must be okay.)

这句话从几个方面揭示了说话者不知道测试是什么。此外，他认为他知道，所以如果他管理测试操作，测试人员将做大量无意义的工作，他会奖励这些工作。

This statement reveals in several ways that the speaker has no idea what testing is all about. Moreover, he thinks he knows, so that if he's managing the testing operation, the testers will be doing a great deal of meaningless work, which he'll reward.

如果我们的软件适用于三个用户，显然它也适用于 100 个用户。

If our software works okay for three users, obviously it will work okay for a 100.

当我向几位测试人员询问有关安排性能测试的问题时，他们回答说：“我们已经做到了。”

When I asked several testers about scheduling performance testing, they replied, "We've already done that."

“真的吗？” 我说。“你到底做了什么？”

"Really?" I said. "What exactly have you done?"

“好吧，我们用一个用户运行系统，响应时间大约是十毫秒。然后我们用两个用户运行它，响应时间是二十毫秒。三个用户是三十毫秒。”

"Well, we ran the system with one user, and the response time was about ten milliseconds. Then we ran it with two users, and the response time was twenty milliseconds. With three users, it was thirty milliseconds."

“有趣，”我说。“但系统应该支持至少一百个并发用户。那么当它满载时你得到的响应时间是多少？”

"Interesting," I said. "But the system is supposed to support at least a hundred simultaneous users. So what response time did you get when it was fully loaded?"

“哦，那个测试太难设置了，而且无论如何，没有必要。显然，响应时间将是一秒——每个用户十毫秒乘以一百个用户。” 这组测试人员犯了线性谬误（组合谬误的一种形式，它假设两个小系统连接在一起只是一个系统的两倍大，但仅此而已）。事实上，如果您有 10 公斤纯铀 235，再加上 10 公斤，就会有 20 公斤。但是如果你再这样做几次，你就没有五十公斤了，你会发生核爆炸。一加一并不总是等于二。[4]

"Oh, that test would have been too hard to set up, and anyway, it's not necessary. Obviously, the response time would be one second—ten milliseconds per user times one-hundred users." This group of testers was committing The Linearity Fallacy (a form of The Composition Fallacy, which assumes that two small systems joined together make just twice as big a system, but no more). It is fact that if you have ten kilograms of pure uranium-235 and you add another ten kilograms, you'll have twenty kilograms. But if you do this a few more times, you won't have fifty kilograms, you'll have a nuclear explosion. One plus one doesn't always equal two. [4]

但是这个组织里的人不理解组合谬误，所以我预测他们的测试情况会随着他们的系统越来越大而变得越来越糟。而且它会变得更大，因为他们不明白他们正在经历什么样的爆炸。

But the people in this organization don't understand The Composition Fallacy, so I would predict that their testing situation will grow worse and worse as their system grows bigger. And it will grow bigger, because they won't understand what kind of explosion they're getting into.

我们不希望我们的测试人员知道我们忽略了他们的信息。

We don't want our testers to know we're ignoring their information.

我刚刚开始合作的一位客户召开了紧急会议，以找出测试阻碍产品发货的原因。在会议上，测试人员提出了 15 个失败的测试，这些测试表明产品甚至没有正确构建，因此无法进行测试。他们与开发人员讨论了每个问题。会议结束后，开发负责人写了一份会议报告的电子邮件摘要，其中只有两个“重要”问题必须在发布前解决。

A client I had just started working with called an emergency meeting to find out why testing was holding up product shipment. In the meeting, the testers presented fifteen failed tests that showed that the product did not even build correctly, so it couldn't be tested. They discussed each of the problems with the developers. After the meeting, the development lead wrote an e-mail summary of the meeting reporting that only two "significant" problems had to be solved prior to ship.

电子邮件被发送给开发经理、营销经理和参加会议的每个开发人员。在会议上提交失败测试的测试人员没有一个被列入抄送列表，所以他们甚至都不知道电子邮件已发送。

The e-mail was sent to the development manager, the marketing manager, and to each of the developers who attended the meeting. Not one of the testers who had presented the failed tests at the meeting was included in the cc-list, so none of them even knew that the e-mail was sent.

在这里，管理人员不仅在伪造信息，而且还向需要了解信息以执行工作的人员隐瞒信息。但更糟糕的是，他们在伪造别人的信息，让测试人员看起来好像在说一套的时候说一套。这个组织不会走得太远——至少不会走得太远。

Here managers are not only falsifying information, they're withholding information from people who need to know it to perform their jobs. But even worse, they're falsifying someone else's information, making it look as if the testers said one thing when they said another. This organization isn't going far—at least not far forward.

我不报告错误，所以开发人员不会生我的气。

I don't report bugs, so the developer won't be angry with me.

Sara 看到一名测试人员在一个组件中发现了五个错误，但测试人员没有将这些错误记录在错误数据库中，而是直接找到该组件的开发人员并口头报告给她。Sara 问测试人员为什么不记录错误，他回答说：“如果我这样做，她会冲我尖叫，因为这让她看起来很糟糕。”

Sara watched a tester uncover five bugs in a component, but instead of logging the bugs in the bug database, the tester went directly to the developer of the component and reported them to her orally. Sara asked why the tester didn't record the bugs, and he replied, "If I do that, she screams at me because it makes her look bad."

如果这个测试员是典型的，情绪是这个组织的主导因素。尖叫管理通常不是非常成功的领导策略。这很可能是典型的行为。我们知道开发人员的经理也使用恐惧，否则为什么开发人员会如此害怕看起来不好？

Emotions are the dominant factor in this organization, if this tester is typical. Management By Screaming is not generally a highly successful leadership tactic. And quite likely, this is typical behavior. We know that the developer's manager uses fear, too, or why would the developer be so afraid of looking bad?

我们不需要测试那个，因为开发人员真的很好。

We don't need to test that, because the developer is really good.

丹尼斯审查了客户的测试计划并注意到没有计划测试其中一个组件。当他问测试经理（刚来公司）为什么缺少它时，他被告知，“我们不需要担心这个。开发经理向我保证，这个开发人员非常细心和认真。”

Dennis reviewed a client's test plan and noticed that there was no plan to test one of the components. When he asked the test manager (who was new to the company) why it was missing, he was told, "We don't need to worry about that. The development manager assures me that this developer is very careful and conscientious."

这个组织中很可能也存在恐惧，尽管没有人这么说。他们所说的是，“我们对真实的人类一无所知。” 但即使他们真的有一个如此优秀的开发人员，他们为什么不利用她来让其他开发人员达到她的水平呢？

Quite likely there's fear in this organization, too, although nobody's saying so. What they are saying is, "We don't know the first thing about real human beings." But even if they actually had a developer who was this good, why aren't they using her to bring the rest of the developers up to her level?

跟进元信息。

Follow up on meta-information.

十四层楼，十四种黑色、白色或灰色。我希望您能够从这些故事中提取元信息。如果您不相信自己已经成功，请考虑他们每个人告诉您（或者，如果没有告诉您，向您暗示）关于从测试中收集的信息的质量——准确性、相关性、清晰度和全面性。

Fourteen stories, fourteen shades of black, white, or gray. I hope you were able to extract meta-information from these stories. If you are not convinced that you have succeeded, consider what each of them tells you (or, if not tells, hints to you) about the quality of the information gathered from testing—the accuracy, relevance, clarity, and comprehensiveness.

但请记住，这些故事只是供您解读的提示。也许反复在地毯上大便的 Sheltie 这样做是因为他有一些需要兽医注意的医疗问题，而不是他的主人怀疑的行为问题。也许在这些 Sheltie 情况的背后都有一个不明显的解释供您跟进。使用提供的提示来验证您的直觉——或找到另一种解释。而且，即使您的直觉准确无误，您也可能很难说服他人您是正确的。您将不得不收集其他证据或其他盟友，以影响能够影响局势的人。

Remember, though, that these stories are merely hints for you to interpret. Perhaps the Sheltie that pooped repeatedly on the rug did so because he had some medical problem requiring a veterinarian's attention, not the behavior problem his owner suspected. Perhaps there's a non-obvious explanation behind each of these Sheltie situations for you to follow up on. Use the hints that are provided to validate your intuition—or find another interpretation. And, even if your intuition is right on target, you probably won't have an easy time convincing others that you're correct. You will have to gather other evidence, or other allies, to influence the people who can influence the situation.

当 Dani 问 Sheltie 的主人为什么她认为小狗在前门抱怨时，女人说：“我想我已经宠坏了他。他一直想出去玩，但我有太多家务活做——特别是因为我花了这么多时间清理地毯上的烂摊子。”

When Dani asked the Sheltie's owner why she thought the puppy was whining at the front door, the woman said, "I think I've spoiled him. He just wants to go out and play all the time, but I have too much housework to do—especially since I spend so much time cleaning up the mess on the rug."

当问题仍然存在时，无论解决方案对您来说多么明显，您都无法说服他人解决问题，直到您发现他们如何合理化对您来说如此明显的证据。在下一章中，我们将了解人们如何使自己免受信息侵害，以及您可以采取哪些措施。

When a problem persists in spite of how obvious the solution is to you, you aren't going to be able to convince others to solve the problem until you find out how they are rationalizing away the evidence that's so apparent to you. In the next chapter, we look at how people immunize themselves against information, and what you can do about it.

概括

Summary

如果您学会使用元信息（关于信息质量的信息），您可以大大提高测试效率并降低成本。

You can greatly improve the efficacy of your testing, and lower your costs, if you learn to use meta-information—information about the quality of information.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.相信所有相关信息都包含在测试报告中：即使报告了所有测试，至少有一半你需要的信息不会在其中。

1. Believing that all relevant information is contained in test reports: Even if all tests are reported, at least half the information you need won't be in them.

2.相信你可以坐在你的办公室里，知道测试的进展情况：你应该通过自己直接观察它们是如何进行的以及它们背后的原因来验证报告的有效性。

2. Believing you can sit in your office and know what is going on with testing: Reports should be validated by your own direct observation of how they have been conducted and what's behind them.

3.相信测试可以“证明”任何事情都是正确的：测试所能证明的只是在特定条件下某些事情失败或没有失败。詹姆斯巴赫这样说：“我不从事证明业务；我从事证据和推理业务。”

3. Believing that tests can "prove" anything correct: All a test can show is that something failed or didn't fail under specific conditions. James Bach puts it this way: "I'm not in the proof business; I'm in the evidence and inference business."

4.相信文件的存在本身就具有一定的价值：如果你不使用它们，它们就毫无价值。如果它们具有误导性并且您使用了它们，那么它们可能比一文不值更糟糕。

4. Believing that the mere existence of documents has some value: If you don't use them, they're worthless. If they are misleading and you use them, they can be worse than worthless.

5.允许等待评估/修复/分配的错误列表超出人类的理解范围：如果你不跟上错误的步伐，士气就会受到影响，你就会落后得更远。最好停止产生新错误并清除旧错误。每个人都会感觉更好，工作也会更好。如有必要，您可以宣布错误特赦：从错误数据库中删除所有错误，并向所有发布者发送通知，告诉他们如果仍然担心错误，请重新提交错误。如果他们仍然担心，请将错误添加回队列中。当我对 14,000 个错误数据库执行此操作时，减少了很多，问题就解决了。

5. Allowing the list of bugs pending assessment/fixing/assignment to grow beyond human comprehension: If you're not keeping up with bugs, morale will suffer and you'll fall further behind. Better to stop producing new bugs and clear up old ones. Everyone will feel better and work better. If necessary, you can declare bug amnesty: Remove all bugs from the bug database and send a notice to all issuers telling them to resubmit a bug if they're still concerned about it. If they remain concerned, add the bug back into the queue. When I did this with the 14,000-bug database, the reduction was enormous and the problem was solved.

6.责备人们，让他们有动力隐藏错误：除非它离开办公室，否则这不是错误。每次有人伪造记录时，您都会丢失可以帮助您管理项目的信息。

6. Blaming people so they feel motivated to hide bugs: It's not an error unless it leaves the office. Every time someone falsifies a record, you lose information that could help you manage your project.

7.奖励走过场的人：为了有效地测试，人们必须集中注意力。没有重点的专注可能看起来不错，但收效甚微。

7. Rewarding people for going through the motions: To test effectively, people have to both concentrate and focus. Concentration without focus might look good, but accomplishes little.

8.不记录每一个已识别的故障：发现的故障非常有价值，不容忽视。如果他们没有被记录下来，他们很可能会被忽略。如果他们被忽视，你就是在浪费金钱和时间。不记录失败以“节省时间”会对您的日程安排产生完全相反的影响。

8. Not recording every identified failure: Caught failures are just too valuable to be ignored. If they're not recorded, they're likely to be ignored. If they're ignored, you're throwing away money and time. Not recording failures to "save time" will have exactly the opposite effect on your schedule.

9.过度记录每个已识别的故障：记录可能很昂贵。James Bach 建议采用 MIP 策略——其中 MIP 代表Mention In Passing。对于某些错误，James 可能不会准备昂贵的正式报告，而是将信息放在电子邮件中，口头报告给开发人员，或在会议上提及。我自己的偏好是在错误数据库中为错误分配一个标识符，至少在电子邮件或对话中引用它。否则，很容易通过玩关于什么被记录和什么没有被记录的游戏来扭曲统计数据。

9. Over-recording every identified failure: Recording can be expensive. James Bach suggests a MIP strategy—whereby MIP stands for Mention In Passing. For some bugs, James may not prepare an expensive, formal write-up, but instead puts the information in an e-mail, reports it orally to the developer, or mentions it in a meeting. My own preference is to assign the bug an identifier in the bug database, with at least a reference to it in the e-mail or conversation. Otherwise, it's all too easy to distort statistics by playing games about what gets recorded and what doesn't.

另一方面，通过提高报告成本，您可以大大提高测试人员自我审查的可能性，因此寻找节省费用的方法。例如，某些类别的错误（例如国际化问题或拼写错误）可能会作为一条记录成批报告，而不是作为单独的记录。

On the other hand, by raising the cost of reporting, you can greatly improve the likelihood that a tester will self-censor, so look for ways to save expense. For example, certain classes of bugs, such as internationalization issues or spelling errors, might be reported in a batch as one record, rather than as separate records.

10.让情绪决定测试和报告的内容：如果你不小心，你会鼓励欺凌和相互依赖。软件构建已经足够艰难了。

10. Letting emotions determine what is tested and reported: If you're not careful, you'll encourage bullying and co-dependency. Software-building is tough enough already.

11.使用虚假模型评估进度：发现的错误越多，就会发现越多，而不是相反。没有完美的开发者，不管他们能说出多好的游戏。

11. Using phony models to assess progress: The more bugs you find, the more you're going to find, not the other way around. There are no perfect developers, regardless of how good a game they can talk.

12.假设官方流程描述始终可靠且正确：流程描述就是描述。而且，它是对理想过程的描述，而不是对实际完成的过程的描述。在没有任何系统可以确保它已被遵循的情况下，假设它已被遵循，是有勇无谋的。

12. Assuming the official process description is always followed reliably and correctly: A process description is just that, a description. And, it's a description of an ideal process, not of what has actually been done. To assume it has been followed, in the absence of any system to assure that it has been, is foolhardy.

13.相信客观性：所有信息都经过解释，因此在某种程度上是主观的。了解影响您使用的信息质量的力量。

13. Believing in objectivity: All information is interpreted and therefore subjective to some degree. Be aware of the forces that influence the quality of the information you're using.

14.没有仔细审查使用模板制作的任何文件：模板确保文件的格式是标准的。这些文件往往看起来很漂亮，但往往掩盖了不可靠的信息。

14. Failing to review carefully any document produced using a template: Templates ensure that the form of documents is standard. Such documents tend to look pretty, but often camouflage unreliable information.

第六章信息免疫

Chapter_6_Information Immunity

 

“一个错误不会因为多次传播而变成真理，真理也不会因为没有人看到而变成错误。” - 政治家和人道主义者圣雄甘地 (1846–1948) 和克里希纳克里帕拉尼 (Krishna Kripalani)，人皆兄弟（纽约：Continuum 国际出版集团，2005 年）。

"An error does not become truth by reason of multiplied propagation, nor does truth become error because nobody sees it." - Mahatma Gandhi, Statesman and Humanitarian (1846–1948),and Krishna Kripalani, All Men Are Brothers (New York: Continuum International Publishing Group, 2005).

尽管测试的目的是提供信息，但人们通常认为这些信息具有威胁性。考虑以下评论中反映的潜在恐惧：

Although the purpose of testing is to provide information, people often view the information as threatening. Consider the underlying fears reflected in the following comments:

项目经理：“由于所有这些错误，我无法安排我的日程安排。”

Project Manager: "With all these bugs, I won't make my schedule."

开发人员：“那个愚蠢的错误向人们表明我没有像我希望的那样成为一名优秀的程序员。”

Developer: "That stupid error shows people I'm not as good a programmer as I'd hoped to be."

营销经理：“这个产品漏洞百出，不会卖得很好，我也做不到。”

Marketing Manager: "This product is so full of bugs, it isn't going to sell very well, and I won't make my numbers."

测试员：“如果我在游戏这么晚的时候报告这个错误，我的老板会咬我的头。”

Tester: "My boss is going to bite my head off if I report this error this late in the game."

由于信息的威胁性如此之大，我们都形成了一种“免疫系统”，可以保护我们免受我们不想听到的信息的侵害。信息免疫力会破坏您所有的最佳测试工作，因为您关于错误的信息可能会被置若罔闻。那么，管理者需要注意什么？下一节将揭示一些答案，探讨恐惧在工作场所扮演的角色。后面的章节展示了如何主要通过消除常见的误解和迷思来消除恐惧。

Because information can be so threatening, we've all developed an "immune system" that tends to protect us from information we don't want to hear. Information immunity can undermine all your best testing efforts because your message about bugs may fall on deaf ears. So what does a manager have to watch for? Some answers are revealed in the following section, which explores the role fear plays in the workplace. Later chapters show how to allay fears primarily by clearing up common misconceptions and myths.

当我们的规则受到威胁时，我们会感到害怕。

We are afraid when our rules are threatened.

当我们害怕时，我们会试图保护自己。我们有很多可用的防御措施，如果一个失败了，我们可以尝试另一个。我们并不总能成功克服恐惧或驱散它的影响，但当我们感到受到威胁时，我们会本能地进行防御。

When we are afraid, we try to defend ourselves. We have many defenses available to us, and if one fails, we may try another. We don't always succeed in conquering our fear or dissipating its effects, but when we feel threatened, we instinctively defend.

FEAR 由作者 Tom Crum 定义为Fantasy Experienced As Reality 的首字母缩写词。[5] 我们的想象力——我们的幻想——告诉我们可能会发生不好的事情。有时是对的，有时是错的，但无论哪种方式，我们都会捍卫。

FEAR is defined by author Tom Crum as an acronym for Fantasy Experienced As Reality. [5] Our imagination—our fantasy—tells us that something bad may happen. Sometimes it's right and sometimes it's wrong, but either way, we defend.

家庭治疗师兼作家弗吉尼亚·萨提尔 (Virginia Satir) 指出，当我们的自尊心低下时，我们会把防御放在首位，并且某些互动会引发生存法则，打破这种法则会使我们对人身安全产生强烈、恐惧的感觉。测试特别容易引发这种生存规则。例如，

The family therapist and author Virginia Satir noted that we bring our defenses to the fore when our self-esteem is low and some interaction invokes a survival rule, the breaking of which leads us to a strong, fearful feeling about our personal safety. Testing is especially prone to provoking such survival rules. For example,

• 如果有人向您展示程序中的错误，您可以援引“我必须永远完美”的生存法则。

• If someone shows you a bug in your program, you may invoke your survival rule that says, "I must always be perfect."

• 如果你正在尝试使用一个程序，但你不能让它正常工作，你可以援引你的生存法则，“我绝不能犯傻”。

• If you're trying to use a program and you can't make it work properly, you may invoke your survival rule that says, "I must never be stupid."

• 如果测试出现大量错误并且项目没有迅速完成，您可以援引您的生存法则，即“我必须始终按时完成”或“我必须始终履行我的承诺”。

• If tests are turning up lots of bugs and a project is not finishing swiftly, you may invoke your survival rule that says, "I must always be on schedule" or "I must always meet my commitments."

• 如果您是一名专业测试人员，您可能会发现自己经常面临生存法则，“如果你不能说些好话，就什么也别说。”

• If you are a professional tester, you may find yourself constantly facing the survival rule, "If you can't say something nice, don't say anything."

• 如果你有生存法则，“如果我没有发现问题，我就没有做好我的工作”，你可能会开始发现各种（挑剔的）问题。如果你是一个不羞于分享坏消息的人，你可能会从你的消息接收者那里得到一个触及你生存法则的反应，“永远不要让任何人生气。”

• If you have the survival rule, "If I don't find problems, I'm not doing my job," you may start to find all kinds of (nit-picky) problems. If you are someone who is not shy about sharing bad news, you may get a reaction from the recipient of your news that touches your survival rule, "Never make anybody angry."

在这种情况下，人们会在构建防御方面发挥无穷的创造力。心理学家将这些防御措施分为六个类别：压抑、合理化、投射、转移、过度补偿和强迫。我们将在以下各节中仔细研究这些防御行为中的每一种。

In such situations, people are endlessly creative in constructing defenses. Psychologists have broken down these defenses into half-a-dozen categories: repression, rationalization, projection, displacement, overcompensation, and compulsiveness. We take a closer look at each of these defense behaviors in the following sections.

我们压制不可接受的。

We repress the unacceptable.

压抑是否认或忽视我们认为不可接受的想法、感受和记忆——例如，在谴责他人迟到的同时，我们忽视了我们过去曾在类似场合迟到的事实。压抑行为的一个众所周知的象征是把头埋在沙子里的鸵鸟：如果我看不到它，它就不存在。

Repression is denying or overlooking what we deem to be unacceptable thoughts, feelings, and memories—for example, while condemning another's late arrival, we overlook the fact that we have been late on similar occasions in the past. A well-known symbol of repressive behavior is the ostrich with its head in the sand: If I don't see it, it doesn't exist.

每种形式的防御行为都可能涉及某种形式的压抑。以我的同事 Ella 在开始熟悉客户的应用程序时的经历为例。Ella 发现将文本从屏幕上的文本框中拖放到另一个窗口中会导致崩溃。她猜想测试员会想知道这个问题，所以她在他的隔间停下来说：“嘿，让我给你看点东西。” 然后她展示了她的发现。

Every form of defensive behavior probably involves repression in some form or another. Take, for example, my colleague Ella's experience while beginning to familiarize herself with a client's application. Ella discovered that dragging text from a text box on the screen and dropping it in another window resulted in a crash. She figured the tester would want to know about the problem, so she stopped by his cubicle and said, "Hey, let me show you something." She then demonstrated what she'd found.

测试人员盯着她看了几秒，然后回答道。“是的？”

The tester stared at her for a few seconds and then replied. "Yeah?"

“你不觉得这是一个错误吗？” “不。用户不应该那样做。”

"Don't you think it's a bug?" "No. Users shouldn't do that."

[就这一点而言，测试者的反应更多的是置换而不是压抑，但随后他继续，有意识地压抑。]

[To this point, the tester's reaction is more an example of displacement than repression, but then he continues, with a conscious repression.]

“此外，开发人员现在有足够多的错误。在他们修复他们已经知道的错误之前，我不想找到更多。”

"And besides, the developers have enough bugs on their plate right now. I don't want to find more until they fix the ones they already know about."

换句话说，现在不能接受的bug多了，就不会有了。

In other words, more bugs now would be unacceptable, so there won't be any.

压抑可以是有意识的，也可以是无意识的，就像人们掩盖真相以引导自己或他人远离感知到的危险一样。举个例子，一个测试人员提交给开发人员的失败案例被驳回并写道：“这不是错误，如问题编号 173 中所述。” 测试人员认识到问题 173 根本没有提到这个失败，并且理解如果他只是接受这个声明，这个错误将保留在应用程序中，开发人员不会对此采取任何措施。虫子是有意识地被压抑了，还是无意识地被压抑了？有关系吗？

Repression can be conscious or it can be unconscious, as when people shade the truth to lead themselves or others away from perceived danger. Take, for example, a failure case that is submitted by a tester to a developer who dismisses it and writes, "This is not a bug, as mentioned in issue number 173." The tester recognizes that issue 173 doesn't mention this failure at all, and understands that if he simply accepts this statement, the bug will remain in the application, with the developer protected from doing anything about it. Was the bug consciously repressed, or unconsciously repressed? Does it matter?

毫无疑问，测试人员从开发人员那里听到最多的压抑就是“我什么都没改”。通过在心里加上句子中被压抑的部分，可以清楚地表明这意味着什么，给出“我没有改变任何应该重要的东西，我认为重要的东西，除了我所做的改变。” [6]

Undoubtedly, the most common repression that testers hear from developers is "I didn't change anything." What this means is made clear by mentally adding the repressed part of the sentence, giving, "I didn't change anything that should matter, that I thought was important, except for what I did change." [6]

通常，您可以通过测试人员和经理之间讨论期间产生的强烈情绪来检测压抑防御措施。在下文中，测试人员压制了一个错误，经理做出了反应：

Often you can detect that repression defenses are in place by the strong emotions generated during a discussion between a tester and a manager. In the following, a tester represses a bug and a manager reacts:

经理：“那不是一个错误吗？”

Manager: "Wasn't that a bug?"

测试人员：“不，它一直都是这样。你只要重新启动就可以了。”

Tester: "No, it does that all the time. You just restart and it's okay."

经理：“你有没有把它作为一个 bug 归档？”

Manager: "Have you filed that as a bug?"

测试员：“不，这不是错误。它就是这样。”

Tester: "No, it's not a bug. It's just the way it is."

经理：“你一定是在开玩笑！”

Manager: "You must be kidding!"

当经理向我描述这次交流时，事情发生已经一年多了，但他仍然非常生气，以至于在讲述这个故事时他几乎浑身发抖。

When the manager described this exchange to me, more than a year had passed since it happened, but he was still so angry that he literally shook as he related the story.

我们将不合理的事情合理化。

We rationalize the unreasonable.

合理化试图使无意义的、愚蠢的或非理性的行为看起来合理——例如，如果开发人员声称“我确实在程序中留下了错误，这样我们就可以知道测试人员是否做得很好”，这就是合理化。

Rationalization is trying to make meaningless, stupid, or irrational actions appear reasonable—for example, a developer is rationalizing if he claims, "I really left mistakes in the program so we'd know if the testers were doing a good job."

考虑以下情况：为我在阿肯色州访问的客户设计的数据库查询系统的结构使得用户可以通过两种方式注销——点击按钮或使用菜单。当用户使用按钮注销时，会出现“确认注销”屏幕，让用户可以选择确认注销或取消命令以保持登录状态。当用户使用菜单注销时，注销是立即，无法取消。

Consider the following situation: A database query system designed for a client I visited in Arkansas had been structured so that there were two ways for users to log out—either by hitting a button or by using a menu. When a user logged out using the button, a "confirm log out" screen appeared, giving the user the option either to confirm log out or to cancel the command to stay logged in. When a user logged out using the menu, log out was immediate, with no option to cancel.

测试人员认为这两个注销选项应该保持一致，但开发人员不同意，“这是一个功能，因为它给了用户两种不同的注销方式，一种是确认，一种是没有。而且，我无法更改它很容易，所以你最好接受它。” 换句话说，如果你不能修复它，那就突出它——一个合理化的完美例子，如果你不深入思考它，这听起来很合理。[7]

Testers thought the two log-out options should be consistent, but the developer disagreed, "This is a feature, because it gives the user two different ways to log out, one with confirmation and one without. Besides, I can't change it easily, so it's best if you accept it." In other words, if you can't fix it, feature it—a perfect example of rationalization, which sounds rational if you don't think too deeply about it. [7]

并不是说测试人员总是理性的。开发人员经常发现测试人员提出不合理的论点，因此并非每一次对测试人员报告的反驳都是合理化或其他病态的例子。但是，对于数据库查询系统，大多数人会同意开发人员的论点是不合理的，注销方法之间的不一致是一个问题，而不是一个特性。

Not that testers are always rational. Developers often catch testers making irrational arguments, so not every push-back against a tester's report is an example of rationalization or some other pathology. In the case of the database query system, though, most people would agree that the developer's arguments are irrational and that the inconsistency between log-out methods is a problem, not a feature.

测试人员如何在不增加情况的感知威胁的情况下吸引开发人员？他可以首先解构开发人员的防御（使用如下第 1、2 和 3 步中所示的逻辑），然后声明需要设计修复（第 4 步）：

How could the tester appeal to the developer without increasing the perceived threat of the situation? He could start by first deconstructing the developer's defense (using logic such as is shown in Steps 1, 2, and 3, below), and then state that a fix needs to be devised (Step 4):

第 1 步。“用户通常不会根据按钮和菜单来索引不同风格的功能。这不是图形用户界面中的典型设计。”

Step 1. "Users generally don't index different flavors of a feature in terms of buttons versus menu. That's not a typical design in graphical user interfaces."

第 2 步。“用户通常希望应用程序以可以撤消的方式运行，除非首先出现警告消息（除非他们在选项对话框中明确关闭了‘确认’）。”

Step 2. "Users generally expect that the application will behave in ways that can be undone, unless there is a warning message first (unless they have explicitly turned off 'confirmations' in the Options dialogue)."

第 3 步。“一致性是改善用户学习曲线的主要因素。这包括应用程序内部的一致性以及与其他流行产品的一致性。”

Step 3. "Consistency is a major factor in improving the user's learning curve. This includes consistency within the application and consistency with other popular products."

第 4 步。“我们需要考虑实施修复的方法。如果修复真的很难，知道这会为我们提供关于此代码开发过程中其他重要问题的可能性的元信息。”

Step 4. "We need to think of ways to implement the fix. If it is really so hard to fix, knowing that gives us meta-information about the likelihood of other important problems in development of this code."

然而，如果这些步骤不起作用，测试人员不应感到惊讶。通常，逻辑论证不会改变逻辑未达成的立场。

The tester, however, shouldn't be surprised if these steps don't work. Usually, logical arguments don't change a position that wasn't arrived at by logic.

我们将自己的负面品质投射到其他人身上。

We project our own negative qualities onto other people.

投射，当消极的时候，批评别人有我们不喜欢的相同品质——例如，如果我暗自怀疑我有点自私或专横，我可能会在另一个人身上发现这些负面品质，抱怨，“他很贪婪”或“她在控制。” 下面的故事演示了投影的侵入行为。

Projection, when negative, is criticizing others for having the same qualities we dislike in ourselves—for example, if I secretly suspect that I am a bit selfish or overbearing, I might pick up on these negative qualities in another, complaining, "he's greedy" or "she's controlling." The following story demonstrates projection's invasive behavior.

每次 Missy（荷兰的一名测试员）在“搜索”字段中输入一个新值时，她的计算机屏幕都会变成空白。完全空白。一分钟后，画面依旧一片空白。在持续两到八分钟的额外时间后，屏幕亮起并显示搜索完成消息，所有常规菜单重新出现。

Each time Missy, a tester in the Netherlands, enters a new value in the SEARCH field, her computer screen goes blank. Totally blank. After a minute, the screen is still blank. After an additional period of time that lasts between two and eight minutes, the screen lights up with the message SEARCH COMPLETE, and all the regular menus reappear.

Ken 是在伦敦以外地区开展业务的开发人员，当 Missy 联系他时，他向 Missy 解释了这种行为：“这不是错误。完成搜索需要一段时间。那里有很多东西要检查。”

Ken, the developer who operates out of London, explains the behavior to Missy when she contacts him: "This is not a bug. It just takes awhile to complete a search. There's a lot of stuff to check in there."

Missy 说，“让工作继续进行而不让用户知道不是一个好主意。几分钟后，用户可能会认为系统崩溃了。”

Missy says, "It's not a very good idea to have work proceeding and not let the user know. After a few minutes, the user may think the system has crashed."

Ken 回答说，“在黑屏的情况下编写一条消息来表明工作仍在进行，这会花费我很多时间。然后我不得不等待更多时间，可能要等到午餐后，才能获得新版本。我没有那种时候。”

Ken replies, "Programming a message to show that work is proceeding despite the blank screen would take me a lot of time. Then I'd have to wait more time, probably until after lunch, for the new build. I don't have that kind of time."

“但这很重要，”米西争辩道。“前几次我试过这个，我以为系统崩溃了。我试着敲了一些键，然后它确实崩溃了。”

"But it's important," Missy argues. "The first several times I tried this, I thought the system had crashed. I tried hitting some keys, and then it did crash."

“好吧，”肯说，“你和所有其他用户只需要学会耐心。你必须欣赏程序正在做的工作量。”

"Well," says Ken, "you and all the other users just have to learn to be patient. You have to appreciate the amount of work the program is doing."

在这里，不耐烦的开发人员将自己的不耐烦投射到所有用户身上，从而使自己不必承认自己在设计代码方面做得不够完美。

Here, the impatient developer projects his own impatience onto all users, thus defending himself from having to admit that he didn't do a perfect job designing the code.

该问题被关闭为“不是错误”。结果发现，随着系统的使用，输入的数据越来越多，延迟越来越长，没有明显的上限。您认为用户的耐心会增加以适应该应用程序吗？只有当用户比 Ken 更有耐心时，它才“不是错误”。

The issue was closed as "not a bug." It turned out that as the system was used and more and more data were entered, the delay grew longer and longer, with no apparent upper limit. Do you think the users' patience increased to accommodate the application? It's "not a bug" only if the users are more patient than Ken.

我们通过推卸责任来开脱自己。

We displace blame to absolve ourselves.

转移是指责某人或某事，这不是我们麻烦的真正根源，从而推卸我们自己的责任——例如，“我的铅笔坏了，所以我无法完成作业。” 位移在以下来自日本的测试故事中得到了生动的说明，测试人员将其报告为“使系统崩溃的三个步骤”：

Displacement is blaming someone or something that's not the real source of our troubles, thereby absolving ourselves of responsibility—for example, "my pencil broke, so I couldn't finish my homework." Displacement is vividly illustrated in the following testing story from Japan, reported by the tester as "three steps that crash a system":

1. 进入添加用户页面。

1. Go to the ADD USER page.

2. 继续添加用户，直到您尝试添加第 64 个用户。

2. Keep adding users until you try to add the sixty-fourth user.

3. 发现屏幕现在显示“内存不足”错误信息并且系统挂起，需要冷重启。

3. Discover that the screen now displays an "out of memory" error message and the system hangs, needing a cold restart.

在与测试人员联系后，开发人员说，“你只允许 63 个用户。这是出于性能原因，所以这实际上是一个帮助管理员远离麻烦的功能。”

Upon being contacted by the tester, the developer says, "You're only allowed sixty-three users. That's for performance reasons, so this is actually a feature that helps the administrator stay out of trouble."

测试人员说：“你不认为有比让系统崩溃更优雅的方式来避免管理员的麻烦吗？”

The tester says, "Don't you think there is a more gracious way to keep administrators out of trouble than by crashing the system?"

[到目前为止，开发人员的声明是合理化的，但随着他将防御策略转变为将责任推给用户，情况很快发生了转变。]

[Up to this point, the developer's statement has been a rationalization, but it quickly turns as he switches his defensive strategy to displacing the blame onto the users.]

开发人员回答说：“他们应该知道他们最多只能有 63 个用户。无论如何，在几次崩溃之后，他们就会学会。聪明的人学得很快，不会做导致系统崩溃的事情。”

The developer replies, "They should know they aren't allowed more than sixty-three users. Anyway, after a few crashes, they'll learn. Smart people learn fast not to do things that make the system crash."

从前面的故事来看，将责任归咎于用户尤其可笑，因为特定的用户列表没有编号，只能在一次显示三个半用户的固定窗口中看到。可能不太容易学习。

Putting the blame on the users is especially ludicrous when viewed in the light of the preceding story because the particular user list wasn't numbered and could only be seen in a fixed window that showed three-and-a-half users at a time. Probably not too easy to learn from.

无论如何，开发人员无法控制“聪明”的人会学到什么。也许用户会学会假设产品随时可能崩溃并丢失数据。也许他们会学会完全避免使用该产品。也许他们会了解使用竞争产品的优点。

In any case, developers can't control what "smart" people will learn. Perhaps users will learn to assume that the product could crash and lose data at any moment. Perhaps they will learn to avoid using this product at all. Perhaps they will learn the merits of working with a competing product.

以下是当开发人员面临测试人员无法接受的问题时我们听到的一些常见的位移投诉。首先，测试仪上有位移：

Following are some common displacement complaints we hear when a developer is faced with an unacceptable problem from a tester. First, there is displacement onto the tester:

• “如果你不能复制它，我也无能为力。”

• "If you can't reproduce it, I can't do anything about it."

• “你太挑剔了。”

• "You're being too picky."

如果没有明显的测试人员参与，开发人员可能会将责任和恐惧转移到其他开发人员身上：

If there's no obvious tester involved, a developer may displace blame and fear onto other developers:

• “这是他们的代码。” （“他们的”通常指第三方的软件，或者——也许更常见——由离开组织的程序员或开发人员编写的代码。）

• "It's their code." ("Their" often refers to a third party's software, or—perhaps even more often—to code written by a programmer or developer who has left the organization.)

• “这不是我的代码。” （有人应该受到指责，但肯定不是我。）

• "It's not my code." (Somebody out there is to blame, but certainly not me.)

开发人员也可能将责任和恐惧转移到他们的经理身上：

Developers may also displace blame and fear onto their managers:

• “他们认为新功能比工作功能更重要，所以我现在要加入新功能。”

• "They think new features are more important than working features, so I'm putting in new features now."

• “我要参加太多的管理会议，所以我没有时间。”

• "I have to go to too many management meetings, so I don't have time."

开发人员甚至可以将责任推到整个宇宙上：

Developers may even displace blame onto the universe at large:

• “这是系统的局限性。所有系统都有局限性。”

• "It's a limitation of the system. All systems have limitations."

• “这就是世界运作的方式。”

• "That's just the way the world works."

• “软件就是这样。”

• "Software is like that."

• “[基础结构组件] [操作系统] [网络] 不允许这样做。”

• "The [infrastructure component] [operating system] [network] doesn't allow that."

我们过度补偿了我们自我感知的缺陷。

We overcompensate for our self-perceived deficiencies.

过度补偿夸大了我们试图弥补某些真实或想象的个人缺陷的努力——例如，一个男人因为觉得自己不讨人喜欢而变成工作狂。以下是我从加拿大的一位客户那里得到的，讲述了过度补偿测试员 Avery 的故事：

Overcompensation is exaggerating our attempts to compensate for some real or imagined personal deficiency—for example, a man becomes a workaholic because he feels he's unlovable. The following came to me from a client in Canada and tells the story of Avery, an overcompensating tester:

Avery 测试了一个配置备份的管理工具。在创建他的测试用例时，他忘记包括测试 CD 备份的用例。当指出这一遗漏时，Avery 通过为 140 多种可能进行备份的不同硬件创建测试用例（包括几十年来未使用的纸带）来过度补偿。

Avery tested an administrative tool that configured backups. When creating his test cases, he forgot to include cases that tested backups to CDs. When this omission was pointed out, Avery overcompensated by creating test cases for more than 140 different pieces of hardware to which backups might be made—including paper tape, which hadn't been used in decades.

当我们感到失去控制时，我们就会变得强迫。

We become compulsive when we feel we're losing control.

强迫性无法背离适得其反的行为模式——例如，一个人无法允许对既定流程的微小偏差。我的一位英国客户的一个例子显示了强迫症的破坏性影响：

Compulsiveness is being unable to depart from a counterproductive behavior pattern—for example, a person is incapable of allowing small deviations from a defined process. An example from one of my British clients shows the damaging effects of compulsiveness:

开发人员 Valerie 找到了一种绕过配置管理系统在构建中插入补丁的方法。测试员 Nigel 在补丁中发现了一个错误，导致系统崩溃。

Valerie, a developer, finds a way to insert a patch in the build, bypassing the configuration management system. Nigel, the tester, finds a fault in the patch, which crashes the system.

Valerie 说，“这个问题不应该进入我们的跟踪系统。我从来没有把补丁放在配置管理系统中，所以这不是官方的错误。我只是在尝试一些东西。”

Valerie says, "The problem shouldn't be entered in our tracking system. I never put the patch in the configuration management system, so it's not an official bug. I was just trying something out."

Nigel 认识到 Valerie 的评论是一种合理化。他很快回答说：“是的，但我们的流程要求任何进入系统的东西都必须经过配置管理，以便进行跟踪。”

Nigel recognizes that Valerie's comment is a rationalization. He responds quickly, "Yes, but our process requires that anything that goes into the system must go through configuration management so it can be tracked."

瓦莱丽声音尖锐地回答，“好吧，下次我想尝试的时候，我不会给系统打补丁。要么我把它放在配置管理系统中，要么我在一个服务器上尝试一下。”我自己的系统。”

Valerie replies with an edge in her voice, "Okay, next time I want to try something out, I won't patch the system. Either I'll put it in the configuration management system, or I'll try it out on a system of my own."

“绝对不是，”奈杰尔坚持道。“不允许开发人员尝试。”

"Absolutely not," insists Nigel. "Developers are not allowed to try things out."

“那么为何不？” 要求瓦莱丽，皱着眉头。

"And why not?" demands Valerie, frowning.

“我已经查看了流程手册。里面没有任何内容允许尝试，”奈杰尔说，他感觉到自己正在失去控制，完美地说明了强迫防御。

"I've checked the process manual. There's nothing in it that permits trying things out," says Nigel, sensing that he is losing control, perfectly illustrating defense by compulsion.

奈杰尔害怕什么？当被问到时，他回答说，“如果我们开始破例，我将失去对这里发生的一切的控制。” 当然，他一开始真的无法控制，但他有一条规则，“我必须始终（感觉）处于控制之中。” 瓦莱丽的行为挑战了他的统治。

What's Nigel afraid of? When questioned, he replied, "If we start making exceptions, I'll lose control of everything that's going on here." Of course, he's really not in control in the first place, but he has a rule that says, "I must always be (feel) in control." Valerie's behavior challenges his rule.

如果我们想更深入地研究奈杰尔的心理，我们可能会发现他真正在做的是压抑和取代。或许他被瓦莱丽吸引了，但将这种感觉压抑为不合适，将其排除在他的意识之外。如此一来，也难怪每当她一出现，他就觉得自己可能会失控。为了保持控制，他通过在所有其他情况下将责任推给 Valerie 和所有其他开发人员来取代这种感觉。

If we want to delve deeper into Nigel's psyche, we might discover that what he's really doing is repressing and displacing. Perhaps he's attracted to Valerie, but represses the feeling as inappropriate, shutting it out of his conscious awareness. If this is the case, it's no wonder that whenever she comes around, he feels he might lose control of himself. To maintain control, he displaces that feeling by pushing blame onto Valerie and all the other developers in all other situations.

概括

Summary

信息是中性的，但人们对信息的反应很少是中性的。要评估测试信息，您必须考虑人们的情绪防御——压抑、合理化、投射、转移、过度补偿和强迫。通过保持警惕、周到和务实，您可以帮助消除情绪混乱并防止不合逻辑的过程破坏您的测试工作。

Information is neutral, but people's reactions to information are rarely neutral. To assess testing information, you must take into account people's emotional defenses—repression, rationalization, projection, displacement, overcompensation, and compulsiveness. By remaining vigilant, thoughtful, and pragmatic, you can help diffuse emotional chaos and prevent illogical processes from undermining your testing efforts.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.当人们害怕时没有注意到：如果你正在寻找防御机制，通常很容易发现它们。

1. Failing to notice when people are fearful: Defense mechanisms are usually easy to spot if you're looking for them.

2.营造令人恐惧的环境：如果你责怪信使带来了你不想听到的消息，你就会因为没有听到你应该听到的消息而得到回报。

2. Creating a fearful environment: If you blame messengers for bringing news you don't want to hear, you'll be rewarded by not hearing the news you should hear.

3.在做决定时让你的恐惧凌驾于事实之上：要在软件业务中取得成功，你需要了解你自己的规则以及它们如何扭曲你对信息的吸收。

3. Allowing your fears to override the facts when making decisions: To succeed in the software business, you need to be aware of your own rules and how they distort your intake of information.

4.做决定时让希望凌驾于事实之上：对任何事情都抱有希望是可以的，但希望与期待任何事情是不一样的。[8]

4. Allowing your hopes to override facts when making decisions: It's all right to hope for anything, but hoping is not the same as expecting anything. [8]

5.沉迷于强迫行为：一个人的强迫行为常常会引起他人的恐惧和防御。你的首要任务应该是努力做到合理。

5. Indulging in compulsive behavior: One person's compulsiveness frequently engenders fear and defensiveness in others. Your first priority should be to strive to be reasonable.

6.假设任何反对你自己观点的论点都是病态的一部分：就像合理化听起来像一个好的论证一样，一个好的论证听起来也像一个合理化。很多人都不愿意争论。许多人没有受过说服艺术方面的训练。学会同情地倾听反对意见和理由。尝试找到并尊重相反观点中有价值的东西——几乎总有值得重视的东西。例如，“解决这个问题太难了”的论点可能是说话者的表达方式，“我不知道如何快速或便宜地解决这个问题，而且我不相信这样做会是一个很好的使用方法我的时间。” 这可能确实是真的。也许值得一谈。

6. Assuming that any argument against your own point of view is part of a pathology: In the same way that a rationalization can sound like a good argument, a good argument can sound like a rationalization. Many people are uncomfortable making arguments. Many are untrained in the art of persuasion. Learn to listen sympathetically to objections and justifications. Try to find and honor what's worthwhile in an opposing viewpoint—there's almost always something there to value. For instance, the argument "It's too hard to fix that" might be the speaker's way of saying, "I don't know how to fix that quickly or cheaply, and I'm not convinced doing so would be a good way to use my time." This may indeed be true. Perhaps it's worth talking about.

7.彻底否认：测试顾问和作家 Pradeep Soundararajan 给我发了一个精彩的故事，说明一个人可以在多大程度上否认事实：在他工作的一家印度公司里，开发人员习惯说“按设计工作” ，或 WAD，拒绝错误。当他报告导致屏幕冻结的错误时，开发人员关闭了该错误，并将其标记为 WAD。至少可以说，他很惊讶。屏幕冻结成为产品设计的一部分是相当不寻常的。

7. Outright denial: The test consultant and writer Pradeep Soundararajan sent me a wonderful story illustrating how far a person can go in denying facts: At a company he worked for in India, the developers had a habit of saying "Works As Designed," or WAD, to reject a bug. When he reported a bug that caused a freeze of the screen, the developers closed the bug, marking it as WAD. He was surprised, to say the least. It's rather unusual for a screen freeze to be part of a product design.

他需要开发人员解释 WAD，并问道：“你是否非常了解设计或参考它？你能指点我那个设计文档吗？”

He needed the developers to explain WAD, asking, "Do you know the design so well or refer to it? Could you point me to that design document?"

一位开发人员回答说，“嗯，我不知道它在哪里，但我非常了解它，因为这是我加入这里后整整一个月都在阅读的内容。” （他加入已经一年多了。） “而且，”他继续说，“你是合同测试员，设计文件是机密的，所以我们不能给你看。”

A developer replied, "Well I don't know where it is, but I understand it very well because that's what I was reading for an entire month after I joined here." (It was more than a year since he had joined.) "Moreover," he continued, "you are a contract tester. Design documents are confidential, so we can't show it to you."

8.认为它不可能在这里发生：我特意从世界各地为本章选择了例子来表明这些防御是人类普遍的反应。它们可以发生在任何地方。

8. Thinking it can't happen here: I intentionally chose examples for this chapter from around the world to show that these defenses are universal human responses. They can happen anywhere.

第 7章如何应对防御性反应

Chapter_7_How to Deal With Defensive Reactions

 

“没有任何激情像恐惧那样有效地剥夺了头脑的所有行动和推理能力。” - Edmund Burke，英国政治家和演说家（1729-1797），对我们崇高和美丽观念起源的哲学探究，编。Adam Phillips（纽约：牛津大学出版社，1998 年）。

"No passion so effectually robs the mind of all its powers of acting and reasoning as fear." - Edmund Burke, British Statesman and Orator (1729–1797),A Philosophical Enquiry into the Origin of Our Ideas of the Sublime and Beautiful, ed. Adam Phillips (New York: Oxford University Press, 1998).

您不必成为心理学家也能更有效地处理使人们对重要信息免疫的防御反应。想象一下，您是我们的英国测试员 Nigel 的经理，您注意到他强迫性地执行规则。知道原因与您无关，而只是通过建立合理的规则和准则来纠正这种情况。也许 Nigel 会回应一条新的“规则”，即“未明确禁止的一切都是允许的”。

You don't have to be a psychologist to deal more effectively with defensive reactions that make people immune to important information. Imagine, for a moment, that you are our British tester Nigel's manager and you notice that he's being compulsive about enforcing rules. It's not your business to know why, but merely to correct the situation by establishing reasonable rules and guidelines. Perhaps Nigel will respond to a new "rule" that says, "Everything that's not explicitly forbidden is allowed."

不仅没有必要成为一名心理学家，玩一个也不是一个好主意。人们有时会产生防卫心理，尤其是当他们感到自己的防卫受到不公正的指责时。事实上，指责防御是一种试图将一个人对辩论的贡献边缘化的流行方式。不要玩那个游戏。它破坏了信息。

It's not only not necessary to be a psychologist, it's not a good idea to play one, either. People sometimes get defensive, especially when they feel unjustly accused of being defensive. In fact, accusation of defensiveness is a popular way to try to marginalize a person's contribution to a debate. Don't play that game. It destroys information.

无论如何，你怎么知道反应是防御性的？即使你是一名有执照的心理学家，你也不知道，但有一些启发式方法会有所帮助。例如，反应似乎与其表面原因不成比例吗？

In any case, how would you know that a reaction is defensive? Even if you were a licensed psychologist, you couldn't know, but there are some heuristics that help. For instance, does the reaction seem out of proportion to its ostensible cause?

最有用的启发式方法首先是不要将反应标记为防御性反应，然后将其视为防御性反应，看看它是否会屈服于温和的测试。

The most useful heuristic is first not to label the reaction as defensive, but then treat it as if it were and see if it yields to gentle tests.

识别恐惧。

Identify the fear.

从一开始，您就需要了解恐惧会引发防御反应——尽管您通常看不到潜在的恐惧。尽管如此，它就在那里。看看你是否能识别出一个人害怕什么，然后看看当你找到减少恐惧的方法时会发生什么。

From the outset, you need to understand that fear drives defensive reactions—although the underlying fear will generally not be visible to you. Nevertheless, it's there. See whether you can identify what a person fears, then see what happens when you find a way to reduce that fear.

与其他人一样，测试人员的防御可以使他们对不愉快的信息免疫。让我们看看我看到测试人员最常表达的辩护：“你不关心质量。” 假设在允许更改产品的最后一天下午晚些时候，我们在英国的测试员 Nigel 在 Valerie 的一个程序中的一条模糊错误消息中发现了一个语法错误。该消息可能仅在具有罕见型号的附加磁盘驱动器的配置中出现（估计只有不到万分之一的客户出现这种情况）。此外，只有当用户激活系统的一项功能时，才会出现该消息，而只有百分之一的用户可能需要。满足所有这些条件的用户将看到消息：输入字符串中有一个或多个错误。

Testers' defenses, like everyone else's, can immunize them to unpleasant information. Let's look at the defense I see testers evince most often: "You don't care about quality." Suppose it's late in the afternoon on the last day when product changes are allowed and Nigel, our tester in Britain, finds a grammatical error in an obscure error message in one of Valerie's programs. The message could occur only in configurations that have a rare model of attached disk drive (estimated to be the case for fewer than one customer in 10,000). Furthermore, the message could occur only if the user activates a feature of the system that only one percent of the users would ever be likely to need. A user who meets all these criteria would see the message: ONE OR MORE ERROR IN INPUT STRING.

当向 Valerie 指出问题时，她承认消息中受影响的部分应该是“ONE OR MORE ERRORS”而不是“ONE OR MORE ERROR”。Nigel 的经理建议他们将问题的严重性归类为“表面现象”，并指出不值得冒险在最后一刻进行更改。听到这个建议，奈杰尔勃然大怒，对他的经理大喊：“你不关心质量！” 如果你是 Nigel 的经理，你会怎么做？

When the problem is pointed out to Valerie, she acknowledges that the afflicted part of the message should have read "ONE OR MORE ERRORS" not "ONE OR MORE ERROR." Nigel's manager recommends that they classify the severity of the problem as "cosmetic," stating that it's not worth risking a last-minute change. At that recommendation, Nigel flares up, shouting at his manager "You don't care about quality!" If you were Nigel's manager, what would you do?

使用批判性思维。

Use critical thinking.

这是批判性思维和测试相遇的众多领域之一。一些辩护——在批判性思维的意义上——是无效的论点。例如，这就是逻辑学家所说的人身攻击（针对人）。但如果奈杰尔没有通过逻辑得出这种辩护，那么再多的逻辑也无法说服他放弃它。因此，在这种情况下使用逻辑的有用方法是找出奈杰尔的论点是否基于逻辑。

This is one of many areas where critical thinking and testing meet. Some defenses—in the critical thinking sense of the word—are invalid arguments. This one, for example, is what logicians call an ad hominem (at the person) attack. But if Nigel didn't arrive at this defense through logic, then no amount of logic is going to persuade him to drop it. Therefore, the helpful way to use logic in such a situation is to find out if Nigel's argument is based on logic or not.

Nigel 的经理与其善意回应并愤怒地告诉 Nigel 去远足，这非常不英式，不如问：“你所说的质量是什么意思？” 如果 Nigel 同意本书对质量的定义——对某些人的价值——他的经理可以问他“如果我们不在今天的版本中修复这个错误，对什么人来说会失去什么价值？”可以澄清这一点。在 Nigel 的回答中，他的经理可以很快发现 Nigel 的论点是基于逻辑还是纯粹的恐惧。

Rather than responding in kind and angrily telling Nigel to take a hike, which would be very un-British, Nigel's manager could ask, "What do you mean by quality?" If Nigel agrees with this book's definition of quality—value to some person—the point could be clarified by his manager asking him, "What value will be lost to what person if we don't fix this error in today's release?" In Nigel's answer, his manager could quickly discover whether Nigel bases his argument on logic or pure and simple fear.

例如，如果 Nigel 没有对他的经理提出的完全合乎逻辑和合理的问题作出合乎逻辑的回答，我们可能会得出结论，Nigel 的动机是产品质量以外的因素。也许奈杰尔确实喜欢瓦莱丽，正在找借口和她一起工作到很晚。或者，也许他曾经因为没有使用复数而被老师打过指关节。不管怎样，没关系。这不关任何人的事（除非奈杰尔以歧视或非法的方式行事，例如骚扰同事，而这种行为确实成为人员和法律顾问的事）。

For instance, if Nigel does not respond logically to his manager's perfectly logical and reasonable question, we might conclude that Nigel is motivated by factors other than the quality of the product. Perhaps Nigel does have a crush on Valerie and is looking for an excuse to work late with her. Or perhaps he was once hit on the knuckles by his teacher for not using a plural. Whatever the case, it doesn't matter. It's nobody's business (unless Nigel has behaved in ways that are discriminatory or illegal, such as harassing coworkers, when such behavior does become the business of personnel and legal advisors).

作为经理，您的职责是及时运送有价值的产品。因此，您向奈杰尔指出，只有不到百万分之一的客户可能会受到此错误的影响，而且即使受到影响，也不太可能因此而受到困扰。您将这种价值损失与如果在深夜的最后一刻修复此错误会导致另一个问题而导致每个客户都可能受到影响的可能性进行对比。然后您继续将错误归类为“表面错误 — 在此版本中不予更正”。

What is your business as manager is shipping a valuable product in a timely manner. So, you point out to Nigel that fewer than one customer in a million can possibly be affected by this mistake, and, if affected, is unlikely to be troubled by it. You contrast this loss of value with the chance that every customer might be affected if fixing this mistake at the last minute, late in the night, results in another problem. And then you go ahead and classify the mistake as "cosmetic—not to be corrected in this release."

如果奈杰尔在几天或几周后继续反对，你就会知道发生了其他事情，对他来说是可怕的事情。观察模式，最终你可能会发现恐惧的根本原因。如果不是，你最终会决定奈杰尔是否值得他不断和强迫性的责备。然后你相​​应地行动。

If Nigel keeps on objecting, days and weeks later, you know that something else is going on, something fearful—to him. Watch for patterns, and eventually you may uncover the root cause of fear. If not, you'll eventually decide whether or not Nigel is worth the bother of his constant and compulsive blaming. Then you act accordingly.

练习，练习，再练习。

Practice, practice, practice.

通过足够的练习，您会更好地识别防御反应并处理它们。其中一些非常常见，您会反复听到它们，例如，

With sufficient practice, you'll grow much better at recognizing defensive reactions and dealing with them. Some of them are so common that you'll hear them repeatedly, such as,

“这是为了用户自己的利益。”

"It's for the user's own good."

“它按照我设计的方式工作。”

"It works the way I designed it."

“它太 [冒险] [昂贵] [难以] 修复。”

"It's too [risky] [costly] [hard] to fix."

“没有人会[注意到][关心]。”

"No one will [notice] [care]."

“有一个解决方法。”

"There's a workaround."

使这些防御有效的原因是它们中的每一个都有一些真实性，在某些情况下它们可能是理性的，而不是合理化。如果他们没有那种理性的萌芽，他们很容易被免除，就像当测试人员对我尖叫时，“你怎么可能知道这个？你从来没有测试过汇编语言程序。”

What makes these defenses effective is that there's some truth in each of them, some circumstances in which they might be rational, not rationalizations. If they didn't have that germ of rationality, they'd be easy to dispense with, as when a tester screamed at me, "What could you possibly know about this? You've never tested assembly-language programs."

考虑到我在这个尖叫者诞生 25 年前首次编写和测试汇编语言程序这一事实，我很容易将这种防御反应确定为不是由逻辑或现实引起的。

Considering the fact that I first wrote and tested assembly language programs twenty-five years before this screamer was born, it was rather easy for me to identify this defensive reaction as not arising from logic or reality.

测试自己。

Test yourself.

当你读完本章关于管理防御反应的内容时，试着测试一下自己。当疯狂的汇编语言测试员冲着我尖叫时，如果你处在我的位置，你会如何回应？或者，练习您将如何应对一位顾问同事向我描述的以下情况：

As you finish reading this chapter on managing defensive reactions, try testing yourself. If you had been in my place when the mad assembly-language tester screamed at me, how would you have responded? Or, practice on how you would respond to the following situation described to me by a fellow consultant:

测试：

Test:

1. 将虚拟内存降低到运行操作系统所需的最小值。

1. Lower the virtual memory to the minimum needed to run the OS.

2. 在应用程序中启动文档。

2. Launch a document in the application.

3. 编辑文档。

3. Edit the document.

4. 保存文件。

4. Save the document.

结果：

Result:

5. 崩溃，需要重启整个系统。

5. Crash, requiring reboot of the entire system.

当收到错误报告时，开发人员用力摇头回应，“哦。那不是错误。”

When given the bug report, the developer responded, shaking his head vigorously, "Oh. That's not a bug."

“‘这不是错误’是什么意思？它崩溃了。”

"What do you mean 'that's not a bug'? It crashes."

“看，”开发商耸了耸肩。“它可能会崩溃，也可能会损坏您的数据。随您选择。”

"Look," shrugged the developer. "It can crash or it can corrupt your data. Take your pick."

这是我们称之为“情况可能更糟”的常见防御反应。而且，是的，情况可能会更糟。这可能是您组织中最好的开发人员。

This is the common defensive reaction we call "It could be worse." And, yes, it could be worse. This might be the best developer in your organization.

概括

Summary

如果你开始得当并保持警惕、深思熟虑和积极主动，你就可以防止情绪混乱主导你的测试工作。

If you start out properly and remain vigilant, thoughtful, and proactive, you can prevent emotional chaos from dominating your testing effort.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.不考虑差异：每个人都有规则。当他们的规则受到威胁时，每个人都会感到恐惧。但规则不同，反应也不同。你必须平等对待每个人，但不一定以同样的方式。

1. Failing to take differences into account: Everybody has rules. Everybody has fears when their rules are threatened. But the rules are different, and so are the reactions. You must treat everyone equally, but not necessarily in the same way.

2.告诉人们他们不关心质量：几乎每个人都关心质量，尽管他们可能不了解如何生产质量。或者，他们可能知道如何生产符合他们的质量概念但不符合您的质量的质量。不要侮辱他们；教他们。尤其要告诉他们，不同的人可能对质量有不同的、有效的看法，并告诉他们在这种特定情况下哪些看法很重要。

2. Telling people they don't care about quality: Pretty much everybody cares about quality, although they may not understand how to produce it. Or, they may know how to produce quality that's consistent with their notion of quality, but not with yours. Don't insult them; teach them. In particular, teach them that different people can have different, valid perceptions of quality— and teach them which perceptions count in this particular situation.

3.把你的大脑留在外面：如果你认为你处在这样一种紧急情况下，你不能考虑错误，你最好现在就退出。

3. Leaving your brain outside: If you believe that you're in such an emergency that you can't afford to think about errors, you might as well quit right now.

4.对自己过分挑剔：需要练习才能学会识别并有效应对防御性反应。如果您犯了一些错误，请放松一下。

4. Being overcritical of yourself: It takes practice to learn to recognize and deal effectively with defensive reactions. Cut yourself a little slack if you make some mistakes.

5.不要批评自己：如果你是一名经理，你的工作就是处理人们影响他们工作的反应。如果你没有提高这项技能，那么你就没有做好你的工作。什么阻碍了你？

5. Not being critical of yourself: If you are a manager, it's your job to deal with people's reactions that interfere with their doing their job. If you're not improving at this skill, then you're not doing your job. What's getting in your way?

Chapter_8_什么是好的测试？

Chapter_8_What Makes a Good Test?

 

“没有好坏之分，是思想使然。” - 威廉·莎士比亚，英国剧作家和诗人（1564-1616 年），《哈姆雷特》，第 2 幕，第 2 场。

"There is nothing either good or bad, but thinking makes it so." - William Shakespeare, English Dramatist and Poet (1564–1616), Hamlet, Act 2, Scene 2.

什么是好的测试？这个问题可以在高度技术层面上得到回答，但这不是我们的目标。事实上，从那场辩论中退后一步，从管理的角度来看这个问题是有帮助的。你怎么知道测试是否做得好？您对测试结果的信任度有多少？

What makes a good test? The question can be answered at a highly technical level, but that's not our goal here. In fact, it's helpful to step back from that debate and look at the question from a management point of view. How can you know if testing is being done well? How much credence can you put in test results?

你永远无法确定。

You can never know for sure.

你可能同意也可能不同意哈姆雷特的观点，即没有好坏之分。不过，为了争论起见，让我们假设存在一个“好”测试这样的东西，然后问这个问题，一个人如何知道一个特定的测试（或一组测试）是否确实是好的？让我们从比“好”更好的东西开始，看看“完美”的定义。一套完美的测试应具有以下特征：

You may or may not agree with Hamlet that there is nothing either good or bad.
