For the sake of argument, though, let's suppose there is such a thing as a "good" test and ask the question, How can one know whether a particular test (or set of tests) is, indeed, good? Let's start with something even better than "good" by looking at a definition of "perfect." A perfect set of tests would have the following characteristics:

A。它会检测系统中的每个错误。

a. It would detect every bug in a system.

b. 它永远不会将非错误检测为错误。

b. It would never detect a non-bug as a bug.

C。它会让我们完全相信它已经完成了 a 和 b。

c. It would give us complete confidence that it has done a and b.

d. 它可以快速、廉价地完成 a、b 和 c，以满足我们的需要。

d. It would accomplish a, b, and c quickly and cheaply enough for our needs.

现在考虑一个被测系统。在最简单的情况下，如果该系统完全没有错误（这种情况可能只存在于我们的梦想中），那么任何未发现错误的测试都满足条件a。一些我们认为非常糟糕的测试也可以满足该条件，但是当针对无错误、完美的系统运行时，它们看起来会很不错。

Now consider a system under test. In the simplest case, if that system were perfectly bug free (a situation likely to exist only in our dreams), then any test that finds no bugs meets condition a. Some tests that we would consider really lousy could meet that condition as well, but when run against a bug-free, perfect system, they would look pretty good.

或者他们会吗？我们事先不知道我们是在测试一个没有错误的系统还是一个有缺陷的系统。（如果我们这样做了，为什么我们需要测试？）所以，想象一下两组测试：完美的测试和糟糕的测试。当针对我们的无错误、完美的系统运行时，两组测试都没有发现任何错误。因此，仅根据他们发现的错误，我们无法区分完美测试和糟糕测试。

Or would they? We don't know in advance whether we're testing a bug-free system or a louse-y system. (If we did, why would we need to test?) So, imagine two sets of tests: perfect tests and lousy tests. When run against our bug-free, perfect system, both sets of tests reveal no bugs. So, on the basis of their bugfinding alone, we couldn't tell the difference between a perfect test and a lousy test.

事实上，对于一个系统的一个实现来说可能是一个充分的测试对于同一系统的另一个实现可能是一个糟糕的测试。换句话说，“goodness”不能是测试的属性，而只是测试和实现之间关系的属性。

In fact, what might be an adequate test for one implementation of a system might be a lousy test for another implementation of the same system. In other words, "goodness" cannot be a property of a test, but only a property of the relationship between a test and an implementation.

更进一步，相同实施的相同测试可能对一个组织来说足够了，但对另一个组织来说就很糟糕了。例如，如果同一实施作为软件产品出售给一千个组织，则足以让单个组织在内部使用的系统的测试可能完全不够。换句话说，“好”不能是测试和实现的属性，而只是测试、实现和情境之间关系的属性。

Going one step further, the same test of the same implementation might be adequate for one organization but lousy for another. For example, a test that is adequate for a system to be used internally by a single organization might be totally inadequate if the same implementation were sold as a software product to a thousand organizations. In other words, "goodness" cannot be a property of tests and implementations, but only a property of the relationship among tests, implementations, and situations.

因此，您永远无法确定，也永远无法通过孤立地查看测试来判断测试是否好——但您确实有很多方法可以判断测试是否可能不好。元测试起着重要作用。随后，在第 9 章中，我们检查了一些“坏”测试的指标。

So, you can never tell for sure, and you never can tell by looking at a test in isolation, whether a test is good—but you do have many ways to tell whether a test is likely to be bad. Meta-tests play an important role. Later, in Chapter 9, we examine some indicators of "bad" tests.

你只能在事后评估好坏。

You can assess goodness only after the fact.

如果您知道系统中有多少错误，您至少可以开始评估一组测试的优劣。例如，在一个系统使用了几年之后，一个谨慎的管理者会统计出该系统有多少缺陷。通过跟踪使用中出现的错误，然后分析它们以查看它们是什么样的，您至少会获得某些类型的信息，例如，

If you knew how many bugs were in a system, you could at least begin to assess the goodness, or not-badness, of a set of tests. For instance, after a system has been in use for a few years, a prudent manager will have statistics on how many bugs were shipped with the system. By keeping track of what bugs turn up in use, then analyzing them to see what they're like, you will have at least some kinds of information, such as,

• 您的测试典型地遗漏了多少错误

• how many bugs your testing characteristically missed

• 您的测试典型地遗漏了哪些错误类型

• what kinds of bugs your testing characteristically missed

了解这些信息可以让您在未来做出更好的估计，即使您不改进您的测试过程。此类信息也可能用于改进开发过程——尽管在这方面，很可能我又在做梦了。不幸的是，您永远无法确定交付了多少错误，因为错误可能会在多年后出现在产品中，或者永远不会出现。

Knowing such information allows you to make better estimates in the future, even if you don't improve your testing process. Such information may also be used to improve the development process—although in this regard, most likely I'm dreaming again. Unfortunately, you never know for sure how many bugs were shipped because bugs can turn up in a product many, many years later, or never.

在我撰写《计算机程序设计心理学》 30 年后，这本书已售出 200,000 多册后，我收到一封信，其中记录了一个从未有人向我指出过的“明显”错误。这是对作者谦逊的有益教训，但它也表明，类似的“明显”错误可能会在产品中潜伏很长时间——尤其是当产品是软件时。软件甚至可能存在系统出厂时不是错误的错误，例如当应用程序与新硬件或新操作系统一起使用时功能失败。

Thirty years after I wrote The Psychology of Computer Programming, and after more than 200,000 copies of the published book had been sold, I received a letter documenting an "obvious" error that nobody else has ever pointed out to me. That was a useful lesson in author humility, but it also suggests that similar "obvious" errors can remain dormant in products— especially when the product is software—for a very long time. Software may even have bugs that were not bugs when the system shipped, such as functions that fail when an application is used with new hardware or a new operating system.

此外，如果您等待五年来评估一组测试的优劣，那么这些信息有什么用呢？你的测试人员，如果他们还在，可能现在使用不同的工具和技术。您可能没有原始源代码或错误报告，或者您可能拥有它们但无法阅读或理解它们。但是如果你只等六个月或一年，并保持良好的记录，你就可以及时评估一组测试的质量，以便评估有助于改进未来的测试。

Moreover, if you wait five years to assess the goodness of a set of tests, what good is the information? Your testers, if they're still around, probably now use different tools and techniques. You may not have the original source code or bug reports, or you may have them and be unable to read or understand them. But if you wait only six months or a year, and keep good records, you may be able to assess the quality of a set of tests in time for the assessment to be useful in improving future tests.

你能比简单地等待经验做得更好吗？你可以根据你的失败理论回顾你的报道和你的预言。您可以随机或任意地改变您的测试，并注意问题是如何出现的。您可以并行比较不同类型的测试，例如与内部测试相比的 Beta 测试，或与动态测试相比的评论。

Can you do better than simply waiting for experience? You can review your coverage and your oracles against your theories of failure. You can vary your tests randomly or arbitrarily and notice how problems emerge. You can compare different kinds of testing in parallel, such as beta testing compared to internal testing, or reviews compared to dynamic testing.

您可能想故意插入错误。

You may want to insert bugs intentionally.

有时，您可以通过播种（或“调试”，我相信我在计算机编程心理学中创造并写下了这个术语）来定量估计软件中可能存在多少问题。在不告诉测试人员的情况下插入已知错误，然后根据他们发现的已知错误的百分比来估计剩余的未知错误的数量。

Sometimes, you can gain quantitative estimates of how many problems might remain in software by seeding (or "bebugging," a term I believe I coined—and wrote about—in The Psychology of Computer Programming). Insert known bugs without telling the testers, then estimate the number of remaining unknown bugs by the percentage of known bugs they find.

为了使调试完全合理地工作，插入错误的分布必须与未知错误的（未知）分布紧密匹配。我学会做的是留下（但秘密地记录）自然产生但已被开发人员发现的错误，也许是在代码审查中，也许是在单元测试中。这使错误具有自然性，但当然不一定是未发现错误的可靠样本。尽管如此，如果未发现某些已知错误，这种做法仍会提供一些信息。不过要小心——即使找到了所有已知的错误，它也不会提供大量可靠的信息。

For bebugging to work at all reasonably, the distribution of inserted bugs must closely match the (unknown) distribution of the unknown bugs. What I learned to do was leave (but document secretly) bugs that were made naturally but had been found by the developers, perhaps in code reviews, perhaps in unit testing. This gives the bugs a naturalness, but of course isn't necessarily a reliable sample of not-found bugs. Still, the practice provides some information if some known bugs aren't found. Be careful, though—it doesn't give a great deal of reliable information even if all the known bugs are found.

善的估计总是统计的。

Estimates of goodness are always statistical.

不过，归根结底，对善的估计只是一个估计。我们只能从统计上估计好坏，因为我们永远无法确定给定系统中现在或曾经有多少错误。系统中实际存在的错误越少，统计数据就越有利于我们。例如，如果有 10 个错误，则 50% 的错误意味着我们可能会减少 5 个错误，但对于 14,000 个错误，我们可能会减少 7,000 个。

In the end, though, an estimate of goodness is just that—an estimate. We can only estimate goodness statistically, because we can never know for sure how many bugs are, or were, in a given system. The fewer bugs there actually are in a system, the more the statistics are in our favor. For example, if there are ten bugs, a 50- percent error means we might be off by five bugs, but for 14,000 bugs, we might be off by 7,000.

为了使您的测试人员看起来不错，您可能希望在他们可以合理管理的情况下尽可能少地进行测试。作为一个额外的好处，测试人员可以自由地寻找困难的错误，如果他们不花时间寻找简单的错误——应该在单元测试期间消除的噪音。不幸的是，许多经理根据他们发现的错误数量来判断测试人员，这意味着质量差的系统会让测试人员看起来更好。如果他们正在测试一个完美的系统，他们永远不会发现任何错误，并且可能会因为无能而被解雇。在这样的衡量体系下，糟糕的开发人员是测试人员最好的朋友。

To make your testers look good, you may want to come into test with as few bugs as they can reasonably manage. As an added benefit, testers are free to look for the difficult bugs if they aren't spending time finding the easy ones—noise that should have been removed during unit testing. Unfortunately, many managers judge testers by how many bugs they find, which means that poor quality systems make testers look better. If they were testing a perfect system, they'd never find any bugs, and probably would be fired as incompetent. Under such a system of measurement, a lousy developer is a tester's best friend.

那么，为什么这个有缺陷的系统如此受欢迎呢？原因之一是测试人员没有努力解释他们如何寻找错误以及为什么他们的策略应该受到尊重。另一个原因是，当经理和开发人员假设产品有效时，告诉他们它有效似乎没有提供任何信息。也就是说，“没有信息”似乎等于“没有价值”。这与人们不更换烟雾报警器电池的原因相同——大多数时候，一个不起作用的烟雾报警器在行为上与一个工作的烟雾报警器没有区别。可悲的是，最常见的提醒更换电池的是火灾。

Why, then, is this flawed system so popular? One reason is the testers' lack of effort to explain how they look for bugs and why their strategy should inspire respect. Another reason is that when managers and developers assume that a product works, telling them it works seems to provide no information. That is, "no information" seems to equal "no value." It's the same reason why people don't replace the batteries in their smoke alarms—most of the time, a nonfunctioning smoke alarm is behaviorally indistinguishable from one that works. Sadly, the most common reminder to replace the batteries is a fire.

你可以估计不坏。

You can estimate not-badness.

在最深的技术层面上，测试涉及一些相当深奥的数学和逻辑。为了评估这些深奥的活动是否做得好，大多数管理者必须依赖独立专家的第二和第三意见。然而，大多数管理者可以通过回答以下类型的问题来做出许多对“不错”的评估：

At its deepest technical level, testing involves some rather esoteric mathematics and logic. To assess whether these esoteric activities have been done well, most managers must rely on second and third opinions from independent experts. There are, however, many assessments of not-badness most managers can make themselves by answering the following kinds of questions:

•测试是否旨在为我提供我想要的信息？如果没有，那显然不好。

• Does testing purport to give me the information I'm after? If it doesn't, it's obviously not good.

•是否记录在案？如果没有，您是否亲自观察过测试，或者它是由您信任的人观察、报告或执行的？

• Is it documented? If not, have you personally observed the testing, or is it observed, reported, or performed by someone you trust?

•诚实吗？可以通过多种方式有意或无意地捏造测试文档。

• Is it honest? There are numerous ways test documentation can be fudged, intentionally or unintentionally.

•我能看懂吗？如果你不能，你怎么可能知道它是好是坏？

• Can I understand it? If you can't, how can you possibly know whether it's good or bad?

•它是否至少涵盖了最重要的内容？您通常无法测试每条路径（记住不可能进行详尽测试），但至少，一组测试应该访问每行代码一次。

• Does it at least cover what matters most? You can't generally test every path (remember the impossibility of exhaustive testing), but at the very least, a set of tests should visit each line of code once.

•它真的完成了吗？任何人都可以在测试计划上打勾。你有办法知道实际做了什么吗？

• Is it actually finished? Anyone can check a box on a test plan. Do you have ways of knowing what was actually done?

•我能区分测试和演示吗？演示旨在使系统看起来不错。测试的设计应该使它看起来像它真实的样子。

• Can I tell the difference between a test and a demonstration? Demonstrations are designed to make a system look good. Tests should be designed to make it look the way it truly is.

•趋势和状态报告是否过于简单和规律？在实际项目中，测试和测试活动有多种规模和形式。如果测试状态报告显示出非常可预测的趋势，则测试可能很肤浅，或者报告可能遗漏了一些重要的东西。

• Are trends and status reports overly simplistic and regular? In real projects, tests and test activities come in many sizes and shapes. If test status reports show extremely predictable trends, testing may be shallow or the reports may be leaving out something important.

•不同类型的测试活动之间是否存在不一致？例如，如果 Beta 测试人员发现了内部测试团队没有发现的错误，或者如果性能测试发现了功能性错误，这可能表明一个或另一个过程运行不正常。

• Are there inconsistencies between different kinds of test activities? For instance, if beta testers find bugs that the internal test team doesn't find, or if performance testing finds functional bugs, that may be a sign that one or the other process is not working well.

•经理可见吗？他们不应该挂在人们的肩膀上，但通常可以通过以关注着称的好奇经理的存在来改进测试。

• Are managers visible? They shouldn't hang over people's shoulders, but often testing can be improved simply by the presence of a curious manager who is known for paying attention.

不幸的是，许多谬误和伪造会扭曲测试，导致测试变坏。管理人员需要了解并防范它们，可以通过应用接下来几章中详述的方法来实现。

Unfortunately, many fallacies and falsifications can distort tests, causing testing to turn sour. Managers need to understand and guard against them, possibly by applying methods detailed in the next several chapters.

概括

Summary

您永远无法确定您的测试是否做得好，但是有很多方法可以知道或估计它是否做得不好。

You'll never know for sure whether your testing was done well, but there are many ways to know or estimate if it was done badly.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.不考虑你在寻找什么信息：当你考虑你在寻找什么时，测试就已经够困难了，而如果你不考虑它，或多或少是不可能的。您通常不会事先知道您要寻找什么信息——事实上，在大多数情况下，您只会有一个大概的想法。因此，您需要考虑您的最终测试目标以及您将如何了解您需要的其他信息。

1. Not thinking about what information you're after: Testing is difficult enough when you do think about what you're after, and more or less impossible when you don't. You won't often know in advance what information you seek—in fact, in most instances, you'll have only an approximate idea. So, you need to think about your ultimate testing goals and about how you're going to learn what other information you're going to want.

2.通过发现多少错误来衡量测试人员：测试人员会对这种衡量方式做出反应，但可能不是您希望他们做出的方式。发现的错误数量会增加，但收集到的信息质量会降低。

2. Measuring testers by how many bugs they find: Testers will respond to this kind of measurement, but probably not the way you intend them to. The quantity of bugs found will increase, but the quality of information harvested will diminish.

3.相信你可以确定测试的好坏：在评估测试的准确性和适当性时要保持警惕和怀疑。如果你不这样做，你就会被宇宙的本性打倒，这不利于完美主义。

3. Believing you can know for sure how good a test is: Be vigilant and skeptical when evaluating the accuracy and appropriateness of a test. If you aren't, you're going to get slapped down by the nature of the universe, which doesn't favor perfectionism.

4.没有考虑背景：几乎没有（如果有的话）在所有情况下都同样重要的测试。如果您不考虑潜在的使用模式，您的测试将是无效的。

4. Failing to take context into account: There are few, if any, tests that are equally significant in all circumstances. If you don't take potential usage patterns into account, your tests will be ineffectual.

5.在不了解产品内部结构的情况下进行测试：有无数种方法可以在有限系列测试中复制特定行为。了解您正在测试的软件的结构可以帮助您识别特殊情况、微妙的功能和要尝试的重要范围——所有这些都有助于缩小软件可以做什么和实际使用期间将做什么之间的推理差距. 第一台计算机的制造者查尔斯·巴贝奇 (Charles Babbage) 在将近 200 年前就知道这一点，所以您没有理由不知道。

5. Testing without knowledge of the product's internal structure: There are an infinite number of ways to replicate specific behavior on a finite series of tests. Knowing about the structure of the software you're testing can help you to identify special cases, subtle features, and important ranges to try—all of which help narrow the inference gap between what the software can do and what it will do during actual use. Charles Babbage, the maker of the very first computer, knew this almost 200 years ago, so there's no reason for you not to know it.

6.在对产品内部结构了解太多的情况下进行测试：很容易考虑到你认为你知道黑匣子内部发生的事情。普通用户可能不会知道足够多的知识来做到这一点，因此您的一些测试最好模拟可能由天真的用户执行的活动。

6. Testing with too much knowledge of the product's internal structure: It's too easy to make allowances for what you think you know is going on inside the black box. Typical users probably won't know enough to do that, so some of your tests had better simulate activities likely to be performed by naive users.

7.给出错误的统计估计，就好像数字是固定的，某些数字：在陈述估计的错误数量时总是给出一个范围（例如，说，“这个版本中有三十到四十个错误。 ”）。更好的是，给出统计分布或图表。

7. Giving statistical estimates of bugs as if the numbers were fixed, certain numbers: Always give a range when stating the estimated number of bugs (for example, say, "There are somewhere in the range of thirty to forty bugs in this release."). Even better, give a statistical distribution, or a graph.

8.未能在测试中应用“坏”的衡量标准：使用清单，提出本章中的问题。

8. Failing to apply measures of "badness" to your tests: Use a checklist, asking questions such as the ones in this chapter.

9.不确保开发完成：开发不良的代码需要良好的测试，但通常会收到不良的测试，从而使问题复杂化。伪代码的良好测试有什么用？

9. Not ensuring that development is done well: Poorly developed code needs good testing but usually receives poor testing, thus compounding problems. What use are good tests of shoddy code?

10.不考虑大量发现的错误导致的测试效率损失：一个“完美”的测试会话是一个完全致力于测试设计和执行的会话（这是例外，而不是规则）。设置、错误调查和报告会占用测试设计和执行时间。发现大量错误可能会让测试人员看起来不错，但发现大量错误会减慢测试速度，减少覆盖范围，或两者兼而有之。

10. Not considering the loss of testing efficiency caused by numerous found bugs: A "perfect" testing session is one entirely dedicated to test design and execution (this is the exception, not the rule). Set-up, bug investigation, and reporting take time away from test design and execution. Finding lots of bugs might make testers look good, but finding lots of bugs slows down testing, reduces coverage, or both.

第 9 章_关于测试的主要谬误

Chapter_9_Major Fallacies About Testing

 

“专家是在扫除大谬误的同时避免小错误的人。” - Benjamin Stolberg，作家和公众人物（1914-1951），引用自 Ralph Woods，The Modern Handbook of Humor for Speakers, Writers, Business and Professional Men and for All Who Enjoy Sharing Humor with Others （纽约：McGraw-Hill， 1967 年），第 14 页。

"An expert is a person who avoids small error as he sweeps on to the grand fallacy." - Benjamin Stolberg, Writer and Public Figure (1914–1951), as quoted in Ralph Woods, The Modern Handbook of Humor for Speakers, Writers, Business and Professional Men and for All Who Enjoy Sharing Humor with Others (NewYork: McGraw-Hill,1967), p.14.

可能有无数种糟糕的测试方式，但有一些非常错误的思维方式可以毁掉任何测试项目。让我们通过观察一些实际的谬误来开始探索为什么会出现糟糕的测试。

There may be an infinite number of ways of doing testing badly, but there are a few very fallacious ways of thinking that can ruin any testing project. Let's start our exploration of why bad testing occurs by looking at some fallacies in action.

指责谬误

The Blaming Fallacy

Able Corporation 的项目经理 Kahn 坐在椅子上叹了口气。日子过得并不顺利，他心情不好。早上第一件事就是在他走进大楼的路上，首席推销员伦道夫 (Randolph) 大声告诉他一些愤怒的顾客。午餐时，卡恩的老板非常有礼貌地责备他说公司因质量问题损失了一笔巨额销售额。为什么她不直截了当地说出她的想法呢？卡恩想。客气的吐槽还是吐槽，要是能切中要害，就快结束了！

Kahn, a project manager at Able Corporation, sinks into his chair and sighs. The day has not gone well, and he is in a foul mood. It started on his way into the building first thing in the morning when Randolph, the top salesman, gave him an earful about some irate customers. Over lunch, Kahn's boss ever so politely chewed him out about a huge sale the company lost due to quality issues. Why doesn't she just come right out and say what's on her mind? Kahn thinks. A polite chewing out is still a chewing out, and if she could just get to the point, it would be over faster!

Kahn 的老板和 Randolph 似乎认为，如果他们将矛头指向责备并用责备的语气和音量说话，问题就会更快、更有效、更高效地得到解决。他们订阅了 The Blaming Fallacy。

Kahn's boss and Randolph seem to think that if they point the finger of blame and speak using a blaming tone and volume, problems will get solved more quickly, effectively, and efficiently. They subscribe to The Blaming Fallacy.

事实上，通常情况恰恰相反：某人花费越多的时间和精力来寻找其他人来解决问题，解决问题的机会就越小。指责谬误的后果很常见：卡恩会把责任推给他看到的第一个脆弱的人。在这种情况下，那个人是他的新测试经理 Rose，他刚刚敲了敲他办公室的门。“你想见我？”

In fact, the opposite is generally true: The more time and effort someone spends looking for someone else to blame for a problem, the less the chance of solving the problem. Fallout from The Blaming Fallacy is quite common: Kahn will pass the blame on to the first vulnerable person he sees. In this case, that person is Rose, his new test manager, who just now knocks on his office door. "You want to see me?"

“罗斯！很好！你收到了我的语音信箱。” 卡恩将自己从沉思中拉出来，开始评估他的新测试经理。一旦我闯入，她就会没事的，他告诉自己。“进来，”卡恩说。“你需要对你所在部门的测试做点什么。”

"Rose! Good! You got my voicemail." Kahn pulls himself out of his reverie and assesses his new test manager. She'll be okay once I break her in, he tells himself. "Come in," Kahn says. "You need to do something about your department's testing."

罗斯在会议桌旁就座，就在大约六周前，他们曾讨论过她的工作职责和测试时间表。“这是怎么回事？” 她问。罗斯对这种责备的环境还很陌生，但她已经学会了不要让自己被吓倒。

Rose takes a seat at the conference table where just about six weeks earlier they had discussed her employment duties and the testing schedules. "What's up?" she asks. Rose is new to this blaming environment, but she's already learning not to allow herself to be intimidated.

“你们部门的检测不够好，就是这样。” 卡恩拿出当天早上早些时候技术支持代表推给他的客户现场报告。他把它推到桌子对面的罗斯面前。“你来这里已经六个多星期了。为什么你对此没有采取任何行动？”

"Your department's testing isn't good enough, that's what." Kahn pulls out the customer-site report a tech support rep had shoved at him earlier that morning. He pushes it across the table to Rose. "You've been here a little more than six weeks. Why haven't you done anything about this?"

Rose 通读了客户的通话记录，其中极其详细地记录了过去两周在客户现场的这一特定安装所出现的问题。“我明白了，”她说。她确实看到了。她看到这位客户在尝试使用 Able Corporation 的软件时感到很痛苦。然而，她不明白这怎么只是一个测试问题，尽管她没有通过指责别人来回应。“在这种情况下，我的部门能提供什么帮助？” 她问。

Rose reads through the customer's call log, which tracks in excruciating detail the past two-weeks' worth of problems with this particular installation at the customer's site. "I see," she says. And she does see. She sees that this customer is in a world of hurt trying to use Able Corporation's software. She doesn't see, however, how it's just a testing problem, though she refrains from responding by blaming someone else. "How can my department help in this case?" she asks.

详尽测试谬误

The Exhaustive Testing Fallacy

“这不是很明显吗？” 卡恩吼道。“这个客户遇到这些问题是因为你的部门没有进行详尽的测试！你的测试人员很懒惰！我在第一天就告诉你，你需要做一些严肃的屁股鞭打。”

"Isn't it obvious?" Kahn bellows. "This customer is having these problems because your department isn't doing exhaustive testing! Your testers are lazy! I told you on Day One that you'd have some serious butt-whipping to do."

“你说的‘穷尽’是什么意思？” 罗斯问道。

"What do you mean by 'exhaustive'?" Rose asks.

卡恩用拳头敲桌子。“什么？你不知道？我还以为你是质量专家呢！”

Kahn smacks the table with his fist. "What? You don't know? I thought you were the quality expert!"

罗斯深吸一口气让自己平静下来。“哦，我知道‘穷尽’对我来说意味着什么。我想知道它对你意味着什么。”

Rose takes a deep breath to calm herself. "Oh, I know what 'exhaustive' means to me. I want to know what it means to you."

卡恩恼怒地翻了个白眼。“我的意思是他们没有测试所有东西，他们应该测试！”

Kahn rolls his eyes in exasperation. "I mean they're not testing everything and they should be!"

到现在为止，Rose 知道在 Kahn 处于责备情绪时，她不应该试图说服 Kahn 摆脱一些在她看来甚至像“详尽测试”这样荒谬的事情。Rose 想了想，沮丧地皱着眉头，Kahn 相信穷举测试谬误，可以测试一切！她慢慢地说，“测试所有东西是不可能的。”

By now, Rose knows better than to try to talk Kahn out of something even so ridiculous to her mind as "exhaustive testing" when he's in a blaming mood. Rose thinks for a second, frowning in dismay, Kahn believes The Exhaustive Testing Fallacy, that it's possible to test everything! Speaking slowly, she says, "It's never possible to test everything."

Rose 明白 Kahn 对测试一无所知，但她现在看到他甚至不知道自己不知道。她很想告诉他，只有当测试人员筋疲力尽无法继续时，才是真正的详尽测试，但她把这个想法留给了自己，简单地回答说：“好吧，我们会看看我们的测试。”

Rose understands that Kahn doesn't know the first thing about testing, but she now sees that he doesn't even know enough to know that he doesn't know. She is tempted to tell him that the only real kind of exhaustive testing is when the tester is too exhausted to continue, but she keeps the thought to herself, replying simply, "All right, we'll look at our tests."

测试产生质量谬误

The Testing-Produces-Quality Fallacy

卡恩还没来得及回答，罗斯就继续说：“现在，在你的语音信箱里，你说了一笔交易失败的事。那是什么事？”

Before Kahn can respond, Rose continues, "Now, in your voicemail, you said something about a lost sale. What's that about?"

“我们失去了 MegaCorp 的交易。” 卡恩摇摇头，一半是愤怒，一半是难以置信。“那本来应该是一次扣篮大甩卖，但当 MegaCorp 的人进行评估时，他们发现了跨国模拟中的一堆错误。” “哦？” Rose 在继续之前略微停顿了一下。“你的意思是像我们在测试中发现的那些？”

"We lost the MegaCorp deal." Kahn shakes his head, partly in anger, partly in disbelief. "That should have been a slam-dunk sale, but when the folks at MegaCorp did an evaluation, they found a bunch of bugs in the multi-national simulations." "Oh?" Rose pauses slightly before continuing. "You mean like the ones we found in testing?"

“什么？” 卡恩啪的一声。

"What?" Kahn snaps.

“记得吗？我在这里的第一周，测试人员报告了多国模拟的问题，但你告诉我们停止。你说我们没有任何客户需要该功能，所以我们应该专注于重要的事情。”

"Remember? My first week here, the testers reported problems with the multi-national simulations, but you told us to stop. You said we didn't have any customers who needed that feature, so we should focus on the important stuff."

“你看，”卡恩不耐烦地在椅子上动了动，然后哼了一声，“你来这里是为了让质量更好。别跟我撒娇。做你必须做的来提高质量。这次会议结束了！”

"Look," Kahn shifts impatiently in his chair, then huffs, "you're here to make the quality better. Don't get cute with me. Do what you have to do to improve quality. This meeting is over!"

罗斯站起来。“好的，我明白了，我会着手处理这些事情的。” 她没有说她会做什么；她也没有说她会做什么。

Rose stands. "Okay, I understand. I'll get to work on these things." She does not say what she will do; nor does she say what she'll work on.

离开卡恩的办公室时，罗斯反思了卡恩要求的荒谬之处。他通过让我除了测试之外什么都不做，然后只允许测试他认为应该测试的东西，从而特别阻止我提高质量。他有迹象表明相关功能已损坏，他明确告诉我不要收集有关它的更多信息。现在他因为我没有解决问题而生气。

Walking away from Kahn's office, Rose reflects on the absurdity of his demands. He's specifically preventing me from improving quality by keeping me from doing anything but testing, and then only allowing testing of what he thinks should be tested. He had an indication that the feature in question was broken, and he explicitly told me not to gather any more information about it. Now he's upset that I didn't fix the problem.

罗斯决定暂时放手。她意识到，如果她坚持这一点，卡恩只会在“测试产生质量谬误”中进一步巩固自己。罗斯决定从慢慢根除卡恩关于测试的根深蒂固的谬误开始。

Rose decides to let this go for now. She realizes that if she pursues the point, Kahn will just entrench himself further in The Testing-Produces-Quality Fallacy. Rose determines to start by slowly eradicating Kahn's deeply ingrained fallacies about testing.

分解谬误

The Decomposition Fallacy

当罗斯在返回办公室的路上经过测试实验室时，她听到一场争论正在酝酿之中，于是她绕道去看发生了什么。

As Rose passes the test lab on her way back to her office, she hears an argument brewing and detours to see what's going on.

一位开发人员正在对她的一位测试人员大喊大叫。“如果你想做一些有用的测试，请告诉我当你在每个模块上运行这些测试时会发生什么。” 巴里一边朝苏西挥舞着一叠文件一边对她大喊大叫。“我这里有测试数据。停止测试那个接口并开始测试这些模块。”

A developer is yelling at one of her testers. "If you want to do some useful testing, tell me what happens when you run these tests on each of the modules." Barry is shouting at Suzy as he waves a sheaf of papers at her. "I've got the test data right here. Stop testing that interface and start testing these modules."

苏西皱着眉头向后退了半步。“听着，Barry，我负责测试这部分系统，所以我要测试这部分系统。测试模块就是单元测试，那不是我的工作。”

Suzy frowns and takes half a step backwards. "Look here, Barry, I'm responsible for testing this part of the system, so I'm going to test this part of the system. Testing modules is unit testing, and that's not my job."

巴里气急败坏地说：“这不是你的工作！不是你的工作！卡恩对你们这些测试人员的看法是正确的——你们是一群懒惰的无知者，总是在寻找工作的出路。看，女士，如果你测试模块并且模块构成了系统，那么你就完成了你的工作。测试部分，你就测试了整体！” 巴里用眼角的余光注意到门口的罗斯。他突然沉默了，意识到自己可能越界了。

Barry sputters, "Not your job! Not your job! Kahn is right about you testers—you are a bunch of lazy ignoramuses always looking for a way out of work. Look, lady, if you test the modules and the modules make up the system, then you've done your job. Test the parts and you've tested the whole!" Out of the corner of his eye, Barry notices Rose at the door. He falls silent suddenly, aware that he's probably stepped out of line.

在苏西捍卫自己的立场之前，罗斯走进实验室，苏西和巴里都能看到她。从她无意中听到的内容，罗斯认识到巴里相信整体只是其部分的总和——分解谬误：测试部分，你就测试了整体。但罗斯已经被这种假设咬伤了很多次，以至于知道要将其扼杀在萌芽状态。“对不起，”她轻声说。在现在静止的实验室里，她的声音在流传。“我可以插话吗？” 不等他们同意，蔷薇凑到巴里身边，轻声说道： “你不觉得，由测试人员来决定如何测试比较好吗？”

Before Suzy can defend her position, Rose steps into the lab where both Suzy and Barry can see her. From what she's overheard, Rose recognizes that Barry is convinced that the whole is simply the sum of its parts—The Decomposition Fallacy: Test the parts and you've tested the whole. But Rose has been bitten by that assumption often enough times to know to nip it in the bud. "Excuse me," she says, quietly. In the now-still lab, her voice carries. "May I put a word in?" Not waiting for their permission, Rose steps close to Barry and speaks in a soft voice, "Don't you think it would be a good idea for the testers to decide how to test?"

巴里脸红了，然后他的文件嘎嘎作响。“如果他们不知道自己在做什么，我就不知道！”

Barry reddens and then rattles his papers. "Not if they don't know what they're doing, I don't!"

“Barry，”Rose 说，仍然轻声说，“测试模块为我们提供了关于模块的信息，而不是关于它们如何协同工作的信息。Suzy 是对的。她应该测试系统，而不是系统的各个部分。”

"Barry," Rose says, still speaking softly, "testing the modules gives us information about the modules, not about how they work together. Suzy's right. She's supposed to test the system, not the parts of the system."

组合谬误

The Composition Fallacy

苏西双手叉腰，瞪着巴里。“看吧，巴里，我是对的。而且，测试系统会自动测试零件。”

Suzy puts her hands on her hips and glares at Barry. "See, Barry, I'm right. Besides, testing the system will automatically test the parts."

呃，罗斯想。组合谬误来了——Suzy 的想法是，如果您将系统作为一个整体进行测试，那么组成系统的各个部分也会被测试。蔷薇转向苏西，再次小声说道，“其实，苏西，不是那样的。是的，如果一个模块坏到系统无法运行，我们可能会发现问题。但是系统测试赢了以我们应有的方式使用模块，以表明我们确实测试了它们。”

Uh-oh, Rose thinks. Here comes The Composition Fallacy—Suzy has the idea that if you test the system as a whole, the parts that make up the system will be tested. Rose turns to face Suzy, again speaking quietly, "Actually, Suzy, it doesn't work that way. Yes, if a module is so broken that the system can't function, we may see a problem. But a system test won't exercise the modules the way we should in order to say we really tested them."

苏西看起来很困惑。“但运行系统测试意味着接触所有模块。”

Suzy looks confused. "But running the system tests means touching all the modules."

“是的，它会触及他们，但可能不会触及他们的所有部位，”罗斯解释道。“这样想吧：如果你只是触摸系统界面，你会说你已经测试过了吗？”

"Yes, it touches them, but probably doesn't reach all parts of them," Rose explains. "Think of it this way: If all you do is touch the system interface, would you say you've tested it?"

苏西用手捂住嘴，喃喃道：“哦，我明白你的意思了。”

Suzy covers her mouth with her hand before mumbling, "Oh. I see what you're saying."

现在轮到巴里一脸困惑了。他对罗斯说。“好吧，假设你是对的。那你说我们应该怎么做？”

Now it's Barry's turn to look confused. He addresses Rose. "Okay, suppose you're right. So what do you say we should do?"

一切测试就是测试谬误

The All-Testing-Is-Testing Fallacy

“Suzy 应该测试系统，而你测试各个模块，”Rose 回答道。“我假设你会做不同类型的测试。”

"Suzy should test the system and you test the individual modules," Rose replies. "I assume you'll be doing different types of tests."

巴里摇摇头。“它们并没有什么不同。我们都通过系统界面执行测试。我只是设计了这些测试用例来强调每个模块的各个部分。”

Barry shakes his head. "They're not that different. We both execute tests through the system interface. I just have these test cases I designed to stress individual parts of each module."

“对，”罗斯说。“你的测试用例针对组件的特定方面。Suzy 的测试针对组件之间交互的特定方面。无论你们两个使用什么接口进行测试，你都在测试不同的东西，收集不同类型的信息。”

"Right," says Rose. "Your test cases target specific aspects of the components. Suzy's tests target specific aspects of the interactions between the components. No matter what interface you two use for testing, you're testing different things, gathering different types of information."

“但他们并没有那么不同，”巴里坚持道。“她可以像她一样轻松地完成我的测试。”

"But they're not that different," Barry persists. "She could do my tests just as easily as hers."

罗斯觉得自己的耐心正在消磨殆尽。“巴里，你想看看你写的模块是否按照你的期望行事，对吧？” Barry 点头表示同意，Rose 继续说道，“而 Suzy，你正试图查明系统是否满足我们在上次会议上讨论的要求，对吧？” 苏西点点头。“你们都看到你们有不同的信息，你们试图从你们的测试中收集吗？”

Rose feels her patience wearing thin. "Barry, you want to find out if the modules you wrote do what you expect them to do, right?" Barry nods agreement as Rose continues, "And Suzy, you're trying to find out if the system meets the requirements we discussed in our last meeting, right?" Suzy nods. "Do you both see that you have different information you're trying to glean from your tests?"

巴里对此摇了摇头。“没有，我没有看到，我也想知道我写的是否符合要求。”

Barry shakes his head at this. "No, I don't see. I want to know if what I wrote meets the requirements as well."

Rose 表示同意，“是的，但这与查明代码是否按照您的意图执行是不同的。您知道这是两个不同的事情吗？”

Rose agrees, "Yes, but that's different from finding out whether the code does what you intend it to do. Do you see how those are two different things?"

“不，我不！” 巴里的声音因紧张而提高。“我所看到的只是我们在争论关于测试目的的语义，而我只想回到我的办公桌以便我可以完成我的工作并编写代码。”

"No, I don't!" Barry's voice rises with tension. "All I see is we're arguing semantics about test purposes when I just want to go back to my desk so I can do my job and write code."

蔷薇有些不耐烦，“两位，都请过来。” 她穿过测试实验室，来到对面墙上的白板前，拿起记号笔，用大写字母写下三个字：

Rose responds, somewhat less patiently, "Both of you, please come over here." She crosses the test lab to the whiteboard on the opposite wall, picks up a marker pen, and writes three words in large letters:

要求

REQUIREMENTS

意图

INTENT

执行

IMPLEMENTATION

“巴里，我想你是在假设你的意图和要求是一样的，”罗斯用记号笔指着中间的词，然后转身面对着巴里和苏西，“但我们不知道，是吗？ ? 我们不知道此时此刻我们对需求的理解和你上周写代码时对需求的理解是一样的。

"Barry, I think you're assuming that your intent is the same as the requirements," Rose points to the center word with the marker pen and then turns to face Barry and Suzy, "but we don't know that, do we? We don't know that our understanding of the requirements at this minute is the same as your understanding of the requirements last week when you wrote the code."

再次面对白板，Rose 画了一条细直线连接“需求”和“意图”两个词，然后在上面画了一条深色斜线。“事实上，”她继续说道，转过身来再次解决这些问题，“我们无法确定您一周前的想法是否与现在的需求文档中所写的一样，只能针对实施情况进行测试。所以 Suzy正在将实施与要求进行比较，看它们是否匹配。”

Facing the whiteboard again, Rose draws a fine, straight line to connect the words Requirements and Intent, then puts a dark slash through it. "In fact," she continues, pivoting to address them again, "we have no way of finding out if what you were thinking a week ago is what is written in the requirements document now, other than to test against the implementation. So Suzy is comparing the implementation against the requirements to see if they match."

不等反应，Rose 转身面对白板，画了一条高弓形线，从“需求”一词延伸到“意图”，连接到“实施”。当她从眼角引用“所有测试都是测试”这一信念的谬误时，她看到巴里皱起了眉头。至少他还在听，罗斯一边想，一边微微转身，用记号笔指着巴里的方向。“您想将您的意图与您的实施进行比较。”

Without waiting for a reaction, Rose turns back to the board and draws a high-arching line that stretches from the word Requirements, up over Intent, to connect to Implementation. As she cites the fallacy in the belief that "all testing is testing," from the corner of her eye, she sees Barry frown. At least he's still listening, Rose thinks as she turns slightly to point her marker pen in Barry's direction. "You want to compare your intent to your implementation."

罗斯画了另一条线，这次是从意图到实施。

Rose draws another line, this time from Intent to Implementation.

“如果我们同时进行这两种类型的测试，我们就会知道这三件事是否都相同。如果不一样，我们可以找出如何解决这些差异。但如果我们假设任何两个这些是相等的，但我们不会测试以确认它们实际上是相等的，我们正在为以后的跌倒做准备。”

"If we do both of these types of testing, we'll know if all three of these things are the same. And if they aren't, we can figure out what to do about the discrepancies. But if we assume that any two of these are equal but we don't test to confirm that they are in fact equal, we're setting ourselves up for a fall later."

回头看看巴里和苏西，罗斯看到他们现在都皱着眉头。她解释说，与“所有测试都是测试谬误”密切相关的是“一切都同样容易测试谬误”，它导致人们对测试时间产生乐观的错误估计，也导致他们感到无助，程序员无能为力使查找错误变得更容易。听了萝丝的解释，巴里和苏西都不置可否。

Looking back at Barry and Suzy, Rose sees that they both are frowning now. She explains that closely related to The All-Testing- Is-Testing Fallacy is The Everything-Is-Equally-Easy-to-Test Fallacy, which causes people to produce optimistically incorrect estimates of testing time, and also leads to their feeling helpless, that there's nothing programmers can do to make finding bugs easier. Neither Barry nor Suzy comments upon hearing Rose's explanation.

任何白痴都能测试的谬误

The Any-Idiot-Can-Test Fallacy

几秒钟后，巴里打破了沉默。“好吧，好吧。它们是不同类型的测试。但我仍然不明白为什么我必须实际进行测试。我有一个要运行的测试列表。实际测试很容易。这只是一个问题敲击键盘。任何白痴都可以做到。如果有人可以，Suzy 应该能够处理它。” Barry 偷偷瞥了 Suzy 一眼，然后软化了打击，“开玩笑吧，有点像。”

After several long seconds, Barry breaks the silence. "Okay, fine. They're different types of testing. But I still don't see why I should have to actually do the testing. I have a list of tests I want run. The actual testing is easy. It's just a matter of banging on the keyboard. Any idiot can do it. And if anybody can, Suzy should be able to handle it." Barry sneaks a sideways peek at Suzy before softening the blow, "Just kidding, sort of."

“啊，”罗斯悲伤地摇摇头，举起手示意巴里和苏西，她希望战争结束。“你以为测试很容易。让我看看你想让我们运行的那些测试。” 巴里把一叠文件递给罗斯。

"Ah," Rose shakes her head sadly and holds up her hand to indicate to Barry and Suzy that she wants the war over. "You think testing is easy. Let me see those tests you want us to run." Barry hands the sheaf of papers to Rose.

罗斯研究文件。她怀疑，由于只有六周的使用该产品的经验，她并不知道设计一套好的测试集所需知道的一切，但她猜想她知道的足够多，足以在糟糕的测试套件中找出漏洞。她没有失望。她看着巴里的眼睛。“我明白你为什么认为测试很容易了。” 她犹豫片刻，继续说道：“这些都是很基础的，比较简单的测试，我们坐下来，再好好想一想。”

Rose studies the documents. She suspects that with only six weeks of experience with this product, she doesn't know everything she'd need to know to design a good set of tests, but she guesses she knows enough to find holes in a bad test suite. She's not disappointed. She looks Barry in the eye. "I can see why you think testing is easy." She hesitates for an instant and then continues, "These are very basic, comparatively simple tests. Let's sit down and think through these tests some more."

令她惊讶的是，巴里和苏西都坐了下来。罗斯看到他们勉强愿意从他们设计有意义的测试以收集有用信息的集体经验中学习，但他们正在做她所希望的。

To her surprise, Barry and Suzy both sit down. Rose sees that they are grudgingly willing to learn from their collective experience in designing meaningful tests to gather useful information, but they are doing what she had hoped.

Barry 即将了解到好的测试总是探索性的——未来的测试会受到先前测试结果的强烈影响。这个过程是调查性的，因此 Barry 的测试列表不会在 Suzy 之前保持很长时间。Barry 认为最好将他对测试背后动机的想法告诉 Suzy，让她根据有关产品和测试的最新信息充实实际测试。

Barry is about to learn that good testing is always exploratory—with future tests strongly influenced by the results of prior tests. The process is investigative, so Barry's list of tests won't stay ahead of Suzy for long. Barry sees that he may be better off giving Suzy his ideas about the motivation behind the tests, allowing her to flesh out the actual tests in the light of up-to-the-minute information about both the product and the testing.

概括

Summary

学会识别一些关于测试的主要谬误可以消除项目经理犯下的一半严重错误。

Learning to recognize a handful of major fallacies about testing could eliminate half the gross mistakes project managers make.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.相信责备从长远来看是有效的：你可能会看到责备的短期结果，但这更像是用棍子戳狗，而不是有益的。

1. Believing that blame works in the long run: You may see short-term results from blaming, but it's more like what you get by poking a dog with a stick than it is beneficial.

2. 相信你对问题的第一印象总是正确的：第一印象很重要，但测试问题通常需要更多的分析——尤其是当你发现自己反复无常地指责他人时。

2. Believing that your first impression of a problem is always correct: First impressions are important, but testing problems generally require a bit more analysis—especially if you find yourself pointing the fickle finger of blame.

3.相信你可以“彻底地”测试任何东西：如果你要求“彻底地测试”，你通常得到的是测试人员以各种方式作弊，躲避他们的经理，并最终反叛。

3. Believing that you can test anything "exhaustively": If you demand "exhaustive testing," what you'll generally get is testers who cheat in various ways, hide from their managers, and ultimately rebel.

4. 认为您可以“快速而肮脏”地开发软件，然后测试质量：快速而肮脏就是这样。肮脏的。而且很难测试，此外。

4. Thinking you can develop software "quick and dirty" and then test quality in: Quick and dirty is just that. Dirty. And very hard to test, besides.

5.跳过单元测试是多余的，因为系统测试会发现所有的错误：系统测试不仅不会发现所有的错误，而且会花费更长的时间和更多的成本——比你通过跳过有效的单元测试节省的更多。

5. Skipping unit testing as redundant because system testing will catch all the bugs: Not only won't system testing catch all the bugs, but it will take longer and cost more—more than you save by skipping effective unit testing.

6.跳过系统测试，认为它是多余的，因为单元测试会发现所有的错误：你会根据所有部件在组装前都经过测试的保证来进行飞机的首飞吗？

6. Skipping system testing in the belief that it's redundant because unit testing will catch all the bugs: Would you fly on an airplane's maiden flight based on the assurance that all parts were tested prior to assembly?

7、期望测试产生质量：质量是整个开发过程的产物。糟糕的测试会导致糟糕的质量，但除非流程的所有其他部分都到位并正确执行，否则良好的测试不会带来良好的质量。

7. Expecting testing to produce quality: Quality is a product of the entire development process. Poor testing can lead to poor quality, but good testing won't lead to good quality unless all other parts of the process are in place and performed properly.

第 10 章_测试不仅仅是敲击键盘

Chapter_10_Testing Is More Than Banging Keys

 

”学生们按照他的命令，每人抓住一个铁把手，铁把手有四十个固定在框架的边缘；并且，让他们突然转动，整个单词的配置完全改变了。他然后命令 6 和 30 的小伙子轻声朗读出现在画框上的几行；并且，当他们发现三四个单词在一起可以构成一个句子的一部分时，他们口述给剩下的四个男孩抄写员。这项工作重复了三四次，每次转动时，引擎都设计得如此巧妙，随着方块木头上下颠倒，文字会移动到新的位置。

"The pupils, at his command, took each of them hold of an iron handle, whereof there were forty fixed round the edges of the frame; and, giving them a sudden turn, the whole disposition of the words was entirely changed. He then commanded six-and-thirty of the lads to read the several lines softly, as they appeared upon the frame; and, where they found three or four words together that might make part of a sentence, they dictated to the four remaining boys who were scribes. This work was repeated three or four times, and at every turn, the engine was so contrived, that the words shifted into new places, as the square bits of wood moved upside down.

“年轻的学生每天花六个小时从事这项工作，教授向我展示了几本已经收集起来的大对开本，其中有断句，他打算将它们拼凑起来；并且，从这些丰富的材料中，给世界所有艺术和科学的完整体……” - 乔纳森·斯威夫特，英国讽刺作家（1667-1745），格列佛游记，第 21 章。

"Six hours a day the young students were employed in this labour, and the professor showed me several volumes in large folio already collected, of broken sentences, which he intended to piece together; and, out of those rich materials, to give the world a complete body of all arts and sciences. . . ." - Jonathan Swift, English Satirist (1667–1745), Gulliver's Travels, Chapter 21.

与 Swift 在 Lagado 大学院的教授一样，Able 公司的开发人员 Barry 认为测试涉及很多随机动作——相信测试本质上只是敲击键盘的问题。为了说服 Barry 不这样，Able 的测试经理 Rose 从左侧向 Barry 提出了一个问题，通过伸出的手掌清楚地表明她不想让她自己的测试员之一 Suzy 回答。“让我们从这个问题开始：来自火星的生物如何知道是否有人在进行测试？”

Like Swift's professor at the Grand Academy of Lagado, Able Corporation's developer Barry thinks that testing involves lots of random actions—believing, in essence, that testing is just a matter of banging on the keyboard. To convince Barry otherwise, Rose, Able's testing manager, directs a question from left field at Barry, making it clear through a thrust-out palm that she doesn't want Suzy, one of her own testers, to answer. "Let's start with this question: How would a creature from Mars know if someone was testing?"

“为什么是火星？” 巴里问道，被这个看似无关紧要的问题推迟了。

"Why Mars?" asks Barry, put off by the question's seeming irrelevance.

“因为众所周知，火星人可以读心术。如果没有读心术，没有人可以仅通过观察他们的行为来确定某人是否在测试。” Rose 清了清嗓子，然后继续说道，“那是因为测试的真正工作是在身体活动之前和伴随身体活动的心理活动。如果你不假思索地敲击键盘，你就不是在测试。而且，如果你是思考但不敲击按键，你很可能正在测试。”

"Because it's a well-known fact that Martians can read minds. Without the ability to read minds, nobody could know for sure whether someone is testing or not, simply by observing their behavior." Rose clears her throat, and then proceeds, "That's because the real work of testing is the mental activity that precedes and accompanies the physical activity. If you're banging keys without thinking, you're not testing. And, if you're thinking but not banging keys, you might well be testing."

巴里挠挠头。“听起来你对测试的定义和我的不一样。” 他迅速看了看苏西，想确定她是否要表达反对意见，但她什么也没说。

Barry scratches his head. "It sounds like your definition of testing is different from mine." He looks quickly at Suzy to determine whether she is about to voice disagreement, but she says nothing.

“也许吧，”Rose 回答，“但我希望我能说服你扩展和完善你的定义。在我看来，测试系统是一个收集有关它的信息的过程，目的是这些信息可以用于某些目的目的。”

"Maybe," replies Rose, "but I'm hoping I can convince you to expand and refine your definition. In my view, testing a system is a process of gathering information about it with the intent that the information could be used for some purpose."

“这对我来说有点抽象，”巴里说。“你能举一些例子吗？”

"That's a little abstract for me," Barry says. "Can you give some examples?"

“当然可以，”罗斯回答。“让我们从敲击键开始吧。这是我十五岁的表弟伊恩的故事。”

"Sure thing," replies Rose. "Let's start with some key banging. This is the story of my fifteen-year-old cousin, Ian."

毫无意义地敲击按键是否是一种测试？

Is banging keys to no purpose a test, or not?

“伊恩花了整整两天时间收集他的新个人电脑的性能特征——启动时间、他的电子邮件程序的启动时间、从他的文字处理器打印一份文档需要多长时间、他一次可以打开多少个浏览器页面“没有崩溃的时间，等等。他将所有这些信息记录在笔记本中，并在两天结束时合上并归档。” 罗斯停顿了一下，然后直视着巴里。“现在你告诉我：他在测试吗？”

"Ian spent two whole days gathering performance characteristics of his new personal computer—start-up time, launch time for his email program, how long it takes to print a document from his word processor, how many browser pages he can have open at one time without crashing, and so forth. He logged all this information in a notebook, which he closed and filed away at the end of the two days." Rose pauses and then looks directly at Barry. "Now you tell me: Was he testing?"

“听起来像，”巴里说。“但他为什么要这么做？”

"Sounds like it," says Barry. "But why was he doing it?"

“好吧，我不是来自火星，所以我无法读懂他的想法，也不知道他是否打算使用这些信息。我问他是否正在建立一个基准来衡量预期的内存升级，或者下一个发布操作系统。他说他不是。

"Well, I'm not from Mars, so I couldn't read his mind and know whether he intended ever to use this information. I asked him if he was establishing a baseline against which to measure an anticipated memory upgrade, or the next release of the operating system. He said he was not.

“然后我问他是否正在测试他将在他母亲的机器上进行这些测量的过程。再一次，没有。接下来我问他是否正在核实推销员的说法，如果这些说法被证实，他打算要求退款是不真实的。

"Then I asked him if he was testing the process by which he would take these measurements on his mother's machine. Again, no. Next I asked if he was verifying the salesman's claims, with the intention of asking for a refund if the claims proved to be untrue. Nope.

“据我所知，除了自娱自乐之外，伊恩想不出他敲键盘的任何原因。所以，尽管他敲了两天键盘，但他并没有真正注意到结果，所以我会说他可能没有在测试。你现在如何回答他是否在测试？

"As far as I could tell, Ian couldn't think of any reason he was banging keys except to amuse himself. So, even though he was banging keys for two days, he wasn't really noticing anything about the results, so I would say that he probably wasn't testing. What would you answer now as to whether he was testing or not?"

“好吧，”巴里同意。“我可以接受他没有在测试的观点。但如果一个人没有敲击键盘，那么他肯定没有在测试。”

"All right," agrees Barry. "I can accept the view that he wasn't testing. But if a person is not banging keys, then he's certainly not testing."

“在你锁定那个想法之前，在我让 Suzy 告诉我们她对 Ian 是否在测试的看法之前，让我告诉你一个在 Able 工作之前我拒绝了一家大型保险公司的工作.它付了更多的钱，但它没有通过白手套测试。”

"Before you lock on to that idea, and also before I let Suzy tell us what she thinks about whether Ian was testing or not, let me tell you about a job I turned down at a large insurance company before taking the job here at Able. It paid more money, but it failed The White Glove Test."

白手套测试

The White Glove Test

“我问我未来的经理，公司是否为其测试人员使用了定义的测试过程。‘哦，是的，’他说。‘所有 150 人都使用定义的测试过程。’

"I asked my prospective manager whether the company used a defined testing process for its testers. 'Oh, yes,' he said. 'All one-hundred-fifty use the defined test process.'

“然后我问他那个过程是什么，他说，'它在我们的测试过程手册中定义，与 CMM 库一起保存。'

"I then asked him what that process was, and he said, 'It's defined in our testing process manual, which is kept with the CMM library.'

“接下来我问他这是否是唯一的副本。他说是的，所以我让他带我去图书馆看看。

"I next asked him if it was the only copy. He said yes, so I asked him to show me the library.

“在图书馆，我戴上了我的白手套——实际上，我用的是白手帕，因为我不是英国女王，所以我没有戴白手套。我把手帕缠在食指上，拖着走测试过程手册的顶部。我带着四分之一英寸的灰尘离开。我在测试吗？让我们根据定义检查结果。

"In the library, I put on my white glove—actually, I use a white handkerchief because I'm not the Queen of England, so I don't wear white gloves. I wrapped the handkerchief around my index finger and dragged it along the top of the Testing Process Manual. I came away with a quarter-inch of dust. Was I testing? Let's check the results against the definition.

“我的 White Glove 测试让我估计了公司的 150 名测试人员自从接触该手册以来已有多长时间。此外，通过让经理确认只有一份手册，我进行了测试公司关于人们如何使用手册的想法。所以，即使我没有敲任何键，我也进行了测试，测试组织的元测试。我决定不想在那里工作。”

"My White Glove Test gave me an estimate of how long it had been since any of the company's one-hundred-fifty testers touched the manual. Also, by getting the manager to confirm that there was only one copy of the manual, I tested the company's idea of how people use manuals. So, even though I didn't bang any keys, I performed a test, a meta-test of the testing organization. I decided I didn't want to work there."

“哇！” 苏西说，再也无法控制自己了。“也许我应该在来这里工作之前申请白手套测试。”

"Wow!" says Suzy, no longer able to contain herself. "Maybe I should have applied The White Glove Test before I came to work here."

“这不会有帮助，”巴里回答道。“为什么不？”

"It wouldn't have helped," replies Barry. "Why not?"

“因为我们没有任何记录在案的测试或其他流程。”

"Because we don't have any documented processes for testing or anything else."

狗粮测试

The Dog Food Test

罗斯看了看时钟，建议他们三个在午餐时继续谈话。Suzy建议去街角的汉堡店，Barry不同意，“我们去别的地方吧，他们的汉堡吃起来像狗粮。”

Looking at the clock, Rose proposes that the three of them continue their conversation over lunch. Suzy suggests the burger joint on the corner, but Barry disagrees, "Let's go somewhere else. Their burgers taste like dog food."

“你怎么知道的？” Suzy 问，对 Barry 扬起怀疑的眉毛。“你吃过狗粮吗？”

"And how do you know that?" Suzy asks, raising a skeptical eyebrow at Barry. "Have you ever eaten dog food?"

在巴里想出巧妙的反驳之前，罗斯回答说：“我希望他有。如果没有，他很快就会开始。”

Before Barry can think up a smart retort, Rose responds, "I hope he has. If not, he's going to start soon."

巴里虽然对罗丝的话不解，但还是决定不去追问。相反，他建议他们绕过拐角到熟食店吃汤沙拉甜点自助餐，这一选择得到了罗斯和苏西的认可。

Although Barry is puzzled by Rose's remark, he decides not to ask for clarification. Instead, he suggests they go around the corner to the deli for a soup-salad-and-dessert buffet, a choice that meets with Rose's and Suzy's approval.

在熟食店，三人占据了一张转角的小桌子，然后分散开来装满汤碗，并从沙拉吧中选择。当他们重新坐在桌旁时，Rose 问道：“Barry，我让你接受了我对测试的看法了吗？”

At the deli, the three lay claim to a small, corner table and then disperse to fill their soup bowls and choose from the salad bar. As they reconvene at their table, Rose asks, "Barry, have I won you over to my view of testing?"

巴里考虑了一下，先用指尖蘸了蘸他的辣椒碗，然后尝了尝，然后拿起胡椒磨，把新鲜的黑胡椒粉磨到辣椒上。“部分。但你应该添加一些关于谁必须做的事情。我的意思是，你不能指望开发人员进行测试。我们有更重要的事情要做。”

Barry deliberates, first dipping a fingertip in his bowl of chili, then tasting it, then picking up the pepper mill and grinding fresh black pepper onto the chili. "Partly. But you should add something about who has to do it. I mean, you can't expect developers to test. We've got more important things to do."

“实际上，”罗斯回答说，“开发人员以多种方式进行测试，或者至少他们应该这样做。”

"Actually," Rose replies, "developers do testing in lots of ways, or at least they should."

Suzy 点头同意，但 Barry 质疑 Rose 的观点。“什么办法？”

Suzy nods in agreement, but Barry challenges Rose's point. "What ways?"

罗斯看了看手表，然后回答了巴里。“好吧，公平的问题。首先，当我编写软件时，我会不断地进行测试。假设我写了一行代码并立即看到一个拼写错误——发现拼写错误是我用眼睛‘测试’代码的结果.我在其他人看到我的代码之前纠正了很多问题。

Rose glances at her watch and then answers Barry. "Okay, fair question. First of all, when I write software, I'm constantly testing. Say I write a line of code and immediately see a typo— spotting the typo is the result of my 'testing' the code with my eyes. I correct many problems before anyone else sees my code."

“好吧，你当然会那样做。每个人都会那样做。” 巴里在沙拉里撒了胡椒粉，苏西忍不住打了个喷嚏。“好吧，我想你可以称之为测试，但它有点微不足道。”

"Well, of course you do that. Everybody does." Barry showers his salad with pepper, causing Suzy to stifle a sneeze. "Okay, I suppose you could call that testing, but it's kind of trivial."

“好吧，”罗斯继续说道。“这是一个更引人注目的例子。我曾经在一家软件公司工作，该公司开发嵌入式软件来控制汽车的刹车和转向。在软件发布之前，每个与该软件开发有任何关系的人都必须驾驶一辆汽车以每小时一百英里的速度在测试跑道上使用该软件。” [9]

"All right," continues Rose. "Here's a more striking example. I used to work at a software company that built embedded software to control brakes and steering on cars. Before the software could be released, each person who had anything to do with development of that software had to drive a car using that software around a test track at a hundred miles an hour." [9]

“凉爽的！” 嘴里塞了一半辣椒，巴里的钦佩之情几乎听不见。“但这与中国豆子的价格有什么关系呢？”

"Cool!" Barry's admiration is barely audible behind a mouth half full of chili. "But what does that have to do with the price of beans in China?"

“首先，它测试了工人对他们产品的信心。这是重要的信息——当然不是决定性的，因为有些开发人员天生就过于自信，而另一些则过于谦虚。” 罗斯用叉子叉了一片泡菜，等着巴里吃完辣椒。“但这是一个很好的起点。” “这种测试很常见吗？” Suzy 从她的沙拉上抬起头来向 Rose 提出问题。

"First of all, it tests the workers' confidence in their product. That's important information—not definitive of course, because some developers are naturally overconfident, while others are overly modest." Rose spears a pickle slice with her fork and waits for Barry to finish his chili. "But it's a good starting place." "Is that kind of testing at all common?" Suzy looks up from her salad just long enough to put the question to Rose.

“嗯，它很常见，有自己的名字——狗粮检测。”

"Well, it's common enough to have its own name—Dog Food Testing."

巴里怀疑地盯着他的空碗。“这意味着什么？”

Barry stares suspiciously at his empty bowl. "What does that mean?"

“这是基于我家乡的一句谚语：‘在你把它喂给你的狗之前，先吃你自己的狗粮。’ 对于养狗的人来说，这可能是个好建议，也可能不是个好建议，但对于应该通过使用它来测试他们的产品的软件开发人员来说，这是一个很好的建议。尽管如此，我经常听到软件开发人员声称，“哦，我们不使用我们的产品.我们把它留给测试人员去做。”

"It's based on a saying back where I come from: 'Before you feed it to your dog, eat your own dog food.' That may or may not be good advice for dog owners, but it's excellent advice for software developers who should test their product by using it. In spite of that, I often hear software developers claim, 'Oh, we don't use our product. We leave it to the testers to do that.'"

“好吧，”巴里耸耸肩，“我们没有。”

"Well," Barry shrugs, "we don't."

“没错，你在日常工作中不会使用它，但你可以假装。或者你可以观看我们的一位客户使用它。”

"That's true, you don't use it in the course of your regular work, but you could pretend. Or you could watch one of our customers use it."

Barry 承认：“我明白这可能有多大的指导意义，但它似乎还不够充分。如果我们所做的只是狗粮测试，我们不会犯——所谓的——抽样错误吗？ “

"I can see how that might be instructive," Barry acknowledges, "but it doesn't seem an adequate test. If all we did was Dog-Food Testing, wouldn't we be making—what's it called—a sampling mistake?"

Rose 笑了，对 Barry 开始理解的方式感到满意。“你完全正确。例如，软件开发人员不是典型的文字处理器用户。他们甚至不是典型的编译器用户。”

Rose smiles, pleased with the way Barry is starting to understand. "You're absolutely right. For example, software developers are not typical word-processor users. They're not even typical compiler users."

测试人员也需要测试。

Testers need testing, too.

苏西用勺子啜了一口番茄汤，然后把仍然盛满的器具放回碗里，用嘴唇吹气。“太辣了，”她喘着粗气说，同时拿起叉子去吃沙拉中的一片菠菜。“我还有一个问题，Rose。还记得上周你让我重新运行 Charlene 已经在 Ply.Able 系统上执行过的测试吗？你已经有了结果，所以它不是为了提供信息。这是否意味着它不是真的是考试吗？”

Suzy sips tomato soup from her spoon, then puts the still-full utensil back in the bowl, blowing air from her lips. "Too spicy," she gasps, as she picks up her fork to attack a piece of spinach in her salad. "I have another question, Rose. Remember last week when you asked me to rerun a test Charlene had already performed on the Ply.Able System? You already had results, so it wasn't for information. Does that mean it wasn't really a test?"

“这取决于你认为你在测试什么。可能是我在测试 Ply.Able 系统的一致性。或者我可能在测试测试环境的稳定性。但在这种情况下，我的目的是测试 Charlene 的能力，因为她是我们测试实验室的新人。换句话说，根据我对测试的定义，Charlene 是一个系统。”

"That depends on what you think you were testing. It could be I was testing the Ply.Able System for consistency. Or maybe I was testing the stability of the test environment. But in this case, my intention was to test Charlene's competence because she's new to our test lab. In other words, Charlene is a system, according to my definition of testing."

Suzy 玩弄她的汤并尝试了另一种口味，这次设法吞下了一勺。“罗斯，知道你在考验我们，这让我很不舒服。”

Suzy toys with her soup and tries another taste, this time managing to swallow a spoonful. "It makes me uncomfortable, Rose, to know you're testing us."

“那是我作为测试经理的工作的一部分。现在，如果我没有告诉 Charlene 我让你复制了她的测试，我会拿 Charlene 的信任冒险，但我确实告诉了她。而且，顺便说一下，我希望你'测试我作为你的经理。”

"That's part of my job as test manager. Now, if I hadn't told Charlene that I had you replicating her test, I'd have risked Charlene's trust, but I did tell her. And, by the way, I hope you're testing me as your manager."

“考验你？我不会那样做的……” Suzy 的脸红得通红，在等待 Rose 的回应时显得很焦虑

"Testing you? I wouldn't do that . . ." Suzy blushes a rosy pink and appears anxious as she waits for Rose's response

罗斯几乎没有跳动。“当然你会——或者至少你应该——就像你测试汤的方式一样。”

Rose barely skips a beat. "Sure you would—or at least you should—just the way you tested your soup."

你可以在没有意识到的情况下进行测试。

You can test without consciously realizing it.

“试过我的汤？你在说什么？”

"Tested my soup? What are you talking about?"

“你尝了尝，觉得太辣了，所以你吃了一些沙拉，”罗斯回答道。

"You took a taste and decided it was too hot, so you ate some of your salad instead," Rose replies.

“但这如何符合我们的定义？”

"But how does that fit our definition?"

罗斯很高兴听到苏西说出我们的定义。“无论你是否意识到，你都在测试，因为你使用结果来做出有关风险的决定。”

Rose is pleased to hear Suzy say our definition. "Whether you were aware of it or not, you were testing, because you used the result to make a decision about risk."

“好吧，所以我是在测试汤。但我当然不是在测试你。”

"Okay, so I was testing the soup. But I certainly wasn't testing you."

“不是用勺子啜饮，而是当你告诉我一项任务让你不舒服时，你是在测试我。你想知道我会如何回应，并基于此，你可能会在未来根据风险改变你的行为” “不，我不会。”

"Not with sips from the spoon, but when you told me that an assignment made you uncomfortable, you were testing me. You wanted to know how I would respond, and based on that, you might change your behavior in the future based on risk." "No, I wouldn't."

“当然会，如果我对你厉声呵斥，你以后可能就不会那么愿意问我任何有挑战性的问题了。”

"Sure you would. If I'd snapped at you, you might not be so willing to ask me any challenging questions in the future."

演示不是测试。

A demonstration is not a test.

Suzy 低下眼睛看着她剩下的菠菜沙拉，然后将目光转向 Barry。“至少我没有敲键盘。”

Suzy lowers her eyes to gaze at the remains of her spinach salad, and then shifts her glance to Barry. "At least I wasn't pounding on keys."

巴里耸耸肩，然后从桌子旁站起来。“你们要甜点吗？” 看到两个女人都没有兴趣接受他的提议，巴里穿过用餐区来到自助餐区，很快就全神贯注地把甜点堆在盘子里。

Barry shrugs and then gets up from the table. "Either of you want dessert?" Seeing that neither woman has any interest in taking him up on his offer, Barry walks across the dining section to the buffet and is quickly absorbed in piling desserts on a plate.

Barry 听不见了，Rose 问道：“Suzy，你昨天下午去哪儿了？我来了实验室三次，但你不在。你生病了吗？”

With Barry out of earshot, Rose asks, "Suzy, where were you yesterday afternoon? I came to the lab three times, but you weren't there. Were you ill?"

“对不起，”苏西几乎没有耳语。“我应该告诉你，但我没有时间。我和 Randolph 在他最好的客户之一的办公室里。他让我设计了一个 Barry 功能集的测试套件供客户查看。这很棘手，因为我必须非常小心，不要使用任何调用已知错误的测试用例。我还确保我的测试不会触发我们已知的任何性能问题。”

"I'm sorry," Suzy barely whispers. "I should have told you, but I didn't have time. I was with Randolph at the office of one of his best clients. He had me design a test suite of Barry's feature set for the client to see. It was tricky because I had to be really careful not to use any test cases that invoked known bugs. I also made sure my tests didn't trigger any of the performance problems we know about."

“我对此不太高兴，”罗斯回答道。

"I'm not too happy about that," replies Rose.

“对不起，下次，我一定会在走之前告诉你。” “哦，离开没关系，如果这对伦道夫有帮助——虽然我想知道你在哪里，以防万一。我不高兴的是你认为你在做测试，而你并没有。 ”

"I'm sorry. Next time, I'll be sure to tell you before I leave." "Oh, leaving is all right, if it helps Randolph—though I would like to know where you are, in case something comes up. What I'm not happy about is that you think you were doing a test when you weren't."

“但我是。我运行了大约二十个不同的测试用例。”

"But I was. I ran about twenty different test cases."

“好吧，回想一下我们的定义。根据那个定义，你不是在测试。你是在帮助 Randolph 进行线下销售宣传，伪装成测试的演示。你不是在收集信息，因为你已经确切地知道了Barry 的程序在所有 20 个案例中会做什么。事实上，Randolph 给你的工作是确保没有从这个伪测试中获得任何信息。Randolph 可能一直在测试你的技术销售能力，而你可能已经通过了闪亮的颜色，但你不是在测试——除了测试客户的轻信性。”

"Well, think back to our definition. According to that, you weren't testing. You were helping Randolph make an off-line sales pitch, a demonstration disguised as a test. You weren't gathering information, because you already knew exactly what Barry's program would do on all twenty cases. In fact, the job Randolph gave you was to make sure that there was no information obtained from this pseudo-test. Randolph might have been testing your technical sales ability, and you might have passed with shining colors, but you weren't testing—except for testing the gullibility of the customer."

当巴里把盛满甜点的盘子放在他们的桌子上时，罗斯结束了她的演讲。巴里仍然站着，指着四块甜点。“你确定你什么都不想要吗？”

Rose finishes her speech just as Barry sets the dessert-laden plate on their table. Still standing, Barry points at the four desserts. "Are you sure you don't want any?"

“好吃。我要尝尝柠檬绒毛。” 罗斯拿起勺子。“尝尝就好。”

"Yum-my. I'll take a taste of the lemon fluff." Rose picks up her spoon. "Just a taste."

苏西拍着手笑了起来。“样品，对吧？测试。”

Suzy claps her hands together and laughs. "A sample, right? A test."

概括

Summary

为了符合测试的条件，一个动作必须寻找会影响动作的信息，无论它是否涉及敲击按键。

To qualify as a test, an action has to seek information that will influence action, whether or not it involves banging on keys.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.认为计算机可以读心：计算机会按照您的要求去做，无论您是否真正想过。

1. Thinking a computer can read minds: Computers do what you tell them to do, whether or not that's what you really had in mind.

2.未能验证软件销售声明：敲击按键无法完成这项工作，但如果您经常因敲击按键而崩溃，这可能会有所帮助。最好有一个基于具体索赔的计划。

2. Failing to verify software sales claims: Banging keys doesn't do this job, though it might help if you experience frequent crashes from key-banging. Better to have a plan based on specific claims.

3.在测试中未能使用覆盖工具（例如，白手套测试）：您可以构建或安装工具来告诉您系统的哪些部分从未被您的任何测试触及。他们可能没有沾上灰尘，但如果他们没有被任何测试所触及，他们当然不能被认为是测试过的。

3. Failing to use coverage tools (for example, The White Glove Test) in your testing: You can build or install tools that tell you which parts of a system have never been touched by any of your tests. They may not have gathered dust, but if they haven't been touched by any test, they certainly cannot be considered tested.

4.认为覆盖测试证明某些东西已经过测试：仅仅因为你可以证明代码的所有部分都被某种测试或其他测试所触及，你不能说这些部分已经过彻底测试。代码覆盖率也不能告诉您所有功能都已经过全面测试。要做到这一点，必须分析测试的相关性和全面性。换句话说，思考。

4. Thinking that coverage tests prove something is tested: Just because you can show that all parts of the code have been touched by some test or other, you can't say that those parts have been thoroughly tested. Nor can code coverage tell you that all functions have been thoroughly tested. For that to be true, the tests have to be analyzed for relevance and comprehensiveness. Thinking, in other words.

5.将流程文档与流程混淆：流程就是您实际执行的操作。流程文档描述了某人希望您做什么，理想情况下。它们很少完全重合，有时甚至根本不重叠。大多数过程根本没有记录，这通常是件好事；否则，我们会被没完没了的文件压垮。最好花宝贵的时间观察流程——人们实际做什么。您可以利用节省下来的时间来决定哪些流程最好由精确的文档支持。

5. Confusing process documents with processes: A process is what you actually do. A process document describes what someone would like you to do, ideally. They rarely coincide exactly, and sometimes don't overlap at all. Most processes aren't documented at all, which generally is a good thing; otherwise, we would be crushed by the weight of endless documents. It is better to spend your valuable time observing processes—what people actually do. You can use the time you save to decide which few processes would be best backed up by precise documents.

6.混淆文档和事实：前一点是一般情况，针对混淆测试脚本和测试、混淆测试报告和测试、混淆需求文档和需求等特殊情况。

6. Confusing documents with facts: The previous point is a general case for such special cases as confusing test scripts with tests, confusing test reports with tests, and confusing requirements documents with requirements.

7.没有“吃自己的狗粮”：如果你害怕或不屑你的产品，为什么有人要买它？

7. Failing to "eat your own dog food": If you are afraid of or disdainful about your product, why should anyone buy it?

8.在狗粮测试中只使用非代表性的“狗”：除非你正在开发软件开发工具，否则完全由软件开发人员组成的样本不太可能代表你的用户群体。

8. Using only non-representative "dogs" in a Dog Food Test: Unless you're developing software development tools, samples composed entirely of software developers are unlikely to represent your population of users.

9.没有测试你的测试人员，或者测试他们太多：每个人的工作都需要评估，但不是无休止的。在某些时候，你必须相信人们会在没有老板监督的情况下完成他们的工作。

9. Failing to test your testers, or testing them too much: Everyone's job needs to be evaluated, but not incessantly. At some point, you have to trust people to do their jobs without a boss standing over them.

10.假装演示是测试：你可以是这个的发送端或接收端。我不确定哪个更糟——愚弄别人还是愚弄自己。

10. Pretending demonstrations are tests: You can be on the sending or receiving end of this one. I'm not sure which is worse— fooling others or fooling yourself.

第 11 章_信息获取

Chapter_11_Information Intake

 

“响亮的声音无法与清晰的声音相提并论，即使是耳语。” - 巴里·尼尔·考夫曼 (Barry Neil Kaufman)，智取您的业力：和其他预定条件（马萨诸塞州谢菲尔德：Epic Century，1996 年）。

"A loud voice cannot compete with a clear voice, even if it's a whisper." - Barry Neil Kaufman, Out-Smarting Your Karma: And Other Preordained Conditions (Sheffield, Mass.: Epic Century, 1996).

在 William Perry 和 Randall Rice 的实用著作《克服软件测试的十大挑战》中，以下四个挑战与纯粹的沟通问题有关：“与开发人员建立关系”、“向经理解释测试”、“与客户和用户沟通”，和“不得不说不”。其他六个挑战也有很强的沟通成分，当您记得测试是一种信息收集活动时，这就不足为奇了。[10]

In William Perry and Randall Rice's useful book Surviving the Top Ten Challenges of Software Testing, the following four challenges pertain to pure communication problems: "Building Relationships with Developers," "Explaining Testing to Managers," " Communicating with Customers—and Users," and "Having to Say No." The other six challenges also have strong communication components, which is not surprising when you remember that testing is an information-gathering activity. [10]

使用 Satir 交互模型来阐明通信。

Use the Satir Interaction Model to unravel communications.

在我与测试人员及其经理的咨询中，我经常采用一种有用的沟通模型，该模型改编自已故家庭治疗师弗吉尼亚萨蒂尔的互动模型。萨提尔被认为是家庭治疗“沟通学派”的创始人，她的互动模型告诉我们一些关于人们头脑中发生的事情的令人惊讶的事情，包括在人与人之间的互动过程中。萨提亚使用这个模型来帮助人们理解家庭的复杂动态，作为每天都在发生快速、神秘互动的系统。我发现它有助于帮助软件测试人员改进他们观察和交流软件状态的系统（其中随时可能发生快速、神秘的交互）。

In my consulting with testers and their managers, I often employ a useful model of communication adapted from the late family therapist Virginia Satir's Interaction Model. Satir is considered to be the founder of the "communication school" of family therapy and her Interaction Model tells us some surprising things about what goes on inside people's heads, including during interactions between people. Satir used this model to help people understand the complex dynamics of families as systems in which fast, mysterious interactions happen every day. I find it useful for helping software testers improve their systems of observing and communicating about software status (where fast, mysterious interactions may happen at any minute).

完整的 Satir 交互模型旨在解释人们交互时发生的情况。我使用该模型来改进我接收和提供有关测试的信息的方式，例如当我进行以下活动时：

The full Satir Interaction Model was designed to account for what happens when people interact. I use the model to improve how I receive and give information about testing, such as when I am doing activities like the following:

• 观察被测系统的行为

• observing the behavior of systems under test

• 直接与他人互动

• interacting directly with others

• 撰写和理解测试报告

• writing and understanding testing reports

• 在工作中观察用户，如可用性测试或 Beta 测试

• watching users at work, as in usability testing or beta testing

• 提出意见和结论

• presenting observations and conclusions

• 在工作中观察自己，以提高

• observing myself at work, in order to improve

模型的工作是简化复杂的过程，因此，作为第一个近似值，Satir 交互模型将任何通信过程分解为四个主要部分：摄入、意义、重要性和响应，如下图所示：

A model's job is to simplify a complex process, so, as a first approximation, the Satir Interaction Model breaks down any communication process into four major parts: intake, meaning, significance, and response, as shown in the following figure:

录取

Intake

在这个过程的摄入部分，一个人从世界上获取信息。有些人认为这个活动描述了整个观察过程，但还有更多的事情要做。摄入不会“刚好发生”；它还涉及一个选择过程。无论我们是否意识到我们在观察时是有选择性的，我们实际上是在对我们的所见所闻进行大量选择。它是摄取，而不是简单的输入。

During the intake part of the process, a person takes information from the world. Some people believe that this activity describes the entire observation process, but there is much more going on. Intake does not "just happen"; it also involves a selection process. Whether or not we recognize that we are being selective as we observe, we are actually exercising a great many choices about what we see and hear. It's intake, not simply input.

意义

Meaning

在这个过程的意义部分，有人考虑感官摄入并赋予它意义。有些人认为意义在于数据，但同样的摄入量可以有许多不同的含义。当用餐者对服务员说“汤还可以”时，她的意思可能只是汤完全令人满意，或者即使汤不是她想要的她也会接受，或者汤非常棒，远远超过期望，或者她的意思可能是“别再问汤的事了，让我一个人享受我的饭菜。”

During the meaning part of the process, someone considers the sensory intake and gives it a meaning. Some people believe that the meaning lies in the data, but the same intake can have many different meanings. When a diner says to a waiter, "The soup's okay," she could mean simply that the soup is completely satisfactory, or that she'll take the soup even if it's not what she wanted, or that the soup is superb and way beyond expectations, or she could mean "stop asking about the soup and leave me alone to enjoy my meal."

换句话说，摄入数据没有意义，直到有人赋予它们意义。意义过程也与摄入过程相互作用。例如，某些推断的含义可能会导致我们接受更多信息或不同的信息。如果汤不是用餐者想要的，服务员可能会询问如何改进。但其他解释可能会导致服务员完全停止进餐——就像“别再问汤了，让我一个人享受我的饭菜”。

In other words, intake data have no meaning until some person gives them meaning. The meaning process also interacts with the intake process. For example, certain inferred meanings may lead us to take in more information or different information. If the soup isn't exactly what the diner wants, a waiter might ask how it could be improved. But other interpretations might lead the waiter to shut off intake altogether—as with "stop asking about the soup and leave me alone to enjoy my meal."

我们将在第 12 章中更详细地研究该过程的意义部分。

We look at the meaning part of the process in greater detail in Chapter 12.

意义

Significance

数据可能会暗示某些含义，但绝不会暗示它们的重要性。这些信息对我很重要吗？有多重要？只有接收方才能做出此决定。

Data may suggest certain meanings, but never their significance. Is this information important to me? How important? Only the receiver can make this determination.

为什么会有显着性步骤？如果我们不根据信息的重要性对信息进行分类和选择，我们所感知的世界将充满大量数据。一旦我们确定了重要性，我们就可以优先考虑一些摄入模式及其意义，而在很大程度上忽略其余部分。

Why is there a signficance step? The world we perceive would be an overwhelming flood of data if we did not categorize and select information in the context of its significance. Once we have determined significance, we can give priority to a few patterns of intake and their meanings and largely ignore the rest.

我们赋予摄入量及其意义的重要性可能会导致我们改变我们的摄入量和意义过程。例如，如果我们认为摄入非常重要，我们可能会停止关注其他摄入来源，而将注意力集中在这一来源上。相反，如果我们认为摄入量不重要，我们可能会转移注意力。

The significance we assign to an intake and its meaning may lead us to alter our intake and meaning processes. For instance, if we decide that the intake is extremely important, we may stop paying attention to other sources of intake and focus our attention on just this one. Conversely, if we think the intake is unimportant, we may shift our attention away.

我们将在第 13 章检验重要性。

We examine significance in Chapter 13.

回复

Response

在流程的响应部分，一个人制定要采取的行动。软件测试人员和他们的经理是观察者，但他们绝不是被动的观察者。他们可能不会（也不应该）立即对他们观察到的一切和任何事情做出反应，但他们会（并且应该）根据观察对观察者的重要性筛选并分配观察的优先级，并将它们存储起来以指导未来的行动。测试人员对不参考可能的操作的观察不感兴趣。例如，测试人员对“寻求更多数据！”的响应特别感兴趣。我们将在第 14 章进一步探讨响应。

During the response part of the process, a person formulates an action to take. Software testers and their managers are observers, but they are never passive observers. They may not (and should not) respond immediately to everything and anything they observe, but they do (and should) sift through and assign priorities to observations according to how important they are to the observer, and store them away to guide future actions. Testers are not interested in observation without reference to possible action. For instance, testers are especially interested in the response, "Seek more data!" We look further at response in Chapter 14.

如果您是一名试图与经理沟通的测试人员，或者是一名努力理解测试人员试图告诉您的内容的经理，Satir 交互模型可以帮助您调试交互。

If you're a tester trying to communicate with a manager, or a manager struggling to understand what a tester is trying to tell you, the Satir Interaction Model can help you debug your interaction.

人们有选择地倾听。

People listen selectively.

涉及测试人员的通信出现问题的一种方式是在引入步骤中出现故障。有些信息很难准确理解，因为人们不想听到它们。例如，经理们特别擅长有选择地倾听有关发布和发货日期的信息。测试人员可能会说，“按照目前我们发现和修复错误的速度，我们在 9 月 1 日之前发布的可能性很小。” 工作危在旦夕的项目经理可能会听到，“等等等等，我们可以在 9 月 1 日之前发货。”

One way communications involving testers go awry is through a failure in the intake step. Some messages are hard to take in accurately because people don't want to hear them. Managers, for example, are particularly good at selective listening about release and ship dates. A tester may say, "At the current rate we're finding and fixing bugs, there's very little chance that we can ship by the first of September." The project manager whose job is on the line is likely to hear, "Blah blah blah blah we can ship by the first of September."

你怎样才能避免这个问题？首先，只提供和接受书面形式的日期。其次，不要提供或接受“点日期”——指定精确 24 小时周期的日期，例如“9 月 1 日”。然后，仅当估计日期被写为范围时才给出和接受它们——例如，“我们估计我们将在 8 月 1 日至 8 月 21 日的时间范围内发布版本 4”——但即便如此，较晚的日期通常会被排除在外摄入量，人们只在心里记下较早的日期。为了强调范围，将估计日期作为概率与日期的关系图给出。我称这些为机会图。

How can you avoid this problem? First off, only give and accept dates in written form. Second, don't give or accept "point dates"—dates that specify a precise 24-hour period, such as "the first of September." Then, give and accept estimated dates only when they are written as ranges—"we estimate that we will release Version 4 in the August 1st to August 21st timeframe," for example—but even then, the later date will often be dropped out of the intake, with people making a mental note of only the earlier date. To emphasize the range, give estimated dates as graphs of probability versus date. I call these what's-the-chance graphs.

数据来源影响摄入量。

The source of the data influences intake.

人们倾向于对从不同来源收到的信息做出不同的反应——通常是根据发送者预先确定消息的重要性。如果您在让人们关注您的测试报告时遇到困难，请尝试通过声誉会让收件人改变或放弃他们的接收过滤器的人发送它们。

People tend to make different responses to information received from different sources—often predetermining the importance of a message based on the sender. If you're having trouble getting people to pay attention to your test reports, try sending them via someone whose reputation will make the recipients change or drop their intake filters.

作为顾问，我经常扮演这个中介角色。不听自己员工意见的经理们通常会听我的。如果他们不打算听我的话，他们一开始就雇用我是愚蠢的。

As a consultant, I often act in this intermediary role. Managers who won't listen to their own employees often listen to me. If they didn't intend to listen to me, they would be foolish to hire me in the first place.

如果您发现其他人更愿意接受您必须传达给其他人的信息，请将这些知识视为测试结果。通过问自己“我过去做了什么会让人们认为我不是可靠的消息来源？我将来需要做什么来提高他们对我作为消息来源的信任度”来继续测试？

If you discover that others are more willing to accept information you have to convey when another person delivers it, think of the knowledge as a test result. Continue testing by asking yourself, "What have I done in the past that would make people think I'm not a reliable source? What do I need to do in the future to raise their trust in me as a source?"

首先检查自己，但最后，您可能会发现问题出在您试图与之沟通的人身上。无论如何，有些人就是不会听来自测试人员的任何东西。如果那是真的，你最好找个别的地方工作，而不是试图修正你的沟通方式——尽管你可能也需要这样做。

Examine yourself first, but in the end, you may find that the problem lies with the person with whom you are trying to communicate. Some people just won't listen to anything that comes from testers, regardless. If that's true, you're better off looking for someplace else to work, rather than try to fix your communication style—though you may need to do that, too.

时机有所作为。

Timing makes a difference.

人们在关注别处时会错过信息。如果你没有引起别人的注意，那么你提供信息就没有意义，因为那个人不太可能接受它。例如，觉得自己已将下一次加薪押在产品通过所有测试上的开发人员不太可能听到有关测试失败的消息。

People miss information when they're paying attention somewhere else. If you don't have someone's attention, there's no point in your providing information because that person won't be likely to accept it. For instance, developers who feel they have staked their next raise on their product passing all tests are not likely to hear a message about test failures.

在责备的环境中，管理人员倾向于认为不断提高赌注（无论是金钱上的、情感上的还是其他方面的）会改进测试。但是，如果赌注太高，人们只会听到责备，因为由此产生的恐惧而充耳不闻。例如，那些认为如果不按时交付产品，他们的工作就会受到威胁的经理将不会接受似乎会增加迟到概率的信息。在极端情况下——我经常看到——经理干脆完全忽略测试报告。

In a blaming environment, managers tend to believe that constantly raising the stakes (whether monetary, emotional, or otherwise) will improve testing. But, if the stakes are too high, people will hear nothing but the blame, made deaf by the fear it engenders. For example, managers who believe their jobs are at stake if they don't ship a product on time will not be open to information that seems to increase the probability of lateness. In the extreme case—which I see rather frequently—the manager simply ignores the test reports altogether.

有时，当受到过多信息的轰炸时，人们会关闭或调低摄入量。测试人员可能会报告如此多的错误，以至于分类会议需要花费数小时。他们可能写了很多报告，没人能读完。在某些情况下，测试人员自己可能就是受害者——收到如此多的规范页面，以至于他们在不得不针对这些规范进行测试之前不可能彻底阅读它们。

At times, people turn off their intake, or turn it way down, when bombarded with too much information. Testers may report so many bugs that triage meetings take hours. They may write so many reports that no one can read them all. In some cases, the testers themselves may be the victims—receiving so many pages of specs that they can't possibly read them thoroughly before having to test against them.

发生的信息过载是信息本身——产生关于组织及其产生和处理信息的方式的元信息。注意到过载的测试人员可能想要修改这些习惯。例如，我的一位客户定期召开分流会议，将大量关键人员长时间捆绑在一起。结果，许多错误报告没有被分类，或者被分类得太粗心或太晚而没有帮助。我们修改了分类程序以遵循三个规则：

That information overload has occurred is information in and of itself—yielding meta-information about an organization and the ways it produces and handles information. Testers who notice overload may want to modify these habits. For example, one of my clients regularly held triage meetings that tied up large numbers of key people for long periods of time. As a result, many bug reports were not triaged, or were triaged far too carelessly or too late to be helpful. We modified the triage procedure to follow three rules:

1. 仅使用四种错误报告类别：0 级、1 级、2 级和 3 级。

1. Use four bug-report categories only: level 0, level 1, level 2, and level 3.

（我们将类别数量从十个减少到四个。）

(We reduced the number of categories from ten to four.)

2. 在用临时的“0 级”分类将其搁置之前，在任何一个错误报告上花费的时间不超过一分钟。（我们使用厨房计时器来执行此规则和规则 3。）

2. Spend no more than one minute on any one bug report before setting it aside with a temporary "level-0" classification. (We used a kitchen timer to enforce both this rule and Rule 3.)

3. 如果时间允许重新检查临时“0 级”错误报告，在将其发送到其他地方以获取更多信息之前，花在任何一个上的时间不超过五分钟。

3. If time permits reexamination of temporary "level-0" bug reports, spend no more than five minutes on any one before sending it elsewhere for additional information.

我们根据以下理由将每个错误报告分配到四个级别之一：0 级问题正在阻止其他测试。我们因为无法在一分钟内分类而搁置的东西被认为是阻塞测试，当然，如果它导致长时间的争论使许多测试人员束手无策，它就会被阻止。如果我们在考虑所有错误后还有时间，我们可以再花五分钟来处理每个临时 0 级错误报告。级别1表示如果此问题未解决，则产品无法发货。级别2意味着如果不解决此问题，产品的价值将大大降低。3级表示只有在产品发货时存在大量类似问题时才重要的错误。

We assigned each bug report to one of four levels according to the following rationale: A level-0 issue is blocking other testing. Something that we set aside because it couldn't be classified in one minute was deemed to be blocking testing, which, of course, it would if it led to long arguments that tied up many testers. If there was time left after we considered all bugs, we could spend another five minutes on each of the temporary level-0 bug reports. A level 1 indicated that the product could not ship if this issue was not resolved. A level 2 meant that the value of the product would be significantly reduced if this issue was not resolved. A level 3 indicated a bug that would be important only if there were large numbers of similar issues when the product shipped.

使用这三个规则，分类团队能够在不到两个小时的时间内对 129 个未分类错误的全部积压进行分类——仅返回三个错误以获取更多信息。其他测试部门分类和解决错误的速度可能会有所不同，但长时间的分类争论可能更多地告诉你团队的心理，而不是分类错误的难度。

Using the three rules, the triage team was able to classify the entire backlog of 129 unclassified bugs in less than two hours— sending only three bugs back for more information. The speed with which other test departments can classify and resolve bugs may vary, but long triage arguments may be telling you more about the psychology of your team than about the difficulty of classifying bugs.

您可以通过减少测试次数来传达更多信息。

You may convey more information by reducing the number of tests.

对于订阅 The Test Everything Fallacy 的人来说，这似乎是自相矛盾的，但通过减少测试生成的数据量，您实际上可以获得更多信息。这是重要性反馈到摄入决定的地方。通过询问“哪些测试将对进一步的测试和开发产生最大的影响？”来缩小您的潜在测试集。

It may seem paradoxical to those who subscribe to The Test Everything Fallacy, but by reducing the amount of data generated by tests, you may actually gain more information. Here's where significance feeds back into the intake decision. Narrow your set of potential tests by asking, "Which tests will have the greatest impact on further testing and development?"

通过了解这个问题的答案，您通常可以确定应该首先查找哪些信息。例如，如果系统在只有一个用户登录时无法返回任何结果，那么测试人员花费数周时间尝试根据系统负载运行性能测试将是愚蠢的。

By learning the answer to this question, you can often determine what information you should find first. For instance, if a system fails to return any results when just one user is logged in, it would be silly for testers to spend weeks attempting to run performance tests based on system load.

矛盾的是，有些信息看似重要，但实际上无关紧要。您可能认为如果安装失败，测试将被阻止，但安装脚本通常独立于实际软件。如果通过钩子或骗子（但不是通过最终安装脚本）您可以获得它们所属的所有部分，您可以测试软件的功能，同时允许并行测试和修复安装脚本。

Paradoxically, some information might seem critical but is actually irrelevant. You might think testing would be blocked if the installation fails, but installation script is often independent of the actual software. If by hook or by crook (but not by the ultimate installation script) you can get all the pieces and parts where they belong, you may be able to test the features of the software, while allowing a parallel effort to test and repair the installation script.

从盒子外面寻求摄入量。
