Seek intake from outside the box.

几年前在浏览互联网时，我读到一个故事，讲的是一个女人打电话给服务台，说她的打印机出了问题。技术支持代表问她是否“在 Windows 下运行它”。

While cruising the Internet some years back, I read a story about a woman who called a help desk about a problem with her printer. The tech support rep asked her whether she was "running it under Windows."

“不，”女人说，“我的办公桌在门旁边。但这是一个好点。坐在我隔壁小隔间里的那个人在窗户下面，他的工作正常。”

"No," the woman said, "my desk is next to the door. But that's a good point. The man sitting in the cubicle next to me is under a window, and his is working fine."

不管真假，这个故事都有一定的道理。有时，我们关注范围之外的潜在数据会影响程序的行为。设备上的阳光会升高温度并导致设备运行不稳定。静电、振动、雷达也是如此，还有谁知道呢？当一台测试机器没有按您预期的方式工作时，可能是其他人使用了它并改变了它的状态。可能是操作系统出了问题。

True or not, this story has a grain of truth in it. Sometimes potential data lying outside our scope of attention can influence a program's behavior. Sunlight on a device can raise the temperature and cause the device to behave erratically. So too can static electricity, vibration, radar, and who knows what else? When a test machine doesn't work the way you expect, maybe somebody else used it and changed its state. Maybe the operating system has been jiggered.

不要混淆解释和摄取。

Don't confuse interpretation with intake.

人类的思想渴望意义。如果你给人们提供一些随机的数据，他们将很难从中推测出意义——他们会很快从吸收阶段进入意义阶段，他们不会意识到这样做。一些看似传达直截了当的事实的陈述实际上需要接受者的解释。

The human mind craves meaning. If you feed people a random bit of data, they'll struggle to divine meaning from it—and they'll move from the intake phase to the meaning phase so fast they won't be aware of doing so. Some statements that appear to convey straightforward facts are actually subject to interpretation by the receiver.

以下是我从客户的测试报告中收集到的几个例子：

Following are a few examples I've gleaned from clients' test reports:

• “错误太多。” “太多”是为了什么？也许只有正确的数字。有时一个太多了，有时一百个也可以。

• "There were too many bugs." "Too many" for what? Maybe there were just the right number. Sometimes one is too many, and other times one hundred is okay.

• “有很多错误。” “很多”与什么相比？

• "There were a lot of bugs." "A lot" compared with what?

• “只有四个错误。” “只有四个”比预期好还是坏？

• "There were only four bugs." Is "only four" better or worse than expected?

• “有四个错误。” “有”是一种解释。演讲者不知道“有”多少错误，只知道发现了多少错误。说，“我们发现了四个错误”，并说明它们是在什么条件下被发现的。

• "There were four bugs." "There were" is an interpretation. The speaker doesn't know how many bugs "there were," only how many were found. Say, "We found four bugs," and say under what conditions they were found.

• “测试表明该项目不得不下滑。” 这实际上是向前迈出重要一步。测试本身并没有显示任何这样的东西，但是有人认为测试只有一个意义，而且那个意义只有一个意义。

• "Tests show that the project has to slip." This is actually a jump ahead to the significance step. Tests themselves don't show any such thing, but someone has decided that there's only one meaning to the tests, and only one significance to that meaning.

提出数据问题以过滤掉解释。

Ask The Data Question to filter out interpretations.

当有人在你需要数据时向你提供测试解释时，请使用数据问题：你看到或听到（或闻到、尝到或感觉到）是什么导致你做出这种解释？通常，您将不得不不断重复数据问题，直到达到您想要的无意义数据的水平。然后，当您最终拥有经过净化的数据时，您可以逆向执行该过程并继续使诸如“我们发现了四个错误”之类的陈述具有意义。

When someone presents you with test interpretations when you want data, use The Data Question: What did you see or hear (or smell or taste or feel) that led you to that interpretation? Generally, you will have to keep repeating The Data Question until you reach the level of meaning-free data you desire. Then, when you finally have the purified data, you can reverse the process and proceed to making meaning of a statement such as "we found four bugs."

概括

Summary

摄入是一个主动的过程。尝试了解限制您的摄入量的因素、信息来源以及数据如何因有偏见的含义而变味。你不是受害者，将数据输入你，但至少有可能控制你接收的内容。

Intake is an active process. Try to be aware of factors that limit your intake, sources of information, and how data may be flavored by biased meaning. You are not a victim, having data put into you, but are at least potentially in control of what you take in.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1. 不去想你在寻找什么信息：不要只接受到来的信息。你有选择。

1. Not thinking about what information you're after: Don't just take what comes. You have choices.

2.不主动寻找你想要的信息：百分之九十九的信息对于测试任务是无用的，但如果你知道如何从糟粕中筛选出金子，那么仍然有很多信息。

2. Not actively seeking the information you're after: Ninety-nine percent of information is useless for the task of testing, but there's still plenty if you know how to sift the gold from the dross.

3.将摄入量和意义混为一谈：在有人确定其意义之前，数据是没有意义的。不同的人赋予相同的数据不同的含义。收集数据，然后坐下来思考至少三种可能的含义。

3. Conflating intake and meaning: Data are meaningless until someone determines their meaning. Different people give different meanings to the same data. Gather data, then sit down and ponder at least three possible meanings.

4.禁止测试人员在某些地方寻找错误：那些被禁止的地方可能充满了数据。

4. Forbidding testers to look for bugs in certain places: Those forbidden places can be lush with data to intake.

5.未能提供足够的检测设备和工具：你会期望病理学家在没有显微镜的情况下工作吗？什么是测试人员而不是软件病理学家？（请注意，工具不必是商业包——如后一章所述。）

5. Failing to provide adequate equipment and tools for testing: Would you expect a pathologist to work without a microscope? What is a tester but a software pathologist? (Please note that tools need not be commercial packages—as elaborated in a later chapter.)

6.屈服于金象综合症：软件测试专家 James Bach 将现代测试中的一种可怕病症称为金象综合症：白象可能是一件大而无用的东西，但如果它是金子做的并且成本很高钱，对某些人来说，无论如何都想尝试使用它。昂贵的测试工具如果设计糟糕、不可靠，或者迫使测试人员以他们不会选择的方式进行测试，除非工具很方便，否则会造成很多麻烦。如果这样的工具便宜，我们会毫不犹豫地把它扔掉。但如果它很贵，买它的人不想看起来像个傻瓜——从而变成一个更大的傻瓜。

6. Succumbing to The Golden Elephant Syndrome: Software test expert James Bach calls one of the terrible pathologies of modern testing The Golden Elephant Syndrome: A white elephant may be a big, useless thing, but if it's made of gold and costs a lot of money, it's tempting to some people to try to use it anyway. Expensive test tools can cause a lot of trouble if they are badly designed, unreliable, or force testers to test in ways they wouldn't have chosen except that it's convenient for the tool. If such a tool were cheap, we wouldn't hesitate to throw it away. But if it's expensive, the person who bought it doesn't want to look like a fool—and thus becomes a bigger fool.

Chapter_12_Making Meaning

Chapter_12_Making Meaning

 

”优柔寡断，n.成功的主要因素；‘因为，’托马斯·布鲁博德爵士说，‘只有一种方法可以什么都不做，而有多种方法可以做某事，因此，可以肯定的是，只有一种方法是正确的，由此可见，犹豫不决的人走入歧途的机会没有向前推进的人那么多——这是对这个问题最清楚、最令人满意的解释。” - Ambrose Bierce，美国作家 (1842–1914) ，The Unabridged Devil's Dictionary，编辑。DE Schultz 和 ST Joshi（乔治亚州雅典：佐治亚大学出版社，2002 年）。

"INDECISION, n. The chief element of success; 'for whereas,' saith Sir Thomas Brewbold, 'there is but one way to do nothing and diverse ways to do something, whereof, to a surety, only one is the right way, it followeth that he who from indecision standeth still hath not so many chances of going astray as he who pusheth forwards'—a most clear and satisfactory exposition on the matter." - Ambrose Bierce, American Author (1842–1914),The Unabridged Devil's Dictionary,eds. D.E. Schultz and S.T. Joshi (Athens, Ga.: University of Georgia Press, 2002).

尽管 Thomas Brewbold 爵士的官方声明是虚构的，但在解释测试数据时犹豫不决确实是一件好事——在一定程度上。这一点是由三原则定义的，它说，在测试数据解释的上下文中：如果你想不出至少三种可能的测试结果解释，那么你想的还不够。

Despite the fictitious Sir Thomas Brewbold's gobbledygook pronouncement, indecision, when applied in the interpretation of test data, is indeed a fine thing—up to a point. That point is defined by The Rule of Three, which says, in this context of test data interpretation: If you can't think of at least three possible interpretations of the test result, you haven't thought enough.

让我们看一些例子，都从 Rocky 开始，他是一个测试人员，他给出了以下坏消息：“测试表明项目不得不失败。有四个错误。” 过滤掉 Rocky 的解释后，您只剩下“有四个错误”。生姜是项目经理。她现在做什么？

Let's look at some examples, all starting with Rocky, a tester who gives the following bad news: "Tests show that the project has to slip. There were four bugs." After filtering out Rocky's interpretations, you're left with "There were four bugs." Ginger is the project manager. What does she do now?

案例一：四个Bug——五种含义

Case 1: Four Bugs—Five Meanings

金杰问洛基：“你测试了什么？”

Ginger asks Rocky, "What did you test?"

“我测试了 X-TERMINATOR，整个东西，”Rocky 愤怒地回答。

"I tested X-TERMINATOR, the whole thing," Rocky replies indignantly.

Ginger 有她的怀疑，但她试图表现得不置可否。“哦，很好。我想阅读错误报告。”

Ginger has her suspicions, but she tries to sound noncommittal. "Oh, good. I'd like to read the bug reports."

洛基的语气现在是防御性的。“我还没有把它们写下来。”

Rocky's tone is now defensive. "I haven't written them down yet."

姜想，要是不写下来，连别人都没有告诉，这就是化验结果吗？但她只是问，“哦？你为什么不呢？”

Ginger thinks, If it's not written down and you haven't even told anyone, is it a test result? but she merely asks, "Oh? Why haven't you?"

洛基看着她，脸上的表情清楚地表明他认为她愚蠢至极。“这应该是显而易见的。XTERMINATOR 是错误跟踪系统，其中一个错误是我无法登录报告错误。”

Rocky looks at her, the expression on his face clearly showing that he thinks she's incredibly stupid. "It should be obvious. XTERMINATOR is the bug-tracking system, and one of the bugs is that I can't log in to report bugs."

“哦，”Ginger 说，既困惑又自言自语。“那么，不知道另外三只虫子会是什么？”

"Oh," says Ginger, puzzled and thinking aloud. "In that case, I wonder what the other three bugs can be?"

“登录屏幕上有三个拼写错误。”

"There are three spelling errors on the log-in screen."

生姜可能会从这个简短的交流中得出以下五种含义中的任何一种或全部：

Ginger might come away from this brief exchange with any or all of the following five meanings:

(a) Ginger 可能会得出结论，Rocky 说他测试了“整个事情”的声明并不是对所测试内容的非常有用的描述，因为如果 Rocky 无法登录，他可以测试什么？

(a) Ginger might conclude that Rocky's statement that he tested "the whole thing" isn't a very useful characterization of what was tested, because if Rocky couldn't log on, what could he have tested?

(b) Ginger 可能想知道登录问题是否只是登录中的一个小故障，可能会在几分钟内修复。她不太了解 XTERMINATOR 的状态，但她突然想到，如果她的开发人员甚至无法正确登录，系统的其余部分可能会更糟。(c) Ginger 对 Rocky 报告情况的方式以及 Rocky 的主动性有一些疑问。她可能会推测，虽然他可能无法登录 X-TERMINATOR，但他仍然可以访问测试人员之前使用的任何报告系统，或者使用优质的老式纸笔。她可能还想知道为什么测试人员仍然使用未经测试的错误报告系统。

(b) Ginger might wonder whether the problem with log-in could be just a glitch in the log-in, which possibly could be fixed in a few minutes. She doesn't know very much about the state of XTERMINATOR, but it occurs to her that if her developers can't even get the log-in right, maybe the rest of the system is even worse. (c) Ginger has some issues with the way Rocky has reported the situation, as well as with Rocky's initiative. She might speculate that although he may not have been able to log onto X- TERMINATOR, he could still have accessed whatever reporting system the testers were using before or by using good old-fashioned paper and pencil. She might also wonder why the testers are using an untested bug-reporting system anyway.

(d) Ginger 可能想知道 Rocky 测试的目的是否只是检查错误跟踪数据库的演示副本。如果是这样，她认为登录问题可能是一个微不足道的安装问题。

(d) Ginger might wonder whether the purpose of Rocky's testing is simply to check out a demo copy of a bug-tracking database. If that is the case, she supposes that the log-on problem may be a trivial installation difficulty.

(e) Ginger 知道 X-TERMINATOR 应该是商业产品，但认为在登录页面上发现三个拼写错误，X-TERMINATOR 可能不是商业品质的产品。

(e) Ginger knows that X-TERMINATOR is supposed to be a commercial product, but thinks that with three spelling errors found on the log-in page, X-TERMINATOR might not be a commercial-quality product.

案例二：四大Bug——七层意思

Case 2: Four Bugs—Seven Meanings

在另一个宇宙中，案件从相同的入场开始，但进程不同。金杰问洛基：“你测试了什么？” “我测试了 X-TERMINATOR，整个东西，”Rocky 愤怒地回答。

In an alternate universe, the case starts with the same intake, but runs a different course. Ginger asks Rocky, "What did you test?" "I tested X-TERMINATOR, the whole thing," Rocky replies indignantly.

Ginger 有她的怀疑，但她试图表现得不置可否。“哦，很好。我想阅读错误报告。”

Ginger has her suspicions, but she tries to sound noncommittal. "Oh, good. I'd like to read the bug reports."

洛基递给她一张单页打印件。“他们来了。” Ginger 阅读错误报告并发现以下内容：

Rocky hands her a one-page printout. "Here they are." Ginger reads the bug reports and finds the following:

错误 1：帐户 #1 具有错误的读/写权限。

Bug 1: Account #1 has the wrong read/write permission.

错误 2：帐户 #2 具有错误的读/写权限。

Bug 2: Account #2 has the wrong read/write permission.

错误 3：帐户 #3 具有错误的读/写权限。

Bug 3: Account #3 has the wrong read/write permission.

错误 4：帐户 #4 具有错误的读/写权限。

Bug 4: Account #4 has the wrong read/write permission.

让我们再次脱离这个故事，检查 Ginger 可能从错误报告中得出的一些含义。

Let's break from the story again and examine some of the meanings Ginger might form from the bug reports.

(a) “整个事情”并不是对所测试内容的非常有用的描述。

(a) "The whole thing" isn't a very useful characterization of what was tested.

(b) Rocky 在权限区域进行了大部分测试。

(b) Rocky did most of his testing in the permissions area.

(c) X-TERMINATOR 中的大多数错误都在权限方面。

(c) Most of the bugs in X-TERMINATOR are in the permissions area.

(d) 可能只有一个与四份报告相关的潜在错误。

(d) Maybe there's only one underlying fault related to the four reports.

(e) Rocky 可能不是很聪明，因为他甚至没有暗示这些错误之间可能存在关系。

(e) Rocky may not be very bright because he's not even suggesting that there might be a relationship among these bugs.

(f) Rocky 可能非常聪明，因为他不会自动假设只有一个错误并丢弃假定的冗余数据。

(f) Rocky may be very bright because he doesn't automatically assume that there's only one bug and throw away supposedly redundant data.

(g) Rocky 没有说什么构成错误，也没有解释他做出该决定的原则或机制。这些报告中的每一个都可以引用一组不同的错误读/写权限。

(g) Rocky hasn't said what constitutes wrongness, nor has he explained by what principle or mechanism he makes that determination. Each one of these reports could refer to a different set of wrong read/write permissions.

请注意，案例 1 和案例 2 以完全相同的方式开始，将完全相同的报告交给项目经理。显然，测试报告不仅仅是编写报告。

Notice that Case 1 and Case 2 begin in exactly the same way, with exactly the same report being handed to the project manager. Evidently, there's more to test reports than simply writing them.

案例 3：四个错误——自己定义

Case 3: Four Bugs—Make Your Own Meanings

想测试自己是否真正了解三法则？是的？好的。通过编写您自己的案例来测试您自己，该案例以与案例 1 和案例 2 相同的方式开始，“有四个错误”，但基于您自己的经验。

Want to test yourself to determine whether you really understand The Rule of Three? Yes? Good. Test yourself by writing your own case that begins the same way as Case 1 and Case 2, with "There are four bugs," but based on your own experience.

James Bach 向我发送了以下案例，以回应我邀请测试人员从 Ginger 的评论开始进行自我测试，“哦，很好。我想阅读错误报告。”

James Bach sent me the following case in response to my invitation to testers to test themselves starting at Ginger's comment, "Oh, good. I'd like to read the bug reports."

“我只能告诉你，”洛基说。“第一个错误是该产品似乎是基于我编写并作为共享软件发布的错误跟踪系统的盗版源代码。第二个错误是该文档似乎是我的错误跟踪手册的剽窃版本第三个错误是该产品应该被称为“XTERMINATOR”，但是，如您所见，启动画面清楚地写着“ROCKY'S BUG MANAGER”。第四个错误是我的版权声明被删除了！如果你需要看书面报告，我可以让我的律师给你发一份经过认证的副本。”

"I can just tell you," says Rocky. "Bug number one is that this product appears to be based on pirated source code from a bug-tracking system I wrote and released as shareware. Bug number two is that the documentation appears to be a plagiarized version of the manual from my bug-tracking system. Bug number three is that the product is supposed to be called 'XTERMINATOR,' yet, as you can see, the splash screen clearly says 'ROCKY'S BUG MANAGER.' The fourth bug is that my copyright notice has been removed! If you need to see a written report, I can have my lawyer send you a certified copy."

我想通过这些例子说明什么？一个目标是向您展示解释数据以产生意义需要勤奋和开放的心态。当然，您应该看到，一个简单的错误计数作为测试报告几乎毫无用处，除非您将其用作进一步调查的起点。不要错误地认为更漂亮的报告更好。如果您认为您的报告系统似乎不需要阅读、分析和解释来赋予意义，那么这意味着您正在被您的报告系统所操纵。无论测试结果如何呈现给您，请注意您可能会被它们看似客观的情况所误导。请注意，三原则说要搜索至少三个含义。只要您将它们全部检查出来，欢迎您选择三个以上。

What am I trying to show by these examples? One goal is to show you that interpreting data to make meaning requires diligence and an open mind. Certainly you should see that a simple bug count is less than useless as a test report unless you use it as a starting point for further investigation. Don't make the mistake of thinking that fancier reports are any better. If you think you have a reporting system that doesn't seem to require reading and analyzing and interpreting to assign meaning, all that means is that you're being manipulated by your reporting system. No matter how test results are presented to you, be aware that you can be misled by their seeming objectivity. Notice that The Rule of Three says to search for at least three meanings. You're welcome to go for more than three, as long as you check them all out.

在你解释之前知道你在期待什么。

Know what you're expecting before you interpret.

计算机科学家 Alan Perlis 曾经告诉我，“没有错误的程序，只有不同的程序。” 直到几个月后，当与我一起工作的团队遇到难题时，我才理解他。我正在为计算机操作员设计一个体验式培训计划，并且想要一个模拟，让操作员可以在操作系统崩溃后同时运行多个程序来练习重新启动操作系统。这不是你可以在讲座中真正学到的东西，所以我需要一个可以随机方式、随机时间使操作系统崩溃的程序。

Computer scientist Alan Perlis once told me, "There are no wrong programs, only different programs." I didn't understand him until a few months later when the team I was working with ran into a difficult problem. I was designing an experiential training program for computer operators, and wanted a simulation that would allow operators to practice restarting the operating system after it crashed while running several programs simultaneously. It's not something you can really learn in a lecture, so I needed a program that would crash the operating system in random ways, at random times.

一遍又一遍地运行这个崩溃模拟器会给操作员大量的练习——但尽管我们可能会尝试，但我们无法设计一个以这种方式使操作系统崩溃的程序。我们正要沮丧地放弃时，一位团队成员说：“等一下。我们不需要构建随机碰撞模拟器。我们已经有了一个。”

Running this crash-simulator over and over would give the operators plenty of practice—but try as we might, we couldn't design a program that crashed the operating system in this way. We were about to give up in frustration when one member of the team said, "Wait a minute. We don't have to build a random-crash simulator. We already have one."

事实上，我们做到了，而且臭名昭著。一些物理学家多年来一直在尝试用一个巨大的、失控的 FORTRAN 程序来模拟某个原子。我们每个人都在不同的时间被叫来帮助他们修复这个程序，这个程序随机崩溃并导致操作系统崩溃。我们拿了一份副本，将其冻结，并用它来培训我们的操作员。

And, indeed, we did, and it was infamous. Some physicists had been trying for years to simulate a certain atom with a huge, out-of-control FORTRAN program. Each of us had, at various times, been called in to help them fix this program, which crashed at random times and brought down the operating system. We took a copy, froze it, and trained our operators with it.

在接下来的四年里（也许更长，但那是我离开现场的时间），物理学家们从未让他们的程序“正确”。不过，对我们来说，它从我们开始使用它的那一刻起就起作用了。它从来没有任何错误，也从来不需要改变。对物理学家来说失败的是对我们来说是一个完美的程序。您通常不会找到完美的程序。

For the next four years (maybe longer but that's when I left the scene), the physicists never got their program "correct." For us, though, it worked from the moment we started using it. It never had any bugs, and never had to be changed. What was a failure for the physicists' purposes was a perfect program for us. It's not often you find a perfect program.

这个有趣（或悲惨）的案例表明，如果你不知道一个程序应该做什么，你就永远不能肯定地说它是错的。在赋予测试报告意义之前，您必须知道您的期望，否则一切看起来或听起来都是正确的。这就是为什么我大力提倡测试先行的理念，即开发人员在编写代码之前编写测试以包含预期结果。五十年前我们就是这样做的，但随着行业趋势将测试与开发分开，这种做法逐渐消失了。

This funny (or tragic) case shows that if you don't know what a program is supposed to do, you can never say with certainty that it's wrong. You have to know what you're expecting before you give meaning to a test report, otherwise everything looks or sounds right. That's why I'm a strong advocate of the test-first philosophy, whereby developers write their tests to include expected results before they write a line of code. It's what we did fifty years ago, but the practice was gradually lost when industry trends separated testing from development.

这种分离最初是因为人们在心理上很难测试自己的程序。如果您依赖测试先行而不依赖结对编程或其他一些需要不止一双眼睛和多个大脑来处理一个程序的过程，那么仍然存在重大风险。有时，测试先行的狂热者认为他们不需要独立的测试人员。由于他们自己的测试主要是在单元级别，然后是主要确认性的验收测试，如果程序简单且独立，他们可能没有独立测试人员的情况是正确的。在更高级别的集成和更高级别的安全要求下工作，他们最好使用由专业人士执行的额外测试。

That separation occurred initially because it's psychologically difficult for people to test their own programs. There's still significant risk if you rely on test-first without pair programming or some other process that casts more than one pair of eyes, and more than one brain, on a program. Sometimes, test-first enthusiasts think they don't also need independent testers. Since their own testing is mainly at the unit level, followed by acceptance testing that is primarily confirmatory, they may be right to go without independent testers if the programs are simple and standalone. Working at higher levels of integration with higher levels of required safety, they'd be well advised to use additional tests performed by specialized professionals.

如果您不知道预期结果怎么办？

What if you don't know what's expected?

如果您在解释测试结果时不知道产品的预期功能，您可以先问以下问题：

If you don't know what a product is expected to do when interpreting test results, you can start by asking the following questions:

• 这件事情是否按照重要的人希望它做的那样做？

• Does this thing do what the people who count want it to do?

• 它不做重要人物不希望它做的事吗？

• Does it not do what the people who count don't want it to do?

• 这些测试结果告诉我什么？

• What do these test results tell me about that?

但是，如果不清楚重要人物想要什么怎么办？在这种情况下，您可以报告您认为他们想要什么、您发现了什么，并列出差异。如果这样做有帮助，您可能想要对他们可能想要的东西提出一些解释，也许您是如何发展这些想法的。但要小心不要用你的想法过度影响他们。如果你这样做，他们可能会同意，只是在你完成测试时说，“不，那不是我想要的。”

But what if it's not clear what the people who count want? In that case, you can report what you thought they wanted, what you found, and list the discrepancies. If it's helpful to do so, you might want to suggest some interpretations of what they could want, and perhaps how you developed those ideas. But be careful you don't over-influence them with your ideas. If you do, they may seem to agree, only to say when you're finished testing, "No, that's not what I wanted."

例如，假设测试显示对话框位于指定内容左侧一个像素。这可以吗？这取决于。

For example, suppose a test shows that a dialogue box was one pixel to the left of what was specified. Is this okay, or not? It depends.

我们可以构建它非常重要的情况和根本不重要的情况。因此，您可以通过不赋予任何意义来处理这种歧义。简单地报告：“对话框在指定内容的左侧一个像素。这可以接受吗？”

We can construct situations in which it would matter very much and situations in which it wouldn't matter at all. So, you can deal with this ambiguity by not making any meaning. Simply report: "The dialogue box is one pixel to the left of what was specified. Is this acceptable?"

使用您拥有的信息。

Use the information you have.

通常，如果不考虑报告中未包含的信息，就无法理解测试报告。在你盲目地要求更多之前，至少从你已经拥有的信息开始。同样，注意充分利用您已有的信息。

Generally, you can't make meaning of a test report without considering information that's not in the report. At least start with the information you already have before you blindly ask for more. Similarly, take care to make the best use of the information you already have.

考虑以下示例：Doug 是一名经理，正在仔细研究错误报告、测试报告、规范和需求文档。他的眼球在纸上。他的一名雇员海伦问道：“道格，你在做什么？”

Consider the following example: Doug, a manager, is poring over bug reports, test reports, specifications, and requirements documents. He is up to his eyeballs in paper. One of his employees, Helen, asks, "Doug, what are you doing?"

Doug 回答说：“我觉得系统有些地方不太对劲。我认为我们不会确定发货日期。我需要证据，所以我正在审查我们迄今为止掌握的所有信息”

Doug replies, "I have a feeling that something isn't quite right with the system. I don't think we're going to make our ship date. I want evidence, so I'm reviewing all the information we have to date."

海伦挠着头，一脸疑惑。“道格，运营部本应在上周进行的验收测试中发生了什么？”

Helen scratches her head and looks puzzled. "Doug, what happened in the acceptance test that Operations was supposed to run last week?"

Doug 抬头叹了口气，“我们没有那个测试的任何结果，所以我不能使用它。”

Doug looks up and sighs, "We don't have any results from that test, so I can't use it."

“我们为什么不呢？”

"Why don't we?"

“因为他们无法安装软件。” “那你还需要什么资料？”

"Because they couldn't get the software installed." "Then what more information do you need?"

运营部无法安装软件本身就是一个至关重要的测试结果。

That Operations was not able to install the software is itself a crucial test result.

使用间接信息。

Use indirect information.

如果记录得当，错误报告包含的信息远不止错误的位置和如何重现问题。注意测试人员有时认为是官僚开销的额外信息：每个测试运行的日期和时间；每份报告的提交日期和时间；谁进行了每项测试；谁提交了每份报告；被测试的软件和版本、操作系统、浏览器、计算机、配置、测试工具和源语言的明确标识); 对早期错误报告的引用；以及各种自由形式的评论。组织这些数据的收集和输入尽可能简单和自动，否则人类不会容忍它。

When properly documented, bug reports contain much more information than just the location of a bug and how to replicate the problem. Pay attention to the extra information that testers sometimes consider to be bureaucratic overhead: the date and time each test was run; the date and time each report was submitted; who ran each test; who submitted each report; unambiguous identification of the software and version(s) tested, the operating system(s), the browser(s), the computer(s), the configuration(s), the test tool(s),and the source language(s); references to earlier bug reports; and all sorts of free-form comments. Organize the collection and entry of this data to be as easy and as automatic as possible, or human beings won't tolerate it.

许多最困难的错误只能根据这些看似偶然的数据来理解。例如，错误报告历史可能会告诉您某个特定错误的报告一直在流传，但没有得到解决。通过注意测试基础架构中的版本更改，您可能会获得有关某些出现和消失的错误含义的有力线索。保持你的眼睛和头脑开放。

Many of the most difficult bugs can be understood only in terms of these seemingly incidental data. For example, the bug report history may tell you that reports of a particular bug have been circulating without being resolved. You may garner strong clues to the meaning of certain bugs that appear and disappear by noticing version changes in the testing infrastructure. Keep your eyes and mind open.

使用你没有的信息。

Use the information you don't have.

互联网上流传的一个故事指出了知道如何根据缺失的信息推断意义的重要性。我更改了名称以掩饰可能牵连的任何真实人员，但故事是这样的：Jarrod 正在测试主要通过高速连接使用的在线系统的拨号功能。他向 Rosella 报告说：“我安装了软件，拨号正常。我能听到。然后我能听到两台计算机连接的声音，但随后连接失败。”

A story circulating on the Internet points out the importance of knowing how to infer meaning based on information that is missing. I've changed the names to disguise anyone real who might be implicated, but the story goes as follows: Jarrod is testing the dial-up function of an online system that's primarily used via a high-speed connection. He reports to Rosella, "I installed the software okay, and it dialed fine. I could hear that. Then I could hear the two computers connecting, but then the connection failed."

Rosella 知道“连接失败”是一种解释，因此她使用 The Data Question 来挖掘更多信息：“你看到或听到什么让你相信连接失败？”

Rosella knows that "the connection failed" is an interpretation, so she uses The Data Question to dig out more information: "What did you see or hear that led you to believe that the connection failed?"

“声音都停了。”

"The sound all stopped."

“声音停止的原因可能有很多。是什么让你认为连接失败了？”

"The sound might have stopped for a lot of reasons. What led you to believe the connection had failed?"

“我不确定沉默意味着什么，所以我拿起电话看看他们是否仍然保持联系。”

"I wasn't sure what the silence meant, so I picked up the phone to see if they were still connected."

“你看到或听到了什么？”

"And what did you see or hear?"

“我什么都没听到，但在屏幕上，我看到了信息，

"I didn't hear anything, but on the screen, I saw the message,

无承运人。所以我知道连接失败了。”

NO CARRIER. So I knew the connection had failed."

这里缺少的信息是 Jarrod 没有太多的拨号连接经验。因此，罗塞拉 (Rosella) 指派他与有这种经验的人一起工作。

The missing information here was that Jarrod doesn't have much experience with dial-up connections. Consequently, Rosella assigned him to work alongside someone who had that experience.

同一个词可能有几个不同的意思。

The same word may have several different meanings.

Rosella 知道“失败”这个词可以有多重含义，这件事让她想起了一个网络谜语：

Rosella knew that the word "failed" could have multiple meanings, and the incident reminded her of an Internet riddle:

问：“你怎么知道你是不是来自加利福尼亚？”

Q: "How do you know if you're from California?"

答：“当你的妻子说‘在回家的路上去拿格兰诺拉麦片’，然后你去日托中心时，你就知道你来自加利福尼亚了。”

A: "You know you're from California when your wife says 'pick up Granola on the way home,' and you go to the day-care center."

在其他 49 个州，格兰诺拉麦片是一种早餐麦片，但加利福尼亚人将他们的孩子命名为格兰诺拉麦片、彩虹或摇头丸，这让那些试图理解他们话语含义的人感到困惑。

In the other 49 states, granola is a breakfast cereal, but Californians name their kids Granola or Rainbow or Ecstasy, much to the confusion of those who try to make meaning of their utterances.

另一个常见的加利福尼亚词是“断层”——如圣安德烈亚斯断层。在地震国家之外，“过错”往往意味着责备，而不是买房时要避免的事情。但在测试用语中，当我们谈论软件故障时，我们指的是潜在的裂痕（在软件中）而不是责备。测试人员应该发现问题，而不是责备别人。当测试人员说有问题时，他们并不是在指责。至少，你希望他们只是在寻找改进的机会，所以在人们转为防御之前检查一下。

Another common California word is "fault"—as in San Andreas Fault. Outside of earthquake country, "fault" tends to suggest blame, not something to avoid when buying a house. But in testing parlance, when we talk about software faults, we mean underlying fissures (in the software) rather than blame. Testers are supposed to be finding fissures, not blaming people. When a tester says there's a fault, they're not imputing blame. At least, you hope they're simply finding opportunities for improvement, so check it out before people turn defensive.

“相同”不一定相同。

"Same" may not be identical.

您可能认为数字只有一种精确含义。不是这样。回到 1956 年，当 FORTRAN 被发明的时候，我有一段时间在编译程序中找出间歇性故障背后的故障。原来 FORTRAN 有一个 bug。当一个实例被编译为源代码常量而另一个实例被作为数据读入时，数字 1.2 不等于 1.2。FORTRAN 团队中的一个人编写了源代码十进制常量到浮点二进制的转换例程，但另一个人编写了十进制输入常量的转换例程。

You might think that numbers have one and only one precise meaning. Not so. Back in 1956, when FORTRAN was invented, I had one heck of a time locating the fault behind an intermittent failure in a compiled program. It turned out that FORTRAN had a bug. The number 1.2 was not equal to 1.2 when one instance had been compiled as a source-code constant and the other had been read in as data. One person on the FORTRAN team had written the conversion routine for source-code decimal constants to floating-point binary, but a different person had written the conversion routine for decimal input constants.

从那以后，我在解释事物时一直持怀疑态度——文字、数字、图片、图表，凡是你能想到的——看起来相同但实际上来自不同的来源。当两件事（假设）相同时，您也可能想要怀疑。所以你可能想用“看起来一样”来代替“一样”，这会让你对你所接受的东西做出不那么乐观的解释。

Ever since, I've been suspicious when interpreting things— words, numbers, pictures, graphs, you name it—that look identical but actually come from different sources. You, too, might want to be suspicious when two things are (supposedly) the same. And so you may want to substitute the phrase "appear the same" for "the same," which will lead you to a less optimistic interpretation of what you take in.

有时不精确会更好。

Sometimes it's better to be imprecise.

矛盾的是，当你试图传达意思时，有时使用模棱两可的语言比非常精确的语言更有效。那是因为人们经常跳过确定意义的机会并直接分配意义。他们对无意识假定的含义的即时情绪反应会阻止他们听到您想要的含义。例如，如果你想让那些无法脱离“错误”或“故障”的指责内涵的人理解你，你可能想使用不准确的词，如“bug”或“issue”。如果您想在含义可能不同的情况下进行有效沟通，请考虑接收者。尝试使用接收者的术语并听取任何口头回应的语气，即使您认为此人不讲理。让我在 Internet 上流传的客户/技术支持对话作为您的模型：

Paradoxically, when you're trying to communicate meaning, it's sometimes more effective to use ambiguous language than to be very precise. That's because people often skip right past the opportunity to determine meaning and go straight to assigning significance. Their instant emotional reaction to an unconsciously assumed meaning then prevents them from hearing the meaning you intended. For example, you may want to use inexact words, like "bug" or "issue," if you want to be understood by people who cannot disconnect from the blame connotation of "error" or "fault." If you want to communicate effectively in a situation in which meanings can differ, think about the receiver. Try to use the receiver's terminology and listen to the tone of any spoken response, even if you think the person is being unreasonable. Let a customer/tech-support dialogue I found circulating on the Internet be your model:

技术支持代表：“好的……现在双击文件管理器图标。”

Tech Support Rep: "All right . . . now double-click on the file-manager icon."

顾客：“这就是我讨厌这个软件的原因——因为图标。我是新教徒。我不相信图标！” （客户声音中的情感告诉代表客户不是在开玩笑。）

Customer: "That's why I hate this software— because of the icons. I'm a Protestant. I don't believe in icons!" (The emotional charge in the customer's voice tells the rep that the customer is not kidding.)

技术支持代表：“好吧，这只是一个行业术语，先生。我不认为它是为了——”（在这里，代表试图保持合乎逻辑和合理性，以便“纠正”客户对这个词的情感联想带有宗教的图标。）

Tech Support Rep: "Well, that's just an industry term, sir. I don't believe it was meant to—" (Here, the rep tries to be logical and reasonable in order to "correct" the customer's emotional association of the word icon with religion.)

顾客：“我不关心任何‘行业’术语！我不相信图标。” （客户在不让代表完成他的句子时表现出更多的情绪。“纠正”人们的情绪几乎肯定可以保证他们不会理解你的意思。）

Customer: "I don't care about any 'industry' terms! I don't believe in icons." (The customer shows even more emotion in not letting the rep finish his sentence. "Correcting" people's emotions almost certainly guarantees that they will not receive your meaning.)

技术支持代表：（代表终于理解了客户的情绪。） “嗯，呃，你为什么不点击文件柜的小图片。‘小图片’可以吗？”

Tech Support Rep: (The rep finally understands the customer's emotion.) "Well, uh, why don't you click on the little picture of a filing cabinet. Is 'little picture' okay?"

客户：[鼠标点击]

Customer: [mouse click]

概括

Summary

数据不会说明一切，也不会含糊不清。为他们接收的数据附加意义取决于人类，每个人的做法都不一样。最好记住，同一数据有多种可能的解释。

Data do not speak for themselves, nor are they unambiguous. It is up to human beings to attach meaning to data they take in, and each person does so differently. It's best to keep in mind that there are many possible interpretations of the same data.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.对数据的含义妄下结论：在行动前至少想出三种可能的含义。（换句话说，按照三原则行事。）

1. Jumping to conclusions about what data mean: Think of at least three possible meanings before you act. (In other words, act according to The Rule of Three.)

2.在没有事先记录预期结果的情况下运行测试：从心理上讲，当它“看起来正确”时，人们很容易宣称测试已经成功并且产品没有错误。在测试之前，记录您对测试结果的期望，但也要为惊喜做好准备。

2. Running tests without documenting the expected results in advance: Psychologically, it's all too tempting to declare that a test has been successful and that the product is bug-free when it "looks right." In advance of testing, record your expectations for test results, but be ready for surprises as well.

3.提前过度记录预期结果：很容易将之前的观点带得太远。通常，您不需要写下诸如“计算机不应该爆炸，操作系统不应该崩溃，用户不应该受到伤害，错误应该产生错误消息，应用程序应该加载而不是破坏其他应用程序，并且执行时间不应太长，以至于用户认为系统已进入无限循环。” 所有这些陈述可能都是正确的，但会分散其他更有价值的预期结果的注意力。这样的预期结果可以为所有测试列出一次。

3. Over-documenting expected results in advance: It's easy to carry the previous point too far. Generally, you don't need to write down things like, "The computer should not explode, the operating system should not crash, the user should not be injured, errors should produce error messages, the application should load and not destroy other applications, and execution should not take so long that the user thinks the system has gone into an infinite loop." All of these statements are probably true, but distract from other, more valuable, anticipated results. Such expected results could be listed once for all tests.

4.试图自己创造意义：很多人的头脑都有多重意义。让整个团队参与进来，以减少忽略重要结论的机会。

4. Trying to make meaning all by yourself: Many minds make multiple meanings. Involve the entire team to decrease the chance of overlooking an important conclusion.

5.认为意义完全决定重要性：从摄入中获取意义时，仅适用三原则是不够的。同样的意义对不同的人来说可能有不同的重要性。“多心多意”没有前一句格言的韵味，但无论如何记住它会有所帮助。

5. Thinking that meaning completely determines significance: It's not sufficient to apply The Rule of Three when making meaning out of intake. The same meaning can have different importance to different people. "Many minds make multiple imports" doesn't have the alliteration of the previous motto, but you will do well to remember it anyway.

第 13 章_确定显着性

Chapter_13_Determining Significance

 

“艺术的目的不是表现事物的外表，而是表现它们的内在意义。” -亚里士多德，希腊哲学家文明语录：人生理想，编。理查德·艾伦·克里格 (Richard Alan Krieger)（纽约：Algora Publishing，2002 年）。

"The aim of art is to represent not the outward appearance of things, but their inward significance." - Aristotle, Greek Philosopher Civilization's Quotations: Life's Ideal, ed. Richard Alan Krieger (New York: Algora Publishing, 2002).

什么是意义？重要性是决定如何处理该错误的人对该错误的重视程度。乍一看，这个定义似乎很简单，但让我们看看它在以下场景中的表现：

What is significance? Significance is the importance attached to the bug by the person who gets to decide what to do about that bug. At first glance, this definition seems straightforward, but let's see how it plays out in the following scenario:

Cheri 在 BQ Enterprises 工作，担任 Bloblin Quinella（一款关于投注 bloblin 比赛的游戏）的项目经理。我们在她领导她的团队参加战略会议时采访了她。再过几个小时，她就要去旧金山参加每月一次的银河游戏聚会。在本月的聚会上，她计划推出 Bloblin Quinella 3.0 版，但当测试经理 Marv 宣布“我们必须推迟发布。我们刚刚发现了一个可怕的错误。随机有时，当一名玩家正在与地精 Bloblin 比赛时，BG 从一个地方消失并重新出现在另一个地方。”

Cheri works for BQ Enterprises as project manager for Bloblin Quinella (a game about betting on bloblin races). We catch up with her as she is leading her team in a strategy meeting. It's a few hours before she is to head off to San Francisco for the monthly Galactic Game Gathering. At this month's Gathering, she plans to introduce Version 3.0 of Bloblin Quinella, but her plan is seriously jolted when Marv, the test manager, announces, "We have to hold up the launch. We've just found a terrible bug. At random times, when a player is racing Bloblin the Goblin, BG disappears from one place and reappears in another."

所有人的目光都注视着他，Marv 深吸一口气，偷偷瞥了一眼 Cheri 的手提箱，它藏在门边的角落里，准备她离开。他继续说道，“如果聚会的人看到这个有缺陷的产品，他们会笑话我们破产。Cheri，你必须打开包装并留在这里，这样你就可以帮助我们解决这个问题，以便在下个月的聚会上推出。 “

With all eyes upon him, Marv takes a deep breath and glances furtively at Cheri's suitcase, which is stashed in the corner by the door, ready for her departure. He continues, "If the folks at the Gathering see this defective product, they'll laugh us out of business. Cheri, you've got to unpack and stay here so you can help us get this fixed for introduction at next month's Gathering."

团队中的每个人都清楚，Marv 认为这个错误非常重要。

It is clear to everyone on the team that Marv attributes great significance to this bug.

营销经理 Rulon 将 Marv 的担忧置之不理，他说：“我们不能那样做。在这次聚会上成功推出 BQ 3.0 将使我们获得比一个月后推出它多 10% 的市场份额，这至少值一亿美元。” 对于 Rulon 来说，这个漏洞微不足道，至少与可能损失的 1 亿美元市场份额相比意义不大。

Rulon, the marketing manager, waves Marv's concerns aside, saying, "We can't do that. A successful introduction of BQ 3.0 at this Gathering will grab us ten percent more market share than we'll get introducing it a month from now, and that's worth at least a hundred million dollars." For Rulon, this bug is trivial, at least when compared in significance to the potential $100 million in lost market share.

每个人都安静下来。Cheri 想，如果这个 bug 出现在聚会上，我就会丢掉工作。她的第一反应是这个错误非常严重，但随后她又进一步思考：如果我们甚至不在聚会上展示 BQ，我就会丢掉工作。Cheri 的重要性是个人的，取决于她以两种不同方式对失去工作的可能性的主观评估。

Everyone falls quiet. Cheri thinks, If the bug shows up at the Gathering, I will lose my job. Her first reaction is that the bug is very significant, but then she thinks things through a step further: If we don't even show BQ at the Gathering, I'll lose my job. Cheri's significance is personal, and depends on her subjective assessment of the chances of losing her job in two different ways.

将与 Cheri 一起前往旧金山领导演示的销售员 Phil 看到 Cheri 左右为难，并试图提供帮助。“别担心，Cheri，我会告诉观众，这个消失的行为根本不是bug，而是其他游戏没有的功能，它会卖一百万份。” 对 Phil 来说，这不是错误，但作为一项功能，它在另一方面具有重要意义。

Phil, the salesman who will travel with Cheri to San Francisco to lead the demo, sees that Cheri is in a quandary and tries to help out. "Don't worry, Cheri. I'll tell the audience that this disappearing act isn't a bug at all but is a feature that no other game has. It will sell a million copies." To Phil, this isn't a bug but, as a feature, it is significant in yet another way.

到目前为止，设计和构建3.0版本的Netta还没有说什么，但现在她低头看着她的笔记，平静地说，“不用担心，Cheri。我可以在十五分钟内修复这个bug，你可以还是赶你的飞机吧，要是不在这里修，我就得跟你一起去旧金山了，这周我真的不能出城了。”

Up to this point, Netta, who designed and built Version 3.0, hasn't said anything, but now she stares down at her notes and speaks calmly, "Not to worry, Cheri. I can fix this bug in fifteen minutes and you can still catch your plane. If I don't fix it here, I'll have to go with you to San Francisco and I really can't be out of town this week."

“不要，不要！” 尖叫菲尔。“你敢取消那个功能！”

"No, don't!" screeches Phil. "Don't you dare remove that feature!"

不同的人对同一信息的重视程度不同。

Different people attach different importance to the same information.

在这种情况下，我们可以很容易地看出错误的重要性确实取决于谁来决定如何处理该错误。除非 Cheri 的老板推翻她的决定，否则 Cheri 将做出决定。该错误对其他人的重要性仅在 Cheri 接受他们的观点时才算数。自然地，其他人认为他们对 bug 重要性的理解是“真正的”重要性，但 Cheri 的工作是综合权衡所有观点，得出这个 bug 的整体项目重要性——如果它确实是一个 bug。

In this scenario, we can easily see that the significance of a bug does depend on who gets to decide what to do about that bug. Unless Cheri's boss overrides her decision, Cheri will decide. The significance of the bug to the others counts only to the extent that Cheri buys into their view. Naturally, the others think their understanding of the bug's significance is the "real" significance, but Cheri's job is to weigh all views together to come up with the overall project significance of this bug—if indeed it is a bug.

理想情况下，Cheri 将从所有团队成员以及 BQ Enterprises 法律部门的律师那里提取他们自己观点的重要性：

Ideally, Cheri will extract from all team members—and from an attorney in BQ Enterprises' legal department—the significance from their own point of view:

她想从测试经理 Marv 那里知道，“如果我们保留它，或者我们修复它，会对测试产生什么影响？”

From Marv, the test manager, she wants to know, "What impact will this have on testing if we leave it, or if we fix it?"

她需要从营销经理 Rulon 那里知道，“如果我们保留它，或者我们修复它，会对未来的销售产生什么影响？”

From Rulon, the marketing manager, she needs to know, "What impact will this have on future sales if we leave it, or if we fix it?"

Netta 是 3.0 版的设计者和构建者，她需要知道，“如果我们保留它，或者修复它，会对开发产生什么影响？”

From Netta, the Version 3.0 designer and builder, she needs to know, "What impact will this have on development if we leave it, or if we fix it?"

她想从销售员菲尔那里知道，“如果我们保留它，或者我们修复它，这会对季度收入产生什么影响？”

From Phil, the salesman, she wants to know, "What impact will this have on quarterly revenue if we leave it, or if we fix it?"

她会通过电话联系一位律师，她想知道，“如果我们保留它，或者我们修复它，这对我们的责任有什么影响？”

From an attorney she'll contact by telephone, she wants to know, "What impact will this have on our liability if we leave it, or if we fix it?"

Swanson 没有出席 Cheri 的会议，但作为支持团队的负责人很重要，她会问，“如果我们离开它，或者如果我们修复它，这会对支持成本产生什么影响？”

And from Swanson, who isn't present at Cheri's meeting but is important as the head of the support team, she will ask, "What impact will this have on support costs if we leave it, or if we fix it?"

有了这些问题的答案，以及对 Bloblin Quinella 感兴趣的任何其他派系的答案，Cheri 就可以评估整个项目的重要性。

With answers to these questions, and answers from any other factions that have an interest in Bloblin Quinella, Cheri can assess the significance for the entire project.

或者她可以吗？

Or can she?

公共意义可能不同于私人意义。

Public significance may differ from private.

如果每个人都合乎逻辑、公平和开放，那么评估重要性就会很简单。然而，人们可能有隐藏的个人议程，这些议程会减少或加强他们对 Cheri 问题的回答。考虑其中的一些可能性和动机：

Assessing significance would be simple if everyone were logical, fair, and open. However, people may have hidden personal agendas that diminish or intensify their answers to Cheri's questions. Consider a few of these possibilities and motives:

Marv 希望在聚会结束后的那个周末在旧金山参加一次千载难逢的稀有棒球卡拍卖会。如果演示被推迟，他将不得不支付自己前往加利福尼亚的旅行费用。

Marv was hoping to attend a once-in-a-lifetime, rare- baseball-card auction in San Francisco the weekend after the Gathering. If the demo is postponed, he'll have to pay for his own trip to California.

Rulon 认为他是下一个担任项目经理职位的人选。如果演示失败，Cheri 可能会丢掉工作，而他会升职。

Rulon thinks he's next in line for a project manager job. If the demo fails, Cheri may lose her job and he'll get promoted to it.

内塔富有的叔叔西尔维斯特来访，传闻他正在写一份新遗嘱。如果她在聚会时出城，她的表妹柯特会给西尔维斯特带来美好时光，她可能会失去一笔巨额遗产。

Netta's rich uncle, Sylvester, is visiting, and he's rumored to be writing a new will. If she's out of town at the Gathering, her cousin Kirt will show Sylvester a good time, and she may lose out on a huge inheritance.

Swanson 认为技术支持没有得到足够的尊重。他认为，如果他能让技术支持看起来很容易解决这个问题，他就会增加高层管理人员的股票。

Swanson feels that tech support doesn't get enough respect. He thinks that if he can make tech support look like it can easily handle this problem, he will boost his stock with upper management.

因此，如果 Cheri 想要对重要性做出合理的估计，她将不得不以某种方式过滤掉所有个人议程——包括她自己的议程。

So, if Cheri is to make a sensible estimate of significance, she will somehow have to filter out all personal agendas—including her own.

重要性取决于上下文。

Significance depends on context.

让 Cheri 确定重要性的能力进一步复杂化的是，它不仅是 bug 和人的属性，还取决于上下文。例如，大多数人对已经发布了几十个错误的一段代码中的错误的重要性与对组件中记录的第一个错误的重要性不同。也许这第 n个错误表示一项容易出错的工作——早期的错误发现是组件未来行为的最佳预测指标。快速发现大量错误表明从长远来看会发现更多错误。

Further complicating Cheri's ability to determine significance is that it is not just a property of a bug and a person, but also depends on the context. For instance, most people would attribute different significance to an error in a piece of code that has already posted several dozen errors than they would to the first error ever recorded in a component. Perhaps this n-th error signifies an error-prone piece of work—early bug findings are the best predictor of a component's future behavior. Lots of bugs found quickly suggests there will be lots more bugs found in the long run.

这就是我们要记录所有错误的原因之一。如果我们未能记录一些错误，我们可能会认为早期错误并不多，因此可能会误判我们发现的重要性。结果是我们隐藏了一个事实，即我们稍后会遇到此组件的问题。

That's one reason we want to record all bugs. If we fail to record some, we may think there aren't many early bugs, and may thus misjudge the significance of our findings. The result is that we hide the fact that we're going to have trouble with this component later on.

还有一个复杂的问题：我们通常只能猜测某些用户实际经历由故障引起的故障的可能性。如果经历一次故障，可能会损失数千美元，但如果只有一百亿分之一的用户可能会经历一次，那有多大意义呢？

Yet another complication: We can often merely guess at the probability that some user will actually experience the failure induced by the fault. A failure might cost thousands if experienced, but if only one user in ten billion is likely to experience it, how significant is that?

从统计学上讲，故障的预期价值是发生故障的概率乘以发生故障时的成本。有些人认为某物的重要性与其预期价值直接相关。例如，如果你每次使用某个系统都会遇到故障，并且你每天使用该系统一次，但每次故障的成本仅为一分钱，那么如果等同于预期价值的显着性是每年 3.65 美元（闰年多加一分钱）。另一方面，如果您预计每年会遇到一次这种故障，但它会破坏您的所有数据并花费 20,000 美元来恢复，那么每年的经济意义就是 20,000 美元。

Statistically, the expected value of a fault is the probability of experiencing it times the cost if it is experienced. Some people consider the significance of something to be directly related to its expected value. If, for example, you experience a failure every time you use a certain system, and you use the system once a day, but the cost for each failure is only a penny, then the significance if equated to expected value is $3.65 a year (plus a penny more in leap years). On the other hand, if you expect to experience this failure once a year but it will destroy all your data and cost $20,000 to recover, the monetary significance is $20,000 a year.

然而，即使您使用预期值，也会出现另一个问题：谁将承担失败的代价？我们关心吗？当我的侄女写她的第一本书时，她使用文字处理器制作可用于相机的副本，制造商从中打印书籍。文字处理器中的一个错误导致文本中每十页左右省略一个词。直到第一次印刷之后，我的侄女才注意到这个问题，这本书印刷了一千册或更多册。她很伤心。碰巧构建文字处理器的团队是我的客户，所以我向它报告了错误。

And yet, even if you use the expected value, there's another complication: Who will incur the cost of a failure? And do we care? When my niece wrote her first book, she used a word processor to produce camera-ready copy from which the manufacturer printed books. A bug in the word processor caused a word to be omitted from the text every ten pages or so. My niece didn't notice the problem until after the first print-run, in which a thousand or more copies of the book were printed. She was devastated. It happened that the team that built the word processor was a client of mine, so I reported the bug to it.

“哦，我们知道那个错误，”团队负责人告诉我。“而你没有修好它？”

"Oh, we know about that bug," the team leader told me. "And you didn't fix it?"

“我们决定不这样做。只有当你的文件超过两百页左右时才会发生这种情况，而且大多数用户都很聪明，不会把所有的鸡蛋都放在一个篮子里。如果我们试图修复它，我们可能会创建其他一些会影响成千上万用户的错误。”

"We decided not to. It only happens if you have a document longer than two hundred pages or so, and most users are smart enough not to put all their eggs in one basket. If we tried to fix it, we might create some other bug that would affect thousands of users."

换句话说，我的客户并不认为我侄女的手稿有那么重要，尽管它对她来说确实很重要。（就像我对我一样。我立即停止使用这个文字处理器来处理我的手稿——我的客户并不在乎。所有的作者都不构成其市场的重要组成部分。）

In other words, my client didn't consider my niece's manuscript all that important, though it sure was important to her. (As mine are to me. I immediately stopped using this word processor for my manuscripts—and my client didn't really care. All the authors out there don't constitute a significant part of its market.)

你不能总是用金钱来判断重要性。

You can't always judge significance in money terms.

回到 BQ Enterprises，当 Cheri 和她的团队继续争论错误/功能的重要性时，出现了更多的复杂情况。首先是该公司一位律师的回电，提醒他们前一年有两个男孩在试图模仿 BQ 竞争对手游戏的功能时自杀了。

Back at BQ Enterprises, as Cheri and her team continue debating the significance of the bug/feature, more complications arise. First comes a call-back from one of the company's lawyers, reminding them that two boys had killed themselves the preceding year trying to imitate a feature from one of BQ's competitors' game.

“如果某个孩子模仿 BG 尝试消失行为而死怎么办？” 律师的声音在免提电话中响起：“我们将被起诉赔偿数百万美元。”

"What if some kid dies trying a disappearing act, in imitation of BG?" the attorney's voice booms over the speaker-phone "We'll be sued for millions."

“哇哦，”内塔喊道。“你在谈论人的生命。你不能为此定价。”

"Whoa," shouts Netta. "You're talking about human life. You can't put a price on that."

但是，当然，人们总是这样做。请允许我离题：在 1930 年代，金门大桥建成时，有 11 名工人在施工过程中死亡。当时，这是一个新的安全记录。桥梁建造者预计每百万美元的建筑成本就有 1 人死亡，因此预计将有 35 名工人在施工期间死亡。如果他们不能为人的生命定价，这座桥就永远不会建成。

But, of course, people do just that all the time. Permit me to digress: In the 1930s, when the Golden Gate Bridge was built, eleven workers died during construction. At the time, that was a new safety record. Bridge builders expected one fatality per million dollars in construction costs, so it was expected that thirtyfive workers would die during construction. If they couldn't put a price on human life, the bridge would never have been built.

金门大桥的建造者也为人命付出了代价，他们决定在地板下悬挂安全网，这挽救了 19 名工人的生命。然而，在 1959 年至 1964 年间，维拉萨诺海峡大桥的建造者并未提供渔网。当三人死亡引发罢工行动时，建筑商认为生命比省钱更重要，因此提供了蚊帐。

Builders of the Golden Gate Bridge also put a price on human life by deciding to suspend a safety net under the floor, which saved the lives of nineteen workers. Between 1959 and 1964, however, the builders of the Verrazano-Narrows Bridge didn't provide nets. When three fatalities provoked a job action, the builders decided lives were more significant than saving money, and so provided nets.

而且，大约一百年前，当布鲁克林大桥正在建造时，有 20 或 30 名工人死亡——但没有人能确定，因为工人的死亡并不重要，不足以保存良好或永久的记录。

And, about one hundred years earlier, when the Brooklyn Bridge was being built, twenty or thirty workers died—but nobody knows for sure because worker deaths weren't significant enough to bother keeping good or permanent records.

在 NASA 的水星计划中，管理美国首次载人在轨飞行，我是一个必须重视人类死亡的团队的一员。我们的错误重要性编号分类反映了我们对安全的承诺。最热门的类别是：

On NASA's Project Mercury governing the first U.S. man-in-orbit flights, I was part of a team that had to attach significance to human deaths. Our bug-significance numbering classification reflected our commitment to safety. The top categories were these:

• 0 级：有人可能因此软件故障而死亡。

• Level 0: Someone could die as a result of this software fault.

• 1 级：任务可能因此故障而中止。

• Level 1: A mission could be aborted as a result of this fault.

• 2 级：发射任务或接回返回的宇航员可能会因此故障而延迟。

• Level 2: Launch of a mission or pickup of returning astronauts could be delayed as a result of this fault.

• 3 级：我们将因此故障产生额外费用。

• Level 3: We would incur additional costs as a result of this fault.

0 级总是胜过其他一切，当时的 IBM 总裁兼董事长 TJ Watson, Jr. 特别指定我来防止任何 0 级错误漏掉的可能性。如果我不能阻止某人改写 0 级错误，我会派人去纽约的 TJ。十四个人试图推翻，但当我说他们必须把他们的案子交给沃森时，他们都让步了。他对重要性有最终决定权，这显然将他们的论点放在了不同的背景下。

Level 0 always trumped everything else, and I was specifically designated by T.J. Watson, Jr., then president and chairman of IBM, to guard against the possibility of any level-0 bug slipping through. If I couldn't stop someone from overriding a level-0 bug, I was to send the person to T.J. in New York. Fourteen people tried to override, but when I said they had to take their case to Watson, they all backed down. He had the last word on significance, which apparently put their arguments in a different context.

不要把重点放在它上面。

Don't put too fine a point on it.

人的生命价值总是主观的；事实上，所有重要的措施也是如此。许多公司进行数字旋转，试图使他们的重要性判断看起来客观。不要被这些人愚弄，也不要自欺欺人认为重要性是客观的。

The value of a human life is always subjective; in fact, so are all significance measures. Many companies perform numerological gyrations to try to make their significance judgments seem objective. Don't be fooled—either by these folks, or into tricking yourself that significance is objective.

为了对抗这些伪目标方案，检查一种情况的元意义。首先问自己，“我的估计有多好？” 我曾经有一个客户用从零到一百的等级来确定错误的重要性。为了提高或降低一个点的重要性，会议中无休止的争论持续了一个小时又一个小时。我跟踪客户花了多少时间对错误进行排名，然后指出几乎所有错误都可以在决定先修复哪个错误的时间内修复。之后，类别数量减少到四个：

To counter these pseudo-objective schemes, examine the meta-significance of a situation. Start by asking yourself, "How good are my estimates?" I once had a client who determined bug significance with a scale that ran from zero to one hundred. Endless hassles went on for hour after hour in meetings to bump significance up or down a point. I kept track of how much time the client spent ranking bugs, then pointed out that virtually all of them could have been repaired in the time it took to decide which would be repaired first. After that, the number of categories was reduced to four:

• 0 级：此问题正在阻止其他测试。

• Level 0: This issue is blocking other testing.

• 1 级：如果此问题未得到解决，我们的产品将无法使用。

• Level 1: Our product cannot be used if this issue isn't resolved.

• 级别 2：如果此问题得不到解决，我们产品的价值将大大降低。

• Level 2: The value of our product will be significantly reduced if this issue isn't resolved.

• 3 级：只有在产品发货时出现大量类似问题时，此问题才重要。

• Level 3: This issue will be important only if there are large numbers of similar issues when the product is shipped.

这四个类别为测试人员提供了足够的详细信息，以供测试人员在从测试角度确定重要性时使用——这是决策执行者想要考虑的几个角度之一。

These four categories provide an adequate level of detail for testers to use when determining significance from the testing point of view—one of several perspectives that the deciding executive will want to consider.

首先解决重大问题。

Address significant problems first.

尽管测试人员对重要性的看法不应该决定如何处理发现的故障，但它们应该影响各种测试的执行顺序。如果测试优先是个好主意，那么显着性优先就更好了。为什么？您可能会执行无数次测试，但如果您实际上执行了数量巨大的测试，您很可能会在所有无价值的垃圾中丢失有价值的信息。执行的测试次数应尽可能少，但不能少。当然，您不能完美地选择它们，但如果您估计每个测试的重要性，然后首先执行最重要的测试，您可以选择得很好。如果你的估计是好的，那么，无论何时你决定停止测试，你都会在你的时间内做到最好。

Although the testers' ideas of significance shouldn't determine what is done about a found failure, they should influence the order in which various tests are executed. If test-first is a good idea, then significance-first is even better. Why? You might perform an infinite number of tests, but if you actually perform even an enormous number of tests, you would likely lose the valuable information among all the worthless crud. The number of tests performed should be as small as possible, but no smaller. You can't choose them perfectly, of course, but you can choose quite well if you estimate the significance of each test, then perform the most significant tests first. If your estimates are any good, then, whenever you decide to stop testing, you will have done the best you could within the time you had.

聆听您的情绪反应。

Listen to your emotional reactions.

关于计算机程序的一件奇怪的事情是，它们有时可能因为错误的原因而正确。一个经常被引用的例子是设计用来正确计算闰年日期的软件。十岁以上的每个人都知道，闰年每四年一次，年份可以被四整除——2012 年、2016 年、2020 年，等等。

One curious thing about computer programs is that they can sometimes be right for the wrong reasons. An oft-cited example is software designed to calculate leap-year dates correctly. Leap years, as everyone over the age of ten surely knows, come every four years, in years divisible by four—2012, 2016, 2020, and so forth.

不是每个人都知道的是，每四个世纪之交的年份中有三个——1500、1900、2100、2200 等等——都不是闰年。除了每 400 年确实出现一个闰年——1600、2000、2400 等等。了解？

What not everybody knows is that three out of every four turn-of-the-century years—1500, 1900, 2100, 2200, and so on—are not leap years. Except that every 400 years, a leap year does occur—1600, 2000, 2400, and so forth. Got that?

我的在线论坛 SHAPE（软件作为一种有效实践的人类活动）的订阅者之一了解异常情况，并在流行的电子表格程序中使用闰年算法进行了一些测试。大卫发现，1900 年 2 月 28 日之后的第二天被确定为 1900 年 2 月 29 日，尽管 1900 年不是闰年。显然，电子表格开发人员过度简化了他们的闰年计算。

One of the subscribers to my online forum SHAPE (Software as a Human Activity Practiced Effectively) understood the exception and conducted some tests using the leap-year algorithm in a popular spreadsheet program. What David found was that the day after February 28, 1900, was identified as February 29, 1900, even though 1900 was not a leap year. Apparently, the spreadsheet developers oversimplified their leap-year calculation.

根据该结果，我猜测 2100 年也将被确定为此电子表格中的闰年，但大卫拒绝了。“电子表格中的 2100 是正确的（不是闰年）。我不知道如何编写代码才能使 1900 年出现错误而 2100 年没有错误。也许他们进行了特殊情况检查？<shudder>”网上的战栗表达了大卫的情绪反应，我也是。

From that result, I guessed that 2100 would also be identified as a leap year in this spreadsheet, but David said no. "The spreadsheet got 2100 right (not a leap year). I don't know how you could code it to get an error for 1900 and no error for 2100. Maybe they put in a special-case check? <shudder>" That online shudder expressed David's emotional reaction, and mine, too.

这就是意义所在——你赋予测试结果意义的情感影响。例如，如果我确定我购买的某些软件存在错误导致它无法使用，我可能会说，“哦，没关系。我买得起九十九美元，所以不值得为此大惊小怪。” 但如果我一文不名，我可能会赋予不同的意义：“这完全不能接受。我要去小额索赔法庭起诉要回我的钱！”

That's what significance is—the emotional impact of the meaning you attach to the test result. For instance, if I determine that a bug in some software I bought makes it unusable, I might say, "Oh, that's okay. I can afford ninety-nine dollars, so it's not worth fussing about it." But if I were flat broke, I might attach a different significance: "That's completely unacceptable. I'm going to Small Claims Court to sue to get my money back!"

或者，我对错误的重视可能根本与金钱无关，而是可能与我反对或支持软件供应商的偏见有关。

Alternatively, the significance I attach to the bug might not have to do with money at all, but instead might be attached to a bias I have against or in favor of the software vendor.

作为这个流行电子表格的个人用户，我可能不会被这个闰年错误所困扰，因为我不在 1900 年，也不会在 2100 年。但是如果我希望将这个电子表格合并到我设计的软件中并卖给写百年贷款和租约的金融机构，这个错误可能会让我损失很多业务。

As an individual user of this popular spreadsheet, I might not be bothered by this leap-year bug because I wasn't around in 1900, and won't be in 2100. But if I were hoping to incorporate this spreadsheet in software I design and sell to financial institutions that write hundred-year loans and leases, this bug might cost me a lot of business.

我可能对特定电子表格对 1900 年和 2100 年的处理方式之间的差异感到非常担心（一种强烈的情绪），因为我对黑匣子内部发生的事情的模型刚刚崩溃。如果我是项目经理，我希望我会要求我的测试员跟进一些额外的测试，所以这正是我要求 David 做的。

I might be very worried (a significant emotion) by the difference between the particular spreadsheet's handling of 1900 and 2100 because my model of what's going on inside the black box has just collapsed. If I had been the project manager, I hope I would have asked my tester to follow up with some additional tests, and so that's just what I asked David to do.

他回答说：“嗯。嗯，我不确定这是否是你要找的，但我通过创建七列在电子表格中模拟了一个测试，列出星期日到星期六的日子。我从日期 1/1 开始/1900。根据电子表格，1900年的元旦是星期天。这也是电子表格支持的第一个日历日。我逐日逐日查看日历的计算结果。果然，它显示了1900是闰年，2 月 29 日是星期三。”

He responded: "Hmm. Well, I'm not sure if this is what you're looking for, but I modeled a test in the spreadsheet by creating seven columns, listing days Sunday through Saturday. I began with the date 1/1/1900. According to the spreadsheet, New Year's Day in 1900 was a Sunday. It was also the first calendar day the spreadsheet supports. I stepped forward through each successive day to see how the calendar works out. Sure enough, it showed that 1900 was a leap year with February 29 landing on a Wednesday."

然后，David 将星期几与 http://www.earth.com/calendar 上的答案进行了比较。他发现 1900 年的一月一日实际上是星期一，而不是星期日。可以在 http://www.timeanddate.com/calendar/?country=1&year=1900 找到对此的证实。因此，对于 1900 年如何出现错误而 2100 年没有错误的解释是电子表格有两个相互抵消的错误：

David then compared the days of the week with the answer at http://www.earth.com/calendar. He discovered that the first of January in the year 1900 was actually a Monday, not a Sunday. Corroboration of this can be found at http://www.timeanddate .com/calendar/?country=1&year=1900. So, the explanation for how there could an error for 1900 and no error for 2100 was that the spreadsheet has two bugs that cancel each other out:

结果是 1900 年 1 月和 1900 年 2 月完全弄乱了，但从 3/1/1900 开始，星期几正确排列。这一切有什么意义呢？对我来说，如果我是项目经理，那么重要的是了解开发人员“在幕后”所做的事情。这很可能是一个特例（糟糕），或者他们有一个包含星期几的日期表，并且根本没有即时生成日历。但需要注意的重要一点是，我不知道他们在做什么。这已经足够重要了。

The result is that January 1900 and February 1900 are completely messed up, but the days of the week line up correctly from 3/1/1900 forward. What's the significance of all this? For me, were I the project manager, the significance is in understanding what the developers were doing "under the covers." It could well be a special case (yuck), or it could be that they had a table of dates including days of the week and did not generate the calendar on the fly at all. But the important thing to note is that I don't have a clue as to what they were doing. And that's significant enough.

这个电子表格故事讲述的故事类似于 Joel Spolsky 在他的 Joel-On-Software 博客上报告的故事，但不同的是，Joel 实际上是电子表格开发团队的一员，并亲自处理问题。有关他的帐户，请参见 http://www.joelonsoftware.com。

This spreadsheet story tells a tale similar to one that Joel Spolsky reported on his Joel-On-Software blog, but the difference is that Joel was actually on the development team for the spreadsheet and dealt with the issues personally. For his account, see http://www.joelonsoftware.com.

概括

Summary

我们的情绪携带着关于事物有多重要的信息。如果我们在不重要的事情之前关注情绪、倾听和解决重要的事情，我们将尽我们所能利用我们拥有的数据。

Our emotions carry information about how important things are. If we pay attention to emotions, listen, and address important matters before unimportant matters, we'll be doing the best we can with the data we have.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.混淆修复难度和意义：一些分类方案是基于代码分析，但修复一个bug只是其潜在成本之一。不要混淆错误的类型和错误的重要性。系统崩溃可能无关紧要，而输入错误可能是灾难性的。我知道有一个案例，一家公司的月度发票上出现的一个打错的电话号码至少要了一个人的生命，因为电话号码被错误地打印在发票上的救护车服务被错误的电话淹没了。

1. Confusing repair difficulty with significance: Some classification schemes are based on code analysis, but fixing a bug is only one of its potential costs. Don't confuse the type of bug with the significance of the bug. A system crash could be insignificant, and a typing error could be disastrous. In one case I know, a mistyped phone number that appeared on one company's monthly invoices cost at least one person his life when the ambulance service whose phone number was mistakenly printed on the invoices was swamped with erroneous calls.

2.错误判断响应速度的重要性：如果测试结果或问题解决方案的可用速度比我们预期的要快，我们就会“怀疑”它们是不正确的。同样，如果生成答案所需的时间符合我们的预期，我们就“知道”它是经过仔细和正确计算出来的。

2. Misjudging the significance of the speed of a response: If test results or the solution to a problem become available more quickly than we anticipate they should, we "suspect" that they can't be correct. Likewise, if the time it takes to generate an answer matches our expectations, we "know" it's been carefully and correctly worked out.

例如，假设地球上的操作员要求火星轨道器上的计算机进行计算，并且他们在不到五分钟的时间内得到了答复。毫无疑问，他们会认为事情大错特错（由于将请求传输到 Orbiter 计算机的时间延迟，这样的速度实际上是不可能的）。如果他们在二十分钟内收到答复，他们不一定认为一切都是正确的，但传输信息的时间确实很重要。

Suppose, for example, that operators on Earth ask the computers on the Mars Orbiter to perform a calculation, and they receive an answer in less than five minutes. They undoubtedly would think something deeply wrong (such speed would be made virtually impossible by the time delay of transmitting the request to Orbiter's computers). If they receive the answer in twenty minutes, they cannot necessarily assume that everything is correct, but the time-for-transmittal information does have significance.

3.没有意识到重要性是政治性的：例如，入狱不能仅用金钱来衡量。

3. Failing to realize that significance is political: For example, going to jail is not measurable solely in monetary terms.

4.相信有一种“理性”或客观的方法来评估重要性：您可以使用数字和算法来帮助您，但最后的评估步骤始终是衡量您对这些数字的情绪反应。

4. Believing there is a "rational" or objective way to assess significance: You may use numbers and algorithms to assist you, but the final assessment step is always to measure your emotional reactions to those numbers.

5.未能在新信息可用时重新评估重要性：重要性是整个系统的属性，包括系统或构建该系统的过程。定期审查您的评估，并准备好进行更改。

5. Failing to reassess significance as new information becomes available: Significance is a property of an entire system, including the system or process that built that system. Review your assessments on a regular basis, and be prepared to change.

6.让摇篮曲语言影响你对意义的评估：无论我们有意还是无意地使用某些词，它们都会使信息带有意义。当有人说“响应应该非常快”时，这到底是什么意思？“应该”、“非常”和“快速”对陈述的信息有何含义？[11]

6. Allowing lullaby language to influence your assessment of significance: Certain words shade information with meaning, whether we use them consciously or unconsciously. When someone says, "The response should be very fast," what does that mean, exactly? What meanings do "should," "very," and "fast" give to the stated information? [11]

7.忽视你的行为对项目团队本身的重要性：测试人员常常对测试如此感情用事，以至于他们很失望地知道他们发现的错误不会在下一个版本中得到修复。他们可能会失去动力，考虑下一轮测试，这些人不会修复这个错误，所以我为什么要报告它？没有人喜欢他们的工作被忽视。尝试区分忽略和有意识地选择不修复某些错误。

7. Ignoring the significance of your actions on the project team itself: Testers are often so emotionally attached to testing that they are disappointed to know that bugs they find will not be fixed in the next release. They might be de-motivated, thinking on the next round of testing, These people will not fix this bug so why should I report it? Nobody likes to have their work ignored. Try to distinguish between ignoring and consciously choosing not to fix some bugs.

第 14 章_做出回应

Chapter_14_Making a Response

 

“博学多才，训练有素，口才好，这是福气。” - 释迦牟尼 (Siddhartha Gautama)，印度哲学家和佛教创始人 对于这个和其他明智的表达，请参见 http://www.buddhanet.net/e-learning/qanda09.html。

"Being deeply learned and skilled, being well trained and using well spoken words; this is good luck." - Buddha (Siddhartha Gautama), Indian Philosopher and Founder of Buddhism For this and other wise expressions, see http://www.buddhanet.net/e-learning/qanda09.html.

对错误的正确回应应该很简单：

The right response to bugs should be simple:

找到他们；图他们；修理他们。

Find 'em; figure 'em; fix 'em.

在一个项目的早期，我们做这个 FFF，但是随着错误的增加，我们的运气用完了，我们没有足够的时间做出正确的反应。为什么会发生这种情况，我们应该如何应对？

Early in a project, we do this FFF, but as the tide of bugs grows, our luck runs out and we don't have enough time to make the right response. Why does this happen, and how should we respond?

是运气不好还是经营不善？

Is it bad luck or bad management?

几年前，在 IBM，我们中的一些人对十几个失败的项目进行了研究，以寻找共性。我们的主要发现是，这些耗资数百万美元的项目中的每一个都因“运气不好”而失败——一场火灾、一场洪水、一场地震、一场流感，导致该项目的一半人员数周内无法工作。我们就这些发现撰写了一份报告，并将其提交给期刊进行审查。对我们来说幸运的是，其中一位评论者问道：“你的控件在哪里？” 呸！

Some years ago at IBM, several of us did a study of a dozen failed projects, looking for commonalities. Our main finding was that each of these million-dollar projects failed because of "bad luck"— a fire, a flood, an earthquake, an influenza epidemic that put half the people on the project out of commission for weeks. We wrote a report on these findings and submitted it to a journal for review. Fortunately for us, one of the reviewers asked, "Where are your controls?" Duh!

我们回去发现了十几个成功的类似项目。你看，这些项目也都经历过“厄运”，但这些项目并没有因此而失败。当火灾、洪水或地震破坏了他们的软件配置时，他们只需恢复安全备份并恢复工作。当一半的团队成员生病时，结对编程和技术审查提供了冗余知识，使他们能够保持关键路径项目的进展。

We went back and found a dozen comparable projects that had succeeded. Lo and behold, each of these projects had also experienced "bad luck," but these projects had not failed because of it. When fire, flood, or earthquake destroyed their software configuration, they simply recovered their safe backups and returned to work. When half the team members were out sick, pair programming and technical reviews provided the redundant knowledge that allowed them to keep critical-path items moving along.

换句话说，杀死前十几个项目的不是运气而是管理不善。意识到是什么注定了这些项目的失败，这给了我另一种识别管理不善项目的方法：项目经理总是援引“运气不好”作为失败的原因。

In other words, it wasn't bad luck but bad management that killed the first dozen projects. Realizing what doomed those projects gave me another way to identify badly managed projects: The project manager invariably invoked "bad luck" as the reason for failure.

为什么项目最后会匆匆忙忙？

Why do projects rush at the end?

我一直不明白，当软件出现的时间还不够长，我们还不能理解它的本质时，怎么会有人谈论“软件的本质”。我参与了几乎整个软件历史，我参与了各种软件项目——汽车嵌入式系统、电脑游戏、约会服务、财务管理、宇宙飞船控制、老虎机、心脏起搏器、数字手表，操作系统、智能卡、文字处理器等等。我从未发现任何共性——除了管理质量似乎是成功与失败的区别因素。

I've never understood how someone can talk about "the nature of software" when software hasn't been around long enough for us to understand its nature. I've been around for almost the whole history of software, and I've participated in all kinds of software projects—embedded systems in cars, computer games, dating services, financial management, spaceship control, slot machines, pacemakers, digital watches, operating systems, smart cards, word processors, and many more. I've never found any commonalities—except that the quality of management seems to be the distinguishing factor between success and failure.

高质量的管理确实会在软件项目中产生一些常见的模式。[12] 例如，当我看到一个软件项目并不匆忙，更不用说恐慌了，接近尾声时，我知道它是一个管理良好的项目。遗憾的是，没有多少人见过管理良好的软件项目，甚至可能不相信这种情况会发生。“软件项目最后总是匆匆忙忙，”他们说。“这就是软件的本质。”

Good-quality management does produce a number of common patterns in software projects. [12] For example, when I see a software project that's not in a rush, let alone a panic, near the end, I know it has been a well-managed project. Sad to say, not many people have ever seen a well-managed software project and may not even believe such a happening is possible. "Software projects are always in a rush at the end," they say. "That's just the nature of software."

尽管可能没有“软件的本性”，但可能存在一些管理不善的软件项目的本性——具有以下顺序的特征——导致它们最终仓促行事：

Though there may not be a "nature of software," there may be a nature of some badly managed software projects—with characteristics such as in the following sequence—that leads them to be in a rush at the end:

1. 管理人员不理解测试、查明和调试之间的区别。

1. The managers don't understand the difference between testing, pinpointing, and debugging.

2. 因为他们不了解其中的区别，所以他们认为测试是他们所经历的项目中的大部分问题。

2. Because they don't understand the difference, they believe that testing caused most of the trouble in projects they've experienced.

3. 因为他们认为测试会带来麻烦，所以他们倾向于尽可能推迟所有形式的测试。

3. Because they believe that testing causes trouble, they tend to postpone all forms of testing as long as they can.

4a. 因为他们选择了推迟测试的流程，所以测试是他们第一次无法再假装一切顺利。

4a. Because they've chosen their processes to postpone testing, testing is the first time they can no longer pretend things are going well.

或者，也许，如果项目管理得更差。. .

Or, maybe, if the project is even more poorly managed . . .

4b. 因为他们选择了推迟测试的流程，并且受到信息免疫的影响，所以即使在完成一些测试之后，他们也可以假装一切顺利。

4b. Because they've chosen their processes to postpone testing and they suffer from information immunity, they can pretend things are going well even after they've done some testing.

5. 因为他们有信息免疫力，所以在项目的所有早期阶段，一切似乎都“顺利”进行。

5. Because they suffer from information immunity, everything seems to be going "smoothly" through all the early stages of the project.

6. 由于管理人员停滞不前，错误——其中许多自最早的需求以来就潜伏在产品中——在后期测试中显露出来。

6. Because managers have stalled, bugs—many of which have lain dormant in the product since the earliest requirements—reveal themselves in late testing.

7. 因为现在整个系统都集中在一起，所以很多错误都很难查明，尤其是开发人员无法帮助查明，因为他们现在像无头鸡一样四处奔波，试图应对突然出现的大量错误。

7. Because the entire system is now lumped together, many of these bugs are difficult to pinpoint, especially since developers cannot help pinpoint because they are now running around like headless chickens trying to cope with the sudden bug glut.

8. 由于开发人员在最后期限的压力下工作，在尝试修复新发现的错误时会犯新的错误，脾气暴躁，头脑麻木，缺勤率上升，会议激增，战略适得其反。

8. Because developers working under deadline pressure make new errors when trying to fix newly found errors, tempers flare, minds numb, absenteeism mounts, meetings proliferate, and strategy backfires.

9. 所以参与者得出结论，“在我们开始测试之前我们没有遇到任何问题。我们的计划是对的。测试把一切都搞砸了。”

9. And so the participants conclude, "We didn't have any problems until we started testing. We were right on schedule. Testing screwed up everything."

背负着这个结论，经理们开始计划下一个项目——下一场惊慌失措的灾难。

Burdened with that conclusion, managers begin planning the next project—the next panicky disaster.

可以肯定的是，还有许多其他类型的错误管理响应——过于雄心勃勃的承诺、配置不足的工具、人员配备不足——所有这些都会导致进展缓慢，并导致最终缩短测试（和维修）时间。因此，对错误的首要反应应该是预测它们。你不会走运，所以从项目一开始就做正确的事情。一定要防止错误，然后 FFF 少数漏掉的错误。

To be sure, there are many other kinds of mistaken management responses—over-ambitious promises, under-provisioned tools, poorly staffed positions—all of which contribute to slow progress and lead to cutting test (and repair) time at the end. So, the first and foremost response to bugs should be to anticipate them. You aren't going to get lucky, so do the right things right from the start of a project. Prevent bugs by all means, then FFF the few that slip through.

接近尾声时，您应该如何应对？

How should you respond when close to the end?

但是，如果您从一开始就没有做正确的事情怎么办？不幸的是，一旦项目发现自己陷入大量错误的匆忙和恐慌中，就真的没有多少好的回应了。如果在项目后期出现大量错误，你所能做的就是诅咒自己没有及早和经常测试，然后抱怨，“为什么我们从来没有足够的时间把它做好，但总是有足够的时间去做结束了？”

But what if you haven't been doing the right things from the start? Unfortunately, once a project finds itself in the rush and panic of overwhelming bugs, there really aren't very many good responses left. If a monsoon of bugs turns up late in the project, all you can do is curse yourself for not testing early and often, and then moan, "Why do we never have enough time to do it right, but always have enough time to do it over?"

即使是管理得最好的项目，在接近发布日期时也几乎肯定会留下一些错误。因此，即使在一个管理良好的项目中，第一反应也应该是为残局安排时间。您需要的不是计划中的简单测试块，而是如下所示：

Even the best-managed projects will almost certainly have some bugs remaining as they near a ship date. Therefore, even in a well-managed project, the first response should be to schedule time for the endgame. Instead of a simple testing block in your plan, you need something that looks like this:

1. 停止所有测试并开始计划残局。

1. Stop all testing and start planning the endgame.

2. 按重要性对剩余的已知故障进行排序。

2. Rank the remaining known failures by significance.

3. 估计您的组织可以在剩余时间内可靠地修复这些故障中的多少（从最严重到最不严重）。

3. Estimate how many of these failures, from the most significant to the least, your organization can reliably fix in the time remaining.

4a. 从装运计划中删除无法修复的功能。4b. 或者，如果第 4a 步要求您丢弃一些使产品无法接受的东西，请取消并重新安排发货。

4a. Drop unfixable features from the shipment plan. 4b. Or if step 4a requires you to drop something that makes the product unacceptable, cancel and reschedule shipment.

5. 按照步骤 2 中确定的重要性顺序继续删除错误。

5. Proceed to remove the bugs in order of significance as identified in step 2.

为什么这是在项目结束时对错误的正确响应？好吧，当您决定发布产品但没有时间修复检测到的任何新错误时，停止搜索要修复的错误是有意义的。（如果你有资源，你可能想继续寻找错误——不是现在修复，而是向客户支持报告——但你需要抵制尝试匆忙修复它们的诱惑。）

Why is this the proper response to bugs as the project ends? Well, when you reach the point at which you've decided to ship a product but you don't have time to fix any new bugs you detect, it makes sense to stop searching for bugs to fix. (If you have the resources, you may want to keep searching for bugs—not to fix now, but to report to customer support—but you'll need to resist the temptation to try fixing them in a hurry.)

与其尝试修复低优先级的错误，不如重新分配你的修复力量。特别是，清理你知道的重大错误，使用你的测试人员帮助开发人员查明潜在的错误。然后，管理测试以揭示修复本身中的任何错误。

Instead of trying to fix low-priority bugs, redistribute your fixing forces. In particular, clean up the significant bugs you know about, using your testers to help developers pinpoint the underlying faults. Then, manage tests to reveal any bugs in the fixes themselves.

为什么对测试所需时间的估计与实际情况相去甚远？

Why are estimates of time that are needed for testing so far from reality?

项目开始时估算不佳是我们倾向于在结束时仓促行事的另一个原因。并不是该项目花费的时间比它应该花费的时间长，而是没有人正确地知道在现实世界中它应该花费多长时间。

Poor estimating at the beginning of a project is another reason we tend to rush at the end. It's not that the project is taking longer than it should, but that no one had the right idea of how long it should take in the real world.

以下小节描述了一些常见的计划错误，这些错误会导致匆忙结束项目以及牺牲测试质量。

The following subsections describe some common planning errors that lead to rushing at the end of projects as well as to sacrificed test quality.

晴天估计

Sunny-day estimating

估计与现实世界不符的主要原因有几个。原因之一是所谓的晴天估计——如果一切按计划进行并且没有错误需要修复，则估计项目将花费的时间。多么愚蠢、危险的概念！如果真的没有任何错误，为什么要安排测试呢？只需编写代码并发布即可。

There are several major reasons why estimating doesn't match the real world. One reason is so-called sunny-day estimating— estimating the time a project will take if everything goes as planned and there are no bugs to fix. What a dumb, dangerous concept! If there really weren't going to be any bugs, why schedule testing at all? Just write the code and ship it.

通过使用正确性的数学证明，计算机科学先驱 Harlan D. Mills 和其他作家认为他们可以完美地构建系统，这样就不需要测试了。他们在一些小的、封闭的子程序上取得了一定的成功，但几十年来，没有人能够为实际应用程序编写完美的程序。此外，随着系统变得越来越复杂，这样做的难度也在不断增加。（我们将在第 15 章详细讨论这个主题。）

By using mathematical proofs of correctness, computer science pioneer Harlan D. Mills and other writers thought they could build systems perfectly so that testing would not be necessary. They were moderately successful for some small, closed subroutines, but for several decades since, nobody has been able to write perfect programs for real applications. Moreover, the difficulty of doing so keeps growing as systems grow more complex. (We look more at this topic in Chapter 15.)

不切实际的过程模型

Unrealistic process models

你有没有看到你附近的房子在建，想知道为什么当你开车经过时房子看起来已经完工了，为什么要花这么长时间才能完成工作？如果您没有清楚地考虑建造房屋，您可能会认为所涉及的只是打地基、砌墙和盖屋顶。所以，如果你估计建造一所房子需要多长时间，但忽略了完成所有“看不见的”收尾工作所需的时间，你就没有得到准确的估计。如果您一开始就认为自己的估计是正确的，您会认为建造这座房子需要很长时间。

Did you ever watch a house going up in your neighborhood and wonder why it took so long to complete the job once the house looked finished as you drove by? If you don't think clearly about house-building, you might assume that all that's involved is laying down a foundation, building walls, and putting on a roof. So, if you estimated how long it takes to build a house, but omitted the time it takes to do all the "invisible" finishing work, you didn't produce an accurate estimate. And if you believed your estimate was right in the first place, you would think it's taking an awfully long time to build the house.

许多软件项目的估计都是错误的，因为它们忽略了关键步骤。通常，他们会省略“完成”步骤，例如查明错误、修复它们，然后重新测试并修复修复中产生的错误。相反，项目估算只是在最后显示了一段未区分的时间，称为“测试”。这类似于仅包括“打地基、砌墙、加屋顶，然后完工”的房屋建造时间表。“完成”至少掩盖了完成建造房屋所需时间的一半——这在软件项目中经常如此。

Many estimates of software projects are wrong because they omit key steps. Commonly, they omit "finishing" steps such as pinpointing bugs, repairing them, then retesting and fixing the bugs generated in the repairs. Instead, the project estimate simply shows an undifferentiated lump of time at the end called "testing." This is akin to a house-building schedule that only includes "build foundation, put up walls, add roof, then finish up." "Finish up" glosses over at least half of the time needed to complete building a house—as it often does in software projects.

劣质过程数据

Poor-quality process data

即使将“完成”更准确地分解为一系列测试-精确定位-修复-重新测试循环，如果使用稍微不准确的输入数据，估计也可能出现严重错误。下面显示了一位测试经理如何得出八周的测试时间表估算：

Even when "finishing up" is broken more accurately into a series of test-pinpoint-repair-retest cycles, the estimate can be seriously wrong if it uses even slightly inaccurate input data. The following shows how one test manager came up with an eight-week, test-schedule estimate:

• 我有400 个测试用例。

• I have 400 test cases.

• 在以前的项目中，我们发现每五个测试用例就有一个错误。

• In previous projects, we found one bug for every five test cases.

• 在本项目中，这意味着估计有 400 个中的 1/5，即 80 个错误。

• In this project, that would mean an estimate of 1/5 of 400, or 80 bugs.

• 在以前的项目中，2/5 的错误严重到需要修复。

• In previous projects, 2/5 of bugs were significant enough to demand fixing.

• 在本项目中，这意味着估计值为 80 的 2/5，或者

• In this project, that would mean an estimate of 2/5 of 80, or

32个错误。

32 bugs.

• 在以前的项目中，大约1/2 的剩余错误需要修复。

• In previous projects, about 1/2 of the remaining bugs needed to be fixed.

• 对于这个项目，这意味着 48 个中的 1/2，或 24 个额外的错误，总共 56 个。

• For this project, that would mean 1/2 of 48, or 24 additional bugs, 56 total.

• 以前的经验表明我们每周可以发现并修复大约 20 个错误。

• Previous experience says we can find and fix about 20 bugs per week.

• 这意味着需要大约三周的时间来处理 56 个错误。. .

• That would mean about three weeks to handle 56 bugs . . .

• 。. . 但是，这些修复中的 1/4 会有错误（14 个）并且必须再次循环，

• . . . BUT, 1/4 of those fixes will have bugs (14) and have to be cycled again,

• 这意味着又过了一周，仍然会有 1/4 的人有新的错误 (4)。

• and that means another week, and will still leave 1/4 of those with new bugs (4).

• 我们应该能够在一周内清除剩下的 4 个错误，还剩下一个。

• We should be able to clear up those 4 remaining bugs in one week, with one left.

• 因此，我将再增加一周的时间进行修复。

• So, I'll add one more week for fixing.

• 然后，再增加一周的时间进行分类以决定什么是重要的。

• Then, add another week for triage to decide what's significant.

• 还有一周的时间进行测试以启动和建立错误积压。

• And another week for testing to start up and build a backlog of bugs.

这总共需要八周，即他们实际开始向开发人员提供错误报告以尝试修复后的五周，而不是意识较差的经理可能估计的三周。

That makes a total of eight weeks, five after they actually start feeding bug reports to the developers to try to repair, not the three weeks that a less-aware manager might estimate.

该估算假设该项目将配备适当的人员并进行适当协调。就我个人而言，我会在计划的测试计划中增加 25%，以便在计划中留出时间来应对疾病、硬件和软件中的阻塞问题、最后一刻的更改以及其他此类计划外事件，从而使称为“测试”的一整块时间总共为 10 周。 “

This estimate assumes that the project will be properly staffed and coordinated. Myself, I would add 25 percent of the projected test schedule to allow time in the schedule for sickness, blocking problems in hardware and software, last-minute changes, and other such unplanned events, making ten weeks total for that lump called "testing."

这些估算基于从过去项目中收集的经验数据，但过去和当前项目估算之间的关系并不总是简单的。假设这些估计是错误的。考虑故障反馈率 (FFR)——实际将另一个错误引入系统的修复百分比。估计的 FFR 为 25%，每修复 4 个 bug 就会引入 1 个新 bug，但根据我的经验，这实际上相当低。如果 FFR 低至 50%，每两次修复就会引入一个新错误，我咨询过的许多组织都会很高兴。请记住，在压力下固定往往会提高 FFR。

These estimates are based on experiential data collected from past projects, but the relationship between past and current project estimates is not always simple. Suppose these estimates are wrong. Consider the fault-feedback-ratio (FFR)—the percentage of fixes that actually feed another bug into the system. The estimated FFR is 25 percent, with one new bug introduced in every four bugs fixed, but in my experience that's actually rather low. Many organizations I consult with would be delighted if their FFR were as low as 50 percent, with one new bug being introduced for every two fixes.
