Remember, fixing under pressure tends to raise the FFR.

尝试重新估计此测试计划，除了将 FFR 更改为 50% 之外，一切都相同，每两次修复引入一个新错误：

Try re-estimating this test schedule with everything the same except change the FFR to 50 percent, introducing one new bug with every two fixes:

• 。. . 三周时间处理 56 个 bug。. .

• . . . three weeks to handle 56 bugs . . .

• 。. . 但是，这些修复程序中有 1/2 会有错误（28 个）并且必须再次循环，

• . . . BUT, 1/2 of those fixes will have bugs (28) and have to be cycled again,

• 这意味着再过两周，仍然会留下 14 个新错误。

• and that means another two weeks, and will still leave 14 new bugs.

•再过一周会清除这些，但会留下 7 个新错误。

• Another week will clear these up but will leave 7 new bugs.

•再过一周就可以把这些清理干净，再剩下 4 个。

• And another week will clear these up and leave 4 more.

• 我们应该能够在一周内清除这 4 个剩余的错误，并留下一个新的错误。实际上是两个，但也许周围有足够多的人无事可做，我们可以降低那一周的 FFR。

• We should be able to clear up those 4 remaining bugs in one week, with one new bug left. Actually two, but maybe with enough people around having nothing else to do, we can reduce the FFR for that week.

• 因此，再增加一周的时间进行修复。

• So, add one more week for fixing.

• 然后，再增加一周进行分类。

• Then, add another week along the way for triage.

• 还有一周的时间进行测试以启动和建立错误积压。

• And another week for testing to start up and build a backlog of bugs.

• 然后为不可预测的事件增加25%。

• And then add 25 percent for unpredictable events.

FFR 从四分之一到二分之一的变化将“测试”时间从十周延长到十五周，尽管更长的时间意味着发生不可预测的事情的可能性更大。

The change of FFR from one out of four to one out of two stretches the "test" time from ten weeks to fifteen weeks, although the longer time means even more chance for something unpredictable to happen.

我见过 FFR 高达五分之四。您可能会尝试使用该 FFR 或更改修复率来重新估计此计划。但请记住，如果您尝试加快修复率，您很可能会提高 FFR。

I have seen FFRs as high as four out of five. You might try to re-estimate this schedule using that FFR, or changing the fix rate. Remember, though, that if you try to speed up the fix rate, you're likely to raise the FFR.

无过程数据

No process data

不幸的是，许多测试估算根本不是基于数据，而仅仅是基于外部的愿望，没有调整范围或过程来削减希望以适应现实。通常，它是这样的：

Unfortunately, much estimating of testing is not based on data at all, but merely on a wish based on externals, with no adjustment of scope or process to trim down the wish to fit reality. Often, it goes like this:

“哦，我们绝对需要从明天开始的 24 周内安装这个软件。我们需要两周的时间来配备人员并获得批准。然后我们需要四个星期的需求，四个星期的架构，四个星期的设计，八个星期几周的编码时间。加起来是二十二周，所以我们还有两周的时间进行测试。”

"Oh, we absolutely need this software in place twenty-four weeks from tomorrow. We need two weeks to staff up and get approvals. Then we'll need four weeks for requirements, four weeks for architecture, four weeks for design, and eight weeks for coding. That adds up to twenty-two weeks, so we'll have two weeks left for testing."

当设计延迟一周时，经理们会召开一个重要会议并说，“哦，我们仍然可以制定时间表。我们将缩短一周的测试时间。一周用于测试应该足够了，因为不会有很多错误——开发人员非常非常好。”

When design slips a week, the managers have a big meeting and say, "Oh, we can still make the schedule. We'll just chop a week off testing. One week for testing should be plenty as there won't be many bugs—the developers are very, very good."

确定您是否已经过了可以有所作为的地步。

Determine whether you've passed the point where you can make a difference.

也许对测试信息最重要的反应是做出任何反应是否可以改进软件本身的决定。为此，您可能需要等待一段时间才能获得更多信息。等待是一种可以接受的回应，只要您明确说明等待的原因即可。永远不要宣布你“只是在等待”，而是总是指一个特定的事件或时间，或两者兼而有之。

Perhaps the most important response to test information is making a decision about whether any response can improve the software itself. To do this, you may have to wait a while for more information. Waiting is an acceptable response, as long as you make clear why you're waiting. Never announce that you're "just waiting," but always refer to a specified event or time, or both.

虽然寻求更多信息是可以接受的回应，但请记住，您的回应不仅仅是您的言语。人们听你的语气，看你的肢体语言。你回应的所有部分都会影响士气，因此请保持你的回应开放、清晰和诚实。

Although seeking more information is an acceptable response, remember that your response is not simply your words. People listen to your tone and watch your body language. All parts of your response can affect morale, so keep your responses open, clear, and honest.

但是，如果您不能再等待怎么办？如果您没有时间获取更多信息怎么办？令人惊讶的是，您仍然有许多备选答案。你可以按原样运送产品，你可以指出故障，你可以警告客户故障，你可以撤回零件，你可以撤回整个产品，或者你可以从事情开始出错的地方重新开始（a与您注意到出现问题的时间点明显不同的时间点）。

But what if you can wait no longer? What can you do if you have no time to get more information? Surprisingly, you still have many alternative responses. You can ship the product as is, you can feature the failures, you can warn customers about failures, you can withdraw parts, you can withdraw the whole product, or you can start over from the point at which things began to go wrong (a point in time distinctly different from the point at which you noticed that things had gone wrong).

最激烈的反应是宣布该项目破产并从头开始。这种反应可能会让你失去工作，但会挽救你的生命。无论这是否会让您失去工作，您都可以使用从本项目中收​​集到的所有知识开始下一个项目。你已经交了学费；这些学习是可选的。

The most drastic response would be to declare the project bankrupt and start over from scratch. This response may cost you your job, but save your life. Whether or not it costs you your job, you can begin the next project using all the learnings you've gleaned from this one. You've paid the tuition; the learnings are optional.

概括

Summary

如果一个项目在测试之前没有得到很好的管理，那么大多数好的响应将不再可用。在许多情况下，没有任何回应可以挽救项目——除非重新开始并从头开始。

If a project hasn't been managed well before testing, most good responses will no longer be available. In many cases, there is no response that will save the project—except starting over and doing it right from the beginning.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.看运气：运气偏向于管理良好的项目。

1. Depending on luck: Luck favors the well-managed project.

2.减少测试时间和资源来制定时间表：如果你不关心质量，你可以制定任何时间表，但是为什么要测试呢？

2. Reducing test time and resources to make a schedule: If you don't care about quality, you can make any schedule, but then why test at all?

3.未能在测试提供有关产品实际状态的信息时调整时间表和估计：没有人对未来有足够的了解，无法做出绝对的承诺。能对未来做出承诺的人一定是某种恶魔。

3. Failing to adjust schedules and estimates as testing provides information on the actual state of the product: Nobody knows the future well enough to make absolute promises. Anyone who can make promises about the future must be some sort of devil.

4.未能收集过程数据：错误是制造出来的，而不是天生的。您对它们的制造地点和时间了解得越多，它们就越容易被检测、查明、定位和修复——或防止下次发生。

4. Failing to collect process data: Errors are made, not born. The more you know about where and when they are made, the easier they are to detect, pinpoint, locate, and fix—or prevent the next time around.

5.不了解测试何时开始：测试在项目构思或之前开始。如果你不知道这一点，你根本就不懂测试。

5. Not understanding when testing starts: Testing starts at project conception, or before. If you don't know this, you don't understand testing at all.

6. 测试一匹死马：如果你发现一个特定的构建有缺陷并且需要大量的修复工作，不要盲目地继续测试和报告错误，因为广泛的修复会使你的错误报告变得毫无意义。[13]

6. Testing a dead horse: If you see that a particular build is crippled and needs a lot of fixing work, don't blindly continue to test and report bugs, because the extensive fix will render your bug reports moot. [13]

第 15 章_防止测试变得更加困难

Chapter_15_Preventing Testing from Growing More Difficult

 

“如果傻瓜坚持他的愚蠢，他就会变得聪明。” - William Blake，诗人、画家和雕刻师，“地狱箴言”，天堂与地狱的联姻[1790–1793]。

"If the fool would persist in his folly he would become wise." - William Blake, Poet, Painter, and Engraver, "Proverbs of Hell," The Marriage of Heaven and Hell [1790–1793].

如果你打算把你的下一个项目做得比上一个好，一个好的开始是理解为什么它实际上会比上一个项目更难。如果你的项目很愚蠢，那就更有理由坚持——不是为了完成或验证那个项目，而是为了从那个项目中学习。

If you're going to do your next project better than you did the last, a good place to start is by understanding why it's actually going to be a more difficult project than the previous one. If your project was folly, all the more reason to persist—not in completing or validating that project, but in learning from that project.

为什么情况越来越糟？

Why is the situation growing worse?

从根本上说，软件测试变得越来越困难，因为我们变得更加雄心勃勃。我们可以看到计算机的无限潜力，因此每当我们成功创建提供有价值的东西的软件时，我们都会暂停一微秒说“谢谢”——然后要求更多！

Fundamentally, software testing is becoming more difficult because we have become more ambitious. We can see the infinite potential of computers, so whenever we succeed in creating software that provides something of value, we pause for a microsecond to say "thank you"—then demand MORE!

因此，随着时间的推移，系统会变得更大。五十年前，一个使用 87,000 字节内存的程序会被认为是巨大的。今天，我用来写这篇文章的文字处理器使用了 870,507,943 个字节，是当时“庞大”的一万倍。

So, over time, systems grow larger. Fifty years ago, a program that used 87,000 bytes of memory would have been considered huge. Today, the word processor with which I wrote this passage uses 870,507,943 bytes, ten-thousand times as big as "huge" was then.

顺便说一下，尺寸增加一万倍似乎可以解释为什么测试变得如此困难，但故事并没有就此结束。早在 20 世纪 40 年代后期，第二次世界大战结束时，美国就充满了恢复和平时期正常活动的活力——雄心勃勃的工程师们有机会从头开始做很多事情，并且把它们做好。例如，在化学加工行业，许多新工厂从绘图板进入建设阶段。一个流行的主题是规模经济——越大越好，因为越大越便宜。事实证明完全不同。

Offhand, a ten-thousandfold increase in size would seem to explain why testing has grown so difficult, but the story doesn't end there. Back in the late 1940s when World War II ended, the United States was abuzz with energy to restore normal peacetime activities—and ambitious engineers had an opportunity to do many things from scratch, and do them right. In the chemical processing industries, for example, many new plants moved from the drawing board to construction. One prevailing theme was the economy of scale—bigger would be better because bigger would be cheaper. The reality proved quite different.

是的，拥有更大的工厂可以降低生产每加仑特定化学品的单位成本——但仅限于工厂生产时。当它被关闭时，成本是无限的。为什么要关闭工厂？当然是因为失败——用软件术语来说，是一个错误。事实证明，在较大的工厂中，失败的成本大于规模节省的成本。对大的热情消亡了。让我们看看为什么。

Yes, having bigger plants reduced the unit cost of producing each gallon of a given chemical—but only when the plant was producing. When it was shut down, the cost was infinite. And why would a plant be shut down? Because of failure, of course—in software terms, a bug. As it turned out, in the bigger plants, the cost of failure was greater than the savings of scale. The passion for bigness died. Let's see why.

首先，当然，工厂越大，可能发生故障的地方就越多（故障次数）。软件也是如此吗？

First of all, of course, the bigger the plant, the more places there were where failure could occur (number-of-failures). Is this true of software, too?

其次，工厂越大，越难查明故障原因（查明时间）。软件也是？

Second, the bigger the plant, the harder it was to pinpoint the cause of failure (time-to-pinpoint). Software, too?

第三，工厂越大，越难在不产生副作用的情况下修复故障（修复时间）。软件也是？第四，工厂越大，每次工厂停机维修时生产力损失就越大（机会损失成本）。软件？

Third, the bigger the plant, the harder it was to fix a fault without producing side effects (time-to-fix). Software, too? Fourth, the bigger the plant, the greater the loss in productivity each time the plant shut down for repair (lost- opportunity cost). Software?

一旦化学公司开始意识到所有这些因素如何相乘以提高规模成本，超出规模经济，他们就放弃了一些最大工厂的建设，并将注意力转向建设较小的工厂。软件制造商能否从他们代价高昂的教训中吸取教训？除了放弃理解不清的项目，管理者还能做什么？

As soon as the chemical companies began to realize how all these factors multiplied together to raise the cost of scale beyond the economies of scale, they abandoned construction of some of their largest plants and redirected their attention to building smaller plants. Can software makers learn from their costly lessons? What can managers do besides abandoning ill-understood projects?

使系统尽可能小。

Keep systems as small as possible.

应对不断增加的测试成本的第一个对策是使系统尽可能小（但不能更小）。控制需求在很大程度上是开发项目本身之外的一项管理工作。这一点做不好，就是管理失败。

The first counteraction to escalating testing costs is to keep systems as small as possible (but no smaller). Keeping requirements under control is largely a management job, outside of the development project itself. It is a management failure when this is not done well.

系统需求不受控制的增长非常普遍，以至于软件分析师、设计人员和开发人员用几个名称来描述这种现象：需求泄漏、需求蠕变、需求漂移。同意向计划中或正在进行的项目“再添加一件事”实在是太容易了，特别是如果您没有一个流程来估计添加对错误成本的非线性影响。

Uncontrolled growth of a system's requirements is so common that software analysts, designers, and developers have several names to describe the phenomenon: requirements leakage, requirements creep, requirements drift. It's just all too easy to agree to "add just one more thing" to a contemplated or ongoing project, especially if you don't have a process for estimating what nonlinear effects the addition will have on error cost.

控制需求的增长变得更加困难，因为它要求决策者或利益相关者区分产品真正需要的东西和有价值但不值得额外成本和风险的东西。当测试使开发人员意识到“嘿——这真的是一个需求！”时，“需求发现”就发生了。我们称之为泄漏、蠕变或漂移的大部分是对一些隐藏的假设的认识，一些在早期需求过程中被遗漏的需求。

Controlling the growth of requirements is made even more difficult because it requires that a decision-maker or stakeholder distinguish between something that really is necessary to the product versus something that would have value but whose value isn't worth the additional cost and risk. "Requirements discovery" happens when testing causes developers to realize "Hey—that really is a requirement!" Much of which we call leakage or creep or drift is recognition of some buried assumption, some requirement that was missed in the earlier requirements process.

开发人员常犯的一个错误是试图处理软件中的每一种可能情况。仅仅因为您可以在软件中做任何事情并不意味着您应该在同一个系统中在软件中做所有事情。

One common mistake developers make is trying to handle every possible situation in the software. Just because you can do anything in software does not mean you should do everything in software, all in the same system.

我曾经有一个客户根据 15,000 多份租约的条款计算并向土地所有者支付矿产权使用费，其中有七份租约非常旧，并且有大量“例外”条件。当客户尝试自动化其手动特许权使用费支付系统时，其特定于租赁的软件项目在测试中陷入困境。我被叫来帮忙，并建议客户至少暂时手动计算和支付这七个租约的版税，就像在自动化之前所做的那样。这一变化将系统的大小减少了一半，并将开发工作减少了十分之一。并不是所有的事情都必须由计算机完成，至少不是所有的第一轮。

I once had a client that calculated and paid mineral-rights royalties to landowners according to the terms of more than 15,000 leases, seven of which were exceedingly old and had a large number of "exception" conditions. When the client tried automating its manual royalties-payment system, its lease-specific software project was bogging down in testing. I was called in to help, and suggested that, for the time being at least, the client compute and pay royalties for these seven leases manually, as it had been doing prior to automating. This one change reduced the size of the system by half, and cut the development effort by a factor of ten. Not everything has to be done by computer, at least not all at the first go-round.

保持你的“系统”模型可扩展。

Keep your model of "system" expansive.

您可能成功地构建了一个小型应用程序，但遇到了麻烦，因为运行时或浏览器或操作系统或网络很大而且多毛。进一步的麻烦可能来自与应用程序交互的人——他们是所有系统中最毛茸茸的。在检查您正在开发的简单系统如何与更大、极其复杂的系统交织在一起时保持警惕。

You might be successful in building a small application but run into trouble because the run-time or browser or operating system or network is big—and hairy. Further trouble may come from human beings who will interact with the application—they're the hairiest systems of all. Be vigilant in checking how the simple system you're developing is intertwined with larger, desperately complex systems.

在具有清晰界面的隔离组件中逐步构建。

Build incrementally in isolated components with clear interfaces.

程序的大小不仅仅根据代码行数来定义（请原谅我之前使用这种简化来说明问题）。物理大小相同的两个程序在其内部复杂性方面可能会有很大差异，最终，这可能是测试工作难度的主要因素。为了帮助控制测试，您可以采取措施来控制复杂性。例如，正如 not-all-at-once 策略所建议的那样，您可以逐步构建，在尝试下一个部分之前先构建、测试和修复每个部分。

The size of a program is not defined in terms of just the number of lines of code (forgive me for using that simplification earlier to make a point). Two programs of the same physical size can differ greatly in their internal complexity, which, in the end, can be a dominant factor in how difficult the testing effort will be. To help keep testing under control, you can take steps to control complexity. For instance, as suggested by the not-all-at-once strategy, you can build incrementally, with each piece built, tested, and fixed before the next piece is attempted.

有许多过程规程采用这种渐进哲学，其中许多都属于“敏捷”的范畴。任何此类方法的基础都是构建足够小的零件，以便您很有可能在成品中不留下任何错误。为什么？因为在某种程度上，您可以确定任何新错误不在您的“已完成”工作中，您可以大大简化在添加到系统的下一个组件中查明错误的过程。

There are a number of process disciplines that employ this incremental philosophy, many falling under the rubric "agile." The foundation of any such method is to build pieces small enough so that you have a high probability of leaving no bugs in the finished product. Why? Because to the extent that you're sure any new bug is not in your "completed" work, you vastly simplify the pinpointing of bugs in the next component you add to the system.

伴随这种增量构建的是测试先行的想法——在开始构建每个组件之前创建一组验收测试。当新组件通过这些测试时，您就可以将其添加到增量开发系统中，现在以调查而非确认的方式对其进行积极测试。

Along with such incremental building goes the idea of test-first—creating a set of acceptance tests before you start to build each component. When the new component passes these tests, then you're ready to add it to the incrementally developing system, now to test it aggressively, in an investigative rather than confirmatory way.

增量开发还有另一个优势，只要它也遵循重要性优先的流程。如果你遇到了意想不到的事情并且不得不在你计划停止之前停下来，你至少已经完成了你在这段时间里本可以完成的最重要的事情。因此，即使您遇到意想不到的问题（而且您会遇到），您也可以按计划交付可能有用的东西，即使最终没有完成。

There's another advantage to incremental development, as long as it is also guided by a significance-first process. If you run into something unexpected and have to stop before you planned to stop, you will at least have done the most significant things you could have done in the time you had. Thus, even if you run into unexpected problems (and you will), you can deliver something on schedule that's likely to be useful, even if not ultimately complete.

有时，当系统在使用中时，您会发现不值得添加这些额外的部件，从而使系统比您最初想象的要小。

And sometimes, when the system is in use, you will discover that it's not worth adding those additional parts, thus keeping the system smaller than you initially thought possible.

减少进入的错误数量。

Reduce the number of bugs going in.

测试难度不仅仅是您从系统中排除了多少错误的问题，还与它们何时消失有关。一般来说，越早消除错误，花费的成本就越少。

Testing difficulty is not simply a matter of how many bugs you take out of a system, but also of when they go out. In general, the earlier you get rid of a bug, the less it costs you.

人们经常混淆 bug 出现的时间和 bug 出现的时间。在开发过程接近尾声的测试中发现的 bug 可能在过程的早期任何时间被引入。关于bug这个词的一个不幸的事情是它暗示错误以某种神秘的方式潜入产品的方式。但他们不会悄悄进来；他们被放进去。由人。随时。而且，由于您想尽早消除错误，因此了解您的开发过程何时引入错误很重要。

People frequently confuse the time a bug comes out with the time a bug was put in. A bug that's revealed in a test near the end of the development process might have been put in at any time earlier in the process. One of the unfortunate things about the word bug is the way it suggests that errors creep into the product in some mysterious way. But they don't creep in; they're put in. By people. At any time. And, since you want to remove bugs as early as possible, it's important to learn when your development process introduces them.

所有这些都表明测试必须尽早开始，并始终保持。正如我们所见，实现这一目标的一种方法是逐步构建，首先进行测试。[14] 这不是唯一的方法，但对于那些认为唯一的测试是在机器上运行代码的人来说，其他方法是不可见的。在下一章中，我们会看到为什么事实并非如此。

All this suggests that testing must be started early, and maintained throughout. One way to do this, as we've seen, is by building incrementally, testing first. [14] That's not the only way, but the other ways are invisible to those who believe that the only kind of testing is running code on a machine. In the next chapter, we see why that isn't true.

概括

Summary

尽管组织和执行不当的测试肯定会延长工作时间，但随着产品变得越来越大和越来越复杂，内在的系统动态会使测试和修复时间更长。如果你了解这些动态，在一定程度上可以通过多种方式来应对它们。

Although poorly organized and executed testing can certainly prolong the effort, there are intrinsic system dynamics that make testing and fixing take longer as products grow larger and more complex. If you understand these dynamics, there are ways they can be countered, up to a point.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.低估旧的、修补过的代码的复杂性：我在我位于新墨西哥州的漂亮的老房子里写了这一部分，当时一名水管工在隔壁房间工作，试图拔掉我的水槽的插头。我原以为他的工作会很简单，而且相对简单，但他花了两个多小时试图弄清楚如何在他清理管道之前改造可能已有 60 年历史的管道。排水管和旧的修补代码的复杂性同样令人困惑。

1. Underestimating the complexity of old, patched-up code: I wrote this section in my old, wonderful house in New Mexico as a plumber worked in the next room trying to unplug my sink. I had thought his job was going to be straightforward and comparatively simple, but he spent more than two hours trying to figure out how to retrofit what is conceivably sixty-year-old plumbing before he could clear the pipes. Complexity in drainpipes and in old, patched-up code can be similarly perplexing.

2.没有让你的工具保持锋利：这种复杂性不仅来自你认为你正在构建的东西，还来自你正在构建的东西。工具（编译器、网络构建平台、通用数据库）中的错误就是您系统中的错误，并且比您直接放入的大多数错误隐藏得更好。我知道当您急于交付您的产品时，推迟工具更新很诱人，但如果您未能使您的工具保持最新状态，您将在以后引发一系列测试问题——这些问题会减慢你比更新工具更失望。

2. Not keeping your tools sharp: This complexity comes not just from what you think you are building, but also from what you are building on. A bug in a tool–a compiler, a web-building platform, a common database–is a bug in your system, and much better hidden than most of the ones that you put in directly. I know it's tempting to postpone tool updates when you're in a hurry to deliver your product, but if you fail to keep your tools up-to-date, you're inviting a host of testing problems later on–problems that will slow you down more than updating the tool would do.

3.不允许讨论这些事情，更不用说衡量了：任何时候你听到有人说，“我们不能谈论那个，”你需要停下你正在做的事情并谈论它。“我们无法衡量”也是如此。

3. Not allowing these matters to be discussed, let alone measured: Any time you hear someone say, "We can't talk about that," you need to stop whatever you're doing and talk about it. The same goes for "We can't measure that."

4.未能按照目前的经验调整过程数据：我不知道有哪个软件开发或维护项目不包含惊喜。这就是为什么测试不能提前计划到完美而必须进行探索的原因之一。

4. Failing to adjust process data as current experience indicates: I don't know of any software development or maintenance project that doesn't contain surprises. That's one reason why testing can't be planned to perfection in advance, and has to be exploratory.

5.使用早期回报作为后期结果的指标：关于初始案例，你总是知道一件事：根据定义，它们与后来的案例不同。

5. Using early returns as indicators of later results: One thing you always know about initial cases: They're different from later cases, by definition.

6.将测试人员视为“阻止交付的坏人”：像任何人一样，一些测试人员也是坏人，但无论好坏，他们只是信息的提供者。他们不做交付决定——如果他们做，那么他们的经理就是坏人。

6. Thinking about testers as "the bad guys who prevent delivery": Like any human beings, some testers are bad guys, but good or bad, they are simply providers of information. They don't make delivery decisions—if they do, then their managers are the bad guys.

7.自认为“质量警察”的测试人员：即使他们是警察，他们也肯定不是法官、陪审团或立法者。

7. Testers thinking of themselves as "quality police": Even if they were police, they are certainly not judges or juries or legislators.

Chapter_16_无机器测试

Chapter_16_Testing Without Machinery

 

“百分之九十九的失败都来自那些有找借口习惯的人。” - George Washington Carver，发明家和植物学家（1864-1943 年），请参阅 http://www.worldofquotes.com/topic/Failure/index.html 以了解有关事物失败原因的观察结果和其他观察结果。

"Ninety-nine percent of all failures come from people who have the habit of making excuses." - George Washington Carver, Inventor and Botanist (1864–1943), see http://www.worldofquotes.com/topic/Failure/index.html for this and other observations about why things fail.

头号测试工具不是计算机，而是人脑——与眼睛、耳朵和其他感觉器官相结合的大脑。再多的计算能力也无法弥补无脑测试，但大量的脑力可以弥补缺少或无法使用的计算机。这一原则指导 James Bach 努力用更相关的“智能测试”取代术语“手动测试”。

The number one testing tool is not the computer, but the human brain—the brain in conjunction with eyes, ears, and other sense organs. No amount of computing power can compensate for brainless testing, but lots of brainpower can compensate for a missing or unavailable computer. This principle guides James Bach's effort to replace the term "manual testing" with the more relevant "sapient testing."

在他的博客 http://www.satisfice.com/blog/archives/99 上，James 生动地表达了他的观点：“手动测试让人联想到链条帮派劳工移动石头的画面。你立刻想知道为什么他们不只是使用反铲。”

On his blog, at http://www.satisfice.com/blog/archives/99, James makes his point vividly: "Manual testing conjures images of chain gang laborers, moving rocks. You immediately wonder why they don't just use a backhoe."

仅通过机器进行测试是远远不够的。

Testing by machine is never enough.

投入大量脑力测试系统的最简单方法是技术审查。当同行作为一个小组坐下来分析和记录某些技术产品（例如代码、设计、规范或用户手册）的优缺点时，就会发生技术审查。在代码的情况下，审查人员不是将产品视为密封（或“黑”）盒，而是执行“白盒”或“透明盒”，或者更好的“开盒”测试。而且，虽然没有人在敲击钥匙，但正在测试它。技术审查确实是一个“收集有关产品的信息，目的是将这些信息用于某种目的”的过程。

The simplest way to put lots of brainpower to work testing a system is the technical review. A technical review takes place when peers sit down together as a group to analyze and document the good and bad qualities of some technical product, such as code, design, a specification, or a user manual. In the case of code, rather than treating the product as a sealed (or "black") box, the reviewers are said to be performing "white box" or "transparent box," or, even better, "open box" testing. And, though nobody is banging keys, testing it is. Technical reviewing is indeed a process of " gathering information about a product with the intent that the information could be used for some purpose."

技术审查的一个明显优势是它们可以应用于无法轻易通过机器测试的项目材料。如何在计算机上测试可行性研究？好吧，当然，需求和设计文档可以接受机器测试的一致性和语法——这样的测试可能很有价值——但与几个人脑处理这些材料所能完成的相比，它们是非常有限的。

One obvious advantage of technical reviews is the way they can be applied to project materials that cannot readily be tested by machine. How do you test a feasibility study on a computer? Well, of course requirements and design documents can be subjected to machine tests for consistency and grammar—and such tests can be valuable—but they are sorely limited compared with what can be accomplished by several human brains working over the materials.

机器测试和技术审查之间的选择不是非此即彼。当与机器执行测试相结合时，技术审查是一种特别强大的测试技术，因为这两种方法倾向于检测不同类型的错误。单独使用任何一种方法（应用于代码并做得很好）可能会发现 60% 到 70% 的错误，而结合使用时，它们通常会发现 90% 以上的错误。

The choice between machine testing and technical reviewing is not either-or. Technical reviewing is an especially powerful testing technique when combined with machine execution testing because the two approaches tend to detect different types of bugs. Whereas either method alone—applied to code and done well— may find 60 to 70 percent of bugs, when combined they often may find 90-plus percent.

尽管如此，出于各种原因，许多开发人员似乎不愿意参与技术审查。[15]

Still, many developers seem reluctant to participate in technical reviews, for a variety of reasons. [15]

奇怪的是，给出的不想审查产品的理由可以为有洞察力的经理提供测试该产品的最强大、最快捷的方法之一。

Curiously, the reasons given for not wanting to review a product can provide the perceptive manager with one of the most powerful, and quickest, ways of testing that product.

即时评论

Instant reviews

多年来，我听到的关于技术审查最常见的抱怨是审查时间太长。缺乏审核经验的组织认为他们花费的时间太长的原因之一是他们的员工不知道审核何时完成。在许多情况下，审核实际上可能在这些缺乏经验的审稿人意识到审核已经开始之前就已经完成了。我将这些类型的审查称为“即时审查”，当有人给出工作产品不能或不应该审查的理由时，就会发生这种审查。下面列出的“原因”都与某人试图阻止评论有关。它们是生产者思维过程中的错误，而不是产品本身的错误，它们本身就是即时评论。

Over the years, the most common complaint I have heard about technical reviews is that they take too long. One reason organizations that lack experience with reviews think they take too long is that their people don't know when a review has been completed. In many cases, a review actually may be finished before these inexperienced reviewers even recognize that it has started. I call these types of reviews, which occur when someone gives a reason why a work product cannot or should not be reviewed, "instant reviews." The "reasons" listed below all pertain to someone's attempt to block a review. They are bugs in the thought process of the producers, not in the product itself, and are themselves instant reviews.

“审查产品需要很长时间。”

"It would take too long to review the product."

当您听到有人将此异议作为不执行技术审查的理由时，要提出的一个问题是产品尺寸不合适，必须以某种方式分解为可审查（即可理解）的部分。

When you hear someone give this objection as the reason for not performing a technical review, the one issue to raise is that the product is not a suitable size, and must be broken down somehow into reviewable (that is, understandable) pieces.

“但产品不能分解成可审查的部分。”

"But the product can't be broken down into reviewable pieces."

在这种情况下，问题在于它是一个难以理解的大块，审查建议是重新开始并将其重建为可审查的内容。如果它太大而无法审查，那么它肯定会太大而无法通过其他方式进行测试。

In this case, the issue is that it's one big incomprehensible lump, and the review recommendation is to start over and rebuild it into something reviewable. If it's too big to review, it's definitely going to be too big to test in other ways.

“除了作者，没有人能理解代码。”

"Nobody but the author could understand the code."

必须将此产品重建为可以使用和维护的形式——除非您愿意并且能够将您交付的每个副本都发送给作者，无论是现在还是在产品的整个生命周期内。

This product must be rebuilt into a form that can be used and maintained—unless you're willing and able to send the author along with every copy you deliver, now and for the entire lifetime of the product.

“这是不言而喻的。”

"It's self-evident."

如果真的不言而喻，为什么要反对审查，这应该需要几秒钟？以我的经验，不证自明的说法从来都不是真的。也许某个地方存在不言自明的产品，但半个世纪以来，我从未见过一款软件或支持材料能够实现这一雄心勃勃的主张。

If it's truly self-evident, why object to a review, which should take a few seconds? In my experience, the claim of self-evidence is never true. Perhaps a self-evident product exists somewhere, but in half a century, I've never seen a piece of software or supporting material that fulfilled this ambitious claim.

“它太小了，不用费心。可能会出什么问题？”

"It's too small to bother with. What could possibly go wrong?"

好吧，如果它那么小，评论会快速而廉价地告诉您可能会出错的地方。您可能想记住有多少次单行代码更改使某个组织损失了 10 亿美元左右，或者这种更改实际上导致某人死亡的次数。工作产品越短，人们就越有可能说它不值得费心——然后懒得仔细去做，或者考虑它与其他系统的交互和依赖性，这可能是巨大的。

Well, if it's that small, a review will tell you quickly and cheaply what could possibly go wrong. You might want to remember the number of times a one-line code change has cost some organization a billion dollars or so, or the times that such a change has actually killed someone. The shorter the work product, the more likely people are to say it's not worth bothering with—and then to not bother to do it carefully, or to consider its interaction with and dependency on other systems, which may be huge.

“来不及复习了。”

"It's too late to review it."

在开发过程中更改产品确实可能为时已晚，但这里的问题是开发过程本身出了问题。当您开始对所有 bug 抱有偏见时，请不要感到惊讶。

It may indeed be too late in the development process to change a product, but the issue here is that something's wrong with the development process itself. Just don't be surprised when you start taking your lumps for all the bugs.

“现在审查它还为时过早。”

"It's too early to review it."

这可能确实为时过早，但如果您的日程安排表明某些内容应该准备好进行审核但实际上没有，那么问题就是您现在落后于日程安排。

It may indeed be too early, but if your schedule says something is supposed to be ready for review and it's not, then the issue is that you're now behind schedule.

“是的，是时候审查它了，但我仍在修复其中的错误。”

"Yes, it's time to review it, but I'm still fixing bugs in it."

如果一个产品有很多错误，立即审查它可能是个好主意，以帮助遇到麻烦的开发人员。如果开发人员拒绝帮助，那就是问题所在。没有哪个开发人员能够始终如一地独自完成任务——而且是正确完成任务。

If a product is very buggy, it's probably a good idea to review it immediately, to help out the developer, who is in some kind of trouble. If the developer refuses help, then that's the issue. No developer is good enough to consistently do it alone—and do it right.

“我们无法审查它，因为我们不知道它应该解决什么问题。”

"We can't review it because we don't know what problem it's supposed to solve."

那你到底为什么要建造它？这里的问题是某些祖先文档或过程未完成或未被理解。或者可能没有产品应该解决的问题，在这种情况下，即时评论建议是“扔掉它，停止浪费金钱”。

Then why the heck did you build it? The issue here is that some ancestor document or process is not finished, or not understood. Or perhaps there isn't a problem the product is supposed to solve, in which case the instant-review recommendation is, "Throw it out and stop wasting money."

“我们的问题陈述并没有真正解决我们正在解决的问题。”

"The problem statement we have doesn't really address the problem we're solving."

好吧，所以这里的问题是在继续之前获得适当的问题陈述——除非你期望未来的用户和维护者是读心术的人。

Well, fine, so the issue here is to get the appropriate problem statement before proceeding—unless you expect future users and maintainers to be mind-readers.

“我们不知道我们正在解决什么问题，因为我们在前进的过程中定义了问题。”

"We don't know what problem we're solving because we're defining the problem as we go along."

我从声称使用某些敏捷开发过程的客户那里听到了这种抱怨。不幸的是，他们不了解敏捷过程的工作原理，而且他们正在审查错误的部分。在敏捷过程中，您审查每个定义部分或“故事”（即下一个软件增量要解决的问题的每个定义）；设计验收测试；审查; 然后测试开发人员和测试人员根据定义得出的工作产品。您以这种方式逐步进行，直到您的客户说没有更多的故事要实施。

I hear this complaint from clients who claim to be using some agile development process. Unfortunately, they don't understand how an agile process works, and they're reviewing the wrong pieces. In an agile process, you review each definition piece, or "story" (that is, each definition of the problem to be solved by the next software increment); design an acceptance test; review; and then test the work product derived by both the developers and testers from the definition. You proceed incrementally in this way until your customer says there are no more stories to implement.

“我们将不得不花费数周时间准备审查。”

"We would have to spend weeks preparing for a review."

如果人们需要数周的时间来准备，这意味着他们还没有产生需要测试/审查的可交付成果。任何值得一提的开发过程的基本原则是，你应该生产这些项目，所以如果你还没有生产它们，那么你就没有完成整个过程——所以根据定义，产品还没有完成。如果修理工说你的车已经修好了，除了他懒得做的修理步骤，你会接受修理厂的车吗？不，这次审查结束了。

If people need weeks to prepare, it means they haven't been producing the deliverables that need to be tested/reviewed. A basic tenet of any development process worth its salt says you should be producing these items, so if you haven't produced them, then you haven't performed the entire process—and so the product is, by definition, not finished. Would you accept your car from the repair shop if the mechanic said it was repaired, except for the repair steps he didn't bother to do? No, this review is over.

“我们不想让任何人看到我们在做什么，因为我们的员工过于敏感。”

"We don't want anybody looking at what we're doing, because our people are oversensitive."

要么错误的人在开发产品，要么他们管理不善。或者他们可能计划使用该程序从您的组织中窃取某些东西。或者从你那里勒索一些东西，因为他们是唯一知道关键程序的人。

Either the wrong people are working on the product, or they're being mismanaged. Or perhaps they're planning to use the program to steal something from your organization. Or extort something from you because they're the only ones who know anything about a critical program.

“你不能审查性能，因为在我们构建它之前我们不知道它会是什么，然后我们会进行优化，这样它就不会成为问题。”

"You can't review for performance, because we don't know what that will be until we build it, and then we'll optimize so it won't be a problem."

有时这个借口被证明是有效的，但为什么要看运气呢？这个产品需要一个简单地问这个问题的评论，“这看起来是否有机会正常运行？” 而且，如果对那次审查的回答是肯定的，那么下一次审查应该提出后续问题：“这是否是以未来优化人员可以理解的方式编写的？”

Sometimes this excuse turns out to be valid, but why depend on luck? This product needs a review that simply asks the question, "Does this look as if it will have a chance to perform properly?" And, if the answer to that review is affirmative, then the next review should ask the follow-up question: "Is this written in such a way that future optimizers can understand it?"

“我们一准备好就会通知你。”

"We'll let you know as soon as we're ready."

审核结束。即时审核结果：审核未完成，因为产品未完成。

Review is over. Instant-review result: Review was not complete because the product was not finished.

“我们的建筑商已经在内部审查过它，所以再审查一次是浪费时间。”

"We builders reviewed it already, internally, so another review would be a waste of time."

如果产品做得很好，第二次审查不会花很长时间，并且会让您确信除了构建者之外的其他人也能理解它。如果内部审查没有做好，那么产品也不太可能做好。

If the product has been done well, a second review won't take long, and will give you assurance that someone other than the builders can understand it. If the internal review wasn't done well, then it's unlikely that the product was done well either.

“我们之前审查过类似的东西。”

"We reviewed something just like this before."

了不起！这意味着您将能够更迅速地查看这个新版本。您还可以比较这两个评论的结果，这将提供更多信息。

Terrific! That means you'll be able to review this new one all the more expeditiously. You may also be able to compare results from the two reviews, which will provide additional information.

“你和你的审稿人在这方面并不完全合格。事实上，只有这个项目才有资格。”

"You and your reviewers aren't fully qualified in this area. In fact, the only qualified people are on this project."

如果项目外部真的没有合格的审查者，我保证这个产品将是一个永无休止的维护问题，并且容易出现重大安全问题。

If there really are no qualified reviewers external to the project, I guarantee that this product will be a never-ending maintenance problem, and will be vulnerable to major security problems.

“这里真的没有什么新东西；都是可重用的代码。”

"There's really nothing new here; it's all reusable code."

精彩的！在那种情况下，如果我们记录了每个可重用部分及其接口的状态证据，那么审查将是简短而愉快的。

Wonderful! In that case, the review will be short and sweet—if we have documented evidence of the state of each reusable piece and its interfaces.

“如果你按照指示去做，就不会出错。”

"If you follow the instructions, nothing can possibly go wrong."

此警告通常意味着构建者不知道如果用户不遵循说明会发生什么。此外，相信这种对任何软件的幻想的人根本就不懂软件。

This warning usually means the builders don't know what will happen if a user doesn't follow instructions. Besides, anyone who believes this fantasy about any piece of software just doesn't understand software.

“我们 [tested] [tried] [demonstrate] 它，它工作正常。”

"We [tested] [tried] [demonstrated] it, and it works okay."

这里的问题是“okay”的定义，这是英语和许多其他语言中最模棱两可的摇篮曲词之一。一旦定义了“好的”，就可以确定工作产品是否完成了它应该做的事情。您想打赌答案是什么吗？

The issue here is the definition of "okay," one of the most ambiguous lullaby words in the English language—and many other languages, too. Once "okay" is defined, then it will be possible to determine whether the work product does what it's supposed to do. Would you like to bet what that answer will be?

“有用。”

"It works."

英语中另外两个最模棱两可的词是“it”和“works”。通常，根据我的经验，这个声明意味着：“我们没有非常努力地让产品失败，我们也没有运行它很长时间或在非常不同的条件下运行它。到目前为止，我们还没有看到任何失败，尽管我们在解释方面一直很慷慨，而且我们也没有仔细观察。”

Two more of the most ambiguous words in the English language are "it" and "works." Usually, in my experience, this pronouncement means: "We haven't tried very hard to make the product fail, and we haven't been running it very long or under very diverse conditions. So far we haven't seen any failures, though we've been generous in our interpretations, and we haven't been looking too closely, either."

“一点问题都没有！”

"There's no problem at all!"

精彩的！那样的话，审核就没有问题了。

Wonderful! In that case, there will be no problem reviewing it.

“我们从来没有遇到过困难。”

"We've never encountered a difficulty."

对你有好处。现在我们将看看非建筑商是否会如此幸运。你预测什么？

Good for you. Now we'll see if non-builders are going to be as lucky. What do you predict?

“我们不知道情况如此糟糕，必须进行审查。”

"We didn't know it was so bad it had to be reviewed."

不要将评论作为对您认为不好的工作的惩罚。审查产品应该是一个标准的、通用的过程。它不应该暗示任何关于产品质量的信息，而只是关于产品“好”的重要性——也就是说，做它应该做的事情。因此，被要求审查您的工作表明您的工作很重要。任何给出这个借口的人都不理解评论的作用。还是您的组织实际上使用评论作为惩罚？

Don't use reviews as punishment for work you might believe is bad. Reviewing a product should be a standard, universal process. It shouldn't imply anything about a product's quality, but rather only about the importance of the product being "good"—that is, doing what it's supposed to do. So, being asked to have your work reviewed signifies that your work is important. Anyone giving this excuse doesn't understand the role of reviews. Or is your organization actually using reviews as punishment?

“我们不知道我们需要审查它。”

"We didn't know we needed to review it."

那你不了解你的开发过程。解决这个问题的方法是教育和沟通。

Then you don't understand your development process. The fix for this is education and communication.

“我们还没有准备好，因为我们落后了，但我们希望运气好，赶上来。”

"We're not ready because we are behind, but we're hoping to get lucky and catch up."

向管理层提交的完整审查报告可以简洁明了：“他们希望运气好。” 希望您的管理层知道运气在软件开发中不是问题。

The complete review report to management can be succinct: "They're hoping to get lucky." Hopefully, your management knows that luck is not an issue in software development.

“我们认为我们做得不好，我们不希望管理层发现。”

"We think we're not doing a good job, and we don't want management to find out."

当然，您永远不会听到明确说明这一点，但这是许多即时评论所检测到的。有趣的是，评论通常表明这些工作成果并不像建设者担心的那么糟糕，尽管不如他们希望的那么好。

Of course, you'll never hear this stated explicitly, but it's what many instant reviews detect. Interestingly, reviews generally show that these work products are not as bad as the builders fear, though not as good as they hoped.

“我们不想与那些程序纳粹分子合作。”

"We don't want to cooperate with those process nazis."

这种情绪很少会被表达出来，但这可能是其他借口背后更深层次的原因：感觉被推来推去而不是受到尊重。有时，复习是班级政治的一种练习——好管闲事的班级想要展示自己的力量。如果人们有这种感觉，请执行快速元审查——审查您的审查系统。这涉及明确审查审查系统，寻找流程错误，例如使用审查作为惩罚，将技术审查纳入人员审查（而不是产品审查），或者可能领导不当的审查。

This sentiment is rarely going to be voiced, but it may be the deeper reason behind other excuses: feeling pushed around instead of respected. Sometimes a review is an exercise in class politics—and the busybody class wants to demonstrate its power. If people feel this way, perform a quick meta-review—a review of your review system. This involves reviewing the review system explicitly, looking for process bugs such as using reviews as punishment, co-opting technical reviews into personnel reviews (rather than reviews of a product), or perhaps badly led reviews.

最差优先审查确定错误的严重性。

Worst-first reviews establish bug severity.

进入审阅室后，可以使用一些相同的即时审阅。一般来说，最快的审查是在“最差优先”的基础上进行的。因此，您只需要求每个审阅者从他或她发现的最严重的问题开始，然后从那里开始解决相对较小的问题。例如，如果程序使用有缺陷的算法，则无需担心界面中的拼写错误。

Some of the same instant reviews can be used once you get inside the review room. In general, the quickest reviews are done by working on a "worst first" basis. So, you simply ask each reviewer to start with the worst problem he or she has found and work from there down to relatively minor problems. If, for example, a program is using a defective algorithm, there's no sense worrying about spelling errors in the interface.

复习是一种测试。从测试人员的角度来看，最严重的错误是那些阻碍测试的错误。测试经验告诉您，测试中最有问题的错误也将是审查中最糟糕的错误。当然，最糟糕的测试错误是任何阻止您测试被测对象的全部或部分的错误。同样的原则也适用于通过审查进行的测试。如果审阅者说，“我不能很好地理解这段代码以确保它有效”，这是一个阻塞问题，因此具有最高的重要性。

Reviewing is a type of testing. The worst bugs from a tester's perspective are those that block testing. Testing experience tells you that the most problematic bugs for testing also will be the worst for reviewing. Certainly, the worst bug for testing is any bug that blocks you from testing all or part of the object under test. The same principle applies to testing by means of a review. If a reviewer says, "I cannot understand this code well enough to be sure it works," this is a blocking issue, and thus has highest significance.

如果您在面对这些阻止语句的某些变化时不知道该怎么办，请将反对意见转化为测试条款。例如，“我们无法审查产品，因为客户不想付款”变成“我们无法测试产品，因为客户不想付款”。你会知道该怎么做，尽管你的客户可能不知道。在那种情况下，明确后果是某人的工作。

If you're puzzled by what to do when faced with some variation on these blocking statements, translate the objection into testing terms. For example, "We can't review the product because the customer doesn't want to pay for it" becomes "We can't test the product because the customer doesn't want to pay for it." You'll know what to do, though your customer might not. In that case, it's someone's job to make the consequences clear.

真相并不总是令人信服。

The truth is not always convincing.

即时评论提供了大量重要的早期信息，以换取少量的时间投入。但请注意：即时评论可能会说服您，但您可能仍需努力说服他人。可以理解的是，他们不会相信别人可以通过如此简单的方式就他们付出如此多努力的事情学到这么多东西。

Instant reviews provide an enormous amount of important and early information in exchange for a tiny investment of time. But be warned: Instant reviews may convince you, but you still may have to work to convince others. Understandably, they won't believe someone else can learn so much in such a simple way about something into which they've put so much effort.

有时，您将不得不经历全面审查的痛苦，以便构建者可以看到审查结果是如何产生的。有时，您必须开始测试并让早期测试结果揭示本应在审查中发现的问题。有时，您只需要将即时审核结果提交给管理层，让其决定是否浪费时间召开正式审核。渐渐地，您的组织将学会自己执行即时审查，然后您将在整个开发过程中发现新的乐趣。

Sometimes, you'll have to go through the pain of a full review so builders can see how a review result occurred. Sometimes, you'll have to start testing and let early test results reveal problems that should have been detected in reviewing. Sometimes, you'll just have to bring the instant-review results to management and let it decide whether to waste time convening a formal review. Gradually, your organization will learn to perform instant reviews itself, and then you'll find new sweetness in your entire development process.

测试人员成为有价值的审阅者。

Testers make valuable reviewers.

经理们经常告诉我，测试人员没有必要参与技术评审，他们这样解释他们的观点：“因为测试人员不写代码，所以他们找不到错误。” 我的回答是，“这根本不是真的。你不必了解任何编程语言就可以找到逻辑错误、主要设计缺陷、糟糕的人机界面、规范歧义和许多其他困难。”

Managers frequently tell me that there's no need for testers to participate in technical reviews, explaining their viewpoint thusly: "Because testers don't write code, they can't find bugs." My response is, "That's simply not true. You don't have to know any programming language to find logic bugs, major design flaws, poor human-machine interfaces, specification ambiguities, and many other difficulties."

即使测试人员确实不会在审查过程中发现错误（事实并非如此），他们仍然能够从经验中学习。评论必须提供的最大的单一好处是通过以下任何或所有方式学习：

Even if it were true that testers will not find bugs in the course of a review (and it isn't), they would still be able to learn from the experience. The greatest single benefit that reviews have to offer is learning, in any or all of the following ways:

1. 通过观察开发人员可能产生的有缺陷的思维模式，测试人员学会编写更好的测试。

1. By observing the patterns of flawed thinking that developers are likely to produce, testers learn to compose better tests.

2. 通过尽早审查规范，测试人员可以在他们的测试计划范围内抢先一步。

2. By reviewing specs early, testers get a head start on the scope of their test plans.

3. 通过熟悉设计，测试人员可以加快检测错误并帮助查明错误的过程。

3. By gaining familiarity with designs, testers accelerate the process of detecting bugs and then helping to pinpoint them.

4. 通过参与评审，测试人员学习如何更好地评审他们自己的测试用例、测试计划、测试驱动程序和工具。而且，作为一个额外的好处，他们可以比那些只是坐着等待开发人员给他们测试的测试人员更快地加快项目的速度。

4. By participating in reviews, testers learn how to be better reviewers of their own test cases, test plans, test drivers, and tools. And, as an added bonus, they can get up to speed on a project much faster than those testers who simply sit and wait for the developers to give them something to test.

概括

Summary

不用电脑的测试方法有很多种，但是不用动脑子的测试方法就没有了。尽早并经常测试；尽你所能。

There are many ways of testing without involving computers, but no way of testing that doesn't involve using brains. Test early and often; use all the brains you can muster.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.没有认识到技术审查作为测试补充形式的价值：如果没有包括定期技术审查在内的流程，无论其机器测试过程多么出色，任何项目都无法超越平庸。

1. Not recognizing the value of technical reviews as a complementary form of testing: Without a process that includes regular technical reviews, no project will rise above mediocrity, no matter how good its machine-testing process.

2.为跳过技术审查（或你的过程的任何部分）的众多论点之一而堕落：在任何系统中，大约十分之九的麻烦、容易出错的组件绕过或捷径了一个或更多的工艺步骤。

2. Falling for one of the many arguments for skipping technical reviews (or any part of your process, for that matter): Roughly nine out of ten of the troublesome, error-prone components in any system have bypassed or short-cut one or more process steps.

3.使用技术审查作为惩罚：营造一种氛围，使每次审查对所有参与者来说都是一次有益的经历。

3. Using technical reviews as punishment: Cultivate a climate where each review is actually a rewarding experience for all participants.

4.跳过评审以节省时间：错误是损失项目时间的第一大原因。跳过审查总是会使项目花费更长的时间。

4. Skipping reviews to save time: Errors are the number one cause of lost project time. Skipping reviews always makes the project take longer.

5.未能审查设计和代码的可测试性：如果您的系统在设计时考虑到可测试性，那么在任何人运行测试之前至少可以削减一半的测试成本。

5. Failing to review designs and code for testability: At least half of your testing costs can be cut before anybody ever runs a test, if only your systems are designed with testability in mind.

6.未能将测试人员包括为评审人员：测试人员为评审的有效性贡献了他们独特的观点。测试人员还需要每个评审提供的教育。

6. Failing to include testers as reviewers: Testers contribute their unique point of view to the effectiveness of a review. Testers also need the education each review provides.

7.未能认识到学习的价值：归根结底，学习是评论中最有价值的部分。也许你没有考虑学习，因为它不容易量化。但它可以，如果你真的想要它。[16]

7. Failing to recognize the value of learning: Ultimately, learning is the most valuable part of reviews. Perhaps you do not factor in learning because it can't be easily quantified. But it can be, if you really want it to be. [16]

第 17 章_测试诈骗

Chapter_17_Testing Scams

 

“在软弱的时刻，很难抗拒幼稚的暗示……” - Bertrand Russell，数学家和哲学家（1872-1970），征服幸福（纽约：Liveright Publishing Corporation，1996）。

"In moments of weakness it is difficult to resist infantile suggestions. . . ." - Bertrand Russell, Mathematician and Philosopher (1872–1970),The Conquest of Happiness (New York: Liveright Publishing Corporation, 1996).

陷入相信测试谬误的陷阱是一回事。成为测试骗局的牺牲品是另一回事。在这两种情况下，我们相信某事是因为我们非常希望它是真的。但在测试骗局时，我们让自己被那些通过欺骗我们而受益的人所欺骗。以下是一些警告信号，表明您有可能成为测试骗局的牺牲品。

It's one thing to fall into the trap of believing testing fallacies. It's another thing to fall prey to testing scams. In both cases, we believe something because we so very badly want it to be true. But in testing scams, we allow ourselves to be gulled by those who will benefit by tricking us. Here are some warning signs that you're in danger of falling prey to a testing scam.

我们会卖给你一个魔法工具。

We'll sell you a magic tool.

当我住在科罗拉多州的 Crested Butte 时，我有时会徒步穿越群山前往阿斯彭。我知道有 5 条远足小径，它们都是以前的收费公路，是旧时淘金时代遗留下来的，当时到达阿斯彭的唯一途径是通过 Crested Butte。

When I lived in Crested Butte, Colorado, I sometimes hiked across the mountains to Aspen. There were five hiking trails that I knew of, all of them former toll roads left over from the old gold-mining days when the only way to reach Aspen was through Crested Butte.

当我努力向上攀登 13,000 英尺和更高的山口时，我常常想知道为什么会有这么多收费公路。当我徒步走完这 5 条路时，我知道了答案：有多条收费公路，因为没有一条是非常好的。每个道路的建设者一定都希望通过建设收费公路的硬道理来发财，但事实并非如此。最终，有人认为从另一个方向更容易到达阿斯彭，于是放弃了收费公路建设业务。

As I struggled to breathe going up 13,000-foot and higher passes, I often wondered why there were so many toll roads. By the time I'd hiked all five, I knew the answer: There were multiple toll roads because not one of them was very good. Each road's builder must have hoped to make a fortune by constructing the last word in toll roads, but it was not to be. Eventually, someone decided it was easier to get to Aspen from another direction, and the toll-road-building business was abandoned.

走在那些废弃的五号公路上，在隘口停下来喘口气时，我想我是否能对浩如烟海的软件测试工具有一个解释。并不是说它们都不好，而是它们都没有完全符合供应商大肆宣传出售它们的神奇承诺。

When hiking on the fifth of those abandoned roads, stopping at the pass to catch my breath, I wondered if I might have an explanation for the vast number of software testing tools. Not that none of them are any good, but that none of them quite meets the magical promises vendors hype to sell them.

回到 Crested Butte 并渴望检验我的理论，我查阅了十几种最畅销测试工具的规格和评论。工具 A 声称可以节省 80% 的测试成本；工具 B 声称节省了 75%。这是否意味着如果我同时使用 A 和 B，我将节省 95% 的测试成本？哎呀，然后我可以添加工具 C，它承诺可以节省 50%，这样我就可以降低到原来成本的 2.5%。

Back in Crested Butte and eager to test my theory, I looked up specs for and reviews of a dozen or so of the best-selling testing tools. Tool A claimed to save 80 percent of testing costs; Tool B claimed a savings of 75 percent. Could that mean that if I used A and B together I would save 95 percent of my testing costs? Gee, then I could add Tool C, which promised to save 50 percent, and I'd be down to 2.5 percent of my original costs.

得出的结论不公平？我认为这是完全公平的，因为 A、B 和 C 的促销声明都吹捧了一种“独特的测试方法”。如果是这样的话，他们的结果应该是独立的——那么我的计算就是正确的，也就不需要像这本书这样的软件测试书籍了。也不太需要测试人员，也不需要在计划中分配时间进行测试。项目经理的梦想。

Not a fair conclusion to draw? I thought it was perfectly fair because the promotional claims for A, B, and C each touted a "unique approach" to testing. If that were so, their results should be independent—so my calculation would be correct, and there would be no need for books on software testing such as this one. Not much need for testers, either, or to allocate time for testing in the schedule. A project manager's dream.

这是关于工具的秘密：好的工具会放大效果。======如果你的测试效果是负面的，添加工具只会放大负面效果。工具供应商或制造商提出的任何其他声明很可能是某种骗局。接下来的部分讲述了更多关于诈骗和诈骗的故事。

Here's the secret about tools: Good tools amplify effectiveness.======If your testing effectiveness is negative, adding tools will only amplify the negativity. Any other claim a tool vendor or manufacturer makes is, most likely, some kind of a scam. The sections that follow tell more of the story of scams and scamming.

我们的示威是骗局。

Our demonstration is a scam.

DataSpew 的推销员 Axel Bass 拉了拉他双排扣西装的夹克，抚平皱纹，然后大步走进 Laverne Weaver 的办公室，伸出手。她坚定的握手和直接的眼神交流让他相信她是在做生意。他知道他的软件工具无法与竞争对手的性能相提并论，因此他已经准备好了令人信服的论据。

Axel Bass, the DataSpew salesman, tugs on the jacket of his double-breasted suit, smoothing out the wrinkles, before striding into Laverne Weaver's office, hand outstretched. Her firm handshake and direct eye contact convince him that she's all business. He knows his software tool can't match the performance of his competitors', so he's come prepared with a convincing argument.

Laverne 示意他坐下，然后坐在高背皮革转椅上，正对着她气势恢宏的柚木玻璃办公桌。“嗯，巴斯先生。我知道你想卖给我一位 DataSpew 报告撰稿人。”

Laverne motions to him to take a seat, then settles herself into the high-backed, leather, swivel-chair centered perfectly behind her imposing teak-and-glass desk. "Well, Mr. Bass. I understand there's a DataSpew report writer you want to sell me."

“请叫我阿克塞尔。” Laverne 点点头，但什么也没说，所以 Axel 继续说道。“是的，我们认为您会发现我们的报告编写器是市场上最好的。事实上，我们非常确定您会发现它的性能超过我们最接近的竞争对手，我们愿意为您提供一周的免费试用期试用两台机器——我们将在一周内派一名性能工程师帮助您设置基准测试，将两台机器并排比较，这样您就可以亲眼看到了。” 阿克塞尔露出他最能赢得自信的微笑，然后坐回椅子上等待她的回应。

"Please, call me Axel." Laverne nods but says nothing, so Axel continues. "Yes, we think you'll find our report writer is the best on the market. In fact, we're so sure you'll find its performance outstrips our closest competitor, we're willing to give you a week-long free trial of both machines—and we'll throw in a performance engineer for the week to help you set up benchmark tests to compare the two machines side by side so you can see for yourself." Axel beams his best confidence-winning smile and sits back in his chair to wait for her response.

拉文在她桌上的便笺簿上记下了一些笔记，然后才回复。“好吧，我愿意接受你的提议。” 他们讨论了更多细节，并通过设定两台机器的交付日期和 DataSpew 的性能工程师 Phyllis 到现场的日期来结束会议。

Laverne jots a few notes on a pad on her desk before replying. "Alright. I'm willing to take you up on your offer." They discuss a few more details, and close their meeting by setting dates for delivery of the two machines and for Phyllis, DataSpew's performance engineer, to come on site.

Phyllis 在星期一的指定时间到达并设置了两台机器，并在工作时解释说她将针对示例错误数据库中的数据编写十份测试报告。截至周四，Phyllis 已经开发并执行了十个测试用例。奇迹中的奇迹，DataSpew 报告编写器在所有十个案例中都明显快于其竞争对手的机器。

Phyllis arrives at the appointed time on Monday and sets up both machines, explaining as she works that she will write ten test reports against data in a sample bug database. By Thursday, Phyllis has developed and executed ten test cases. Miracle of miracles, the DataSpew report writer is significantly faster than its competitor's machine in all ten cases.

Laverne 会落入这个骗局吗？

Will Laverne fall for this scam?

Laverne 可能认为她见过将一位报告作者的表现与另一位报告作者的表现进行比较的测试，但 Phyllis 并不是在测试——她只是在展示。有意无意地，结果被操纵了。如果 Laverne 以这种所谓的测试为基础购买 DataSpew，她将成为 The Demonstration Scam 亚种的受害者。此版本是性能基准骗局。

Laverne may think she has seen tests comparing the performance of one report writer against another, but Phyllis was not testing—she was demonstrating. Consciously or unconsciously, the outcome is rigged. If Laverne buys DataSpew on the basis of this so-called test, she will have fallen victim to a subspecies of The Demonstration Scam. This rendition is The Performance Benchmark Scam.

正如我们在前面的章节中看到的，演示不是测试。它们可能会教育客户，但它们不是测试，因为它们专门设计用于证明一个观点，最重要的是，避免意外。

As we've seen in previous chapters, demonstrations are not tests. They might educate a customer, but they are not tests because they are designed specifically to prove a point and, above all, to avoid surprises.

我从个人经验中知道这一点，因为几年前，我的部分工作是将性能基准测试设计为一种销售策略。对于任何两个系统——我雇主的产品和品牌 X——我总是可以创建一个性能“测试”来“证明”我的系统是优越的。而且，如果我受雇于 Brand X，我就可以“证明”它的系统优于所有其他系统。

I know this from personal experience because, years ago, part of my job was to design performance benchmark tests as a sales tactic. For any two systems—my employer's product and Brand X—I could always create a performance "test" that would "prove" that my system was superior. And, if I'd been in the employ of Brand X, I could have "proved" that its system was superior to all others.

Phyllis 的十份报告旨在展示 DataSpew 报告作者的实力。当然，如果 Phyllis 不能创建十份报告来证明她公司产品的优越性，那将是有趣的新信息。从消极的方面来说，失败的骗局尝试是一种考验。

Phyllis's ten reports were designed to showcase the strengths of the DataSpew report writer. Of course, if Phyllis hadn't been able to create ten reports that demonstrated the superiority of her company's product, that would be interesting new information. In a negative way, an attempted scam that fails is a test.

有了所有这些推荐，它一定很好。

With all these testimonials, it must be good.

通常，供应商甚至不需要使用演示来欺骗您。销售宣传资料经常包含伪测试结果（例如，产品比较、认证或认可），这些结果看似包含信息，但实际上仅识别出为使用其名称而收取费用或某种实物付款的江湖骗子。在意大利买一瓶水，你会发现各种各样的“医生”都对产品表示赞同，他们声称如果你喝了里面的东西，就会有各种美妙的效果。在 . 中购买压缩包装软件。. . 哦，你知道我的意思。

Often, a vendor doesn't even need to use a demonstration to scam you. Sales literature frequently contains pseudo-test results (for example, product comparisons, certifications, or endorsements) that appear to contain information, but which really only identify charlatans who took a fee or some payment in kind for the use of their names. Buy a bottle of water in Italy and you'll find endorsements of the product from all sorts of "doctors" who claim all sorts of wonderful results if you drink the contents. Buy shrink-wrapped software in . . . oh, you know what I mean.

如果您想要可靠的工具或软件推荐，请亲自获取。如果可能，拜访参考客户，观察他们在正常过程中如何使用产品，并与实际使用它的人交谈。如果供应商不希望您这样做，请保持怀疑。我知道自动化供应商会禁止任何有实践经验的人进行推销演示。这些供应商只想向大钱包销售产品，并且会竭尽所能阻止实际使用该工具的人传播他们的经验——无论产品是否及格或受到抨击。

If you want reliable tool or software testimonials, get them in person. If possible, visit referenced customers, watch how the product is used in their normal process, and talk to people who actually do use it. If a vendor doesn't want you to do this, be suspicious. I've known automation vendors to bar from sales-pitch presentations anyone and everyone with hands-on experience. Such vendors want to sell only to the big wallets, and will do anything they can to prevent people who are actually using the tool from airing their experiences—whether or not the product gets a passing grade or is slammed.

我们可以用我们的定价来骗你。

We can scam you with our pricing.

通过只卖给大钱包，以高价，供应商也获得了认知失调的影响，防止客户抱怨表现不佳。The High Price Scam 的受害者可能会一直抱怨自己的产品，因为他们担心自己会因为在一个无用的工具上花了这么多钱而显得愚蠢。此外，尽管工具没有完成工作但仍被迫使用该工具的测试人员保持沉默，以保护他们老板决策的智慧。

By selling only to the big wallets, for a big price, vendors also enlist the effect of cognitive dissonance that prevents customers from complaining about poor performance. Victims of The High Price Scam may keep complaints about the product to themselves because they fear they would look stupid for having spent so much money on a useless tool. Moreover, testers who are forced to use the tool despite its not doing the job keep quiet to protect the wisdom of their boss's decision.

与高价骗局相关的是低价骗局：以虚伪的方式诋毁竞争性工具，暗示“价格这么低，这些工具怎么可能好用？” 我听到一位供应商声称开源（免费）工具很危险，因为它们“没有支持”。这简直就是一个谎言——聘请开源工具的作者提供支持是微不足道的。此外，当我深入了解该供应商自己的技术支持时，我发现它完全不够——尽管价格过高。

Related to The High Price Scam is The Low Price Scam: discrediting competitive tools with disingenuousness, suggesting, "With a price so low, how could those tools be any good?" I heard one vendor claim that open-source (free) tools are dangerous because they have "no support." This is simply a lie—it's trivial to hire the authors of open-source tools to provide support. Moreover, when I looked deeper into this vendor's own tech support, I found it to be entirely inadequate—though overpriced.

试图诋毁实际用户的任何负面评价的供应商会延续另一个骗局。一位销售员告诉我，“技术人员天生挑剔，就像猫一样。你真的不能相信他们所说的十分之九。” 也许这是真的，但至少一只猫有 10% 的时间说真话，这与某些推销员不同。

Vendors who attempt to discredit any negative testimonial from actual users perpetuate another scam. One salesman told me, "Technical people are naturally finicky, like cats. You really can't believe nine-tenths of what they say." Perhaps that's true, but at least a cat tells the truth 10 percent of the time, unlike certain salesmen.

我们的工具可以读心术。

Our tool can read minds.

我正在与一位项目经理讨论工具骗局，当时他提出向我展示他刚刚以比我的咨询费高得多的价格购买的自动化测试工具（因此，这一定是一个好工具）。我们走进了该客户的测试实验室，他的一名测试员 Sherry 正在那里使用该工具。“告诉杰里你在做什么，”经理问道。

I was talking with a project manager about tool scams when he offered to show me an automated test tool he had just purchased for a sum much greater than my consulting fee (and which, therefore, must have been a good tool). We walked into this client's test lab where Sherry, one of his testers, was using the tool. "Tell Jerry what you're doing," the manager asked.

“你敢打赌，”她说，兴奋得几乎从椅子上跳起来。“我刚刚编写了一个自动化测试来证明搜索软件是有效的！”

"You bet," she said, so excited she nearly jumped out of her chair. "I just wrote an automated test that proves the search software works!"

“给我看看，”我说。

"Show me," I said.

雪莉开始了测试。它打开搜索表单，输入查询条件，然后单击“搜索”按钮。脚本完成后，会弹出一个窗口，提示测试已通过。“嗯，”我说。“它怎么知道测试通过了？” “它就是知道。这个工具足够聪明，可以知道。” 雪莉高兴地注视着绿色的隘口。

Sherry launched the test. It opened the search form, entered query criteria, and clicked the Search button. When the script completed, a window popped up saying that the test had passed. "Hmm," I said. "How does it know the test passed?" "It just knows. The tool is smart enough to know." Sherry gazed happily at the green Pass.

“我可以试试吗？” 我问。

"May I try something?" I asked.

“当然可以，”雪莉和经理异口同声地说。

"Sure," said Sherry and the manager in unison.

“好吧，你能借我一个开发人员几分钟吗？最好是写这个搜索功能的那个。”

"Okay, can you lend me a developer for a few minutes? Preferably the one who wrote this search function."

我们走出隔间，找到了开发商梅兰妮。我和她挤在一起，请她为我编写一个与她的搜索程序具有相同界面的小程序，但一个从不实际搜索并且总是返回零的小程序，无论搜索条件如何。

We went out among the cubicles and found Melanie, the developer. I huddled with her and asked her to write me a little program with the same interface as her search program, but one that never actually searches and always returns a zero, regardless of the search criteria.

当我分散 Sherry 的注意力时，Melanie 插入了虚拟搜索例程来代替原来的例程。雪莉对这个工具的神奇描述着迷不已，甚至没有注意到梅兰妮做了什么。“你能再做一次那个测试吗？” 我问。

While I distracted Sherry, Melanie inserted the dummy search routine in place of the original. Sherry was so enraptured describing the tool's wonders, she didn't even notice what Melanie had done. "Could you run that test again?" I asked.

“当然！” 雪莉再次运行测试。这一次，系统显示了一条错误消息，NO RECORDS FOUND，但该工具仍然弹出一个窗口，声明测试已通过。

"Sure!" Sherry ran the test again. This time, the system displayed an error message, NO RECORDS FOUND, but the tool still produced a window declaring that the test had passed.

“嘿！” 雪莉惊呼道，愤怒地转向我。“你做了什么？你把我的考试搞砸了！” Sherry 没有看到 Melanie 和我刚刚证明，尽管屏幕上出现令人愉快的绿色 Pass，但测试工具并不“只知道”测试应该通过还是失败。

"Hey!" Sherry exclaimed, turning to me in anger. "What did you do? You messed up my test!" Sherry failed to see that Melanie and I had just proved that despite the cheerful green Pass on the screen, the test tool didn't "just know" whether the test should have passed or failed.

这里真正的问题是该工具不知道系统的响应应该是什么。Sherry 相信该工具会奇迹般地知道软件是否正常运行。她非常确定这个工具最了解她，所以她并不担心关于一个根本不进行任何搜索的程序测试的通过报告。她假设该工具确切地知道应该找到哪些记录。

The real problem here is that the tool doesn't know what the system's response is supposed to be. Sherry believed the tool would miraculously know whether or not the software was behaving correctly. She was so certain the tool knew best that she wasn't concerned by the Pass report on a test of a program that didn't do any searching at all. She assumed the tool knew exactly what records should be found.

这是无所不知的工具骗局。该工具以如此权威的方式运行，以至于用户认为它实际上正在以与人类操作员相同的详细程度进行测试。一些工具供应商鼓励这种心态。毕竟，他们的生意是卖工具。他们出售他们的工具的前提是该工具将以最少的人工参与来测试软件。但要注意：工具只是工具。他们仍然需要人类，有思想的人类，来有意义地操作它们。

This is The Omniscient Tool Scam. The tool operates with such authority that the user assumes that it is actually testing at the same level of detail as a human operator. Some tool vendors encourage this mentality. After all, their business is selling tools. They sell their tools on the premise that the tool will test the software with minimal human involvement. But beware: Tools are just tools. They still need humans, thinking humans, to operate them meaningfully.

在我职业生涯的早期，我有幸了解到人们可以用无所不知的工具骗局来自欺欺人。我被要求审查增加 2500 万美元的预算（是当前预算的两倍）。要构建的产品不仅仅是一个自动测试仪；它是一个“自动调试器”。其概念是，您将程序 X 放入这个出色的工具中，然后生成的程序 X 消除了所有错误。显然，它会读懂你的想法，了解你想要什么。

Early in my career, I had the good fortune to learn just how far people could go in fooling themselves with The Omniscient Tool Scam. I was asked to review a budget increase of 25 million dollars (doubling the current budget). The product to be built was not just an automatic tester; it was an "automatic debugger." The concept was that you put program X into this wonderful tool and out came program X with all the bugs removed. Apparently, it read your mind about what you wanted.

信不信由你，这家大型计算机公司的高管们相信了这一论点并将预算增加了一倍。所以我了解到人们可以相信任何事情，只要听起来足够好。买家当心（您自己的意愿）。

Believe it or not, the executives of this large computer company bought the argument and doubled the budget. So I learned that people can believe anything, if it sounds good enough. Buyer beware (of your own wishes).

我们保证您无需做任何事情。

We promise that you don't have to do a thing.

您是否曾经从测试服务中获得过如下报价？“我们会处理你所有的测试。我们甚至会编写测试脚本。你只需给我们你想要测试的软件，其他一切都交给我们。我们可以进行单元测试、正面测试、负面测试、边界测试、功能测试测试、性能测试、负载测试、压力测试、验收测试，甚至高杠杆用例协同数据测试。”

Have you ever had an offer like the following from a testing service? "We'll handle all your testing. We'll even write the test scripts. You just give us the software you want tested and leave everything else to us. We can do unit testing, positive testing, negative testing, boundary testing, functional testing, performance testing, load testing, stress testing, acceptance testing, and even high-leverage use-case synergistic data testing."

这有多诱人？交出你的软件，你所有的测试难题都会随之而来。您再也不用担心那些烦人的测试问题了。

How tempting is this? Hand over your software, and all your testing headaches go with it. You'll never have to worry about that pesky testing stuff again.

事实上，测试服务中的人员可能有能力做好工作。然而，就像内部测试人员一样，他们需要知道他们应该收集哪些信息。需要有人仔细考虑测试服务提供的价值，可以合理预期它会发现的信息，然后管理合同以确保测试服务确实提供了项目管理团队最需要的信息。

The people in the testing service may, in fact, be capable of doing a good job. However, just like internal testers, they need to know what information they're supposed to be gathering. Someone needs to think through the value the testing service offers, the information it can reasonably be expected to uncover, and then manage the contract to make sure the testing service is indeed providing the kind of information the project management team most needs.

一个相关的骗局是 Outsourcing Bait-and-Switch Scam，在这种骗局中，供应商使用高级测试人员来吸引客户，但一旦签订合同，就会用廉价、缺乏经验的初级测试人员取代这些高级测试人员——通常以高级测试人员的价格.

A related scam is The Outsourcing Bait-and-Switch Scam in which the vendor uses senior testers to attract a client but, once the contract is signed, replaces those senior testers with cheap, inexperienced, junior testers—often at the senior-tester price.

如果它好得令人难以置信，它可能不是。“你不必做任何事”的承诺始终是一个骗局。

If it's too good to be true, it probably isn't. The "You Don't Have to Do a Thing" Promise is always a scam.

我们暗中勾结。

We are secretly in cahoots.

一些经理梦想从远处控制软件开发，仅使用数字而不是个人观察来至少验证这些数字。当管理人员采取这种立场时，他们就会让自己陷入共谋骗局，在这种骗局中，两方聚在一起玩弄这个系统。

Some managers dream of controlling software development from a distance, merely using numbers instead of personal observation to, at the least, verify those numbers. When managers adopt this stance, they open themselves to collusion scams in which two parties get together to game the system.

例如，Bugfests 很容易玩。它是这样工作的：开发人员和测试人员秘密合作。开发人员在 bugfest 之前插入错误。然后合作伙伴“发现”这些错误并为每个错误获得赏金，之后合作伙伴平分战利品。我知道有一个例子，测试人员在检测到骗局之前用赏金购买了一艘新的摩托艇，但很可能从未报告过大多数 bugfest 骗局。

Bugfests, for example, are easy to game. Here's how it works: A developer and a tester secretly team up. The developer inserts bugs just before the bugfest. The partner then "finds" these bugs and receives a bounty for each, after which the partners split the loot. I know of one instance where the tester bought a new powerboat with the bounty money before the scam was detected, but it's quite likely that most bugfest scams are never reported.

另一个很好的共谋骗局是测试人员秘密向开发人员报告错误。然后开发人员查明、定位并修复错误，然后告诉测试人员提交报告——然后在一小时后清除。开发人员因最快的错误清除者而受到赞誉。测试人员可能不会直接得到奖励，但开发人员通常会想办法。第一次见这种串通骗局，开发人员和测试人员是夫妻。

Another fine collusion scam has a tester reporting bugs secretly to a developer. The developer then pinpoints, locates, and fixes the bugs, then tells the tester to submit a report—which is then cleared an hour later. The developer gets credit for being the fastest bug-clearer. The tester may not be rewarded directly, but the developer usually finds a way. The first time I saw this collusion scam, the developer and tester were husband and wife.

以下是如何避免诈骗。

Here's how to avoid scams.

识别骗局的一种方法是他们总是不劳而获。Performance Benchmark Scam 承诺供应商将免费提供大量测试工作。“你不必做任何事”的承诺表明这只是钱的问题，这是无所事事的一种形式。Omniscient Tool Scam 假定工具可以在不知道您最初的意图的情况下运行。

One way to recognize scams is that they always promise something for nothing. The Performance Benchmark Scam promises that a vendor will provide lots of testing work for free. The "You Don't Have to Do a Thing" Promise suggests that it's only a matter of money, which is one version of nothing. The Omniscient Tool Scam presumes that a tool can operate without knowing anything about what you intended in the first place.

同样的经验法则适用于测试骗局和骗子和电话律师：如果听起来好得令人难以置信，那它可能不是真的。人们可能很容易相信有偏见或毫无意义的测试结果。吞下伪造的结果可能比挑战它们的创造者更可取。但是测试骗局会导致基于无效信息的决策过程。尽管拒绝接受看起来很划算的交易可能很困难，但清理接受交易的后果就更难了。你从“无”中得到的唯一“东西”就是遗憾。

The same rule of thumb applies to testing scams as to con artists and telephone solicitors: If it sounds too good to be true, it's probably not true. It may be tempting to believe the results from biased or meaningless tests. It may be preferable to swallow faked results than challenge their creator. But testing scams result in a decision process based on invalid information. And as hard as it may be to turn your back on something that looks like a good deal, it's even harder to clean up the aftermath of accepting the deal. The only "something" you'll get for your "nothing" is regrets.

概括

Summary

每当您迫切希望清除错误并发布产品时，您很容易受到各种承诺快速、无痛缓解的测试骗局的攻击。

Whenever you're desperate to clean up the bugs and ship a product, you're vulnerable to a variety of testing scams that promise quick, painless relief.

常见错误

Common Mistakes

1.完全依靠数字来管理项目：数字可能是有用的，但前提是它们通过个人观察得到验证，并通过关于它们的故事来设置。

1. Relying solely on numbers to manage a project: Numbers can be useful, but only if they're validated by personal observation and set in context by a story about them.

2.通过第三方接受推荐信：不要指望任何你无法通过直接与提供它的人交谈来验证的推荐信。

2. Accepting testimonials through a third party: Don't count on any testimonial you can't validate by talking directly to the person giving it.

Chapter_18_Oblivious 骗局

Chapter_18_Oblivious Scams

 

“乐观者看到的是玫瑰，而不是它的刺；悲观者盯着荆棘，却忘记了玫瑰。” - Kahlil Gibran，作家、诗人和艺术家（1883-1931），The Kahlil Gibran Reader：Inspirational Writings （纽约：Citadel，2006 年），p. 45.

"The optimist sees the rose and not its thorns; the pessimist stares at the thorns, oblivious to the rose." - Kahlil Gibran, Writer, Poet, and Artist (1883–1931), The Kahlil Gibran Reader: Inspirational Writings (New York: Citadel, 2006), p. 45.

有很多骗子和秃鹰随时准备利用您对测试困难的绝望，这已经够糟糕的了，但最常见的骗局是无意的、不经意的、自作自受的骗局。当我们不自觉地忽略一些棘手的信息时，它们通常源于乐观，这些信息的痛苦会迫使我们意识到情况到底有多糟糕。

It's bad enough that there are lots of scammers and vultures ready to take advantage of your desperation over testing difficulties, but the most frequent scams are unintentional, oblivious, self- perpetrated scams. They usually arise from optimism when we unconsciously ignore thorny bits of information, the pain of which would force us to realize how bad a situation really is.

当我们延迟文档时会发生什么？

What happens when we delay documentation?

此类诈骗最常见的情况可能发生在测试人员等到周末才记录他们所做测试的详细信息时——错误和测试数据。测试人员可能需要等待几天才能对测试进行解释，但没有人能准确记住整整一周的按键敲击的详细数据。（这就是为什么我在半个世纪前推荐使用跟踪日志和工具，并且现在我们拥有更好的技术仍然推荐它们。）

Perhaps the most common case of such scamming occurs when testers wait until the end of the week to record the details of the testing they've done—the bugs and test data. A tester may need to wait a few days for interpretations of testing to gel, but nobody can remember exactly the detailed data of a full week of key banging. (That's why I recommended using tracing logs and tools half a century ago, and still recommend them now that we have even better technology available.)

模棱两可的测试报告就像流沙。

Ambiguous test reports are like quicksand.

语言表达丰富，这意味着它可能很昂贵。一方面，同一句话对许多不同的人来说可能有许多不同的含义，而且对测试报告的不同解释可能代价高昂。当我帮助客户评估通过其测试发现的错误的重要性时，我个人就知道了一个例子。一个特别的功能是错误的，我觉得它应该从产品中删除并重新构建。项目经理迫于压力发布该功能并问我，“它到底有多糟糕？”

Language is rich with expression, which means that it can be expensive. For one thing, the same sentence can carry many different meanings to many different people, and different interpretations of test reports can be costly. One example to which I personally was privy came when I was helping a client assess the significance of the bugs uncovered by its testing. One particular feature was so buggy that I felt it should be removed from the product and rebuilt. The project manager was under the gun to ship the feature and asked me, "How bad is it really?"

“你的客户接受现状的可能性不超过一百分之一，”我说，并尽可能强调这句话，让我和其他任何人都无法知道未来。

"There's no more than one chance in a hundred that your customers will accept this as it is," I said, putting it as strongly as I could, allowing that neither I nor anyone else can know the future.

我离开了，当我下个月回来时，我发现经理已经决定发布产品——只是为了招致客户的愤怒，因为这个功能使他们的数据库变得混乱。“你为什么要发货？” 我问。

I went away, and when I returned the next month, I found that the manager had decided to ship the product—only to incur the wrath of his customers when this feature bollixed up their databases. "Why did you ship it?" I asked.

“嗯，”他说，“你告诉我顾客有可能接受它。”

"Well," he said, "you told me there was a chance the customers would accept it."

“我说了，只有百分之一的机会。” “对。所以我抓住了这个机会。”

"I said there was no more than one chance in a hundred." "Right. So I took that chance."

当你的工作岌岌可危并且你有机会误解一个模棱两可的陈述时，猜猜你会用哪种方式来解释它。

When your job is on the line and you're given a chance to misinterpret an ambiguous statement, guess which way you'll interpret it.

伪造的测试报告阻碍改进。

Falsified test reports impede improvement.

出于人道原因，检测报告经常被骗。James Bach 在Lessons Learned in Software Testing中讲述了一个故事，测试人员通过不报告错误来帮助开发人员。[17]

Test reports are often scammed for humane reasons. James Bach tells a story in Lessons Learned in Software Testing of testers helping out the developers by not reporting bugs. [17]

如果测试人员觉得他们不需要在发现错误时报告错误，那么，这本身就是有关项目的信息。他们是否觉得有必要保护开发人员免受指责管理？如果是这样，我保证你会发现这个组织中有各种各样的骗局，旨在误导管理层——完全破坏有效的项目规划。

If testers feel they don't need to report the bugs as they find them, well, that in and of itself is information about the project. Do they feel the need to protect the developers from a blaming management? If so, I guarantee you'll find all sorts of scams in this organization calculated to mislead management—to the total disruption of effective project planning.

或者，也许这些测试人员只是想减少保存记录的开销负担。在那种情况下，记录保存有问题，但该骗局使管理层无法了解需要修复的内容。

Or perhaps these testers were simply trying to reduce the overhead burden of keeping records. In that case, there's something wrong with the record keeping, but the scam prevents management from knowing what needs fixing.

这个借口之所以奏效，是因为有时理由是真正的人道。詹姆斯与我分享了他在那种情况下学到的东西：“我是那个项目的管理人员。如果我认为它可以解决一个重要问题，我可以自由地改变流程。

The reason this excuse works is that sometimes the reasons are truly humane. James shared with me what he learned in that situation: "I was part of management for that project. I was free to change the process if I thought it would solve an important problem.

“同意推迟正式报告错误确实是关于该项目的信息：我希望这是关于管理层以适合他们的方式与人们合作的灵活性的信息，而不是让我的管理锤子敲在人们的头上。我是试图在那个群体中建立一些信任。这也是我们有一个相当紧张的开发人员的信息。

"Agreeing to defer officially reporting bugs was indeed information about the project: I hope it is information about the flexibility of management to work with people in ways that are okay with them, as opposed to bringing my management hammer down on people's heads. I was trying to build some trust in that group. It was also information that we had a developer who was rather high strung.

“我同意正式推迟报告，而不是完全避免它。我们减少了这个过程的官僚主义，仅此而已。

"I agreed to postpone reporting officially, not to avoid it entirely. We made the process less bureaucratic, is all.

“通过达成该协议，我能够在不使用我的管理锤的情况下更早地访问代码。

"By making that agreement, I was able to get earlier access to the code without using my management hammer.

“还有一个有趣的后记。那件事发生大约五年后，我再次遇到那个程序员 [high-strung developer]，并提醒他我们的安排。令我惊讶的是，他说，'是的，我真是个混蛋“那我应该让你无条件地测试产品。” 人会成长。”

"There's also an interesting postscript. About five years after that incident, I met that programmer [the high-strung developer] again, and reminded him of our arrangement. To my surprise, he said, 'Yeah, I was such a jerk back then. I should have just let you test the product, unconditionally.' People grow."

确实如此，创造成长环境始终是一种很好的管理方法。请注意，您了解偏离成功流程的所有真正原因，以及您可能发送的意外信息。

Indeed they do, and creating an environment for growth is always a good management approach. Just be careful you understand all of your true reasons for deviating from a successful process, and what accidental messages you might be sending.

去别的地方报仇吧。

Take your revenge somewhere else.

遗憾的是，并非所有伪造的测试报告都是为了让开发人员看起来不错。如果测试人员和开发人员之间的关系紧张，测试人员很容易让特定开发人员看起来好像他们做得很差。通常，这是测试运行和测试人员对 bug 重要性评估的无意识偏差，但它可以有意识地和恶意地进行。如果是这样，这是一个病态组织的标志。

Sad to say, not all falsified test reports are trying to make developers look good. If relationships between testers and developers are strained, it's easy for testers to make particular developers look as if they're doing a poor job. Generally, this is an unconscious skewing of tests run and of the testers' assessment of bug significance, but it can be done consciously and maliciously. If so, it's a sign of a sick organization.

提前退货会误导您。

Early returns will mislead you.

另一种常见的自作自受的骗局是根据早期回报预测测试需要多长时间，如下面的声明：“让我们看看，我们在第一周修复了 20 个错误，我们有 200 个已知错误，所以它需要总共十周才能完成。” 不，不是真的。一般来说，您修复的前 20 个错误属于最容易修复的错误——它们是您最先修复的错误，所以（几乎）根据定义，它们是最容易修复的错误——所以这种“方法”严重低估了多少需要时间来修复其他 180。

Another common self-perpetrated scam is predicting how long testing will take based on early returns, as in the following proclamation: "Let's see, we fixed twenty bugs in the first week, and we have two-hundred known bugs, so it will take ten weeks overall to finish." No, not true. Generally speaking, the first twenty bugs you fix are among the easiest bugs to fix—they're the ones you fixed first, so (almost) by definition, they were the easiest ones to fix—so this "method" seriously underestimates how much time will be needed to fix the other 180.

在 Beta 测试期间会发生相同类型的错误。产品的早期用户不太可能深入使用该产品——事实上，甚至可能因为错误而无法尝试某些功能。因此，Beta 测试结果往往会严重低估产品中不太常见的功能中的错误。与其使用一些伪造的“统计”推理，不如分析在测试过程中突然出现的各种问题（不是产品中的问题，除非产品难以测试以至于您可以安全地预测它将是一个无限的过程）。

The same type of error occurs during beta testing. Early users of a product are less likely to exercise the product in depth— and may, in fact, be blocked by bugs from even trying certain features. Thus, beta-testing results tend to seriously underestimate bugs in the less common features of a product. Rather than using some bogus "statistical" reasoning, you may want to analyze the kinds of problems that crop up in the doing of the testing itself (not problems in the product, unless the product is so hard to test that you can safely predict it will be an infinite process).

“数量”不是质量的代名词。

"Quantity" is not a synonym for quality.

许多不经意的骗局都依赖于错误的信念，即大量的测试运行或检测到的错误必然意味着已经完成了彻底的测试工作。如果您上了“数量-均值-质量”骗局的当，您就会暴露在各种误导性信息中。一些常见的品种如下。

Many oblivious scams depend on the fallacious belief that a large number either of tests run or of bugs detected necessarily means that a thorough job of testing has been done. If you fall for The Quantity-Means-Quality Scam, you expose yourself to all sorts of misleading information. Some common varieties follow.

轰动因素

The Thud Factor

一位开发副总裁被问及测试如何使他的工作更轻松。他的回答出乎所有人的意料：“我希望测试文档中包含大量因素。你看，我们的客户问我们，‘我们怎么知道你们的东西好用？’ 一直都在。我想给他们带来一个大而厚的测试计划，然后把它砸在他们的办公桌上，以向他们展示质量对我们的重要性。”

One vice president of development was asked how testing could make his job easier. His answer surprised everyone: "I want thud factor in the test documentation. You see, our customers ask us, 'How do we know your stuff is any good?' all the time. I want to bring them a big, fat, test plan and slam it down on their desks to show them how important quality is to us."

换句话说，如果你想知道的事情（质量）太难衡量，那就衡量一个替代品（在这种情况下，文档的厚度）。

In other words, if the thing you want to know about (quality) is too hard to measure, measure a substitute (in this case, thickness of documentation).

Hack-'n'-crack/Whack-a-bug

Hack-'n'-crack/Whack-a-bug

错误不会随机发生。如果你把每一个都当作一个孤立的案例来解决，你就会错误地估计真正的成就。很多时候，如果您查明失败的根本原因，您将同时解释并消除多个失败。但是，如果您将每个错误都视为一个孤立的随机事件，那么您将花费更长的时间并错过很多本可以轻松删除的错误。或者，您将删除您不知道自己正在删除的错误，并高估了剩余的工作量。

Bugs do not occur at random. If you fix each one as if it were an isolated case, you'll misestimate the amount of real accomplishment. Quite often, if you pinpoint the root cause of a failure, you'll explain—and eradicate—several failures at once. But if you treat each bug as an isolated, random event, you'll take a lot longer and miss quite a few bugs you could have easily removed. Or, you'll remove bugs you didn't know you were removing, and overestimate the amount of work remaining.

回归测试≠新测试

Regression Tests ≠ New Tests

如果管理层奖励测试人员执行大量测试，您可能会发现自动回归测试在每次运行时都会被计算在内。即使大量测试很重要，多次计算相同的测试也是骗局。如果有的话，回归测试运行的次数越多，对被测产品和过程的影响就越大。为什么要多次运行回归测试，除非你需要多次来解决同一个问题？

If management rewards testers for performing a large number of tests, you may find that automated regression tests are counted each time they are run. Even if large numbers of tests were significant, counting the same test multiple times is a scam. If anything, the more times a regression test is run, the worse that augers for the product under test, and the process. Why run a regression test multiple times unless it takes you multiple times to fix the same problem?

数数≠思考

Counting ≠ Thinking

计数测试会产生许多不利影响。例如，当测试被计算在内时，测试人员可能会避免创建任何冗长或复杂的测试。他们可能会停止互相帮助进行测试，并停止进行其他不算作测试用例的有用测试活动。通常，他们会想方设法复制带有细微变化的测试，并将它们称为不同的测试。

Counting tests can produce many sinister effects. For instance, when tests are counted, testers may avoid creating any long or complicated tests. They may stop helping each other with tests, and stop doing other useful testing activities that don't count as test cases. Often, they find ways to copy tests with slight variations and call them different tests.

用测试计数来代替观察、对话和思考是如此诱人。将所有内容简化为数字可以实现惊人的效率，因为我们可以假设所有事情而无需听到它们。当然，这会因遗漏而造成大量谎言。允许您的听众继续对您正在做的事情做出错误假设很容易撒谎。
